The Witches Bodyguard

by TaylorKomClexakru

Summary

When award-winning actress Agatha Harkness begins receiving escalating threats from a dangerous stalker, her agent hires elite bodyguard Rio Vidal and her team to protect her. Rio is disciplined, guarded, and determined to keep things strictly professional—but Agatha, America’s beloved yet notoriously difficult star, has other plans. Sparks fly as the line between duty and desire blurs, forcing them to balance the glare of the public eye, the lurking danger of a relentless stalker, and the growing pull of a love neither expected.

Notes

I've had this idea stuck in my head for a while. I'm going to try to post semi-regularly. I've already written a few chapters and have them ready to go. Please leave a comment and kudos if you enjoy.

S.H.I.E.L.D

Rio’s internal alarm woke her at 6:00 a.m. on the dot, just as it always did. Years in the Special Forces had drilled the habit into her: wake before the birds, before the sun, before the rest of the world.

She got out of bed and pulled on a sports bra and loose sweatpants, her body moving on autopilot. On her way out, she stopped at Victoria’s terrarium. The tarantula stirred as Rio dropped in her breakfast. Most people thought she was crazy for keeping one, but Victoria had been with her through everything, deployments, long nights overseas, and the hollow ache of her discharge.

Crossing the penthouse, Rio watered her plants. She found peace in the simple act, the ritual of checking each leaf and stem. Over time, her home had transformed into more of a greenhouse than a penthouse, but she wouldn’t have it any other way. While Rio wouldn't call herself extremely rich, she is well off, having saved as much of her military earnings and her earnings from her Bodyguard business.

Finally, she locked the door and set off on her usual morning run. One of the perks of waking before God herself was that the streets were almost empty, save for the occasional straggler or stray animal. This was her favorite time of day—quiet, steady, and hers alone.

She was three miles into her five-mile run when her phone buzzed. Maria Hill’s name flashed across the screen.
Rio slowed her pace and veered off to the side of the trail before answering. She and Maria had been friends for over twenty years, their bond forged in the military. Rio had been a team leader in Delta Force, and Maria a commander in MARSOC—Marine Raiders. They first crossed paths on a joint operation and hit it off instantly.

Maria’s career ended abruptly after a dishonorable discharge under the “Don’t Ask, Don’t Tell” policy. Years later, when Rio herself left the service—this time honorably—they reconnected. Out of that reunion, their company was born: S.H.I.E.L.D. (Specialized Hostile Intervention & Elite Life Defense). A bodyguard company for the elite, including Actors, musicians, politicians, athletes, and billionaires/millionaires.

Rio had insisted Maria take the title of CEO; she never cared for the day-to-day bureaucracy. She preferred the fieldwork, the action. Co-CEO suited her fine—close enough to keep a hand in the business, far enough to stay private.

She thumbed her headset on. “Good morning, Maria. What went wrong this early?”

“Good morning, Rio,” Maria replied, amused but exhausted. “Why do you always assume something went wrong?”

Rio smirked, wiping sweat from her brow. “Because you don’t usually call me at six in the morning when you know I’ll be in the office in a few hours. So what’s so urgent you couldn’t wait to tell me face to face?”

“I just got off the phone with an agent for a very high-profile actress,” Maria explained. “She’s requesting our services—and she asked for you specifically to lead the team. The agent will be here at nine to go over everything, but she wouldn’t give me much over the phone.”

“Do you have a name? And any idea why she asked for me in particular?” Rio asked, already pivoting on her heel and heading back toward home. She needed a shower and a change of clothes before the meeting.

“She only gave her first name—Lilia. Said she’d explain more when she got here. I pressed her, but she was tight-lipped. From her tone, though, I’d say she’s rattled about something.” Maria’s clipped voice carried that edge of annoyance Rio knew well—the kind that came when someone tried to withhold intel.

“I might’ve protected one of her clients before.” Rio quickened her pace. “Is the actress herself coming to the meeting, or just Lilia?”

“Just the agent for now,” Maria confirmed. “Once we have the logistics and know exactly what we’re walking into, then we’ll meet her client, if we take the job.”

“Understood. I’ll be in after I change.”

Maria grunted her acknowledgement, and Rio ended the call.

The rest of the run home blurred as her mind churned. Who was the client? Why had Lilia insisted on her, specifically? And what was so urgent—and dangerous—that an agent this seasoned sounded cagey on the phone?

By the time Rio made it home, the clock read 7:30. She didn’t waste a second—jumped into the shower, dressed quickly, and pulled on her usual work attire: black slacks and a crisp white button-up. As always, she rolled her sleeves to the elbows, exposing the ink that marked her left arm.

Her sleeve tattoo wound upward from wrist to shoulder, an old oak tree etched in striking detail. Each leaf represented someone she’d lost—teammates, loved ones, ghosts she carried with her every day. Vines stretched from the trunk, twisting across her ribs and back like roots refusing to let go. On her right arm, the insignia of her Delta Force unit stood bold, under a portrait of Santa Muerte, a nod to her call sign, Lady Death, and a quiet tribute to her Puerto Rican roots.

One more glance at the clock told her it was time to move. Grabbing her keys, she slipped into her Lincoln Aviator SUV and made a quick detour to her local coffee shop. The baristas knew her well enough to start her usual order the moment she walked in. One of them tried to flirt, as always. Rio responded with polite deflection, offered a small smile, left a tip, and was gone.

The rest of the drive passed quickly. She knew the back routes of L.A. like the palm of her hand, weaving around traffic until she pulled into the garage at 8:30 sharp—record time.
Inside, she scanned her ID, offered a nod to the security guard, and stepped into the elevator. She pressed the button for the top floor, the domain she and Maria ran together.
The elevator doors slid open with a muted chime, and Rio stepped into the quiet, polished corridor of the top floor. The walls were lined with framed commendations, photos of past clients, and discreetly displayed medals, equal parts professional polish and subtle warning.

Maria’s office door was already open. Rio knocked once on the frame before stepping inside.

Maria sat behind her desk, posture straight, expression sharp, though the faint crease between her brows betrayed her exhaustion and irritation. A neat stack of files was spread out in front of her, but Rio knew Maria had already memorized every line.

“Right on time,” Maria said, glancing at the clock.

“Of course,” Rio replied, setting her coffee on the edge of the desk and handing Maria’s coffee order to her before leaning against it. “Any updates from our mysterious Lilia?”

Maria gave a tight shake of her head. “Nothing. I’ve run her name through our system—too common. Could be anyone. No background, no trail, no agency records that match. Either she’s covering her tracks, or someone’s covering them for her.”

Rio hummed, her eyes narrowing. “So we’re walking in blind.”

“Not the first time,” Maria said dryly, though her tone carried the weight of experience.

Rio smirked faintly. “And it won’t be the last.”

Maria closed the folder in front of her and folded her hands. “She’ll be here in about thirty minutes. I want us on the same page before she walks through that door. No promises, no commitments, not until we know who we’re protecting and what we’re protecting them from.”

“Understood,” Rio said. She straightened, her jaw tightening with anticipation. “If she asked for me by name, then it’s already personal. And I don’t like going in blind when someone else is pulling strings.”

Maria studied her for a long moment, then gave a small nod. “Then let’s see what kind of game Lilia is playing.”

The room fell quiet, the hum of the city below faint through the glass windows. Both women knew that whoever was about to walk through their doors wasn’t bringing them a simple assignment, this was going to be trouble.

Maria and Rio made their way to the sleek conference room they always reserved for clients. The room smelled faintly of polished wood and fresh coffee, the kind of neutral space meant to make negotiations feel safe. A call came through from the front desk: they’re escorting Lilia up now.

They only had to wait a few minutes before the doors opened. Lilia entered first, flanked by discreet but imposing security. The moment she crossed the threshold, the atmosphere in the room shifted.

Rio’s instinct kicked in immediately—her mind cataloguing Lilia’s movements, her attire, the aura she carried. The woman’s presence was commanding, almost regal, like an old-world matriarch who’d seen generations rise and fall. She wore a long Italian coat that looked more heirloom than fashion, the fabric catching the light in wisps as if it had a history of its own. Rio couldn’t shake the sense that she’d seen her before, though the exact memory eluded her.

Both Maria and Rio stood to greet her.

“Hi, Lilia. I’m glad you made it alright. Would you like anything to drink?” Maria asked with her usual measured politeness.

“No thanks, dear,” Lilia replied smoothly, her voice warm but carrying steel beneath it. “I would rather we just get straight into it. I’m sorry for the secrecy, but given the recent events I figured, better safe than sorry.”

Rio immediately appreciated her no-nonsense approach. But what caught her off guard was how Lilia’s gaze lingered on her. Not a passing glance, but a careful, deliberate study, as though the older woman was reading her like tarot cards.

“Of course,” Maria said, motioning for everyone to sit. “Please tell us who your client is, and how we may offer our assistance.”

Lilia’s posture straightened as if she were about to deliver a verdict. “My client’s name is Agatha Harkness.”

Rio froze. She knew that name—everyone knew that name. Agatha was an international megastar, a two-time EGOT winner whose career stretched back to childhood. Agnes of Westview. Witches Road. The cult hit Salemites. She was a household name, and for Rio, something more personal. Agatha had been her gay awakening, her untouchable celebrity crush. The woman whose very existence had shifted her own.

Her shock must have been written across her face, because Lilia allowed herself the faintest smile before moving on.

“Agatha has a stalker,” she explained. “She’s dealt with stalkers before, but this one has escalated in ways that are… troubling. The security we’ve hired previously failed to contain them. Worse, one was bribed into selling private footage from inside her home. Whoever this is, they’re bold, resourceful, and not stopping. I know you are the best at what you do, and I am willing to pay whatever is needed to ensure Agatha’s safety.”

Maria jotted down notes, her expression composed. Rio forced herself to focus, though her pulse quickened.

“How long has this been going on? We’ll need a record of every incident since it started,” Rio pressed, slipping into her professional cadence. “And why me specifically? Why ask for me to lead the team?”

Lilia met her eyes again, and this time her tone softened, the weight of something deeply personal carried in her voice.

“This began about three years ago. At first, it was fan mail, then it turned possessive. Gifts left on her car, her doorstep, even her bed. Friends and colleagues threatened. Phones hacked. The pattern has only grown worse. As for you, Rio… I asked for you because my full name is Lilia Calderu. You knew my son.”

The name hit Rio like a shockwave. Calderu. Her brain scrambled, then locked onto it—Colten “Pots” Calderu. The youngest of her unit, eager, bright, shadowing her every move like a kid brother. He’d earned his call sign because his name closely resembles cauldron. And his love of cooking. He’d idolized her.

Rio’s throat tightened. When she was discharged, her team had stayed behind. Their last mission had claimed them all. She had never stopped carrying that guilt, and Colten, sweet, loyal Colten, was the heaviest weight of all.

She gasped softly, the realization cracking through her professional mask.

“Ma’am, I am so sorry. I carry the weight of his passing with me every day. Colten is one of the main reasons I started this business. I couldn’t protect him, but I will protect my clients with my life, if I must.”

She held Lilia’s gaze, hoping the older woman could hear the sincerity and the guilt. Woven through her words.

Lilia’s lips curved into a warm but sorrowful smile. She lifted her hand in a gentle wave, dismissing the apology.

“No need, dear. My Colten wrote me almost every day, and he always spoke of you like you hung the moon and the stars. You were the sister he never had. He would never blame you, and I sure as hell don’t either. With the way he talked about you, and adding in your very impressive, decorated reputation, I trust no one more with Agatha’s safety.”

Maria, who had been silently observing, felt the weight settle in the room. She saw how Rio carried her ghosts, how the guilt of her team’s deaths still lingered like a shadow. That decided it for her.

“We’ll take Agatha as a client,” Maria said firmly, closing her notebook and rising from her chair. “Rio will assemble her best team today while I draw up the paperwork. If you can bring Agatha in tomorrow to meet the team and finalize the necessary documents, we can have her security detail in place before tomorrow night.”

“Thank you so much. Agatha can be… difficult, and at times self-destructive,” Lilia admitted, her voice softening with a note of affection. “But she deserves the best, and this company is it.”

She stood, shaking both Maria’s and Rio’s hands with firm gratitude before sweeping from the room.

Rio watched her go, the weight of the responsibility settling on her shoulders. She pulled out her tablet and began scrolling through her roster, mind already racing through names. This would require nothing less than a six-man team—the threat level was high, and the danger almost guaranteed to escalate. Only her A-Team would do.

Maria gave a final nod, gathering her notes as she headed out to begin the paperwork. The office fell quiet, leaving Rio alone with her thoughts. She exhaled slowly, pinching the bridge of her nose before scribbling down potential assignments.

Tomorrow. Tomorrow she’d meet the Agatha Harkness—America’s darling, beloved and feared in equal measure. Rio only hoped she wouldn’t make a fool of herself in front of the woman whose name carried so much fire.

She Hired Protection and Found Temptation

Chapter Summary

Agatha gets talked into taking on a Security detail, and Agatha and Rio meet!!

Chapter Notes

Not proofread because it's 3 A.M and my sleep paralysis demons are calling me, and i just wanted to make sure this chapter was out for you guys. Hopefully, another 2 chapters will be released tomorrow.

All mistakes are mine, please leave a comment and Kudos.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio spent the night poring over files, chasing the perfect balance. She needed professionals who could follow orders and execute flawlessly—dangerous, loyal, and disciplined enough to know when to pull the trigger and when to hold back. This job was bigger than just keeping Agatha safe; it would be round-the-clock, relentless, and under constant scrutiny.

And then there was Agatha herself. Rio knew her reputation—charming, flirty, a self-proclaimed menace. From a distance, Rio had always found it endearing, even funny. But facing it head-on, twenty-four hours a day, she wondered if she had the patience to match her professionalism against Agatha’s chaos.

When it came to her team, Rio played it smart. No one who might be swayed by Agatha’s magnetic charm. Everyone chosen was either happily partnered or simply not interested in women. While fraternization wasn’t technically against company policy, it was frowned upon—and one scandal could mean investigations, ruined reputations, and jobs lost.

By dawn, she had her six. Files spread across her desk like a hand of cards, Rio tapped out individual messages summoning them to the office at 10 a.m. sharp.

Alice Wu-Gulliver: Former cop and detective, daughter of rock icon Lorna Wu—though she preferred her stepfather’s name, Gulliver. Rio’s closest friend, apart from Maria, and one of the first hires when SHIELD was founded. Alice would head tech, security systems, and fortification of Agatha’s home.

Natasha Romanov-Hill: Once a KGB assassin, now Maria’s wife—and still one of the most intimidating operatives Rio had ever met. Natasha would serve as second-in-command, accompanying Agatha and Rio to public events, and whenever they go out in public

Yelena Belova: Natasha’s adopted younger sister, equally trained in espionage, though a touch more reckless. Ruthless when she needed to be, Yelena would lead house and vehicle security, rotating with Bucky, and join major public appearances where an extra layer of muscle was essential.

Clint Barton: A debate in Rio’s mind, but ultimately an asset she couldn’t overlook. Older, edging toward retirement, but still sharp, still deadly accurate. A marksman, a driver, and a watcher at the gate. Clint was family to Natasha and Maria, which made him family to Rio as well.

Bucky Barnes: Rio’s longest-running ally. They’d served side by side in Delta, and she still thought of him as an older brother. After years as a CIA assassin, he’d joined SHIELD three years earlier, settling down with his husband, Sam Wilson. He would serve as third-in-command, shadowing Rio and Natasha on every high-profile outing.

The list was clean, solid, unshakable. Rio fired it off to Maria, who sent back her immediate approval. Satisfied, Rio closed her laptop. Tomorrow would be the start of something big—new client, new risks, new team dynamic. She could only hope she wouldn’t let anyone down.

Especially not Agatha Harkness.

Across town, Lilia was doing her best to reason with an increasingly restless Agatha. The actress paced the length of her living room, heels clicking against hardwood, agitation radiating from her with every step. She wasn’t angry at Lilia, not really—just furious that things had escalated to the point where a 24/7 security detail was no longer optional.

“Agatha, these people are the absolute best at what they do,” Lilia pressed, voice steady but firm. “They guard half of Hollywood’s elite. I met with the CEOs today—they’re more than willing to take you on. The team leader, Rio—she was my son’s squad leader in Special Forces. He trusted her with his life and idolized her. I’ve done my research on the company, and they’re legit. They’ve never lost a client, never had one harmed.”

That made Agatha stop mid-pace. Lilia rarely mentioned her son. Everyone knew he’d died overseas, but the details had always been private.

“Didn’t he die during a mission?” Agatha shot back sharply, the words out before she could stop them. “Where was this Rio person when he died?”

The look on Lilia’s face gutted her.

Jennifer Kale, Agatha’s publicist, winced, while Billy Maximoff—Agatha’s ever-patient assistant—appeared at her side with a glass of water. On the other end of the couch, Wanda Maximoff watched with open disapproval.

“Rio was injured during a previous mission,” Lilia said tightly, but with dignity. “She was honorably discharged before the mission that took my son’s life—and that of his entire unit. I spoke with her today, Agatha. She still carries that loss as heavily as I do. They were inseparable—like siblings. Nothing she could have done would’ve changed the outcome.”

The fight drained from Agatha in an instant. She collapsed onto the couch, pressing the heel of her hand against her forehead. “I’m sorry. That was low. I just…” She gestured helplessly. “I don’t want to be watched, followed, treated like a baby in a world that’s waiting to break me.”

Wanda slid onto the couch beside her, looping an arm over her shoulders. “Agatha, this isn’t about control—it’s about survival. The last security team couldn’t handle you on their best day. These people can. Trust me. When I had that obsessed fan a few years back, this company handled it. The woman they sent me? Professional. Terrifying. One day, that fan was outside my gate, and the next… he was gone. They get results. They’ll take care of you.”

Agatha sighed, leaning into Wanda’s comfort despite herself.

Wanda had been in her life for almost 20 years since Agatha was 25 and Wanda was sixteen, a newcomer to Hollywood. Agatha had taken her under her wing, and though the public had always speculated, shipping them as something more. The truth was simpler and deeper. Wanda had Vision, her first love, her husband, the father of her twins.

Agatha… Agatha had never been one for relationships. She lived fast, burned bright, and left people dazzled but never tied down. More of a fuck e'emand leave em kind of girl.
They weren’t lovers. They were sisters. And Wanda wasn’t about to let her sister throw herself to the wolves.

“Fine, I’ll meet with them. But Wanda’s coming with me,” Agatha declared, tone leaving no room for argument.

“Of course,” Wanda said easily, squeezing her friend’s hand.

“Perfect,” Lilia replied with relief. “We leave in an hour. You’ll be meeting the entire team today—six of the best operatives SHIELD has to offer.” She stood, pulling out her phone to message Rio, then paused at the door. “Oh, and Agatha? Do not sleep with your bodyguard. I don’t want Jen suffering a heart attack cleaning up that scandal.”

Lilia left, but the warning had the opposite effect. Agatha’s head snapped up, eyes glinting. “Wait. Did she just imply my bodyguard’s hot?”

Wanda groaned, already seeing the spark of trouble. She smacked Agatha lightly on the back of the head. “No. Agatha, no. Cool your libido for once. She’s going to be in charge of your life. Don’t screw it up by screwing her.”

Agatha wasn’t listening. She pulled out her phone and navigated straight to SHIELD’s website, smirking when she found the staff directory. It didn’t take long to spot Rio Vidal—her new team leader and co-CEO of the entire company.

Agatha nearly dropped her phone. Holy shit. Tan skin, sharp jawline, warm honey-brown eyes that seemed to stare right through the screen. A faint tattoo peeked from her collar, hinting at more ink hidden beneath. Commanding. Gorgeous. Dangerous. Hot.

Suddenly, the idea of a bodyguard 24/7 seemed far less suffocating.

“Fuck. She’s hot,” Wanda muttered, leaning over Agatha’s shoulder. “If I weren’t married, I’d do unspeakable things to that woman.”

“Please,” Jennifer Kale scoffed, crossing her arms. “I am single. Maybe I’ll shoot my shot.”

Agatha’s head whipped around, glaring daggers. The surge of jealousy was ridiculous—she hadn’t even met Rio yet—but the thought of anyone else trying it? Unacceptable. She smirked to herself. This is going to be fun.

An hour later, Agatha, Wanda, Lilia, Jen, and Billy pulled up to SHIELD headquarters. The sleek building loomed like a fortress, humming with quiet authority.

Inside the lobby, Maria Hill was waiting. “Welcome to SHIELD. I’m Maria Hill, co-founder and CEO. I can promise you, there are no safer hands than ours. Rio has assembled an all-star team, and frankly? I fear for the lives of anyone foolish enough to test them.” She shook each of their hands, then signaled security as she led them toward the elevators.

Agatha, never one to waste an opportunity, smirked. “So… is everyone in this company hot, or is that just part of the hiring process?”

Lilia groaned. Jen rolled her eyes. Wanda buried her face in her hands.

Maria only smirked. “Rio anticipated your… charm. She handpicked a team of professionals, happily taken or not interested in women. I’d also advise you not to flirt with me when we go inside. My wife is on your detail, and she’s very possessive.”

That earned a ripple of laughter from Lilia, Jen, and Wanda. Agatha blinked, impressed despite herself. “Fine. Which one’s your wife, so I know who not to flirt with?”

“The redhead,” Maria replied dryly as the elevator chimed open.

Moments later, she pushed open the conference room doors. Conversations cut off instantly. The team stood. And then Rio turned.

Agatha’s breath caught.

Rio was even more devastating in person—broad-shouldered in a tailored black suit, a sharp contrast to her warm eyes. Authority clung to her like armor, and that faint neck tattoo teased Agatha’s imagination in dangerous directions.

Rio, for her part, nearly forgot how to breathe. Agatha Harkness. Standing there in deep purple trousers, crisp white blouse, and a navy coat that belonged on the cover of a magazine. Stunning. Untouchable. Everything Rio had crushed on in secret—now inches away.

Professionalism saved her. Barely.

“Hello, Ms. Harkness. And hello again, Lilia.” Rio’s voice was steady, controlled, even though her pulse thundered. “Thank you for coming. I’ll introduce you to the team, we’ll go over ground rules and protocols, sign paperwork, and then escort you home. Your new security detail begins tonight.”

Agatha’s lips curled into a slow, mischievous smirk. Game on.

Rio straightened, professional mask firmly in place. “Allow me to introduce you to your detail, Ms. Harkness. Each of them is the best at what they do.”
She gestured to the woman closest.

“Alice Gulliver.” Alice, in dark jeans and a leather jacket, gave an easy nod. “Tech, surveillance, systems security. I’ll make sure your home, vehicles, and digital footprint are locked tighter than Fort Knox.”

Agatha tilted her head, amused. “So you’ll know if I order midnight pizza?”

Alice smirked. “I’ll know if you breathe near your phone, Ms. Harkness.”

“Terrifying. I like her already.” Agatha winked. Rio cleared her throat.

“Natasha Romanov-Hill.” The redhead stepped forward, calm but with an edge that could cut steel. “ Apart from Rio, you will be seeing me the most. You’ll see me at public events, alongside Rio.”

Agatha arched a brow. “The redhead. Right. So you’re the wife I was warned not to flirt with?”

Natasha’s lips twitched. “Correct. And consider this fair warning back, you really don’t want to test that theory.”

Wanda coughed to hide her laugh. Jen mouthed yikes. Rio gave Agatha a look that said Behave.

“Wait, you are who was sent to protect me a few years back from that obsessed fan, I see you are still as terrifying as I remember. I'm glad to see Agatha is in good hands though.” Wanda says, recognizing the redhead, it took her a second to place her, but she can never forget the women who possibly saved her life and the life of her family.

“It is good to see you again Mrs. Maximoff, glad to see you have stayed safe and out of trouble. “ Natasha said, nodding to Wanda.

“Yelena Belova.” The younger blonde said with a cocky grin and a wave. She leaned against the wall as if she owned it. “House and vehicle security lead. You’ll see me at major events too. I’m the one who tells you when to duck.”

Agatha chuckled. “And what if I don’t?”

“Then I throw you over my shoulder and run. You’ll thank me later.”

“Bold,” Agatha purred, but Yelena just grinned wider. Agatha got the sense her and Yelena will get along very well seeing as their personalities seem to match.

“Clint Barton.” A man in his forties with sharp eyes and a laid-back stance gave a half-wave. “Driver, marksman, gate security. I’ll get you where you need to go and make sure no one’s following.”

Agatha smirked. “So basically, my chauffeur?”

“Chauffeur with a gun and a very high tolerance for divas.” Clint shot back smoothly.

Wanda actually snorted. Agatha pretended to look offended, but clearly loved it. At least its looking like her team isn't all a bunch of stuck-up men in suits who wouldn't know fun if it smacked them in the face.

“Bucky Barnes.” He was tall and broad, steady, with short dark hair. “Third-in-command. I’ll be with Rio and Natasha at all public appearances. Think of me as the wall between you and the world.”

Agatha studied him, noting the quiet power in his presence. “Big wall. Sturdy. Handsome. I approve.”

“Glad to meet your standards,” Bucky deadpanned.

Finally, Rio straightened, drawing every eye back to her.

“And I am Rio Vidal. Co-CEO of SHIELD, your team leader, and the one directly responsible for your safety. Everything goes through me.”

For a beat, silence hung in the air.

Agatha let her gaze trail over Rio openly, unapologetic. The suit. The tattoos. The warm, unflinching eyes. She smiled like a cat who’d found cream.

“So you’re the one I’ll be seeing… twenty-four seven?” she asked, voice velvet, laced with mischief.

Rio held her ground, though her pulse stuttered. “Yes, ma’am. Twenty-four seven.”

Agatha’s smirk deepened. “Well. Suddenly, this whole bodyguard thing doesn’t sound so terrible.”

The team collectively groaned under their breath. Wanda buried her face in her hands again. Lilia just pinched the bridge of her nose, already feeling a migraine coming on.

Rio, unshaken, moved briskly on. “We’ll review ground rules and protocols now. Ms. Harkness, please try to keep your comments… professional.”

Agatha leaned back in her chair, eyes never leaving Rio. “No promises.”

Chapter End Notes

Guarding Agatha

Chapter Summary

Security Detail officially starts, Agatha being herself, Jen being done with Agatha and Rio trying to contain the gayness.

Please comment and Kudos, they feed my soul and keep me writing.

Maybe another chapter coming tonight, if not one will be released tomorrow.

Everyone gathered around the table, the air charged with a mix of seriousness and Agatha’s usual flair for chaos.

“Alright,” Rio began, voice crisp and commanding, “my team will need Ms. Harkness’s full schedule—every event, location, time, duration. We need to coordinate with event security and ensure there are no gaps. All fan mail goes through Yelena and Alice first. Ms. Harkness is not to touch anything before one of us clears it.”

“As much as I’d love you calling me ‘Ms. Harkness’ in some more… intimate setting when we’re doing other things, just call me Agatha, darling,” Agatha said with a sly grin.

Rio kept her expression neutral, her training the only thing stopping her from reacting.

Before the silence stretched too long, Jen produced a spray bottle and spritzed Agatha right in the face.

“No. Bad Agatha. No sleeping with security,” Jen scolded like she was training a dog.

Agatha gasped, affronted. Wanda nearly fell out of her chair laughing while Lilia and Billy hid their amusement behind polite coughs. The security team looked stoic, though their eyes betrayed their amusement.

“Hey, can I get one of those?” Yelena asked.

Rio shot her a glare before snapping the conversation back to order.

Agatha’s lips parted, ready to say something scandalous about how much she’d enjoy that, but Jen—predictably—sprayed her again.

Wanda leaned forward, her protective instincts overriding her usual composure.

Rio’s tone softened, steady and reassuring. “Alice was in the Threat Management Unit—specializing in stalking cases. She’s never lost one. Natasha, Yelena, Clint, and Bucky are former spies. “So…” Agatha leaned forward, eyes bright with curiosity. “I’ve basically got a squad of assassins watching my back?”

Silence.

“Wait—really? You’re all assassins?” she asked, far more interested now, impressed… and, judging by the way her gaze lingered on Rio, slightly turned on.

“Yelena and Nat are former KGB. Bucky and Clint, CIA. And I was Delta Force,” Rio confirmed evenly. “You’ve got the best watching over you.”

Agatha and her entourage just stared, jaws slack.

“Damn,” Jen muttered, breaking the tension with a crooked grin. “Maria was right. I’m starting to feel bad for the stalker.”

The room was still reeling from the reveal of everyone’s backgrounds. Even Wanda, who had been skeptical, sat back in her chair and slowly nodded.

Agatha, of course, smirked, leaning forward with that familiar gleam in her eye.

“Well, this just got a lot sexier,” she purred.

Yelena snorted. “God, I really do need one of those,” she said, grinning.

Rio ignored the chaos like a seasoned professional. Her voice cut through the laughter, steady and commanding. “My team isn’t here to be your playthings or the punchline to a joke. We’re here because whoever is out there doesn’t see you as ‘America’s sweetheart,’ Agatha. They see you as theirs. That is dangerous. They will not stop. And we—” she glanced to her team, each one stone-faced and ready “—will not fail.”

The weight of her words sobered the room instantly. Wanda reached over, resting a hand on Agatha’s arm in silent agreement. Lilia’s sharp eyes flicked toward Rio, measuring the steel in her tone.

Agatha, uncharacteristically quiet for a beat, finally tilted her head, lips curving into a smaller, softer smile.

“Fine. I’ll behave… mostly. But if you ever do have to carry me over your shoulder, darling, I expect at least dinner first.”

Jen didn’t hesitate. Spray.

“Alice, get the equipment loaded. Yelena, Bucky, vehicles. We’ll rendezvous out back,” Rio ordered, her tone leaving no room for argument. Her team nodded in unison and filed out.

Jen spoke up, half defensive, half curious. “We already have a car waiting for us.”

Rio turned her gaze on her. “We’ll be using entirely new vehicles, cameras, passwords, and codes. Everything gets replaced. If your stalker has half the resources I suspect, they already know your routines. They may have hacked your feeds, they've even bribed someone who used to be on payroll. We’re cutting every thread they might pull on.” Her words were sharp, but the logic irrefutable. Even Lilia gave a reluctant nod.

Especially since Agatha had been her unattainable teenage fantasy, her wet dream. Now here she is just inches away.

Rio moved to Agatha’s side, close enough that Agatha caught her scent—vanilla, fresh flowers, something grounding and impossibly warm. For the first time in months, Agatha’s teasing faded. Fear had been gnawing at her, even beneath her bravado, but Rio’s presence felt like armor.

The team moved in formation: Rio at the front, Natasha guarding the rear. Bucky and Yelena melted back into place, weapons on their hips, shadows of lethal intent. Agatha’s pulse spiked, not from fear this time, but from the dawning realization that she was no longer on her own, and that she was safe.

Wanda slipped her arm around her sister’s, squeezing gently. Agatha leaned into it, grateful for the unspoken reassurance.

Out back, two black SUVs idled. Alice stood alert before one, Clint before the other, both scanning rooftops and alleys. Rio steered Agatha toward Clint’s SUV, never breaking her watch of the surrounding buildings. She opened the back door without taking her eyes off the skyline.

Agatha slid in first, Wanda following, then Jen. Lilia lingered, hand on Billy’s shoulder. “We’ll take our own car, meet you at the house.” She gave Rio a curt nod before leading Billy away.

Rio climbed in beside Agatha, shutting the door with deliberate calm. Natasha took shotgun with Clint. Yelena and Bucky ran one last sweep before loading into the lead SUV with Alice.

The convoy rolled out, sleek and silent, the city swallowing them whole.

“Sooo,” Agatha finally broke the silence, her tone playful but edged with curiosity. “Tell me a bit about yourselves. If we’re going to spend the foreseeable future together, might as well get to know you. Maria said You’re all taken?”

Natasha went first, her voice even. “Maria and I have been married for ten years, and known each other for fifteen. Her unit was sent to take me out when I was still KGB. Instead, I fell in love with her and defected.” She simplified it, but her fond smile carried the weight of a lifetime.

“Well, if that didn’t come straight off BookTok, I don’t know what did,” Jen muttered. Agatha and Wanda both laughed.

Clint picked up next, tone measured but proud. “I’ve been married to my wife, Laura, for fifteen years. We met at the CIA. Natasha and I have known each other just as long—our paths crossed when the CIA partnered with MARSOC to try to take her down. Instead, we became best friends. Laura and I have three beautiful children.”

“Damn, congratulations,” Wanda said, impressed. Then her brow furrowed as she turned to Natasha. “Also, how dangerous are you that it took both the Marines and the CIA to try to stop you?”

Natasha only smirked, saying nothing.

All eyes drifted to Rio, who had been quietly scanning the surroundings, ever alert.

“What about you, hot stuff?” Agatha teased, leaning slightly toward her.

Jen didn’t even bother reaching for the spray bottle this time. She just sighed.

Rio kept her gaze on the street, voice clipped. “I’m not seeing anyone. I focus on my work.” Her tone left no cracks to pry into, but Agatha still smirked, storing that tidbit away.

Jen, trying to deflect the sudden tension, blurted out, “Is Alice single?”

The car went quiet. Every pair of eyes turned toward her. Jen’s cheeks flushed crimson.

“Hey! If I can’t sleep with hot stuff over here, you can’t sleep with Alice. That’s not fair,” Agatha protested, indignant.

Rio’s ears burned hot. She quickly looked away, but Natasha caught the flicker in her expression through the mirror and smirked knowingly.

“Technically,” Jen said slyly, “there’s nothing scandalous about me sleeping with security. They’re not protecting me.”

That got the reaction she wanted—Agatha lunged to swat her, but Wanda grabbed her arm with a sharp, “Sit down!”

The rest of the ride settled into a rhythm of small talk and stretches of silence, though Agatha kept sneaking glances at Rio, testing, waiting. Rio refused to bite, her eyes fixed on the job.

It was getting late by the time they finally reached Agatha’s estate. Natasha and Bucky hopped out first, manually opening the gates. Bucky covered her while she worked, scanning the sidewalk and nearby cars with sharp precision. Once the SUVs rolled through, Clint and Alice split off to begin their sweep.

The house loomed like something from a dream. Sleek and modern, but softened with gothic touches. Black-framed windows gleamed in the moonlight, while ivy curled up charcoal stone walls. Lights along the pathway cast a mystical glow. Out back, an infinity pool shimmered like molten silver, edged in black marble. An underground garage—newly installed—waited to shelter Agatha’s cars.

Rio’s chest tightened as she took it in. She wasn’t poor, but this level of wealth felt like another world. Still, she thought, the place suited Agatha perfectly—elegant, mysterious, and a little witchy.

Agatha moved to open her door, but Rio’s arm shot out, stopping her, bringing them in close, her voice low but firm.

“You stay in the car until the grounds are cleared.”

The sudden closeness caught Agatha off guard. Her breath hitched, eyes darting briefly to Rio’s lips. For once, words failed her. She only nodded dumbly, heat creeping up her neck.

Rio slipped out of the car, joining Clint while the rest of the team secured the perimeter.

Inside, Wanda smirked. “You are so down bad.”

“I am not,” Agatha snapped defensively. “I’m just… having fun. This is Lilia’s fault for hiring the most attractive people alive.”

“She’s not wrong,” Jen muttered, thinking of one particular red-streaked operative.

“They’re also killers,” Wanda reminded them flatly. “So maybe keep that in mind before you start planning weddings.”

“That only makes them hotter,” Agatha shot back with a smirk.

Wanda groaned. “There’s something seriously wrong with you.”

Before Agatha could retort, Rio opened the door. “It’s all clear, ma’am. Clint is reprogramming the gate access and checking for vulnerabilities. Alice and Bucky are replacing the cameras. Nat and Yelena are patrolling the grounds.”

Rio offered Agatha her hand. Agatha didn’t need the help, but she accepted it anyway. Her palm tingled at the contact, but she played it cool as they stepped out. Natasha stood guard at the entrance, eyes scanning every shadow.

The inside of the house matched the exterior’s grandeur. Open-concept, with soaring ceilings framed in dark oak beams etched with runes and celestial motifs. Stars, moons, witchy details woven into the architecture.

At Rio’s raised brow, Agatha chuckled. “They call me the Witch of Hollywood. Might as well own it.”

The living room opened around a sunken seating pit—midnight-blue cushions forming a circle that felt less like a lounge, more like a coven’s sanctum. To the side, a kitchen gleamed with marble counters veined in gold, old-oak tables, and lanterns that lent the space an enchanted farmhouse glow. It was unmistakably Agatha’s world.

Lilia and Billy arrived a few minutes later. Clint halted the SUV at the gate, allowing them to walk the rest of the way up the long drive. Meanwhile, Bucky drove Agatha’s old car several blocks away before calling a tow truck to have it impounded, getting rid of any trace of the previous compromised security detail.

Once everyone regrouped, Lilia joined Rio, Wanda, Jen, and Billy in the living room. The group circled the sunken seating area, the room’s ambient glow catching on the runes carved into the beams above.

Jen opened her tablet and began sharing Agatha’s schedule. “Tomorrow, Agatha’s on set to meet with the director for Coven of Chaos. They may also film a few scenes, depending on readiness. The rest of the week, there’s a photoshoot, plus several interviews, promotion for both Coven and Agnes of Westview.” She forwarded the schedule to Rio’s secure line, who accepted it with a curt nod, already running logistics in her head.

“Thank you,” Rio said, voice even. “You’re free to roam the grounds and keep your routines, but if you plan to leave the property, you must inform me or one of my team first.”

Agatha scoffed lightly, crossing her arms, but didn’t argue. “Fine.” Her eyes tracked Rio as she continued. “I assume your team will take the spare rooms here?” Agatha asked, already knowing the answer but fishing for another exchange.

“Yes, ma’am,” Rio confirmed. “We’ll remain onsite at all times. Will that be an issue?”

Agatha tilted her head, a smirk tugging at her lips. “Not at all. In fact, I rather like the idea.”

Rio ignored the implication. “Have a good night, ma’am. If you need anything, don’t hesitate to reach out to one of us.” She gave a short nod before excusing herself to check in with her team outside and getting away from the temptation that is Agatha Fucking Harkness.

Through the windows, Agatha could see Alice on a ladder, installing new night-vision cameras under the eaves. Motion sensors blinked red as they powered on, and Clint worked on securing access panels at the gate. The team moved with efficiency and quiet discipline, weaving their presence into the very bones of the property.

Agatha lingered by the glass, watching Rio’s silhouette in the courtyard as she briefed Bucky and Yelena. Her stance was steady, her voice low but firm. She commanded the space without even trying. Agatha sighed. She wasn’t used to longing; it felt ridiculous, almost juvenile. Yet the thought of Rio’s tattoos, her steady hands, her sharp eyes, sent Agatha to bed buzzing.

After Wanda, Jen, Lilia, and Billy left, each with a hug and a promise to check in, Agatha slipped into her nightly routine. The house was silent save for the faint shuffle of footsteps outside, her protectors settling in.

And yet, as Agatha slid beneath the sheets, her thoughts refused to quiet. All she could picture was Rio: the brush of her arm earlier, the way she smelled of vanilla and something wild, the doe eyed intensity behind her professionalism.

Agatha fell asleep with a smile on her lips, dreaming of the woman who now guarded her life.

Fideos & Foundations

Chapter Summary

Rio and Agatha bond privately. Team gets first test out in public, and Agatha continues to be a menace. Someone please get Jen an Advil and another spray bottle.

Chapter Notes

It was barely 7 a.m. when Agatha stirred awake. Normally, the world knew better than to bother her before noon, or at least before two cups of coffee. But something had pulled her from her sleep, and wrapped in her silk robe, she padded downstairs, curiosity outweighing her irritation.

She froze at the window.

Outside, Rio was running the property line, dressed in only a sports bra and shorts. Morning light caught on the sheen of sweat across her toned stomach, illuminating the sharp lines of her abs, the curve of her shoulders, the sculpt of her traps. Tattoos wound down her arms and across her torso, ink etched into muscle like a story written on living marble.

Agatha’s mouth went dry. She was certain she was drooling. Holy shit. She already knew she’d need to change her underwear.

Rio slowed, instinct prickling. She turned and caught Agatha staring.

Agatha should have looked away. She tried to look away. Instead, her gaze lingered like a sinner locked in confession. Rio smirked faintly before turning toward the house, and panic jolted through Agatha. She spun too fast, pretending to be casual, only to slosh steaming coffee straight onto her chest.

“AHH!” she yelped.

The shout brought Bucky charging through the door, gun-hand twitching before he registered the scene: Agatha hopping in place, clutching her robe, cheeks redder than the burn. His eyes flicked to Rio jogging up the steps, then back to Agatha, and a slow, knowing smirk curved his lips.

“Ma’am.” He gave a polite nod before retreating, clearly entertained.

Agatha wanted to bury herself six feet under.

Rio entered, breath even despite the run, eyes scanning her quickly. “Everything alright, Ms. Harkness?”

“I told you, call me Agatha,” she huffed, trying for dignity while blotting coffee from silk. “And yes, I’m fine. Just annoyed I wasted a perfectly good cup.”

Then inspiration struck. Wicked inspiration.

With deliberate slowness, Agatha slipped the robe from her shoulders, letting it fall. She stood in nothing but boxer shorts, bare from the waist up.

“Here.” Her voice was tight. “Put this on.”

Agatha took the opportunity to drink her in up close. They weren’t just art. They were memory, history, devotion carved into skin.

Agatha tilted her head, filing the questions away for later. Too soon to pry. But god, she wanted to know everything.

Rio finally risked a glance back at her. Their eyes met. Just for a moment.

And it was electric.

Agatha wrapped the oversized jacket tighter around herself, still smirking as she leaned against the counter. Rio was trying very hard to look at anything but her, the floor, the window, the coffee machine, the faint dusting of flour on the marble countertop, but her eyes kept darting back, betraying her.

“So,” Agatha drawled, her voice softer now, “do all bodyguards come with abs sculpted by the gods, or is that just a you thing?”

Rio pinched the bridge of her nose, exhaling. “Agatha—”

“Yes, darling?”

“You should… really put on a shirt,” Rio said, struggling to keep her composure. At this rate it's a toss-up on who will die first from gay panic, Agatha or Rio?

Agatha grinned, but it lacked her usual bite. She slid onto one of the stools, propping her chin on her hand. For once, she didn’t press further. “You know,” she murmured, “most people in my life don’t tell me what to do. They either kiss my ass or use me.”

Agatha grew up in Hollywood. Her first acting gig was when she was just a child and starred in the now cult classic Salemites. She has seen the dark side of Hollywood, lived it for a while. This industry has always been about eat or be eaten, everyone trying to outdo each other, and they don't care who they have to hurt in the process to do so. 

Rio turned, caught off guard by the shift in tone. Agatha’s smirk had faded; in its place was a weariness Rio recognized all too well.

“I don’t really know what to do when someone looks me in the eye and says ‘no,’” Agatha admitted with a wry laugh. “Guess it’s… refreshing,” she shrugged

Rio leaned against the opposite counter, finally meeting her gaze. “I’m not here to use you. Or kiss your ass. My job is to keep you alive. That means telling you ‘no’ when I have to.”

Rio was quiet for a moment, weighing whether to be honest. But because Agatha had opened up, she decided she owed the same in return.

“I lost a lot of good people during my time in the force, as has anyone who’s served,” Rio began. “Then I was in an accident that led to a medical and honorable discharge. “So when I reconnected with Maria and we started talking, SHIELD was born. A way to use our skills to protect people who need it most. While we mainly cater to the elite, we also provide free services to battered women, people in domestic violence situations, and kids in dangerous homes. No one should ever feel like there’s no one in their corner.”

Agatha looked at her so tenderly that it made her chest ache with something she refused to name. Here was this perfect woman who had lost so much, yet still kept her heart intact and looked after the little guy. Without thinking, Agatha reached out and squeezed Rio’s hand. Their eyes locked, and for a long moment neither of them moved.

Then Yelena walked in.

Agatha sipped her coffee, her 3rd of the day, watching Rio over the rim of her mug. “You know,” she drawled, “for someone who insists on calling me Ms. Harkness, you sure boss me around like we’re married already.”

Fans pressed against barricades, cameras flashing, voices rising in a chorus of screams, the second Agatha’s car pulled into view. The paparazzi swarmed like vultures, jostling for the best shot. Usually, there aren't as many people at the studio, but because Agatha has been away from the spotlight for a few months, fans have all come for the opportunity to see the Legend.

Agatha rolled her eyes. “Darling, you’re no fun.”

“You’ll thank me when you’re not crushed by a hundred screaming fans,” Rio deadpanned.

The door opened, and noise slammed into the SUV like a tidal wave. Bucky appeared first, scanning the crowd, then motioned. Rio slid out, her body automatically shifting into shield position as she offered her hand to Agatha.

The moment Agatha stepped onto the pavement, chaos erupted. Flashes exploded. Fans screamed her name. Paparazzi surged forward, shouting questions about her new film, her “mystery security detail,” and even started asking about whether the woman in the suit at her side was more than just a bodyguard, trying to get any reaction out of the star

Agatha flashed her trademark smile, waving as if the chaos were a red carpet. She leans in close to Rio, using the excuse that she needs to be heard over the loud fans. “If I’m going to be mobbed, at least I’ll look good doing it.”

Rio tightened her stance, moving them forward in a bubble of controlled force. The team fell into perfect formation: Bucky and Natasha ahead, parting the sea of bodies; Clint covering the rear; Rio sweeping for threats with eagle eyes.

A fan broke past the barrier, lunging forward with a phone extended. Rio intercepted instantly, one hand gripping Agatha’s waist to pull her out of reach while Bucky stepped in and redirected the man back toward lot security with a glare.

Agatha’s breath hitched—half surprise, half something else—as Rio’s arm remained firm around her. She recovered quickly, plastering on a dazzling smile for the cameras. “Darling, if you wanted to hold me, you could’ve just asked,” she whispered against Rio’s ear.

“Not the time,” Rio muttered, jaw tight, keeping her eyes peeled and refusing to let Agatha get under her skin

By the time they reached the studio entrance, Agatha was laughing, sunglasses tilted just so for the cameras. To the world, she looked untouchable, radiant. But as soon as the heavy doors slammed shut behind them, muffling the roar of the crowd, her shoulders sagged.

“That,” she admitted quietly, “was… actually terrifying.” She has been mobbed by fans before, but this felt worse, maybe because of the stalker problem, or maybe she isn't as used to this as she lets on.

Rio studied her for a moment, then nodded. “And that was with a controlled perimeter. The stalker hasn’t shown themselves yet. Which means they’re waiting.”

Agatha met her gaze, the mask slipping just long enough to reveal the fear beneath. But Rio’s steady presence, the lingering warmth of her hand at her waist, grounded her.

“Well,” Agatha said finally, forcing her smirk back into place, “good thing I have my very own squad of assassins, isn’t it?”

From behind them, Natasha smirked. “You’re welcome.”

On set, everything went smoothly. Director Peggy Carter was more than willing to cooperate with Rio’s team, and together they laid out a plan to ensure the chaos from outside wouldn’t happen again. Bucky and Natasha stayed posted at the studio entrance, Clint kept a sharp eye from outside, tracking every movement, and Rio remained by Agatha’s side, never crowding her, but never far enough that she couldn’t step in at a moment’s notice.

No filming was scheduled for the day. Instead, Agatha spent hours in meetings with wardrobe, hair, and makeup, and the production team, prep work for the upcoming week when shooting would officially begin. By the time they wrapped, the sun was setting. Outside, the mob had thinned considerably. Only the most desperate paparazzi lingered, and the fans had long since dispersed after catching a glimpse of their beloved star.

Back at the house, Agatha finally sagged, letting the mask of untouchable celebrity slip away. Within the safety of her home, she could exhale.

Rio checked in with Yelena and Alice. Other than a few photographers Yelena had to chase off, the day had been uneventful. The new security system was officially online, every sensor and camera in place, and Alice was still combing through the internet. She’d even started comparing wording from the stalker’s letters to online posts, hoping to catch a digital trail.

Jen headed out for the night, but Billy stayed, retreating to one of the spare bedrooms to FaceTime his boyfriend, Eddie.

Rio eventually found Agatha in the kitchen, scrolling through her phone.

“Have you eaten anything today besides catering?” Rio asked, though she already knew the answer.

Agatha looked up with a smile and shook her head.

“I can make fideos,” Rio offered. “Puerto Rican comfort food. My mom used to make it all the time when I was growing up.”

Agatha’s eyes widened dramatically. “So let me get this straight, you’re badass, protective, fit, covered in tattoos, and you can cook? You’re the perfect woman.” She sighed theatrically, like she was lovesick.

Rio shook her head with a fond smile as she moved to gather ingredients. “Anyone ever tell you you’re an annoying menace to society?”

Agatha smirked. “No. Why have you heard something?” She laughed, then added, “You don’t have to cook, though. I usually just order takeout, watch trash TV, and then crash.”

“It’s my job to protect you,” Rio countered, pouring oil into a pan. “That includes protecting you from starvation and a terrible diet. Besides,” she tossed noodles into the pan with practiced ease “I like cooking.”

Agatha leaned her elbows on the counter, chin in hand, watching her every move. “Careful, darling. You keep cooking for me and saving my life, so I’ll have to marry you. Those are the rules of the universe.”

Rio smirked, shaking her head as she stirred the noodles until they browned. “Those are the rules, huh?”

“Unbreakable,” Agatha said with a grin. Rio shook her head with a small smile. 

“Do you like spicy?” Rio asked, sprinkling in seasoning.

“It depends. I can handle it, but not, like, devil’s-anus-level spice.”

Rio laughed, an unrestrained, warm laugh that made Agatha’s heart squeeze. She swore she’d do anything to hear that sound again.

Content, Agatha pulled her phone back out and scrolled through social media, chuckling. “You know,” she said, “you’ve got your own little fandom growing.”

Rio raised a brow. Agatha grinned and started reading aloud.

@AgathasWhore: Who are the hotties guarding Agatha? #Agatha #AgathasBodyguards
@SlvtforAgatha: Did she hire her new security off a runway? Most attractive security I’ve ever seen. #AgathasBodyguards
@AgathasCoven: The woman in the suit can throw me into traffic, and I’d thank her.
@AgnesO’Connor: Agatha’s new bodyguard could stab me with her jawline, and I’d apologize for existing in her space.
@WitchyAgatha: Did you see how protective she was? Surprised no one dropped dead from that glare. Love me a protective baddie. If I were Agatha, I’d be jumping her bones.
@CallMeDaddy: Step on me, hot bodyguard. I’ll call you Daddy. #Daddy #Protectmybody

By now, Agatha was doubled over, laughing so hard she had tears in her eyes. “And those are the tame ones,” she said between giggles. “You do not want me to read the graphic ones.”

Rio’s cheeks flamed red. “Your fans are freaks.”

Agatha leaned closer, voice dropping into a purr. “Well, so am I, darling. Maybe one day you’ll let me show you just how much.”

Rio nearly dropped the plates she was carrying but managed to set them down before she embarrassed herself. She made sure to leave enough for the others before sliding into the seat beside Agatha.

Agatha took one bite and let out a low, sinful moan. “Oh my god. I would marry you for this dish alone. This is the best thing I’ve ever eaten in my life.”

Rio shifted uncomfortably, the sound hitting her like a live wire. She swallowed hard. “Thank you,” was all she managed.

They ate side by side, conversation light, the silence between them comfortable. Agatha felt something she rarely did: safe. She’d never had a family: her mother was a nightmare, her father a ghost, no siblings to speak of. The closest thing to family is the one she’d built, consisting of Wanda, Lilia, Billy, and even Jen. But sharing a quiet meal, watching Rio laugh, tasting food cooked just for her. it was something she’d never experienced.

For the first time, she felt like she had a home. And she found herself wanting many more nights just like this.

Jen, somewhere in the distance *Smells air* Something Gay just happened *Gets spray bottle ready*
