Stalkers, Spotlights, and Safe Places

Chapter Summary

Stalkers, Spotlights, and Safe Places.

Chapter Notes

Things are heating up! Buckle up, sapphics, gays, and theys

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The next morning, Agatha had a full-day photoshoot scheduled for a magazine spread, promotion for both her upcoming film, Coven of Chaos, and her last detective series, Agnes of Westview. It promised to be grueling. Some of the shots were supposed to capture the dark romance of the show, where Agatha played a small-town cop tracking down a serial killer—who also happened to be her wife, portrayed by Wanda. With Wanda in New York for a chemistry read and unable to attend, the magazine hired a stand-in model. Agatha, of course, had already decided she would use the opportunity to get some sort of reaction out of Rio.

Meanwhile, Rio sat with her team in the living room, and Clint was stationed outside at the gate on guard duty. The morning briefing was focused and sharp: reviewing yesterday’s mob incident, fine-tuning tactics, and running through scenarios for when the stalker made their next move.

Alice scrolled through data on her laptop. “Have you talked to Agatha about anyone she might suspect? An ex, a bad fan interaction, anyone she’s pissed off?”

Rio sighed. “Unfortunately, the list is long. Agatha’s a known womanizer. She has a trail of one-night stands all over the globe, any of whom could be bitter. And her fans? Many are parasocial and obsessive. It’s hard to narrow it down. But I did get a list of all the women Agatha remembers sleeping with and sent it to you to cross-check for red flags.”

Yelena, draped lazily across the couch with a knife spinning expertly between her fingers, smirked. “You gonna add your name to that list?”

“What? No. Absolutely not.” Rio’s voice hitched. “Agatha is my client. I do not sleep with my clients.”

Alice didn’t even glance up as she added fuel to the fire. “It’s not every day your client happens to be Agatha Harkness—aka your celebrity crush since you were twelve.”

Natasha leaned back, smirking. “And let’s be honest, Agatha isn’t going to stop until she gets what she wants. She’s stubborn like that.”

“Stubborn is putting it lightly,” Bucky muttered from his corner, where he was trying to become one with the wall. “She’s been ready to jump your bones since the moment she saw you. And she’s not exactly subtle about it.”

Rio scrubbed a hand over her face. “She doesn’t actually like me. She’s just flirty that’s who she is. It’s not real.”

Every pair of eyes in the room turned toward her like she’d grown a second head.

“Are you dumb?” Yelena asked flatly, looking genuinely concerned.

Rio bristled. “I know she wants to sleep with me. But it’s just sex for her. She doesn’t actually like me like that.”

Alice snorted. “Okay. Keep telling yourself that, bud.”

Natasha arched a brow. “Why are you so against it, anyway? It’s not against company policy.”

“I know it’s not,” Rio snapped. “I wrote the damn policy. But it’s my personal rule. It’s unprofessional. Crossing that line could ruin the company’s reputation. And I’m the Co-CEO. I don’t get the luxury of being careless.”

The room fell quiet, but the looks exchanged around her made it clear no one was buying her excuse. They were able to finish the rest of the meeting without a hitch and went back to their respective duties. 

Today, only Rio would be escorting Agatha. Natasha would handle the driving and remain with the vehicle, while Bucky had already gone ahead to the lot earlier that morning to coordinate with studio security. He’d ensured Agatha would arrive and depart through a back entrance, safely out of reach of paparazzi or fans.

Agatha finally came downstairs around noon, finding Billy and Jen in the kitchen as usual. The scent of food greeted her, and she quickly noticed Rio had already made breakfast for them.

“Your breakfast and coffee are on the counter to the right of the stove,” Rio said without turning, her voice calm and steady. She didn’t need to look to know Agatha was there; she had felt the subtle shift in the air, the almost imperceptible presence that followed Agatha everywhere.

Jen and Billy jerked their heads up, startled. Neither of them had heard Agatha enter. Agatha only smirked.

“You’ve got spidey senses or something?” she teased, amused but secretly touched. She rarely ate an actual breakfast, usually grabbing just a cup of coffee before being rushed out the door. The simple gesture wasn’t lost on her.

Rio didn’t bite at the joke. She simply turned, clean and precise as ever, and began to lay out the plan for the day. Agatha nodded when appropriate, but the words themselves barely registered.

Because already, without even realizing when it had happened, Agatha trusted Rio completely. And that was something she had never allowed herself to do so quickly with anyone before.

They arrived at the photoshoot with plenty of time to spare. Thanks to Bucky’s groundwork, no screaming fans or paparazzi were waiting outside, but Rio remained on alert all the same. She led Agatha, Billy, and Jen inside, her sharp eyes scanning the building’s layout—exits, cameras, blind spots, while committing the face of every passerby to memory with clinical precision.

The photographer hurried up to greet them, his smile wide but a little strained. Rio caught the nervous twitch in his movements. Whether it was her presence unsettling him or something else, she couldn’t be sure, but she cataloged it all the same.

“Ms. Harkness,” he said, his voice warm but slightly unsteady. “Thank you so much for being here. It’s an honor to photograph you today. One of my assistants will take you to wardrobe and hair and makeup, and then we’ll begin with solo shots before moving on to the duo.”

He was short, with wavy brown hair that hung low over his eyes, so low Agatha had to resist the biting urge to ask how he even saw through a camera lens. She smirked to herself but refrained, just this once.

With a practiced nod, Agatha let the assistants guide her away. This was routine to her, the constant cycle of wardrobe, makeup, hair, and then posing for someone else’s vision. Jen stayed behind to talk with the photographer and the magazine editor about scheduling, promo, and release dates.

Rio, as always, followed Agatha, eyes flicking to every doorway, every hallway, every unfamiliar face. She walked with the quiet precision of someone who expected danger to slip out of the shadows at any moment.

The first outfit was a statement in itself. A black-and-white striped button-up, casually rolled at the sleeves, the collar left open for just enough relaxed charm. The pants were high-waisted black leather, quilted at the thighs with gold button accents—a fusion of sleek luxury and biker-edge toughness.

Rio said nothing from her spot outside the door, but her eyes betrayed the briefest flicker of appreciation before they snapped back to scanning the halls.

The first round of solo shots wrapped without a hitch. Agatha had slipped easily into her public persona: smirks, tilted chins, the effortless aura of a woman who owned every inch of the lens.

After a few more outfit changes and more solo shoots, which also went flawlessly, Agatha brought the perfect amount of sultry, flirty, and professional. Rio watched from the sidelines, resisting the urge to just watch Agatha, but she was able to remain professional and stay alert. 

But when it came time for the duo shots, a quiet ripple of panic went through the crew. The stand-in model had called in sick at the last minute.

The photographer wrung his hands. “We can reschedule—”

“Absolutely not,” Agatha cut in smoothly, already slipping into problem-solving mode. “I cleared my schedule for this, and I will not be available for a few months, plus we can't waste this perfect lighting. We’ll find a replacement.”

The assistant stammered, “W-we don’t have anyone else prepped—”

Agatha’s eyes gleamed as they slid over to Rio.

“Oh no,” Rio said immediately, already reading her mind. “Absolutely not. I’m not a model. I’m your bodyguard.”

Agatha sauntered toward her, already dressed in her second look: an all-black suit, no shirt beneath the jacket, the low plunge leaving nothing to the imagination. “Darling,” she purred, “you’re gorgeous, intimidating, and already in uniform. You’re perfect.”

Rio crossed her arms. “Agatha, I’m not here to play dress-up for a magazine spread.” She holds firm; she can't be in a magazine. Her work is behind the scenes, not in front of the camera.

Agatha leaned closer, her smirk wicked. “I’ll behave for the rest of the week if you do this one little thing for me.”

Rio’s jaw clenched. “That’s a lie, and we both know it.”

“True,” Agatha admitted with a laugh. “But it’ll be fun.” She tilted her head, lower lip caught between her teeth. “Please? For me?” Rio refused to look at her, knowing that if she does, she would relent.

The crew was staring now, waiting. Jen, traitorous as ever, piped up from the sidelines. “She’d look great on camera.” 

Rio shot her a withering glare and made a mental note to put sand in Jens' coffee. She can't believe Jen is on board with this, but Agatha clasped her hands dramatically, eyes wide and pleading. “Pretty please, gorgeous? My stalker may get me at some point, don’t deny me this simple joy today.”

Rio groaned. “That is manipulative.”

“And effective,” Agatha replied with a grin.

“And I would never allow that to happen,” Rio said, but she already knows she lost the battle and sighs, preparing herself for the torture she's about to endure and the reactions from the team when they find out she agreed to this.

Minutes later, Rio was standing stiffly in front of the backdrop, jacket reluctantly removed. The white button-up hugged her shoulders and chest in a way that made Agatha’s breath catch, and the black slacks emphasized every clean line of her form. Her sleeves rolled up, showcasing the tattoos that drive Agatha mad. 

Agatha, of course, looked like sin incarnate in her plunging black suit.

The photographer, now revitalized, clapped his hands. “Perfect! The contrast is striking—dark and light, dominance and restraint.”

Rio muttered under her breath, “Kill me now.”

“Not before the pictures, darling,” Agatha whispered back, her voice like velvet.

The poses started simple, and Agatha and the photographer helped Rio relax and not look like she's being held at gunpoint, but if you asked Rio, she prefers that:

 Agatha put a hand on Rio’s arm, both facing the camera. Agatha leaned into Rio’s space, lips inches from her ear, a wicked smirk tugging at her mouth.

“Don’t blush,” Agatha teased softly. “The camera will catch it.”

Rio’s ears turned pink anyway.

“Closer,” the photographer urged. “Yes, yes—Agatha, angle your chin down. Rio, look at her like you’re about to stop her from running.”

Rio did, and the room went quiet. The glare she gave wasn’t just protective, it was hungry, fierce. Agatha’s lips parted, her smirk faltering for the first time all day.

The next pose had Rio behind Agatha, one hand at her waist, pulling her back against her chest. Agatha let out a low, pleased hum that only Rio could hear. Rio had to use every bit of self-restraint she had not to moan at the sound and how good it felt having Agatha pressed up against her. 

“You’re enjoying this too much,” Rio muttered.

“And you’re fighting it too much,” Agatha countered, voice silky.

The photographer snapped away, delighted. “That’s it! That tension is electric!”

For the final shot, Agatha had turned fully toward Rio, a hand braced on her chest, their eyes locked in a battle of wills. Both of them were breathing harder than the lights should warrant.

“Perfect,” the photographer whispered, lowering his camera. “That’s the cover.”

The spell broke. Rio stepped back immediately, reaching for her jacket like it was a lifeline. Agatha, however, only smirked, adjusting her suit casually as if she hadn’t just unraveled her bodyguard in front of a dozen people.

“Darling,” she purred, “if you ever quit this whole saving my life thing, you’ve got a career in modeling.”

Rio shot her a glare, but her flushed cheeks betrayed her. Agatha filed the reaction away, savoring it like a victory.

The photographer practically bounced on his heels, giddy with excitement. He couldn’t believe his luck. This shoot was ten times better than it would have been with the stand-in model.

“That was incredible,” he gushed. “The tension, the push and pull. You two captured the exact longing and conflict from the show. Honestly, your acting chops are better than I expected. My publisher is going to be very pleased.” Agatha smirked, right “acting”

He shook Agatha’s hand vigorously, holding on a bit too long and too roughly. Rio stepped in, placing a steadying hand on Agatha’s shoulder while gently but firmly prying the photographer away with a glare that can melt ice.

Billy appeared at Agatha’s side, handing her a water bottle, a granola bar, and a towel to dab at the sweat on her brow.

Before she could thank him, Jen swooped in with a mischievous grin and a spray bottle, spritzing both Agatha and Rio in the face.

“You two need to leave room for Jesus,” she scolded.

Rio snatched the bottle out of her hand, glaring as she tossed it in the trash.

Agatha snorted. “You don’t even believe in Jesus, you witch.”

Jen only shrugged, completely unbothered.

“This photoshoot alone is going to skyrocket publicity,” she said excitedly. “I can already see it trending across social media. This is exactly the kind of buzz we needed for your next film, Agatha.”

She was right, Agatha’s sapphic fanbase was going to lose their collective minds over the images, especially given the heat that had radiated off the set. And Rio, whether she wanted to admit it or not, was quickly building her own following after just a handful of photos at Agatha’s side had hit the internet the day before.

Agatha smirked, sipping her water as if she hadn’t just rewritten the trajectory of her press cycle. Rio, meanwhile, stood stoic beside her—only the faintest flush on her cheeks betraying that she knew exactly how much trouble this photoshoot was about to cause.

Before anyone could say anything else, Natasha’s voice cut through the comms, urgent and breathless.

“We might have a situation. Secure Agatha. Possible stalker sighting. I’m in pursuit.”

The sound of her running echoed in the background.

Rio didn’t hesitate. She grabbed Agatha’s hand and pulled her toward the dressing room. Billy and Jen stumbled after them, panic already rising in their voices.

“What’s going on?!” Agatha demanded, startled.

“Just move. Stay in this room and drag the desk in front of the door. Open it for no one except me, you understand?” Rio barked, pushing them all inside once she’d cleared the space. She shut the door, weapon drawn, then turned to the gawking crew and ushered them away from the hallway. The urgency in her voice sent them scattering.

Inside the dressing room, Agatha tried to steady her breathing. Jen looked rattled, and Billy looked like he might cry.

“Is it the stalker?” Billy asked, his voice trembling.

“I don’t know,” Jen said quickly, forcing calm into her tone. “But Rio and Natasha can handle it.”

A gunshot cracked in the distance. They all jumped. Another followed. And then another.

The next fifteen minutes stretched into an eternity, heavy and silent. Agatha’s mind spun with possibilities, her chest tight with dread. Not knowing was worse than anything. Every sound from the hallway made her flinch, every second without news felt like it might break her.

Then, finally, a knock.

“It’s me. You can open the door now.”

Rio’s voice.

Relief hit all three of them like a tidal wave. They shoved the desk aside and threw open the door. Agatha didn’t think; she just launched herself at Rio, arms wrapping around her in a desperate hug.

Rio was unharmed. Thank god.

Behind her, Agatha spotted Yelena and Bucky, newly arrived and tense, weapons still in hand. They scanned the hall in tight formation, eyes sharp, bodies coiled like springs.

“What happened? Where’s Natasha?” Agatha asked, pulling back just enough to look at Rio’s face.

“I’ll answer your questions, but first, we need to get you in the car.”

Rio’s tone left no room for argument. She moved quickly, escorting Agatha and the others out. Bucky and Yelena closed in around them, bodies forming an impenetrable shield.

At the SUV, Rio opened the door for Agatha. Bucky and Yelena angled themselves to block every sightline until Agatha was safely inside. They got in the front seat and took off. 

“Alright,” Agatha snapped the moment the door shut, her voice sharp with fear and frustration. “Now spill. What the hell just happened? Was it the stalker? We heard gunshots! Is Natasha okay?”

Rio slid in beside her, her calm steadiness a stark contrast to the chaos. “While Natasha was watching the vehicles, she spotted a man she vaguely recognized from yesterday. He approached and tried to place something under one of the cars. She confronted him, and he bolted. She pursued. A few blocks out, he turned and opened fire. She dodged, returned fire, and clipped his shoulder, but he had a car waiting. He got away.

“But Natasha got a good enough look at him to describe him, and he left DNA at the scene. She’s giving her statement now and collecting the blood sample so we can run it through our system.”

Agatha, Jen, and Billy stared, wide-eyed.

“Do you think it was the stalker?” Jen asked quietly.

“I think it’s very likely,” Rio said. “Either the stalker himself or someone they hired. Either way, we’re closer to finding them.”

Billy swallowed. “What did he try to put on the car?”

“A tracking device,” Rio explained. “The old vehicles you used were covered in them. I suspect he wanted to tag the new ones so they could track your every move and set up an ambush. Natasha stopped him before he attached it. We recovered it nearby.”

Jen straightened, her publicist instincts kicking in. “I’ll monitor the press. We cannot let this story get out. If the media learns Agatha has a stalker, it could embolden the stalker to act more publicly. This has to stay contained. I will talk to the crew at the photo shoot and try and keep them quiet.”

Rio nodded. “We already have feelers out to hospitals, clinics, even morgues. Anyone showing up with a gunshot wound to the right shoulder will be flagged immediately.”

Her voice softened as she reached over and squeezed Agatha’s hand. “You’re safe.”

Agatha hadn’t realized she’d been holding her breath. She squeezed Rio’s hand back, anchoring herself in the warmth of her touch.

Agatha looked outside and realized they weren't headed to her house like she thought they were, “Where are we going? My house is the other way.” 

“For tonight, you will be staying at my house. Alice has picked up someone trying to interfere with the systems, and a drone was flying above the house, while I'm sure that was just the paps, Clint still shot it down. Until we are sure they can't penetrate the security, you will stay at mine, it should only be for the night, maybe two nights at the max. Yelena and Bucky will drop us off at mine, bring Jen and Billy to your place, and will guard the house like you are still there.” Rio informed.

Twenty minutes later, they pull up to Rio’s penthouse. Jen and Agatha’s jaws drop. “YOU'RE RICH?!” Agatha exclaimed shocked

“I am a CEO, Agatha, and I still have earnings from my time in the service. I don't spend my money on many things,” Rio smirked, glad to finally be the one to catch Agatha off guard.

Rio opens the car door for Agatha and gets out, taking Agatha's hand and helping her out of the car. Yelena nods at Rio, and she shuts the door, and they drive off, leaving the two on the sidewalk. Rio patches in her security code, and the gate opens, allowing the two entry. 

The moment Agatha stepped inside, she froze.

Her eyes swept upward, following the sheer wall of glass that stretched two stories high, capturing the entire skyline like a painting. The sunlight poured in, catching on polished wood, steel, and glass, making everything gleam. The telescope by the window, the sectional sofa, the sharp lines softened by plants scattered artfully around the space, it all screamed understated elegance, and was very Rio.

“This is your place?” Agatha finally said, her voice climbing in pitch as she spun slowly in a circle, drinking it all in. “You’ve been hiding a Bond-villain lair this whole time and didn’t think to mention it?” Agatha said, still shocked, she never would have taken Rio to live luxuriously. 

Rio gave her the smallest, faintest smile. “It’s just an apartment.”

“Just an apartment,” Agatha repeated, her jaw dropping dramatically. She gestured toward the ceiling, then the glass, the plants spilling over in the corner like they’d been styled by a magazine editor. “This is not just an apartment. This is a magazine spread. This is Architectural Digest. This is-” she trailed off, pressing a hand to her chest. “This is so unfair. You’re already a heavily tattooed, protective lesbian who can cook like a dream, and now I find out you live in the chic modern dream loft of my gay little fantasies?”

Rio raised an eyebrow. “Gay little fantasies?”

“Yes!” Agatha cried, striding dramatically into the living room. “Do you know where I live? A glorified witchy museum where everything is black and brooding and smells faintly of incense. Meanwhile, you’re up here in the clouds like some stoic goddess of light, with a rainforest scattered around your floor plan!” She bent over and inspected one of the plants with exaggerated seriousness. “And they’re alive, Rio. Do you know how many plants I’ve killed?”

Rio smirked faintly. “Probably all of them.” She is finding much enjoyment in Agatha’s reaction. It's like Agatha is forgetting she lives in a multimillion-dollar mansion with a private arcade, a movie theater, a bowling alley, and an infinity pool, but Rio won't mention that right now; she's much too amused. 

“All of them!” Agatha shouted, throwing her hands up. “And now you’re telling me you can keep these leafy little bastards thriving while also saving my life from deranged stalkers?!” She stalked over to the couch, flopping down and spreading her arms wide. “That’s it. I live here now. You can’t stop me.”

Rio sighed, but her lips twitched like she was fighting a smile. “You have your own house.”

“Yes, but does my house have this view?” Agatha countered, pointing out the window. “No. No, it does not. And the universe clearly wants me here with you. I mean, look at this sofa. Look at it! It’s begging for a tragic lesbian to faint across it while being comforted by her stoic, mysterious protector.” She collapsed into the cushions to demonstrate, her head lolling back dramatically.

Rio shook her head, but when Agatha peeked up at her, she swore she saw the faintest blush at the tips of her ears.

Agatha smirked. Oh yes. Tonight is going to be fun. 

Rio ignored Agatha’s dramatics and moved to arm every security feature of the house. Her movements were automatic, practiced, a ritual of safety that she could never forgo. Somewhere in the back of her mind, she thought of Maria looking after her tarantula, Victoria—something Maria had agreed to very reluctantly while Rio was on the job.

“Would you like something to drink?” Rio asked kindly, slipping off her suit jacket and draping it neatly over the kitchen counter.

Agatha, sprawled across the couch like she owned the place, watched her every move with shameless interest. “You got anything alcoholic?”

Rio nodded silently and pulled two beers from the fridge. She carried them over, handed one to Agatha, and sat down on the other end of the sofa, leaving space between the two but still close enough they could feel the warmth coming from the other.

“Takeout?” Rio asked after a sip, her tone more statement than question. She already knew Agatha well enough to predict her mood; tonight called for comfort food, not homemade dishes.

“Fuck yes. I could fuck some pizza up right now,” Agatha groaned. Her stomach growled loudly on cue. The only real food she’d had all day was the breakfast Rio had made that morning.

Rio didn’t comment, though the corner of her mouth twitched upward. She ordered from her favorite place just down the road.

Of course, deciding what kind of pizza turned into its own small war. What started as a heated debate escalated quickly, each woman digging her heels in over toppings with the kind of ferocity usually reserved for politics or blood feuds. By the time Jen FaceTimed in the middle of it to let them know they made it back to Agatha’s, she swore the two of them looked like they were one insult away from wrestling on the floor.

Finally, they compromised. They ordered both pizzas, still grumbling about each other’s “atrocious taste” but secretly pleased with the outcome.

Rio leaned back, sipping her beer in silence. Agatha smirked into hers, already planning the next little battle she’d pick just to see how far she could push the unshakable bodyguard.

The buzzer at the gate rang a short time later, and Rio rose from the couch with the smooth efficiency of someone who never let her guard drop, even at home. She let the driver through after double-checking the cameras and retrieved the pizzas from the delivery kid and shut the door, setting the boxes on the kitchen counter.

“Smells like heaven,” Agatha groaned, padding over with her beer in hand. She flipped open the boxes and immediately grinned. “Ah, yes. The superior pizza.” Agatha’s pizza is a black garlic, olive, pepperoncini, and pepperoni pizza with gorgonzola cheese.

Rio raised a brow. “You mean the one that looks like a crime scene with all of that?”

“Excuse me, hot stuff, but this—” Agatha pointed at her loaded slice like it was sacred text—“is art. Yours is just… bread with sadness.”

Rio smirked faintly and slid a slice of her minimalist Spicy chorizo and roasted poblanos onto a plate. “At least mine won’t give me heartburn and regrets.”

Agatha took a massive bite, moaning dramatically around the mouthful of cheese. “Mmmm. Worth every regret.”

They carried their plates back to the couch, beers within reach, and for a while the apartment was filled only with the sounds of chewing and the occasional muffled groan of appreciation. The city lights glittered beyond the glass walls, but the space between them on the couch felt warmer, cozier.

It was Agatha who broke the silence, grabbing the remote like she was claiming a throne. “Alright. Since you cooked breakfast and ordered dinner, I get to pick the show.”

Rio arched a brow. “This should be good.”

With a sly grin, Agatha queued up Below Deck.

Rio blinked. “Really?”

“Yes, really.” Agatha settled deeper into the couch cushions, smug. “It’s trash, it’s chaotic, and it’s mine.”

“You?” Rio said, half-amused, half-incredulous. “The woman who terrifies producers and eats interviewers for breakfast… watches reality TV about yacht crews?”

Agatha shrugged, unapologetic. “Even witches need guilty pleasures, darling. Now shut up and watch my disaster children argue over laundry.”

Rio tried to keep her expression neutral, but the corner of her mouth twitched. “This is worse than pineapple on pizza.”

Agatha gasped, clutching her chest. “You take that back.”

“Not a chance.”

For the next hour, they bantered lightly, Agatha heckling the cast like she was part of the crew, Rio offering dry commentary in between bites of pizza. But eventually, the chatter softened. By the second episode, they’d fallen into a comfortable silence, the glow of the television painting them in shifting colors.

Agatha leaned back, the edge of her shoulder brushing against Rio’s. She didn’t move away, and neither did Rio.

For once, there was no press, no cameras, no stalker. Just two women, pizza boxes, beer bottles, and the soft absurdity of strangers fighting over bunk assignments on a yacht.

And Agatha thought, as her eyes drifted to Rio’s profile in the flickering light: if this was what peace looked like, she could get used to it.

Coffee, Confessions and Chaos

Chapter Summary

Agatha and Rio start to open up to each other and get closer

Chapter Notes

Please leave a kudos and a comment; they are what keep me writing.

No smut in this chapter, it just didn't fit in with the flow I am trying to achieve. Sorry, you horny dogs. But I have already written the scene, I just need to find the right time to put it in, and let me tell you it's SPICY!!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The morning sun streamed in through the windows, painting the living room in pale gold. Rio stirred first, her body attuned to early hours no matter how late she’d gone to bed. She shifted slightly, only to realize there was a surprising weight draped over her.

Agatha.

The actress was tucked firmly against her side, one arm slung over Rio’s stomach, her head resting comfortably on Rio’s shoulder. At some point during the night, they had both slipped down into the cushions, pizza boxes abandoned on the coffee table, Below Deck still paused on the television screen.

Rio froze, her muscles instinctively going rigid. She could face down gunfire without blinking, but the warmth of Agatha’s breath tickling her collarbone was a different kind of battlefield altogether.

For one reckless moment, she let herself feel it, the softness of Agatha’s curls brushing against her jaw, the weight of her body pressed close, the quiet peace that settled in her chest. It was… nice. Too nice.

Agatha shifted in her sleep, nuzzling closer with a contented sigh.

Rio squeezed her eyes shut. She was never a believer of god, but she shot him a prayer anyway, God help me.

She carefully tried to extract herself, but Agatha’s grip tightened like a vice. Even asleep, she was stubborn.

“Mm… don’t move,” Agatha mumbled, voice husky with sleep. Her voice went straight to Rio’s core, the raspiness doing something to her. Agatha’s eyes cracked open just enough to catch Rio’s flustered expression. A wicked grin spread across her face. “Well, good morning, darling. I knew you’d give in eventually.”

Rio scowled, though her ears betrayed her by turning pink. “We fell asleep. Accident. Nothing more.”

“Of course, of course,” Agatha teased, stretching like a cat but making no effort to remove herself from Rio’s side. “Totally an accident that you let me cuddle you all night.”

“You clung like a koala. I had no choice.”

Agatha laughed softly, the sound warm and unguarded in the quiet apartment. “You’re lucky, I’m adorable.”

Rio sighed and finally slid out from under her, standing far too quickly too escape the situation. “Breakfast. I’ll make something.”

Agatha flopped back into the cushions, watching her with an infuriatingly smug smile. “See? Perfect woman. Honestly, it’s not fair.”

Rio shook her head, but as she moved into the kitchen, she couldn’t quite fight the small smile tugging at her lips.

For the first time in a long time, the morning felt less like the start of a mission and more like the beginning of something she couldn’t name.

Agatha trailed after Rio into the kitchen, still heavy with sleep, still raw from the anxiety yesterday had carved into her bones.

“Can I help cook this time?” she asked, voice softer than usual. She leaned against the counter, watching Rio move with her usual quiet precision. “I feel kinda bad—you’re always cooking for me on top of, you know, saving my life.”

Rio looked up, and for once, Agatha wasn’t hiding behind a smirk or quip. There was no flirting in her tone, no teasing spark in her eyes, just sincerity. Rio realized she wasn’t just asking to help with breakfast. Agatha was reaching for control, trying to reclaim a piece of herself after everything the stalker had stolen.

“We’re making huevos con amarillos with café con leche,” Rio said gently. “How do you like your eggs?”

“Scrambled,” Agatha said immediately, a smile tugging at her lips. “I’ve always hated runny eggs.”

Rio smiled back, not surprised she’d guessed right. “Figures.”

They fell into an easy rhythm, Rio handing Agatha ingredients and giving her small directions while she set up the pans. To their quiet surprise, they moved around each other with comfort and ease, domestic in a way that neither of them had expected.

“You cook a lot of Puerto Rican dishes,” Agatha said, whisking the eggs. “I’m gonna assume you’re Puerto Rican?”

Rio didn’t look up from slicing plantains. “Yes. My mother was Puerto Rican, my dad was American. We lived in Puerto Rico until I was twelve. After my mom passed, we moved to the States. I still go back to visit.”

Agatha glanced up at that but didn’t press. She could tell Rio wasn’t looking for pity. So she did what she always did when the air got heavy: she flirted.

“So-” Agatha smirked, tilting her head. “Does that mean you speak Spanish?”

Rio’s lips curved. “Sí, entre otros idiomas. ¿Por qué, te prende?”

Agatha’s breath caught. She didn’t know what Rio had just said, but her body sure as hell reacted. Her mind scrambled for a response, but Rio cut her off casually:

“The eggs are going to burn.”

Agatha cursed under her breath, whipping her eyes back to the pan. “You’re evil.”

Rio only smirked, finishing the plantains and pouring out two mugs of café con leche. They carried everything back to the couch.

Agatha took one sip of the coffee and nearly moaned. “Oh my god. I think I just ascended. You know you’re going to have to make this for me all the time now, right?”

Rio just shook her head, smiling fondly.

Agatha caught herself staring at her then—really staring. For the first time, it felt like Rio had finally set her armor down. She looked calm. Soft. And it made Agatha’s chest ache with something unfamiliar and warm.

“You’re staring,” Rio said, arching a brow. “Do I have something on my face?” She grabbed a napkin and wiped her mouth.

Agatha shook her head, smiling softly. Normally, she’d deflect with some filthy quip. But this time, she wanted to sit in the moment. Just the two of them, no walls, no masks.

Rio studied her a beat longer, trying to read what had shifted, but couldn’t pin it down.

They ate mostly in silence, trading the occasional jab, but the quiet wasn’t awkward. It was steady. Comfortable.

Finally, Agatha leaned back, swirling her coffee with a grin. “We should play twenty questions.”

Rio gave her a wary look. “…That sounds dangerous.”

“That’s the point, darling,” Agatha smirked. “You keep your walls up so high, I need a crowbar to pry anything out of you. Rules of the game. You gotta answer.”

“This feels like a trap,” Rio said skeptically

“Of course, it's a trap, but it's a fun one. And because you keep dodging all my advances, this is the only way I will ever learn anything about you.” Agatha said excited

Rio just sighs and leans back against the arm of the couch facing Agatha, resigned to her fate. “Fine.”

Agatha clapped like a kid on Christmas and tucked her feet underneath herself on the couch, eyes sparkling. “First question. Favorite color?”

“Green,” Rio answered quickly.

“Mine is purple. Your turn.”

“Favorite animal?” Rio asked, still keeping things light.

Agatha’s grin softened into thought. “A rabbit. They’re always portrayed as sweet, timid, and fragile, but in reality, they’re survivors. They’re cunning.”

Rio blinked, not expecting such a layered answer. She studied Agatha with new appreciation. “That makes sense.”

“What about you?” Agatha prompted, leaning forward eagerly.

Rio hesitated, then let the words flow. “That’s harder for me. I’ve always felt tied to different animals at different times. Spiders—because they’re misunderstood, but they build and rebuild with quiet strength. Wolves—protectors of the pack, disciplined, loyal. And snakes… snakes have always spoken to me. Maybe it’s my Puerto Rican roots, maybe it’s how they shed their skin. I feel like I’ve lived a lot of lives myself.”

Agatha listened intently, hanging on every word. Her lips curved. “You know, those fit you perfectly.”

Before the silence could deepen, she pivoted with a mischievous grin. “Guilty pleasure?”

Rio smirked. “Trashy action movies. And food? Korean corn dogs.”

Agatha cocked her head. “What the hell is a Korean corn dog?”

Rio’s eyes lit up, a rare spark of excitement. “Hot dog dipped in batter, rolled in sugar, covered in fries or Hot Cheetos. I prefer the Cheetos. Had them on a deployment once. I swear I died and came back. I will have to make it for you one day.”

Agatha found herself smiling, warmth blooming in her chest at the thought of Rio cooking for her again. “So you’re a foodie.”

“Shut up,” Rio muttered, smirking. “My turn. What’s something you’re most proud of?”

Agatha’s posture straightened. “My career. I know that sounds conceited, but it’s true. I fought tooth and nail to be here. Directors, producers, even other actors told me I’d never make it. When my bitch of a mother outed me, I thought it was over. But instead, the country rallied around me. Somehow, against all odds, I made it. And I’m proud of that.”

Rio’s lips softened into a rare, proud smile, but before she could comment, Agatha fired off: “First celebrity crush. Mine was Angelina Jolie. God, that woman is fine.”

Rio stiffened. Her face burned. She stayed quiet too long, and Agatha noticed.

“What? Is it embarrassing? Oh god—was it a man?” she teased.

Rio muttered something under her breath.

Rio blurted, face red hot, “It was you!”

Agatha froze, stunned into silence, then burst into uncontrollable laughter. “Darling… your celebrity crush has been trying to fuck you for weeks, and you keep turning her down!”

Rio groaned, rubbing her face. “Next question.”

“Coward,” Agatha teased, but she let it go.

“First love?” Rio asked quickly, desperate to change the subject.

Agatha’s laughter died in her throat. The light in her eyes dimmed. She almost deflected, but Rio caught the shift in her body language immediately. She slid closer, resting a hand on Agatha’s knee, steady and grounding.

“You don’t have to answer,” Rio offered gently. “We can skip it.”

Agatha drew a slow breath and shook her head. “No. It’s fine.”

I was going to propose on our third anniversary.” She swallowed hard. “But I came home early from a job,  and found her in bed with a director. She laughed in my face. Told me she’d never loved me. That she’d used me to climb her way up.”

Her jaw trembled, but she forced a crooked smile. “After that, I never settled. I just moved from bed to bed. Easier to stay untouchable than risk that kind of humiliation again.”

Rio’s stomach turned, rage flickering hot and fast. It took every ounce of control not to ask for a name. Instead, she tightened her grip on Agatha’s knee, steady and fierce. No wonder she keeps everyone at arm’s length.

Agatha blinked quickly, brushing away the sting in her eyes. “Your turn.” Agatha tried to joke.

Years later, I was recruited into Delta Force. That’s where I met her. My rival at first, then my partner. It was Bucky, actually, who pointed out we were bickering because we liked each other.”

Her voice softened, breaking at the edges. “We fell in love. Quietly, because of ‘Don’t Ask, Don’t Tell.’ We served side by side in some of the worst places on earth. But we had each other, and that made it bearable. She was… everything.”

Rio’s throat closed. She forced herself to continue. “On my last mission, the ambush—the one that ended my career—she saw it coming before I did. She threw herself over me when the mortar hit. She took the full force. I was severely injured, but I lived because she gave her life for me.”

Her voice cracked, tears threatening. “The last thing I saw in her eyes wasn’t fear. It was love. Relief that I was alive. She’s one of the main reasons I built SHIELD.”

For once, there was no smirk, no quip. Just two women, sitting in the quiet aftermath of honesty, their walls stripped bare.

Agatha whispered, “You deserved better. We both did.”

Rio’s lips parted, a shaky breath slipping free. “So are you.”

And then Rio’s phone, lying on the coffee table, began to buzz loudly.

“Someone better be dying,” Agatha muttered.

Rio answered. “What?”

Jen’s voice came through, tight with urgency. “The shooting’s leaked. It’s all over the press already. Paparazzi, blogs, even mainstream outlets, they’ve got the story that someone fired on Natasha during your photoshoot yesterday. They don’t have all the details yet, but they know it’s connected to Agatha.”

Rio’s jaw clenched. “How bad?”

“Bad,” Jen confirmed. “#PrayForAgatha is already trending. Some outlets are speculating about a stalker given she's hired you guys recently, others think it was a random attack. Either way, the story’s out. And it’s spreading fast.”

Rio closed her eyes, pinching the bridge of her nose. “Keep me updated. Do not comment to anyone. We’ll handle it.” She hung up, exhaling slowly before turning to Agatha.

Agatha raised a brow, masking the worry flickering in her eyes with a crooked grin. “Well. So much for our cozy little bubble.”

Rio glanced at her, still tense, still processing. But she caught the softness in Agatha’s expression, the worry she wasn’t hiding fast enough.

And suddenly, Rio realized—whatever this pull was with Agatha could wait. Protecting Agatha couldn’t.

Agatha shut the phone off with a sigh and turned to Rio. Her expression softened, just for her. “Well. There goes our quiet morning.”

Rio met her gaze, torn between irritation at the mess and something gentler that flickered despite herself.

And just like the night before, Agatha couldn’t help but think: even if the world was chaos, sitting across from Rio like this felt like the only thing grounding her.

Agatha curled her legs under her and sipped the last of her café con leche. The sweetness lingered on her tongue, warmth blooming in her chest.

Her eyes drifted to Rio, always alert, always scanning, even in her own home. Always ready to run straight into the fire.

Agatha’s lips curved into a quiet smile. “You’ll let me kiss you one of these days.”

Rio looked up sharply, startled. For once, she didn’t have a comeback.

And Agatha knew then: she was right.

Breaking Down Walls

Chapter Summary

Photoshoot Reactions: Agatha and Rio get much closer. Agatha and the Security team finally bond, and shenanigans/banter ensue.

Chapter Notes

For the next hour, both women were glued to their phones, Agatha fielding calls from Jen and Lilia, Rio coordinating with her team, Alice, and legal contacts. It wasn’t until Agatha shifted on the couch and caught a whiff of herself that she realized she hadn’t showered since yesterday morning.

Use whatever’s there, and I’ll grab you some clothes that’ll fit.”

Agatha collapsed against the bathroom counter, laughing so hard her stomach cramped. Tears pricked at her eyes as she gasped for air, the image of Rio’s wide-eyed panic and muttered apology to a door burned into her memory forever.

Even as she stepped into the steaming shower, Agatha kept chuckling to herself. For once, she hadn’t even been trying to fluster her stoic bodyguard, yet somehow, she’d managed to unravel Rio Vidal completely.

And oh, she was never going to let her live it down.

Rio stormed down the stairs like a woman fleeing a battlefield, muttering curses under her breath. Her toe throbbed, her pride was in shambles, and she was fairly certain she had just apologized to a door.

She needed an outlet.

Without thinking, she headed straight for the small home gym tucked off the main living space. Within seconds, she was in her sports bra and slacks, slamming fists into the heavy bag like it had personally ruined her life.

Stupid. Stupid. You looked right at her. You said she had— she punched harder —nice tits. Out loud. To her face. While she was naked. In her bathroom. While you were supposed to be professional.

Rio clenched her fists tighter. Working out wasn’t helping. If anything, every drop of sweat just reminded her of how much Agatha got under her skin.

Meanwhile, Agatha stood under the spray of the shower, hot water cascading down her shoulders. She closed her eyes and let herself breathe for the first time all day.

It should have been a moment of quiet, but her mind spun with thoughts of Rio.

Not just how Rio had looked, flushed and flustered, tripping over herself in the most endearingly uncharacteristic way, but what it meant. Ever since the two met, Agatha had been pushing, teasing, throwing every innuendo she had at Rio. And finally, finally, she’d cracked.

But it wasn’t just that.

Agatha pressed her palms to the tile, chest tightening. She’d watched Rio carry her burdens like armor, putting everyone else before herself. And yet when Rio had shared about her first love, the grief still raw in her voice, Agatha had felt something stir inside her that went deeper than desire.

Something dangerous. Something she hadn’t let herself feel in years.

She exhaled shakily. “You’re in trouble, Harkness.”

Freshly showered, Agatha rifled through the clothes Rio had left. A pair of black joggers hung low on her hips, just a touch too big, and she paired them with one of Rio’s button-ups, rolling the sleeves to her elbows. The fabric smelled faintly of cedar and vanilla—her.

Agatha smirked at her reflection. “Perfect.”

When she came downstairs, she followed the rhythmic sound of fists hitting leather. She leaned against the doorway of the gym, arms folded, watching Rio punish the heavy bag like it had personally offended her.

“Well, well,” Agatha purred. “Is this how you cope after seeing me naked? Beating the poor punching bag half to death?”

Rio’s fists stilled instantly. She turned, breathless, strands of hair sticking to her damp forehead. And then she saw Agatha, lounging casually in her clothes, the shirt hanging loose in all the wrong ways, collarbones peeking out, lips curled in a teasing grin.

Rio’s brain short-circuited all over again.

“Why,” Rio asked flatly, “are you wearing my clothes?” 

Agatha pushed off the doorframe and sauntered closer. “Because, darling, you gave them to me. And because”—she tugged lightly at the hem of the shirt, smirking, “they smell like you. Vanilla and something earthy. Very comforting.”

Rio swallowed hard, muscles tense from more than just her workout. “You’re impossible.”

“And you,” Agatha countered, stepping into her space, eyes dancing, “are very, very easy to fluster. Which, I have to admit, I enjoy more than I probably should.”

Rio forced herself to look away, grabbing her water bottle like it was a lifeline. “You should eat something. You’ve had a long day.”

Agatha chuckled, circling her like a cat that had finally cornered its prey. “Always so professional. Always so serious.” She leaned in close enough that Rio could feel her breath on her neck. “But I know what I saw. And I know what you said.”

Rio shut her eyes, pulse hammering. “Agatha…”

Agatha pulled back with a victorious grin, her laugh low and husky. “Don’t worry, darling. Your secret’s safe with me.”

She winked, turning on her heel and heading for the kitchen, leaving Rio rooted in place, fists still clenched, heart pounding like she’d just run into gunfire.

And Agatha, for all her teasing, couldn’t stop smiling. She finally had proof that beneath all that armor, Rio Vidal was just as undone by her as she was by Rio.

Dinner was quiet, the kind of quiet that felt earned after the week they’d had. Neither of them wanted to cook, so Rio had tossed a Stouffer’s mac and cheese into the oven. They ate it straight from mismatched bowls, sitting shoulder to shoulder on the couch with Below Deck flickering on the screen.

Rio would never admit it, not even under interrogation, but she’d started to enjoy the chaos of the yacht crew almost as much as Agatha did. Agatha knew though with every time Rio smirked at a sarcastic comment or muttered “idiots” under her breath, it gave her away.

They didn’t talk about what happened earlier. Rio avoided it, and Agatha, smug as a cat, let her. The knowing smirks, the little chuckles under her breath—it was enough of a reminder.

Halfway through the episode, Rio finally broke the silence. “Tomorrow I’ll take you back to your house. But I’ll need to return to S.H.I.E.L.D. headquarters for a few hours—paperwork, signatures, some diplomatic nonsense with another client. Bucky will take point until I’m back.”

Agatha hummed in acknowledgment, chewing slowly. She wouldn’t admit it, but she would miss Rio’s constant presence. Still, a few hours with the rest of her bodyguards could be… entertaining.

“Jen said they’re releasing the digital copy of the photoshoot tomorrow,” Agatha said suddenly. “They were going to wait until next week, but she thinks it’ll help take attention off the stalker.”

Rio stiffened almost imperceptibly. She hadn’t seen the pictures yet, and the thought of herself splashed across the internet beside Agatha made her stomach twist. She wasn’t a model. What if she looked awkward? What if she dragged Agatha’s image down? The fans adored Agatha—she didn’t want to be the weak link in her orbit.

Agatha caught it instantly. She slid her hand onto Rio’s knee, warm and grounding. “Hey. They’ll love it. I know my fans—they’ll be drooling. Hell, half of them are already thirsting over you, and that’s just from blurry paparazzi shots.”

Rio shook her head, unconvinced.

“I mean it,” Agatha pressed, voice softer. “You’re gorgeous. And people already love you. You’ve got nothing to worry about.”

Rio’s gaze lifted, locking onto Agatha’s. Something unspoken passed between them. Then, softly, reverently, Rio whispered:

“Eres la mujer más hermosa del mundo.”

Agatha’s breath caught. She didn’t know exactly what Rio had said, but the way she said it, like it was sacred, like it hurt to even say aloud told her everything.

Before Agatha could ask, Rio pushed back from the couch. “I need a shower. It’s late. Good night, Agatha.” Her voice was gentle, but final. She cast one last lingering glance over her shoulder before disappearing up the stairs, her door shutting with a quiet click.

Agatha exhaled, her chest tight, and gathered their empty plates. She rinsed them in the sink, washed and dried them, partly to be polite, partly to keep herself busy.

Then, with the dishes done, curiosity got the better of her.

She wandered the hall, her fingers trailing over the picture frames lining the walls. A young Rio smiled back at her in one photo, nestled between two adults who must have been her parents. The gap between her teeth made Agatha’s lips curl, adorable, she thought, against all her better instincts.

In another, Rio as a teenager stood proudly with her father at her high school graduation. Her father’s expression was pure, unfiltered pride.

But it was the next picture that stopped Agatha cold.

Rio in full Delta fatigues, rifle slung across her body. Her old team crowded around her, some goofing off, others solemn. But Agatha’s eyes found only one person: a tall brunette with dimples, smiling like she’d just won the world. Her eyes were locked on Rio—only on Rio—with such raw devotion it made Agatha’s chest ache.

The woman Rio had spoken about. The one who had died to save her.

Agatha’s fingers hovered just above the glass. She could almost feel the warmth of the woman’s joy radiating through the photo. A pang of something sharp and jealous twisted low in her gut, followed quickly by guilt. That woman had given everything for Rio. Agatha had no right to feel envious of a ghost.

Still, she couldn’t look away. Not from the way Rio had smiled in that photo, not from the way love seemed to shine between them so clearly it could burn.

Agatha swallowed hard and stepped back, forcing herself down the hall. She didn’t know what unsettled her more, the photo, or the realization that for the first time in years, she wanted to be the one someone looked at that way.

And God help her, she wanted that someone to be Rio Vidal.

 

 

Agatha woke to the smell of coffee and the faint hum of movement downstairs. For one hazy second, she thought she was at home—until she rolled over and saw the earthy green comforter of Rio’s guest bed.

Her lips curved. Right. Rio’s clothes. Rio’s shower. Rio’s very memorable meltdown.

She stretched, tugged on the joggers and shirt Rio had given her, and padded downstairs.

Rio was already dressed in a crisp suit, hair pulled back, moving around the kitchen with military precision. Her face was composed, unreadable—the armor back in place.

“Morning,” Agatha said brightly, leaning against the counter. “No dramatic apologies to inanimate objects today?”

Rio froze mid-pour of the coffee and shot her a look. “You’re never going to let that go, are you?”

“Not in this lifetime,” Agatha smirked, taking the mug Rio slid across to her. “But don’t worry. It was adorable.”

Rio muttered something in Spanish that Agatha pretended not to hear, sipping her coffee with a satisfied little smile. The silence that followed was comfortable, though Agatha couldn’t stop glancing at her—at the set jaw, at the subtle shadows under her eyes. She thought about the photo in the hallway, about the way Rio had once been looked at with so much love.

For the first time in a long time, Agatha wanted to be seen the same way.

Rio cleared her throat, jolting her back. “Eat something before we go. It’ll be a long day.”

Agatha smirked, masking the pang in her chest. “Bossy. I like it.”

By late morning, Rio pulled the SUV up the discreet back entrance of Agatha’s property. The front was swarmed with paparazzi and fans, cameras flashing like a wall of lightning, but Bucky and Alice had cleared a quiet way in.

“Stay close,” Rio murmured, one hand hovering near her weapon as she opened Agatha’s door.

Inside, Clint was stationed at the gate monitors while Natasha scanned the perimeter. Yelena leaned against the kitchen island, flipping a knife idly between her fingers.

“Clear,” Bucky reported, shutting the door behind them.

Rio guided Agatha toward the living room. “Status.”

Alice straightened, tablet in hand. “We’ve traced the leak to the tech who broke his NDA. Legal’s on it. Press speculation is still running with the ‘carjacking’ cover story. Nothing stronger has surfaced—yet.”

“Good,” Rio said, though her tone was clipped. “Keep the team tight today. No one leaves their post. Agatha’s not to step outside without clearance.”

Agatha bristled a little at the phrasing—like she was a mission instead of a person, but she held her tongue.

Natasha glanced up. “You still heading to HQ?”

Rio nodded. “Paperwork. Shouldn’t be more than a few hours. Bucky will take point.” She turned to Agatha, her gaze steady but softer now. “You’ll be safe.”

Agatha tilted her chin, feigning nonchalance. “Safe, yes. Bored, probably.”

Yelena snorted. “Don’t worry, I’ll keep you entertained.”

“God help me,” Rio muttered under her breath, which made Agatha laugh outright.

But when their eyes met again, something unspoken lingered there. Agatha knew it wasn’t just about safety, or paperwork, or even the stalker.

For all of Rio’s armor, leaving her, even for a few hours wasn’t easy.

And for Agatha, watching her go felt far heavier than it should have.

 

 

Jen and Lilia arrived not long after, the older woman’s expression softening with maternal concern the second she laid eyes on Agatha.

Agatha’s chest tightened at the sight. She could still remember the very first time they met—an afterparty when she was only fourteen, cornered by a drunk executive whose comments had turned lewd and invasive. She had frozen, too scared to move. Then Lilia appeared like a storm, sweeping Agatha away and staying glued to her side the rest of the night. By morning, Lilia had drawn up legal documents that severed Agatha’s mother as her agent, replacing her herself.

Agatha had never asked what strings Lilia pulled, what threats or bargains she made, but she’d been grateful every day since. In the years that followed, Lilia had been more mother to her than her own blood ever was.

“How are you holding up, dear?” Lilia asked gently, her hand brushing Agatha’s arm.

“I’m fine,” Agatha said honestly, though a small smile tugged at her lips. “Rio helped a lot last night to take my mind off everything.”

“I bet she did,” Yelena quipped from across the room, smirking like a cat.

Agatha didn’t miss a beat—she grabbed the nearest throw pillow and launched it at her. Yelena caught it one-handed without even glancing up, laughing smugly.

Lilia chuckled too, shaking her head with the fond exasperation of someone who had long accepted Agatha’s brand of chaos.

Jen, scrolling rapidly on her phone, suddenly lit up. “The photoshoot just went live. It’s already blowing up—#Agathario is trending, and you two are being shipped like crazy. Fans are thirsting over both of you, losing their collective minds.”

Bucky blinked, looking between them. “What pictures? Why are people shipping you two?”

Agatha’s smirk turned downright wicked. “Oh, right. You guys missed that part. The model they booked for me called out last minute. No time to find a replacement. So I convinced Rio to step in.”

Yelena practically cackled. “No way. No way. Show me.”

She whipped out her phone and pulled up the shots. Within seconds, Natasha and Bucky were peering over her shoulder. Their reactions were immediate and unanimous—their eyebrows shot up like rockets.

Even through the screen, the chemistry was unmistakable. The tension in the photos wasn’t posed; it was real. The way Rio and Agatha leaned into each other, eyes locked, hovering on the edge of fight or kiss—it radiated heat.

Natasha let out a long, low whistle. “Damn. These photos are hot. And it looks like your fans agree.”

“Oh yeah, they’re drooling—and honestly, same,” Alice chimed in from the corner. She had pulled up the photoshoot on her laptop, scrolling through the flood of fan reactions while cackling.

“This is exactly what we needed,” Jen added with a satisfied grin. “The attention is off the stalker, and the buzz for your next film just shot through the roof. Press is calling this one of the best promo shoots of your career.”

The group kept scrolling, trading comments back and forth, laughing at the unhinged thirst of Agatha’s coven. The memes were already spiraling out of control. Agatha joined in with the laughter, but her mind kept drifting. She couldn’t help but wonder what Rio was doing right now, probably being bombarded with the same notifications, maybe even being mercilessly teased by Maria. The thought made her smirk.

After a while, the noise of it all grew heavy. Agatha excused herself and slipped upstairs to change. If she was stuck here, she might as well take advantage of the pool and the California sun.

She chose a purple bikini that hugged her curves, tossed her sunglasses on top of her head, and carried a towel outside. The air was warm, the sky a cloudless blue. She set her towel down on the pool chair before sliding into the water with a smooth grace.

The cool embrace of the pool melted away her tension instantly. Agatha tilted her face to the sun and let herself drift onto her back, floating lazily, the world beyond the water’s surface muffled and distant.

From the corner of her eye, she could see Bucky posted by the back door, eyes sharp, ever-watchful. Natasha was pacing the fence line further off, scanning for paparazzi or overeager fans trying to sneak a peek. Yelena’s voice carried faintly now and then, checking in over comms as she patrolled the outer perimeter. Alice had claimed the front gate, her posture deceptively casual, but her focus razor-sharp. Clint, on his well-earned break, is fast asleep.

Protected on all sides, Agatha felt safe enough to close her eyes.

And her thoughts, like they always seemed to slid right back to Rio.

The way she moved with that soldier’s discipline yet somehow softened around the edges when she thought no one was looking. The accidental slips, the blushes, the way her walls had cracked in little flashes, confessions shared over coffee, laughter that slipped past her guard, panic when caught staring.

Agatha floated, the water rocking her gently, and smiled to herself. For years, she’d kept her heart locked down, throwing herself into flings and distractions to avoid the ache of real connection. But Rio… Rio made her want to test those locks again.

Dangerous. Terrifying.

And maybe exactly what she needed.

Agatha floated lazily on her back, sunglasses shielding her eyes, though she kept sneaking glances toward the back door where Bucky stood on duty. He looked impossibly still, arms folded, gaze scanning the yard like a hawk.

Finally, she broke the silence. “You know, for someone with the nickname Winter Soldier, you’d think you’d be more chatty in the sun.”

Bucky’s lip twitched, the closest thing to a smile she’d seen from him since breakfast. “I’m paid to watch, not talk.”

“Mm. But you’ve known Rio a long time, haven’t you?” Agatha asked casually, drifting toward the pool’s edge. She propped her elbows on the side and tilted her head at him. “Teammates. Friends. Whatever Delta Force bonding looks like.”

Bucky didn’t move, but his blue eyes flicked toward her. “Yeah. Long enough.”

Agatha smirked, sensing the opening. “Then tell me, what’s her deal? She doesn’t talk about herself much. Unless it’s work or how she’s going to drag me over her shoulder if I don’t listen.”

That almost earned her a laugh. Almost.

“Rio’s… steady,” Bucky said slowly. “She’s had to be. She doesn’t let people in easily. When she does, it’s because they’ve proven they won’t quit on her.”

Agatha’s smirk softened. “And who did she let in?” But she already knows the answer, she is just trying to find out as much as she can.

This time, the silence stretched long. Agatha thought he might refuse, but finally, Bucky shifted, jaw tightening. “Valkyrie. Same team as us. Hell of a soldier. They were inseparable.”

Agatha stayed quiet, letting him speak.

“She was the first person Rio ever looked at like the rest of the world didn’t exist. And Rio was the same for her.” Bucky’s gaze was fixed far away now, lost in memory. “When the ambush happened… Val didn’t hesitate. Saved Rio’s life by ending her own. That kind of thing—changes you.”

Agatha’s chest tightened. She thought of the photo she’d seen in the hallway—the brunette’s radiant smile, the way her eyes had been locked only on Rio. “She loved her,” Agatha murmured, more to herself than to Bucky.

“Yeah,” Bucky said softly. “And Rio loved her. Still does, in some ways. She doesn’t talk about it much, but you can see it if you know what to look for.” He turned his head, studying Agatha now. “Why are you asking?”

Agatha pushed her sunglasses up, meeting his gaze head-on. “Because… I want to understand her. And maybe—” she paused, biting back the vulnerability that threatened to spill out. “Maybe I want to know if she’s capable of letting someone in again.”

Bucky’s expression didn’t change, but his tone was gentler when he finally answered. “She is. But she won’t make it easy. And if you’re playing games with her, Agatha… don’t. She deserves better than that.”

Agatha let out a short laugh, though it lacked its usual sharpness. “You think I don’t know that?”

Bucky gave her a long, unreadable look, then turned back toward the fence line, scanning the horizon once more. “Then prove it.”

Agatha sank lower into the water, her smirk fading into something quieter, more contemplative. For once, she didn’t have a comeback.

Agatha nearly collided with Rio the moment she stepped back inside, towel still slung low around her hips, droplets of pool water trailing down her skin. Rio’s hands shot out instinctively, steadying her—one on each hip.

“We really have to stop meeting like this,” Agatha smirked, delighting in the contact.

Rio realized where her hands were and stepped back so fast she nearly tripped over her own boots. She cleared her throat, trying for professionalism, though the faint pink in her cheeks betrayed her. “How has today been?”

“Relaxing.” Agatha’s grin widened. “Did you see the fan reactions to our photoshoot?”

Rio’s ears turned scarlet. She rocked on her heels, gaze fixed firmly anywhere but Agatha’s face.

“I’ll take that as a yes,” Agatha laughed, brushing past her.

“Your fans are… very impassioned,” Rio admitted at last, though the corner of her mouth betrayed a reluctant smile.

Agatha leaned in as she passed, her arms grazing lightly down Rio’s as if it were the most natural thing in the world. “Darling, that’s the polite way of saying they’d sell their souls to see you bend me over a chair.”

Rio nearly choked on air. Agatha just chuckled, sauntering toward the stairs.

“I was thinking,” she said, pausing at the bottom step and glancing back over her shoulder. “Tonight, everyone should compete in a bowling championship. I’ve got a bowling alley that doesn’t get enough love. Team bonding, you know? If my life is in your hands, I should know you all better.”

Rio’s brows arched. “You realize that could end in physical brawls? This group doesn’t exactly… handle losing well.”

Agatha’s grin turned wicked. “Well, now it’s a must. Gather everyone in the alley. You’ve got alarms set, and with all of you in one room, I’ll be safe. So don’t start worrying.”

She ascended the stairs, hips swaying just enough to make Rio’s jaw tighten.

Rio stood there for a long moment, pinching the bridge of her nose and muttering something in Spanish that sounded a lot like a prayer.

Tonight was going to be chaos.

And somehow, she knew Agatha wouldn’t have it any other way.

The private bowling alley gleamed under dimmed lights, neon strips glowing down each lane. Agatha was already perched on one of the couches, purple lounge set hugging her frame, a glass of wine in hand. She looked far too entertained for someone who claimed this was “team bonding.” She and Jen have decided to sit out the competition, saying they just want to drink and enjoy the scenery.

“All right,” Rio said, clapping her hands once with a soldier’s command presence. “We’ll split into teams. Winner gets bragging rights. Loser—” her eyes swept over Yelena, who was already twirling a ball like she meant to weaponize it—“does dishes duty for a week.”

“That’s cruel and unusual punishment,” Clint muttered, tying his shoes.

“Don’t lose, then,” Natasha shot back.

Bucky smirked, already chalking his hands like he was prepping for a mission. “Oh, I don’t lose.”

Rio’s jaw ticked. “We’ll see about that.”

Agatha raised her glass in salute. “God, this is better than TV already.”

Teams

  • Team 1: Rio, Natasha, Clint

  • Team 2: Bucky, Yelena, Alice

Yelena fist-pumped. “We’ve got this in the bag. Barnes, you better not bowl like an old man.”

“Kid, I was putting bullets through moving targets before you were out of diapers,” Bucky deadpanned.

“That’s not the same thing!” Yelena laughed, nearly dropping her ball.

Alice, bouncing on her toes, grinned. “I don’t even care if we lose. This is amazing.”

Clint took the first shot for Team 1, lining up with exaggerated precision. “Watch and learn, rookies.”

He released. The ball curved beautifully… then missed every pin except one.

Natasha groaned, massaging her temple. “You’re pathetic.”

“Pathetic? That was a warm-up shot,” Clint protested.

“Uh-huh.” Nat stepped up next, her form clean and sharp, sending the ball down for a flawless strike. She turned back with smug ease. “That’s how it’s done.”

“Show-off,” Clint muttered.

On the other lane, Yelena skipped up with no real strategy, flung the ball, and laughed hysterically when it ricocheted into the gutter. “Oops.”

Alice clapped like she’d just witnessed a miracle. “That was still really fun to watch!”

Bucky stepped forward, muscles taut, eyes narrowed like he was lining up a sniper shot. The ball thundered down the lane, pins exploding everywhere—strike. He didn’t smile, just nodded once, as if to say of course.

Rio’s competitive streak lit up like a fuse. She grabbed her ball, rolled her shoulders, and matched Bucky’s strike with one of her own. When she turned back, their eyes locked.

“Not bad,” Bucky drawled.

“You’ll be eating those words by the end,” Rio shot back.

Agatha leaned toward Jen, who had joined her with popcorn. “If those two don’t arm wrestle by midnight, I’ll eat my towel.”

As the game went on, Natasha and Clint devolved into bickering like siblings at Thanksgiving.

“You’re stepping into my line of sight,” Clint accused.

“You don’t need a line of sight to throw a ball,” Natasha retorted. “Just stop sucking.”

Meanwhile, Yelena had discovered that spinning in a circle before releasing the ball was “more fun,” even if it never hit more than three pins. Alice cheered for her like she’d just won gold at the Olympics.

Rio and Bucky traded strike for strike, tension mounting each round. Both were silent, deadly serious, as if the fate of the world depended on who hit more pins.

Agatha, sipping wine like a queen watching her court, couldn’t resist needling them. “You know, you could just admit you’re in love and get it over with.”

Both Rio and Bucky froze mid-motion, turned slowly toward her, and said in unison: “No.”

Agatha cackled, nearly spilling her drink.

It all came down to the last frame. Tied score. Team 1 with Rio up, Team 2 with Bucky.

The room went silent.

Rio inhaled, exhaled, and sent the ball rocketing down the lane. Strike. Clean, perfect, merciless.

Bucky smirked. “Cute.” He stepped up, rolled his own… and struck as well.

The scoreboard flashed: Tie.

Everyone groaned.

“That’s not fair,” Yelena whined. “We can’t both do dishes!”

Agatha stood, clapping her hands together. “Oh, I think this calls for a tiebreaker.” She gestured grandly toward the empty lanes. “Single frame. Rio versus Bucky. Sudden death.”

The two soldiers squared off, fire in their eyes.

Natasha sighed, crossing her arms. “If this ends with broken furniture, I’m not explaining it to Maria.”

Agatha leaned back, savoring every second. “Oh, darling. I wouldn’t dream of stopping them.”

The air in the bowling alley thickened with anticipation. Rio and Bucky squared off, each holding a ball like it was a weapon.

Agatha perched on the back of the couch, wine glass in hand, a smirk plastered across her face. Jen sat beside her, popcorn bowl in her lap, whispering commentary like a sports announcer.

“Ladies, gentlemen, and lesbians of all ages,” Jen said dramatically, “we are about to witness the ultimate showdown: The Brooding Bodyguard Bowl-Off.”

Agatha raised her glass. “Place your bets, people. I’ve got fifty on Rio.”

“Traitor,” Clint muttered, but he didn’t bet against her.

Alice crossed her arms, smirking. “I’ll take Barnes. He has the longer reach.”

“Excuse you,” Agatha drawled, eyes still on Rio. “Rio has discipline. Precision. She’s hotter. It’s not even a competition.”

Rio flushed, shoulders tensing, while Bucky coughed into his fist to hide a laugh.

Rio stepped up first, lining her shot with calm focus. Just as she pulled back, Yelena shouted from behind her: “Don’t choke, boss lady!”

The ball veered slightly right but still managed to take down eight pins. Rio exhaled sharply, muttering in Spanish, and shot Yelena a glare that would have sent lesser mortals fleeing.

Yelena only grinned. “What? Encouragement!”

“Sabotage,” Natasha corrected, though she didn’t sound sorry.

Bucky swaggered up next. Just as he bent to release, Clint shouted, “Bucky! You bowl like a geriatric grandpa!!”

The ball ricocheted off the bumper and hit only four pins.

Bucky turned slowly, death in his eyes. “You’re dead, Barton.”

“Worth it,” Clint wheezed, doubled over in laughter.

“Barnes, honey, try aiming this time,” Agatha called sweetly. “And Rio—oh darling, that little frown line you get when you’re mad? Devastating. Keep it up.”

Jen leaned toward her. “You’re the devil.”

“I know,” Agatha said smugly.

Rio tried to block out the noise, jaw set. She rolled her second ball—strike. Clean, perfect.

“YES!” Agatha cheered, nearly spilling her wine. “That’s my girl!”

Rio’s ears turned pink.

Bucky growled, lined up his own, and threw with so much force the ball cracked against the pins like a gunshot. Strike.

Both tied again. It all came down to this.

Rio inhaled deeply, the room falling into hushed silence. She stepped forward, smooth and steady, and released. The ball thundered down the lane, pins exploding in another strike.

Bucky rolled his shoulders, smirking. “Not bad.” He hefted his ball, ready to match her.

Agatha cupped her hands around her mouth. “Hey, Bucky!”

He glanced back instinctively. “What?”

Agatha grinned wickedly. “Rio bowls hotter than you.”

Bucky snorted, rolled his eyes, and let the ball fly—only to watch it drift just an inch too far left. Nine pins fell. One wobbled… then stayed standing.

The alley erupted.

“AND THE WINNER IS—RIO VIDAL!” Jen bellowed like a ring announcer.

Yelena booed dramatically, stomping her feet. Natasha chuckled, patting Bucky’s shoulder. Alice clapped like she’d just witnessed history. Clint was doubled over in tears.

Agatha leapt from the couch, wine glass raised like a trophy. “Victory is ours!” she declared, grabbing Rio’s arm and holding it aloft like a champion prizefighter.

Rio shook her head, muttering under her breath, but she couldn’t hide the smile tugging at her lips.

Bucky growled halfheartedly. “Rematch. Tomorrow.”

Agatha winked. “Anytime, darling. But for now… the dishes are all yours.”

Bucky groaned, and the team dissolved into laughter.

The bowling alley was still buzzing with leftover laughter as the team drifted out in pairs, their voices echoing faintly down the hall. Bucky and Clint were arguing about rematch conditions. Natasha and Yelena were bickering over who cheated more. Alice trailed after them, humming happily, still replaying the chaos. Jen follows her, trying to strike up a conversation. 

Agatha lingered behind, half-empty glass of wine in her hand, watching Rio methodically shut down the scoring console and switch off the neon strips over the lanes.

“You always clean up after everyone else,” Agatha said softly.

Rio glanced over her shoulder, a faint smile tugging at her lips. “Occupational hazard.”

Agatha set her glass aside and crossed the space between them, barefoot on the glossy wood. “No, it’s more than that. You carry everything, don’t you? Every room you walk into, you take responsibility for it.”

Rio didn’t answer. Her jaw flexed, her eyes dropping to the floor as if she could deflect the weight of Agatha’s words.

Agatha reached out, lightly touching her arm. “Rio, look at me.”

Slowly, reluctantly, Rio did. And Agatha let her mask slip. No smirk, no coy flirtation, no teasing lilt. Just raw truth.

“I know I flirt too much. I know I come off like I don’t take anything seriously. But I do. Especially this. Especially you.” Her voice wavered but didn’t break. “I don’t want just another fling. Not with you. I don’t want a distraction, or a one-night stand, or something I can laugh off in the morning. I want you. Really you. Mess and scars and all. And that scares the hell out of me.”

Rio’s breath caught. For a moment, her carefully constructed walls trembled. She searched Agatha’s face, as if trying to find the joke, the trap, the performance. But there was nothing but honesty staring back at her.

Agatha’s hand slid down Rio’s arm until their fingers brushed. “So why are you holding back?” she whispered. “Because I can feel it, Rio. You want this too. So why?”

Rio closed her eyes, exhaling like she’d been carrying the weight for years. “Because I can’t…” Her voice cracked. “I can’t watch someone I care about die again. Not after Valkyrie. Not after watching her while she bled out because I couldn’t protect her. She was my first love, Agatha, and she died saving me. I live every day with that guilt. And I don’t know if I could survive losing someone else I—” She cut herself off, shaking her head. “Not you. Not like that.”

The words hit Agatha square in the chest. She reached up, cupping Rio’s face, forcing her to meet her eyes. “You don’t get to protect me from everything, Rio. That’s not how life works. But you don’t get to protect me from this, either. I’m right here. I’m choosing you.”

Her thumb brushed gently across Rio’s cheek. “So if you’re going to push me away, do it now. Because I need you to know, I’m not playing this time.”

Rio’s defenses were shattered. Her hand slid to Agatha’s jaw, the other curling around her waist, pulling her in like she’d been holding back for a lifetime.

Their lips crashed together, fierce and hungry, all the tension and longing between them igniting in a single spark.

Agatha melted into her, fingers tangling in Rio’s shirt, pulling her closer. The kiss deepened, Rio tilting her head, every ounce of restraint gone. It wasn’t gentle. It was desperate, consuming, like they’d both been starved and had finally given in.

When they finally broke apart, both breathless, Agatha leaned her forehead against Rio’s, smiling through the tears pricking her eyes. “Took you long enough, hot stuff.”

Rio laughed—quiet, shaky, but real—and pulled her back into another kiss.

 

Chapter End Notes

THEY FINALLY KISSED!!!!! *Cue confetti* It just took a minute, both have pasts that haunt them, and I wanted them to stew in that and understand each other fully first before they actually kissed.

Next Chapter: Interviews, Agatha starts filming, and Stalker makes another move.

Threads in the Dark

Chapter Summary

Stalker makes dangerous moves, Rio and team begin to unravel mystery and put pieces together.

Chapter Notes

Drama incoming, fasten your seatbelts, kids. From here on, the story is going to pick up a little in terms of drama and action.

Enjoy, and I love you all :)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The kiss left them both breathless, lingering in the quiet of the darkened bowling alley. The faint hum of the neon signs still cooling filled the silence, but neither woman moved right away. Rio’s hand stayed on Agatha’s waist, firm but trembling ever so slightly, like she wasn’t sure if she should let go.

Agatha leaned back just far enough to meet her eyes. She smiled softly, the cocky grin she usually wore replaced with something gentler, almost shy. “See? Was that so hard?”

Rio huffed a quiet laugh, shaking her head. “Harder than you think.”

“You don’t have to keep running from me, darling.” Agatha’s thumb brushed along Rio’s jaw. “I’m not going anywhere. Not unless you tell me to.”

Rio swallowed, the weight of her confession still heavy in the air. “I just don’t want to fail you the way I’ve failed before.”

Agatha leaned in, pressing her forehead to Rio’s. “You won’t. And even if something happens because life is chaos. I’d rather take the risk than pretend this doesn’t exist.”

For a long moment, Rio said nothing, just breathed her in, grounding herself in Agatha’s words. Then, finally, she nodded. A silent surrender.

Agatha grinned, stealing another quick kiss—softer this time, playful, lingering just enough to leave Rio dazed. “God, I knew you’d be good at that.”

Rio rolled her eyes, though her lips betrayed the faintest smile. “Of course you’d turn this into flirting again.”

“It’s not flirting,” Agatha corrected, tugging lightly on Rio’s shirt as she stepped back. “It’s truth.”

Rio watched her retreat a few steps toward the door, already missing the warmth pressed against her. Agatha turned, smirk firmly back in place but her eyes still soft, vulnerable in a way Rio wasn’t used to seeing.
