“Goodnight, hot stuff,” she murmured, and with a sway of her hips, she disappeared up the stairs.

Rio exhaled, running a hand down her face, equal parts wrecked and exhilarated. For the first time in years, she wasn’t sure if she was terrified or hopeful.

 

The next morning, the smell of fresh coffee drifted through the kitchen. Natasha was already seated at the table, scrolling through her phone. Clint yawned his way in behind her, and Yelena raided the fridge like she owned it. Alice leaned against the counter, nursing a mug, while Bucky stood by the back door keeping his quiet watch as usual.

Then Agatha came downstairs.

She was glowing, hair loose and tousled, lips just a little too red for someone who “hadn’t been up to anything,” her body moving with a kind of lazy ease no one had ever seen in her before. She greeted them with a cheerful, “Good morning, darlings,” and breezed past to the coffee pot.

A beat later, Rio followed, her usually unshakable composure just slightly… off. She kept her eyes on the floor, muttered a stiff “Morning,” and went straight for the fridge like she needed something to do with her hands.

The shift was immediate.

Natasha’s brow arched. Clint stifled a laugh into his mug. Yelena froze mid-bite of cold pizza and then grinned like a wolf. Alice’s eyes lit up, and even Bucky smirked faintly from his post.

“Oh my god,” Yelena whispered loudly. “It happened.”

“Definitely happened,” Clint agreed, leaning back in his chair with a smug grin.

Natasha didn’t look up from her phone. “Took them long enough.”

Agatha, never one to miss a cue, sipped her coffee and smirked. “You all gossip worse than my fanbase.”

Rio nearly choked on the orange juice she’d just poured. “It’s not— we didn’t—” She trailed off, ears turning crimson.

The team erupted into knowing laughter.

Even Bucky, who almost never commented on anything not mission-critical, tilted his head and rumbled, “About time.”

Agatha winked over her mug, delighting in Rio’s mortification.

Rio set the juice down a little too hard, her jaw tightening as she muttered something in Spanish under her breath. She turned on her heel, clearly ready to escape the room.

That’s when Alice stepped in, cutting her off with a hand on her arm. “Hey. Breathe.”

Rio froze, meeting her best friend’s steady gaze.

“Look, I know this freaks you out,” Alice said gently, voice pitched low so only Rio could hear. “But you’re allowed to be happy, Rio. You’re allowed to let someone in again. No one here thinks less of you. In fact, we’re rooting for you.”

Rio’s throat worked, but she didn’t reply.

Alice squeezed her arm once before letting go. “Don’t sabotage it because you’re scared, okay?”

Rio nodded faintly, unable to form words. Her chest felt tight, but not in the old, suffocating way. In a new way. A way that whispered maybe Alice was right.

Behind them, Yelena stage-whispered, “Can we PLEASE have a wedding on a mission? I want to wear a tux.”

Rio groaned, pinching the bridge of her nose, while Agatha just cackled into her coffee.

The kitchen was still buzzing with laughter when Agatha set her mug down and slipped beside Rio, who was doing her best to look busy slicing fruit she had no real intention of eating.

Agatha leaned in just close enough for her voice to be private. “You’re not overwhelmed, are you? I know people can be a lot when they’ve scented gossip.”

Rio exhaled slowly, her knife pausing mid-cut. “I’m fine,” she said, though her shoulders stayed taut.

Agatha tilted her head, studying her. “You know ‘fine’ is actress code for ‘I’m falling apart inside but my mascara still looks good.’”

That earned the faintest huff of amusement from Rio. “I don’t wear mascara.”

Agatha’s lips curved into a sly smile. “Shame. You’d make it look devastating.”

Rio shook her head, cheeks tinged pink, and tried to return to her task. But Agatha touched her wrist lightly. “Seriously. If this is too much—me, them, all of it—tell me. I’ll rein it in.”

Rio finally met her eyes, and there was no teasing in her voice when she answered. “You don’t need to rein it in. I can handle it.”

“Good,” Agatha said softly, before her grin snapped back into place. “Because I’m not planning on reining it in anytime soon.”

Before Rio could reply, Yelena leaned across the counter, pilfering a strawberry from Rio’s cutting board. “Ugh, are you two done being disgustingly tender? Some of us are trying to carbo-load before work.”

Clint tossed a granola bar at her head. “You don’t even work, you just stir trouble.”

Natasha sipped her coffee, smirking. “And she’s very good at it.”

Alice, who’d been reviewing something on her tablet, clapped her hands. “Okay, focus. Today’s schedule is full. First, Agatha is on the Drew Barrymore show, then it’s Agatha’s first official day of filming. Security checks are already lined up, Bucky’s on vehicle duty, Natasha’s handling access clearance at the gate. Clint, you’re with me on surveillance. Yelena—”

“I’m the fun one,” Yelena interrupted, mouth full of stolen fruit.

“No,” Alice corrected with a patient smile, “you’re inside with Rio, shadowing the set perimeter. Try not to pick fights with anyone.”

“No promises,” Yelena sang.

Agatha chuckled, stretching languidly in her chair. “See? Family breakfast and my own personal army. Who needs Hollywood when I’ve got this circus?”

“Hollywood pays the bills,” Natasha reminded her dryly.

“Ah, right.” Agatha winked at Rio. “Then let’s go make some magic.”

Rio rolled her eyes, but when Agatha brushed against her on the way out, she found herself smiling despite the chaos.

Before they left for the studio, Agatha tugged Rio into a quiet corner of the house, away from the bustle of the team checking gear and running last-minute sweeps. She folded her arms, eyes soft but serious.

“During this interview, Drew is going to bring up the photoshoot, and probably the fan speculation about us,” Agatha said. “Do we just keep this quiet between us? How much do you want me to disclose?”

Her tone was steady, but Rio could see the flicker of vulnerability there. Agatha had been in the spotlight long enough to know how invasive these questions could get, even from friends.

Rio was quiet for several beats, her jaw working before she finally spoke. “I want to keep this quiet for as long as we can. I’m not ashamed of you, and we’re not doing anything wrong, but I want to keep this as professional as possible in public.” She held Agatha’s gaze, dark eyes steady, trying to communicate everything she couldn’t quite put into words—the need to protect, the fear of losing, the line she wasn’t sure how to walk.

Agatha’s expression softened. She reached out, resting her hand lightly against Rio’s chest. “Absolutely, darling. We’ll go at your pace when it comes to the public. I’ve had years to get used to this circus, you haven’t.”

Rio exhaled a breath she hadn’t realized she was holding, and Agatha tilted her chin up, closing the space between them. The kiss was tender, unhurried, fireworks in the simplest brush of lips, the kind that left both of them aching for more.

When they finally pulled apart, Agatha’s smirk returned, softer this time. “Alright, then. Let’s go give the world a show without actually giving them the show.”

Rio managed the faintest smile at that, then followed her back into the main hall where the team was already gathering, gear checked and ready. Within minutes, they were loading into the SUVs, headed for their first stop: Drew Barrymore’s stage.

 

The set of The Drew Barrymore Show gleamed under bright studio lights, the audience buzzing as Drew swept onto the stage with her signature warmth.

“Okay, everyone, today is very exciting because we have with us one of my oldest and dearest friends, an actress I’ve known since we were both awkward teenagers trying to figure out which camera to look at first.” Drew beamed toward the wings. “Please welcome America’s witchiest sweetheart… Agatha Harkness!”

The audience erupted in cheers as Agatha strutted onto the stage, purple silk blouse catching the light. She and Drew embraced tightly, laughing into each other’s shoulders like old friends who’d shared a hundred inside jokes.

“Can you believe this?” Drew said as they sat down, shaking her head fondly. “We did our first movie together when we were fifteen, and now you’re, like, the face of half the internet memes.”

Agatha smirked. “Not just memes, darling. I’m also the face of questionable tattoos and at least three thirst accounts on Twitter.”

The audience roared. Drew giggled so hard she almost snorted. “Oh my God, you haven’t changed a bit.”

Backstage, behind the camera, Rio stood with arms folded, her usual neutral expression firmly in place. But her eyes never left Agatha—not once.

Drew leaned forward eagerly. “So, let’s get into it. Marvel fans are freaking out about Coven of Chaos. This is your first Marvel Movie, joining Wanda in the MCU, what can you tell us?”

“Well, you know I can’t say much,” Agatha teased, twirling a strand of hair. “Kevin Feige has snipers, and I happen to like my life. But I can tell you that the show dives deeper into witch lore within the MCU, and let’s just say… my character is here to cause trouble.”

The audience whooped, and Drew fanned herself dramatically. “You are so good at playing bad. And speaking of Wanda—you two have this incredible on-screen friendship, and fans swear there’s something more there.”

Agatha leaned back, smirking at the audience’s knowing laughter. “Wanda is one of my best friends in the world. We’ve shared sets, trailers, and a frankly unhealthy number of margaritas. But sorry to break hearts, we’re platonic. Sister-wives energy at best.”

The audience groaned playfully, and Drew wagged her finger. “You’re sure? Because some of those interviews…”

Agatha grinned. “What can I say? We have chemistry. Blame Wanda, she’s irresistible.”

The crowd clapped, clearly eating it up. Agatha glanced toward the wings, catching Rio’s stoic figure, and gave a sly little wink. Rio shifted on her feet, her jaw tightening just a fraction.

Drew’s eyes twinkled as she shifted gears. “Okay, so I have to bring this up because my producers would kill me if I didn’t. That photoshoot.”

The audience screamed before Drew even finished the sentence.

Agatha laughed, covering her face. “Oh, God, I knew this was coming.”

“You and your new security, Rio Vidal.” Drew leaned in conspiratorially. “First of all, that photoshoot was… whew. I needed a fan. And second—who is this woman? Because the internet is convinced you two are the new Brangelina.”

Agatha dropped her hands and smirked directly at the camera. “Rio is my bodyguard. She’s professional, terrifyingly competent, and if you believe my fans, singlehandedly responsible for about sixty percent of the sapphic internet losing their minds. I would be jealous of her claiming my throne, but I, too, am one of the sapphics losing my mind. ”

The audience howled.

“Actually,” Drew said, picking up a card, “I have some examples. Do you want to hear a few thirst tweets?”

Agatha clapped her hands. “Oh, please, let’s traumatize my poor security detail.”

Rio’s eyes narrowed from the sidelines, but Drew began reading with glee.

“@AgathasCoven: Agatha’s new bodyguard has tattoos for days, and I just know she could ruin me in every possible way.”

The audience shrieked. Agatha gasped dramatically, fanning herself. “They’re not wrong, darling.”

“@Witchy4Rio: Who do I talk to about getting Rio Vidal to step on me while reciting her kill count in Spanish?”

Agatha threw her head back laughing. “Oh, that’s a good one. I may have to steal that line.” She turned and gestured toward Rio offstage. “Did you hear that, dear? You’ve got groupies now.”

Rio gave her the blankest look imaginable, but the faintest flush rose up her neck.

Drew, still grinning, shuffled her cards. “And don’t worry, Agatha, I didn’t forget you. Because the fans have plenty to say about you, too.”

“Of course they do,” Agatha smirked, crossing her legs with mock vanity.

“@HexedandBlessed: Agatha in that black suit? I saw the photos and immediately forgot how to breathe.”

The audience cackled. Agatha smirked wickedly, mouthing you’re welcome to the camera.

“@DarklingDreamer: If loving Agatha Harkness in leather pants is wrong, then lock me up and throw away the key.”

“Darling, that’s the best confession I’ve ever heard,” Agatha purred.

“And finally—” Drew could barely get it out through her giggles, “@WitchPlease: Agatha’s smirk in that shoot made me gay again. Yes, again.”

The audience was in stitches, clapping and cheering. Agatha preened, tossing her hair. “What can I say? I’m a public service.”

Drew couldn’t stop giggling. “The internet is unhinged, and I love it.”

“But seriously,” Agatha added once the laughter died down, “Rio and her team are here to keep me safe. That’s their priority. The rest is just… noise.” She paused, shooting another wicked little smirk at Rio. “Very, very loud noise.”

Drew cackled. “I love you so much.”

“I know,” Agatha winked. “I love me too.”

The two dissolved into laughter, the audience cheering with them, while Rio silently prayed for strength behind the camera.

The rest of the interview went by quickly after that. The second Agatha stepped offstage, the roar of the audience still echoing, she spotted Rio leaning against the wall, arms folded tight across her chest. The bodyguard’s face was composed, but her ears were still pink from Drew reading those tweets aloud.

Agatha sauntered over, a smug grin firmly in place. “You know, tattoos for days might be my favorite one. Though personally, I’d have said tattoos for nights, since I tend to imagine you more in—”

Rio cut her off with a low groan, pressing a hand to her forehead. “Agatha, please. I’m begging you.”

“Begging, hm?” Agatha purred, delighting in the way Rio froze. “Good to know.”

Rio shot her a look that was equal parts exasperated and flustered, then muttered something under her breath in Spanish before pushing off the wall. “We’re leaving before you get us both in trouble.”

Agatha laughed, looping her arm through Rio’s as if nothing was more natural. “Fine, darling. But admit it, you secretly love the chaos.”

Rio didn’t answer, but the twitch of her lips was enough to give her away.

 

By the time they made it to the film set to begin the first day of shooting Coven of Chaos, the playful energy had dissipated, Agatha in actress mode and Rio in full protector mode. Trucks lined the perimeter, crew members hauled equipment across the asphalt, and walkie chatter echoed from every direction. To most, it looked like organized chaos. To Rio, it looked like a hundred potential vulnerabilities.

She stepped out of the SUV first, scanning the lot with sharp, deliberate precision. Bucky peeled off immediately to do a second perimeter check, Natasha headed for the gate to liaise with studio security, and Clint moved to a rooftop vantage point with a long lens camera. Alice stayed with the surveillance van, laptop open and headset on, eyes flicking between feeds.

Yelena fell into step beside Rio, chewing gum like she didn’t have a care in the world, but her eyes were as sharp as Rio’s.

“Place looks clean,” Yelena muttered, shoving her hands in her jacket pockets. “But I don’t like it.”

“Neither do I,” Rio replied quietly, her gaze tracking a women lingering too long by a lighting rig. Her hand twitched toward her comm, but then she saw the badge. Crew. Still, she filed her face away.

Agatha exited the SUV a moment later, sunglasses on, hair and makeup already flawless. Jen hovered close with her ever-present binder, Billy a few steps behind, arms full of garment bags. Agatha flashed a smile at the photographers hired by the studio to document the first day, but Rio could see how tight her grip was on her coffee cup.

“Rio, darling,” Agatha drawled, “you’re scowling again. People will think you don’t like being here.”

“I don’t,” Rio said flatly, never taking her eyes off the crowd.

Yelena snorted. “She means she doesn’t like people she can’t control.”

Agatha raised an amused brow. “Hot stuff, if you’re this tense now, what will you be like when I actually start filming?”

Rio didn’t answer. She was watching a shadow slip just behind one of the trailers—too fast to be crew, too deliberate to be casual.

“Yelena.”

“I see it.” The blonde’s gum stilled as her posture straightened, hand brushing the inside of her jacket where a blade was tucked.

“Stay casual,” Rio murmured. “We’re not spooking the actress on her first day.”

Agatha glanced between them, sensing the sudden shift in tone. Her smile faltered. “What is it?”

Rio forced her expression neutral. “Nothing you need to worry about yet. Go on. Meet your director. We’ve got you covered.”

Yelena leaned close as Agatha walked away with Jen and Billy. “Gut says we’ve got company.”

Rio’s eyes narrowed at the trailer. “Mine too.”

Neither woman moved, but their shoulders squared, their attention locked like predators circling unseen prey. Whatever was waiting for them today, it was already here.

Rio followed Agatha inside while Yelena peeled off to check the possible intruder. Rio’s gut told her something was wrong—and her gut had never let her down. She stayed in Agatha’s shadow, close enough to intervene, but just far enough to let the actress move freely.

Agatha slipped into full-on actress mode the moment she spotted Peggy, the director. They laughed, going over the day’s schedule.

“Today is mostly blocking,” Peggy explained warmly. “Positions, lighting, making sure everything flows. We’ll shoot one scene—the first time your character is finally free from the bindings the Scarlet Witch put on you. Wanda won’t be on set until later in the week, so we’ll frame it without her for now.”

Agatha nodded, absorbing it all. It sounded like a simple day, at least on paper.

Rio blended into the background, scanning constantly, her posture deceptively relaxed. Agatha asked smart questions, offered thoughtful suggestions to deepen her character, and Peggy took them all in stride.

Yelena’s voice crackled through comms. “False alarm on our suspicious person. Just an assistant who had a bathroom emergency. Don’t ask how I found that out. Heading back now.”

Rio had to bite back a laugh. Relief flickered through her, but the prickling at the back of her neck never eased. Something was still off.

She glanced up toward the catwalk above the stage—just in time to see the clip holding one of the heavy lights straining, metal warping under pressure.

Her blood ran cold.

“Agatha—!”

Rio sprinted forward, diving at the actress just as the clip gave way. She tackled her to the ground, shielding her with her own body as the massive light crashed down, shattering inches from where Agatha had been standing only seconds before.

The crash reverberated through the soundstage like thunder, glass and metal scattering across the floor. Crew members screamed and dove out of the way. The director’s chair clattered backward as Peggy lurched to her feet, shouting for safety.

Rio’s arms locked around Agatha as they hit the ground, her body caging the actress in, shielding her from debris. For a heartbeat, all Agatha could register was the weight of Rio’s body pressed against hers, her rapid heartbeat thundering in her chest, and the way her perfume still clung to her skin even through the chaos.

Agatha blinked up, dazed.

Rio eyes were sharp, scanning above them, tracking the catwalk. Her voice rang through the comms, clipped and urgent. “Possible sabotage. Catwalk, northeast quadrant. Lock it down.”

“Yes, ma’am,” Natasha’s voice replied instantly.

Yelena swore in Russian through the line. “On it.”

Bucky’s voice followed, low and grim. “I’m already moving.”

Rio finally pushed herself up enough to check Agatha over, her hands brushing over her arms, her waist, her face with uncharacteristic urgency. “Are you hurt?”

Agatha, still a little breathless, shook her head. “No, I’m fine. Thanks to you.” She tried to sit up, but Rio kept her firmly pressed down for another beat, as if she didn’t trust the world not to collapse on her again.

The crew was in chaos, people shouting, someone radioing for medics, Peggy barking orders to clear the stage. Jen and Billy stood frozen watching in shock.

Alice’s voice came through comms, calm but urgent. “I’m rewinding camera feeds now. That clip didn’t just fail, it looks like it was tampered with.”

Rio’s jaw tightened, her gut twisting. She knew it.

“There was a women I saw up their earlier, she was wearing a crew badge, but something felt off about her, try and find her,” Rio ordered

She hauled Agatha gently to her feet, keeping a protective hand at the small of her back as she guided her away from the wreckage. Agatha leaned in close, her voice quieter now, more serious. “That wasn’t an accident, was it?”

Rio’s silence was answer enough.

The set lights still buzzed overhead, the wreckage of the fallen lamp smoking faintly at their feet. But Rio’s focus was entirely on Agatha, making sure she stood, unshaken, alive.

Rio silently vowed: whoever was behind this, they’d just declared war.

Rio, flanked by Alice and Natasha, moved swiftly at Agatha’s side as they guided her back toward the trailer. Jen and Billy ran alongside them finally coming out of their daze. Peggy intercepted them, face pale with worry, reaching for Agatha.

“Agatha, are you alright? I—”

Natasha stepped neatly between them, voice calm but firm. “Later. Right now, our priority is getting her safe.”

Peggy hesitated, torn between concern and the authority of the security team, then nodded tightly. “Fine. But someone is going to answer for this.” She turned on her heel, already barking orders at the crew, demanding explanations and accountability.

The small formation pressed forward. Clint and Bucky joined in seamlessly, closing ranks around Agatha, their presence forming a wall of quiet steel. Yelena’s voice crackled faintly over comms, she was still up on the catwalk, already interrogating crew members and snapping photos of the broken clip for evidence.

Agatha walked in silence, every step a little heavier than the last. She kept her head high, sunglasses still perched like armor, but Rio could feel the tremor in her movements. With the team’s bodies surrounding her, the chaos of the set faded behind them, replaced by the low hum of radios and the heavy press of what-ifs lingering in the air.

Agatha stopped walking, completely frozen. Agatha turned to face them all, mask cracking just a little. “I almost died,” she admitted quietly, like the words tasted strange on her tongue. Her eyes flicked to Rio’s, searching for something solid to hold onto.

“You didn’t,” Rio said firmly, almost fiercely, as if sheer will alone had made it true. She led Agatha to her trailer.

Inside the trailer, the air was still, too still. Rio’s instincts screamed before her eyes even registered the details. She raised a hand, halting Agatha in the doorway. Alice slipped past her with weapon drawn, Natasha right behind, moving in a fluid sweep of the space.

Seconds later, Alice’s voice came sharp. “Clear. But… you need to see this.”

Rio guided Agatha inside carefully, keeping her body angled just slightly in front of her. The familiar warmth of the trailer had been shattered, literally. The vanity mirror had been smashed, jagged pieces scattered across the floor like glittering teeth. Agatha’s stack of fan mail had been torn open and shredded, bits of half-chewed paper littering the carpet as if rats had gnawed their way through her privacy.

But it was the bed that stopped them all cold. Jen gasped.

On top of the carefully made covers lay a single piece of paper, the words scrawled in thick, uneven strokes:

Now try to ignore us. You belong to us.

Agatha’s breath caught audibly, her hand flying to her mouth. She swayed, and Rio caught her by the elbow before she could stumble. Billy rests his hand on her back, trying to hold her up as well.

Natasha bent, gloved fingers hovering over the note without touching. “They were in here recently. The air’s still cold from the AC being reset.”

Alice was already at the door, scanning the lock with narrowed eyes. “No forced entry. Whoever it was had access. Either a duplicate key or inside help.”

Rio’s grip tightened on Agatha’s arm, grounding her. “You’re safe now. We’re here.”

But Agatha’s eyes were locked on the broken mirror, her reflection fractured into a hundred jagged shards. For the first time, the mask of the untouchable actress slipped completely. Her voice trembled. “They were this close. In my space. In my bed. They tried to KILL me!”

Rio gently turned her away from the sight, pulling her against her chest, as her own gut twisted with fury. “We’ll find them.” Rio kissed the side of Agatha’s head, hoping to bring comfort. 

The team exchanged tense looks around her, unspoken understanding sparking between them. This wasn’t random. It was the Stalker. And it had just escalated.

The trailer felt smaller with every second that passed. Rio made the call without hesitation. “We’re pulling her. Now.”

Natasha scooped the note into an evidence bag, Bucky collected photos of the damage, and Alice swept the doorway for prints. Yelena rejoined them with a stormy expression, jaw tight from whatever she’d pried out of the crew.

Within minutes, the team had Agatha moving. Clint and Bucky formed a wall at the front, Natasha and Yelena took the flanks, Alice watched the rear. Rio stayed glued to Agatha’s side, her hand hovering just at her back, ready to catch her if her knees gave out again.

They didn’t linger. Through the lot, past Peggy’s frantic questions, through the crowd of gawking crew, the team moved with precision, ignoring the stares. Rio didn’t let anyone get close.

The SUV doors slammed shut one by one, the bubble of security sealing tight around her again.

Agatha sat pressed into the leather seat, sunglasses shielding her eyes though the sun had already started going down. She didn’t say a word. Her hand, however, found Rio’s on the seat between them, gripping it hard, like she needed something tangible to tether her to the moment.

Rio didn’t pull away. She only squeezed back, silent, as the convoy pulled out and carried them toward the only safe place left—home.

The convoy pulled through the gates, engines rumbling to a stop in tight formation. The team spilled out quickly, weapons and instincts already tuned to danger. Natasha barked orders for a perimeter sweep, Bucky checked the garage access, and Yelena stalked toward the back fence like she dared the stalker to be there waiting.

Rio stayed at Agatha’s side, her hand warm and steady at the small of her back. “Come with me.” Her tone left no room for argument, though it was soft enough that Agatha didn’t bristle.

She guided her inside, past the bustle of the others securing the house, and down a quiet hallway. Only when they reached the study, a small room lined with maps, files, and a sturdy oak desk, did she stop. She shut the door firmly behind them.

For a moment, Agatha stood frozen, still wrapped in the armor she always wore. Shoulders squared, chin lifted, lips pressed into a tight line. But Rio just stepped closer, steady and unyielding, and said gently, “You don’t have to hold it together for me.”

That undid her.

Agatha’s breath hitched, then broke. She crumpled forward into Rio’s chest, the first sob tearing out of her like it had been clawing at her ribs all day. Rio caught her easily, arms wrapping around her, holding her like she’d never let go.

“They were in my trailer,” Agatha choked, her voice muffled against Rio’s shirt. “They touched my things, my bed—God, they could’ve been standing over me while I slept, they tried to kill me, why are they doing this?” Agatha rambled. 

“Shh,” Rio murmured, her voice low and steady, one hand stroking slow circles between her shoulder blades. “You’re safe now. I’ve got you.”

Agatha clung to her, fingers curling into the fabric at her back, shaking with every breath. It wasn’t the poised star or the sharp-tongued flirt now; it was just a woman who’d been pushed to the edge, terrified and vulnerable.

And Rio held her through it, letting her fall apart, strong enough for both of them until Agatha could stand again.

Downstairs, a little while later, Rio joins the team after putting Agatha to bed, after finally getting her to calm down. Jen and Billy both agree to stay the night, sleeping in the same bed with Agatha, so she isn't alone. 

The dining room had been converted into a temporary command center. Laptops hummed, photos and maps were spread across the table, and half a dozen cups of coffee stood forgotten as the team gathered.

Alice tapped the trackpad of her laptop, pulling up a grid of images on the big monitor mounted to the wall. “Okay. I’ve been combing through every candid, paparazzi shot, and social media post of Agatha over the entirety of her career. At first, I didn’t notice anything, but after cross-referencing patterns, I found her.”

A woman’s face appeared on screen, pulled from a long-distance photo. She was in the background, blurred, but unmistakably there. Blonde hair, sharp cheekbones, eyes fixed on Agatha.

“At first she looks… almost smitten,” Alice said, cycling through images. In each one, the woman lingered somewhere behind Agatha, sometimes across a street, sometimes in a crowd at a premiere. Always watching. In the earlier photos, her expression was soft, affectionate, almost dreamlike.

Alice advanced to later years. “But the longer it goes on, the more it changes.” The woman’s features hardened in each new frame. Happy glances turned into scowls. Admiration shifted into resentment. In one shot, her fists were clenched at her sides as Agatha laughed with a co-star. “She disappears entirely for almost a decade. Nothing. And then…”

The most recent photo appeared. Taken just last week, outside a restaurant. The woman stood across the street, partially hidden by a lamppost. Her eyes were locked on Agatha with open fury.

“She’s back,” Alice said grimly. “And she’s not alone. The note said us. This is a group.”

Bucky leaned forward, arms crossed. “Makes sense. The shooter Natasha chased wasn’t working solo.”

“That shooter,” Natasha began, her tone colder than ice. “We got confirmation.” She pulled up another file. A mugshot filled the screen. “Ralph Bohner. Low-level criminal, mostly petty theft and assault. His DNA matched the blood he left on the street when I clipped him.”

“Except Ralph isn’t a problem anymore,” Clint added. “He turned up dead this morning in an abandoned car lot downtown. Gunshot to the head, execution style. Somebody silenced him.”

Yelena scoffed, kicking her boots up on the table. “Clean-up job. Whoever’s pulling the strings didn’t want him talking.”

Alice frowned and clicked into another document. “There’s more. Ralph Bohner was married for a few years to Raven Corvin. Ring a bell?”

Natasha’s brows lifted. Rio’s jaw tightened.

“Yeah,” Clint muttered. “That was Agatha’s old assistant, right?”

Alice nodded. “Fired after Agatha caught her stealing jewelry and… underwear.” She winced at the word. “Raven disappeared after that, no jobs, no public record. Until now, when her ex-husband shows up trying to plant trackers on Agatha’s car.”

Yelena let out a low whistle. “Stealing her underwear? That’s a special brand of obsessed.”

“Which means Raven has motive,” Clint said. “But Ralph wasn’t any mastermind. He was just muscle.”

“Exactly,” Alice agreed, her tone sharper now. “They’ve got money, connections, inside access. We’re talking about slipping people onto closed sets, tampering with trailers, and bribing studio security. That doesn’t happen without serious pull.”

Natasha nodded once, her face cold. “Whoever is leading this isn’t some random ex-assistant. They’re well connected. Powerful enough to bankroll operations, buy loyalty, and dispose of liabilities when they’re no longer useful.”

“Like Ralph,” Bucky muttered. “Dead weight, literally.”

Rio looked around the table, her jaw tight. “From this point forward, we’re not protecting Agatha from a stalker. We’re protecting her from an organized group with a leader smart enough to stay hidden. They’ve been watching Agatha for years. They know her habits, her homes, her vulnerabilities. And now they’re escalating. We can't afford any gaps or complacency; this is only going to get worse until we catch these guys."

Silence settled for a moment as the weight of it sank in.

Natasha broke it. “So the question is what’s their endgame? Obsession? Revenge? Or something worse?”

No one answered, but the grim looks around the table said it all. Whatever it was, they weren’t finished.

Chapter End Notes

Did you enjoy the more action-packed chapters with the stalkers, or would you guys like me to add more Agatha and Rio intimate moments in the chapters? Let me know what ya'll think.

Smear Campaign

Chapter Summary

Stalkers launch a smear campaign against Agatha. Team rallies.

Chapter Notes

I am severely sleep-deprived, so sorry for any mistakes. I love you all and thank you truly for all the love and support. I never thought so many would like this idea as much as I do.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The house was quiet, but the living room was alive with the hum of tension. Papers littered the table in neat but overwhelming stacks, photos marked with red circles, lines drawn from face to face, lists of names and motives pinned down in Rio’s sharp handwriting. It was organized chaos, and she hadn’t slept a minute.

One by one, the rest of the team drifted in. Alice arrived first, scrolling through her phone for updates, eyes already sharp. Bucky came next, gripping the coffee pot like it was keeping him alive. Clint leaned against the wall, too alert for someone who’d only just rolled out of bed. Natasha appeared calm as ever, and Yelena scowled at her sister’s composure as she twisted her hair up into a bun.

Rio straightened from the table, her voice steady and commanding. “We slept on it, now it’s time to put a plan of action in place. Here’s what we know so far: this isn’t one person—it’s a group. The muscle handled Ralph, and when he outlived his usefulness, they cut him loose permanently. We’ve traced hacks in Agatha’s old security feeds to at least two separate individuals, which means two hackers. There’s the saboteur who rigged the lights, the infiltrator who got into Agatha’s trailer, and then the mastermind—the one funding everything, pulling the strings. We can’t say for certain that’s the whole roster, but those are the confirmed roles.”

“Right,” Clint said, nodding. “And we can safely assume Raven is in the mix somewhere. We don’t know which role yet, but we’ll find out.”

Rio handed out folders, crisp and color-coded. “Clint, Bucky, you tap your CIA contacts. Find the hackers, track their movements, figure out how they’re staying hidden. Natasha, Yelena, you two are best at flushing people out. Find Raven. Alice, run facial recognition on the blonde from the paparazzi photos. Cross-reference with security footage, see if we can nail down her name. Also, run the sketch I made of the figure on the catwalk yesterday, and try to find stills of whoever entered Agatha’s trailer. Our top priority is identifying these individuals, then neutralizing them—by any means necessary.”

Alice nodded, already typing.

Rio’s gaze swept across the team. “From here on out, every crew member on set is run through extensive background checks. IDs are verified, no exceptions. Alice and Clint stay behind today to monitor feeds in case someone wants to try lying in wait at the house or breaking in. Everyone else comes with me and Agatha. She does not breathe without two sets of eyes on her. I’ll also call Maria and request two more agents for permanent house security so we can focus on taking the offensive.”

She let the silence settle for a moment before she added the part weighing most heavily.

“And don’t underestimate the mastermind. To infiltrate sets, bypass security, pay off guards, and hire fall guys, that takes money, influence, and connections at a high level. We’re not dealing with amateurs. This is someone powerful enough to move people like chess pieces, and we’ve only just started pulling at the threads.”

The room went still, the weight of her words pressing down on everyone present. This wasn’t just about obsession anymore.

It was about power.

And whoever was pulling the strings wasn’t planning to stop until Agatha belonged to them.

The team began dispersing to their assignments, but Rio stayed behind, pacing the length of the living room with her phone already at her ear. The fatigue from a sleepless night pressed against her temples, but her voice was steady when Maria picked up on the second ring.

“Talk to me,” Maria said without preamble.

“We need reinforcements,” Rio said. “Agatha’s stalkers aren’t amateurs. We’ve confirmed it’s a group, possibly networked. We’re looking at multiple roles—hackers, infiltrators, muscle—and a mastermind with money and serious connections. I want two more people stationed at the house full time. That frees us up to focus on tracking and extraction.”

There was silence on the line, just Maria processing. Then: “Who do you want?”

“Sonya. She’s former Russian Special Forces, ex-KGB. She knows Yelena, they’ve worked together before. That rapport means they’ll fall into rhythm fast.” Rio stopped pacing, pressing a hand to the back of her neck. “And Steve Rogers. If there’s anyone I trust to hold this line when we’re spread thin, it’s him. He’s steady, disciplined, and he won’t crack under media pressure if this escalates further.”

Maria let out a soft exhale. “Big guns, Rio. You’re pulling from the top shelf.”

“That’s because this isn’t a game anymore,” Rio said quietly. Her eyes drifted to the stairs where Agatha was still asleep, oblivious to the war being mapped out downstairs. “Send them in as soon as possible.”

“You’ll have them by tomorrow morning,” Maria promised. “Hold the line until then.”

The call ended, and Rio set the phone down, bracing her hands on the table. Relief flickered through her, but only for a moment. With Sonya and Steve on their way, the house would be stronger, but the fact that they even needed that kind of backup only confirmed how dangerous this had become.

The house had gone quiet again, the buzz of the debrief fading as everyone slipped into their tasks. Jen and Billy came down the stairs, fixing themselves coffee.

“Any progress on finding the bastards who tried to kill Agatha yesterday?” Billy asked, his jaw tight, voice sharp with anger. His fists were clenched at his sides, and for once, his usual warmth was buried under fire. He had known Agatha his whole life—Wanda and her had been close friends since before his birth. To him, Agatha wasn’t just a boss. She was a constant, a protector, sometimes even a second mother. When he’d first offered to be her assistant, Agatha had hesitated. But with Wanda’s insistence, and his own persistence, she’d let him in. And Billy took that trust personally.

“Yes,” Rio said evenly, her voice a calm counterweight to his fury. “My team and I have uncovered a lot. More than I expected this quickly. But I’d rather explain once, to you guys and Agatha so nothing gets lost in translation.” She glanced up the staircase. “She’s still asleep?”

Jen, who was perched on the arm of the couch with her phone in hand, nodded. “Out cold. For once.”

Rio exhaled through her nose, some of the tension in her shoulders loosening. “Good. Let her rest. She needs it more than she’ll ever admit.”

Billy gave a stiff nod, but his hands were still trembling with the urge to do something. “Fine. But the second she’s awake, I want to hear everything. She deserves to know who’s coming after her. And I want to know how we stop them.”

Rio met his gaze, steady and unflinching. “Trust me, Billy. No one wants them stopped more than I do.”

A little while later, Rio climbed the stairs slowly, each step heavier than the last. For all her discipline, for all the walls she’d built, she found herself hesitating outside Agatha’s door.

She knocked lightly, then pushed the door open.

Agatha was still in bed, tangled in the purple sheets, the morning light spilling across her skin in golden stripes. She stirred, blinking awake, then smiled faintly when she saw Rio standing there.

“You look like hell,” Agatha rasped, voice husky with sleep.

Rio huffed a laugh despite herself. “Didn’t sleep.”

Agatha stretched lazily, the blanket slipping lower. “Of course you didn’t. Always protecting everyone but yourself.” Her eyes softened. “What time is it?”

“Late morning. We’ve got a busy day ahead, so I thought I’d wake you.” Rio lingered by the doorway, suddenly unsure if stepping closer was crossing a line. But then Agatha reached out, crooking a finger.

“Come here, soldier.”

Rio obeyed before she could overthink it, crossing the room and sitting on the edge of the bed. Agatha shifted, propping herself up on her elbows, close enough now that Rio could smell the faint trace of her perfume—warm, spiced, uniquely her.

For a beat, neither spoke. The storm of yesterday, the threats of today, the looming unknown, they hung over them like smoke. But here, in this room, it was quiet. Just the two of them.

Agatha reached out, her fingers brushing the back of Rio’s hand, then sliding higher to her wrist. “You’re allowed to breathe, you know. To have something good, even in all this.”

Rio swallowed hard, every instinct telling her to pull back, to keep that last wall intact. But then Agatha leaned in, her lips hovering just shy of hers, waiting.

Rio closed the distance.

The kiss was soft at first, tentative, then deeper as Agatha tilted her head and tugged her closer by the collar of her shirt. Rio let herself go, just for this moment, hovering over Agatha on the bed, one hand cupping Agatha’s jaw while the other held her up to keep her weight off the actress below. Agatha moaned into her mouth, a sound that made Rio’s stomach flip, and soon they were tangled together, the storm outside the door forgotten.

When they finally broke apart, breathless, Agatha pressed her forehead against Rio’s. “See? Not so scary.”

Rio let out a shaky laugh, her thumb tracing Agatha’s cheek. “Terrifying,” she whispered. “But worth it.”

For the first time in what felt like forever, the world outside didn’t matter. Not the stalkers, not the war brewing. Just them, stealing a moment of calm before the storm crashed down again.

“You ever going to let us go all the way, hot stuff? Or are you the wait-till-after-marriage kind of gal?” Agatha teased, her voice low and playful. She was refusing to let her mind drift back to yesterday’s chaos, clinging instead to this moment—to the warmth of the woman she was quickly, dangerously falling for.

Rio’s lips quirked into a smile. “I can’t think about that right now, hermosa. But the day will come. First, I want to take you on a real date. I’m old-fashioned that way. But don’t worry—” her eyes deliberately swept down Agatha’s body, lingering just long enough to make her squirm—“I definitely won’t be able to wait till marriage.”

Agatha’s breath hitched at the trail of those eyes. Heat coiled low in her belly. “So what I’m hearing,” she said, grinning wide enough to show all her teeth, “is that you want to marry me.”

Rio silenced her the best way she knew how—by kissing her. The kiss quickly deepened, melting into another long, heated tangle of lips and hands, neither willing to let go until they forced themselves apart before things spun too far.

They pulled back, breathless, foreheads pressed together. Agatha reached up, brushing her thumb along Rio’s jawline, her smirk softening into something raw. “Stunning,” she whispered. No innuendo. No deflection. Just truth.

Rio caught her hand, turned it, and pressed a kiss into the inside of her wrist, lingering for a second before standing. “My team uncovered a lot last night,” she said gently. Not the usual clipped, commanding tone, but softer, more human. “Get showered and dressed, then meet us downstairs. We’ll go over everything together. We’ll need your help identifying people, and your insight into the ones we already suspect.”

For once, Agatha didn’t crack a joke or deflect. She just nodded, eyes following Rio until she slipped out of the room.

The smell of fresh coffee lingered in the kitchen as Jen and Billy sat at the counter, scrolling through their phones while the security team murmured in the living room. It had been a long twenty-four hours, and both of them were running on caffeine and nerves.

Agatha descended the stairs 45 minutes later, freshly showered, hair still damp and curling at the ends. She looked relaxed, almost glowing in a way neither of them had seen since the whole stalker ordeal began. She padded across the kitchen, breezing past Rio, who was leaning over the table with papers spread out, and without breaking stride, Agatha let her hands rest on Rio’s hips in a casual, familiar way before continuing toward the coffeepot.

Rio looked back at Agatha and gave a soft, shy smile.

Jen’s jaw dropped. Billy’s phone slipped out of his hand and clattered onto the counter. Both turned in unison, wide-eyed, then looked back at each other.

“Oh my god,” Jen whispered loudly, leaning toward Billy. “Rio finally pulled her head out of her ass.”

Billy’s grin spread so wide it nearly split his face. “I knew it! I knew it!” He slapped the counter for emphasis.

Agatha glanced over her shoulder, smirking like the cat who caught the canary. “What’s with the faces? Don’t tell me you’re surprised. I am irresistible, after all.”

Rio groaned, pinching the bridge of her nose. “Agatha…”

Jen practically vibrated with glee. “No, no, don’t you Agatha this away! Do you have any idea how unbearable she’s been since you got here? I’ve been spraying her with a water bottle like she’s a misbehaving cat, and it still didn’t stop her.”

Agatha poured her coffee and leaned lazily against the counter, mug in hand, utterly unbothered. “Persistence pays off, darling.”

Billy laughed so hard he nearly knocked over his cup. “I can’t wait to tell my mom. She owes me fifty bucks!”

Rio’s head snapped up. “You two were betting on us?”

Jen grinned like the devil himself. “Oh, honey. Everyone was betting on you two.”

Rio muttered something in Spanish under her breath, cheeks heating as Agatha only looked more pleased with herself.

For the first time in days, the tension in the house gave way to laughter.

Rio spread the files out across the dining table, her usual precision on display as she slid each photo and document into neat stacks. Jen and Billy sat on one side, Agatha on the other, her mug of coffee steaming between her hands. She looked composed, but Rio caught the faint tightness in her jaw, a lingering echo of yesterday’s close calls.

“Alright,” Rio began, her tone clipped but calm, “here’s where we stand. We know this isn’t a lone wolf. It’s a group. Roles we’ve identified so far: two hackers, a saboteur, an infiltrator, the muscle who took out Ralph, and a mastermind funding everything.”

“Who the fuck is Ralph?” Jen asks confused

Rio tapped the folder in front of her. “Ralph Bohner’s confirmed dead. His DNA matched that of the person whom Natasha had clipped during the chase after he tried to plant trackers on Agatha’s car. He was married to Raven Corvin—Agatha, you fired her years ago for theft.”

Agatha’s eyes narrowed, memory flashing. “Yeah. Jewelry, clothes… underwear. Creepy little thief. I knew I’d see her again one day.”

Rio gave a short nod. “Exactly. Which means Raven has motive, and now Ralph’s gone, she may be even more unhinged.” She flipped to the next photo—a series of paparazzi shots stitched together on a board. “Alice also flagged this woman. She shows up in the background of your photos for years. At first, she looks happy, infatuated even. But the more recent ones—bitterness, resentment. Then she disappears entirely… until last week.”

She slid the clearest shot of the blonde forward. Agatha stiffened, her grip tightening on the coffee mug.

“I know her,” she said flatly.

Billy leaned forward. “You do?”

Agatha exhaled slowly, eyes fixed on the photo. “She used to run my biggest stan account on Twitter. At first, I thought she was just another obsessed fan, but then she came to a con, got backstage. She tried to… sleep with me.” Her voice soured, disgust rolling under it. “She was underage. I rejected her immediately and cut all contact. But she didn’t take it well. I blocked her, had my team keep her away from events, but clearly… she didn’t let it go.”

Jen’s brows furrowed. “Do you remember her name?”

Agatha nodded grimly. “Renna. That’s all I ever got. Just Renna.”

Rio’s jaw clenched, her pen digging into the paper as she wrote it down. “That helps. A name, even a partial one, is more than we had yesterday. Alice can run it against known aliases and tie it back to the photos. If she resurfaces again, we’ll find where.”

The table fell into silence, the weight of it sinking in. For years, Renna had been circling Agatha’s life like a shadow. And now she wasn’t lurking in the background anymore.

She was moving center stage.

“I know this feels like a lot, Agatha,” Rio said softly, her tone cutting through the tension. “But we’ve already identified two suspects. We know their roles, and tomorrow two more guards will arrive to stay at the house full-time. That means the rest of us can focus entirely on you. We are making progress, I promise.”

Agatha’s jaw tightened. The frustration wasn’t aimed at Rio, but at the situation itself, at the constant shadow stalking her every move. She squeezed Rio’s hand in silent thanks and brushed a quick kiss across her lips.

Before Rio could respond, Jen’s phone lit up with rapid notifications, buzzing like a hornet’s nest. At the same time, Agatha’s phone started ringing nonstop.

Billy frowned. “Did the media find out about what happened yesterday on set?”

Jen glanced at her screen, her face draining of color. “No. It’s worse. #BoycottAgatha is trending. Someone just dumped a flood of false claims, saying you’re rude to fans, that you scream at crew, and that you are a diva.”

“WHAT?!” Agatha’s voice cracked through the room, sharp with horror. She knows what happens to women in Hollywood who get labeled as difficult to work with: they don't get jobs.

The entire security team came charging in from the other room, hands already hovering near weapons, eyes scanning for danger.

“What happened?” Natasha asked calmly, her gaze sharp as a blade.

Rio’s jaw flexed as she forced her voice to stay level. “The stalker group is going on the offensive again. This time, they’re aiming for her reputation. If they can’t get to her physically, they’ll destroy her in the court of public opinion.”

Jen paled further. “Oh God—it just got worse. There’s a deepfake video going viral right now. It shows you screaming at an assistant and shoving them. And ‘sources’ are popping up, claiming they were harassed or bullied by you.”

Agatha’s hands shook as she grabbed her phone, her voice ragged. “That’s a lie. I would never—I’ve always treated every crew member with respect. I—” She broke off, breathing too fast, panic rising like a wave.

Billy rushed to the fridge, yanking out a bottle of cold water and pressing it into Agatha’s hands. “Here. Drink.”

Rio slid closer, a steady hand rubbing slow circles into Agatha’s back. “Breathe, hermosa. We’ll fix this.”

Agatha looked up at her desperately. “How? If we pull the video, people will just say I’m hiding something. If I deny it, they’ll say I’m lying. How do I fight shadows?”

Rio’s voice sharpened, all business now. “Here’s the plan. Alice will run a forensic program on the video. Every deepfake has a tell; we’ll prove it’s fabricated. Jen, you start contacting everyone who’s ever worked with Agatha. Directors, crew, co-stars, get them posting to their socials. Drown the lies in real testimonials.”

Jen nodded quickly, already typing.

Rio turned back to Agatha, her eyes locking onto hers. “And you, you think carefully. Do you have a trusted journalist? Someone you’re close with, but not publicly tied to? We’ll bring them in, have them shadow you on set. They’ll talk to the crew directly and write a piece that dismantles these lies before they stick. We don’t just defend—we turn the narrative.”

The room held still for a beat, every set of eyes on Agatha. She clutched the water bottle, breath still uneven but steadier now, a flicker of fire returning to her gaze.

“Jessica Jones,” Agatha said after a moment of thought, her voice steadier now. “We met years ago. No photos, no public appearances together. But we’re good friends. She’s respected, used to write for Access Hollywood, now works for the L.A. Times.”

Rio’s lips curved into the faintest nod. “Good. Call her. Ask her to come shadow you on set today. We’ll give her enough of the truth to frame the story, then let her leak just enough. Once the public sees what’s really happening, that you’re the target of a smear campaign, they’ll rally. They’ll turn on the ones spreading these lies.”

Jen tapped furiously on her phone, already drafting a message. “And the timing’s perfect. If Jessica’s piece starts circulating today, we can drown out the deepfake before it gets another twenty-four hours of traction.”

Agatha exhaled slowly, the panic ebbing as a clear path took shape. She still hated that it had come to this, fighting ghosts and shadows in the media instead of scripts and cameras, but with Rio’s hand steady at her back and the plan laid out, she finally felt the ground beneath her feet again.

Billy looked between them all, his expression fierce. “So we fight fire with fire.”

“No,” Rio corrected quietly, but firmly. “We fight lies with truth. And we win.”

Agatha slipped into the study, shutting the door softly behind her. Her hands still trembled, but she steadied them enough to scroll through her contacts. Jessica’s name was there—buried under years of people she hadn’t spoken to in forever—but the second she saw it, relief hit her like a breath of fresh air.

She pressed call.

The line rang once, twice. Then came a familiar, gravel-edged voice: “Harkness? Either the world’s ending or you butt-dialed me, and if it’s the second, I’m hanging up.”

Despite everything, Agatha laughed—a real one, short and sharp. “It’s the first, darling. And I wouldn’t call you unless it was important.”

Jessica hummed, skeptical. “I saw the hashtag. BoycottAgatha, right? Thought it was bullshit. What’s going on?”

Agatha sank into the leather chair, closing her eyes. “I don’t have time for details over the phone. But I need your help. Come to set with me today. Shadow me, talk to the crew, write what you see. You know me better than most—you know this isn’t who I am.”

There was a beat of silence. Then Jessica’s voice sharpened. “You’re telling me someone’s coming after you?”

“Yes. A group, actually. They’re organized, dangerous, and now they’re trying to destroy me publicly because they can’t get to me physically.”

Another pause, then the sound of a cigarette lighter flicking on. “Alright. I’m in. Text me the address. And Agatha?”

“Yes?”

“Don’t bullshit me when I get there. If you want me to help, I need the real story.”

Agatha smiled faintly. “Wouldn’t dream of doing otherwise.”



The studio lot buzzed with its usual chaos: crew hauling cables, cameras rolling across the floor, production shouting back and forth. But Rio’s team had already turned the place into a fortress. Natasha was at the gate, Bucky circling the perimeter, Yelena high on a catwalk, pretending to be casual but watching like a hawk. Everyone, including the crew, was on high alert after the events of yesterday.

The black SUV pulled up to the side entrance. Rio went first, scanning, then motioned for the others to stand down as Jessica Jones stepped out.

Dressed in her usual leather jacket, dark jeans, and boots, she looked like she owned the place already. Her sunglasses came down just enough for her to glance at Rio. “So, you’re the infamous Rio. You look like you could break me in half. Good. I like knowing Agatha’s in one piece.”

Rio gave a curt nod, stone-faced, though the corner of her mouth twitched almost imperceptibly.

Jessica turned to Agatha, who was waiting just inside the doorway. “Jesus, Harkness. Leave you alone for five minutes and you’ve got a death cult on your ass.”

Agatha smirked, though her eyes softened at the sight of her old friend. “What can I say? I’m popular.”

Jessica’s lips quirked. “Popular, sure. But not invincible. Now, ” she pulled out her notebook, flipping it open, “show me where the skeletons are buried. If someone’s trying to ruin you, I’ll make damn sure the world sees who’s holding the shovel.”

Rio stepped in close to Agatha, murmuring low enough only she could hear. “I like her.”

Agatha grinned, brushing her hand over Rio’s arm before striding onto set with Jessica in tow. “Told you she was the right one for this.”

The studio was buzzing when Agatha stepped onto set with Jessica shadowing her like a storm cloud in boots. Crew members nodded politely, some outright staring, the kind of quiet awe Agatha always drew in professional spaces. But Jessica wasn’t watching like a fan. She was watching like a hunter—taking in body language, the energy of the room, how people reacted when Agatha walked by.

Rio stayed close, always in Agatha’s shadow but never crowding her. Jessica clocked that instantly, the way Rio’s gaze never stopped scanning. Protective. Calculating. A fortress in a suit.

Agatha slipped into “leading lady” mode with ease. She greeted Peggy warmly, joked with the makeup team, and even teased a PA about tripping over their own shoelaces. Jessica scribbled notes: Professional. Lighthearted. Not a diva. Crew at ease around her. She muttered under her breath, “Yeah, real monster, my ass.”

After ten minutes of watching, Jessica slipped away, working her way toward the craft table where a few crew members were clustered. She introduced herself casually, not flashing credentials, just letting her name settle. Once recognition hit, the tension eased, and they started talking.

“She’s one of the best people I’ve worked with,” a camera operator said. “Remembers names, makes sure everyone gets thanked. Bought the crew lunch out of her own pocket a few days ago.”

“She actually listens,” another chimed in. “If you suggest something that’ll make the shot better, she hears you out. Doesn’t act like she’s above anyone.”

Jessica nodded, jotting it all down. Then one of them leaned closer, lowering his voice.

“The thing that rattled people the most wasn’t the headlines—it was the light. That thing would’ve crushed her if security hadn’t been paying attention.”

Jessica’s pen stilled. “The light?”

The man nodded. “Came down out of nowhere, like the clip just snapped. But I’ve been in this business a long time—gear doesn’t just fail like that. Not with fresh rigging. Someone messed with it.”

Jessica’s jaw tightened. “Convenient no one outside the set heard about that.”

She moved on, circling toward the wardrobe department, and got another tidbit: Agatha’s trailer. A mirror was smashed. Fan mail shredded like an animal had gotten to it. And then, the note.

Jessica underlined the words in her pad three times: Now try to ignore us. You belong to us.

By the time she circled back toward the central monitors, she found Jen with her phone glued to her ear, barking into it at lightning speed. Jessica waited until she hung up before stepping in.

“Jones,” Jen said, giving her a once-over. “Figured Agatha would pull you in. She trusts so few people.”

Jessica smirked. “Smart woman. Fill me in—what are you dealing with on your end?”

Jen sighed, rubbing her temple. “My job’s damage control. I’m calling every producer, every director, every PA Agatha’s ever worked with. If the internet wants to paint her as some kind of tyrant, I’m going to flood the timeline with firsthand accounts that prove otherwise. She’s got a spotless record, and I intend to remind people of that. But the lies spread faster than truth, and the deepfake video? That’s my nightmare. Once an image burns into people’s minds, it doesn’t matter how fake it is.”

Jessica tapped her notebook. “Then we give them more powerful images. Her working, laughing with the crew. Being herself. I’ll handle the narrative—you keep her allies talking.”

Jen gave a sharp nod, her respect for Jessica clear.

Jessica’s next stop was Peggy. The director was pacing by the monitors, headset slung around her neck, eyes flashing as she oversaw blocking. Jessica caught her between instructions.

“You’ve worked with her long?” Jessica asked.

“Off and on for about 15 years,” Peggy said, not missing a beat. “She’s always been like this—sharp, generous, funny. Never pulls rank. And if someone tries to? She’s the first to defend the crew. Look—do you think I’d still be working with her if she was even a fraction of what they’re saying? I’d have shut her down myself. She’s family to me.”

Jessica jotted it down, satisfied.

Finally, she found Billy near the trailers, nervously scrolling through his phone. He perked up when he saw her.

“You’re Jessica, right? Agatha’s friend?”

Jessica nodded. “That’s me. You’re her assistant?”

“Yeah. But she’s… more than that. She’s basically family. She was there my whole life. I know her better than most, and I can promise you, she’s not what they’re painting her as. She’s tough, sure, but she’s kind. She gives a damn. Sometimes too much, honestly. She hides when she’s scared so no one else has to see it, but I do. She’s hurting. And it’s killing me to watch her go through this.”

Jessica closed her notebook slowly. She didn’t need to write that one down. It was already burned into her head.

By the time she returned to Agatha’s side, her notes were full, her instincts razor sharp. She stood back for a moment, watching Agatha work, commanding, charismatic, magnetic. She wasn’t barking orders, wasn’t sneering at assistants. She was leading.

Jessica muttered under her breath, “These bastards picked the wrong woman to try and tear down.”

She flipped her notebook shut, turning toward Rio, who was still scanning the catwalks like the soldier she’d always be.

“Your girl’s got every single person here ready to go to war for her,” Jessica said quietly.

Rio didn’t look away from the rafters. “She deserves better than this circus.”

Jessica’s voice softened, just slightly. “Then I’ll make sure the world knows it. You keep her alive, Vidal. I’ll keep her untouchable.” Jessica said, before she took her leave to begin writing the article

For the first time all day, Rio’s lips curved into a faint, fleeting smile.

The day on set came to a close; luckily, nothing eventful happened, and Agatha and the team were able to make it back home safe and without incident. 

Agatha lay on the couch, her head in Rio’s lap, a Wine glass in hand. Bucky and Yelena are on perimeter sweep while the rest of the team takes their breaks and sleeps while they can. Jen is on the sectional to their right, and Billy has gone to his room and is fast asleep. 

“Jessica released her article,” Jen said, smiling already seeing the positive reactions pouring in.

L.A. Times Exclusive
 By Jessica Jones

The Witch Hunt Against Agatha Harkness: Why the Rumors Don’t Add Up

The internet loves a scandal. And right now, Agatha Harkness—the actress beloved by millions for her sharp wit, magnetic screen presence, and unapologetic queerness—is the target of one.

Over the past twenty-four hours, hashtags calling for a boycott of Harkness have exploded across social media. Allegations range from the absurd (that she bullies crew and belittles fans) to the damning (a falsified video circulating online shows her allegedly screaming at and shoving an assistant).

But after spending a day on set with Harkness and speaking with those who know her best, I can tell you this: the narrative being spun is a fiction designed to destroy her.

A Career Built on Respect, Not Fear
 I spoke with camera operators, grips, hair and makeup staff, and the director herself, Peggy Carter. Every one of them described the same Agatha: collaborative, kind, quick to laugh, generous to crew, and fiercely protective of those around her.

“She’s one of the best people I’ve ever worked with,” one camera operator said. “Remembers names, thanks people personally, and never acts like she’s above anyone.”

“She’s family,” Carter told me bluntly. “If she were even a fraction of what they’re claiming, I’d have shut her down myself years ago.”

The Deepfake Problem
 Experts are already analyzing the viral video. Early analysis shows hallmarks of manipulation—facial warping in frames, mismatched shadows, unnatural voice syncing. In other words, it’s a fake.

But the damage is in the circulation. Deepfakes don’t need to be real to ruin reputations—they just need to be believable enough to plant doubt.

A Pattern of Escalation
What makes these smears more chilling is what’s happening off-camera.

Yesterday, while rehearsing, a stage light came crashing down inches from Harkness. Security intervened in time, but the equipment had been deliberately tampered with. Later, her trailer was broken into. A mirror smashed, fan mail shredded. A threatening note was left on her bed: Try to ignore us now, you belong to us

This is not the behavior of critics or random trolls. This is targeted harassment. A campaign. And now, it’s bleeding into the public sphere with lies meant to isolate her.

The Woman Behind the Headlines
 On set, I watched Agatha Harkness work. I saw how the crew smiled when she approached, how she made jokes to ease tension, how she threw herself into rehearsal with the same fire that’s made her a household name for decades.

This is not a tyrant. This is not an abuser. This is an actress—one who has fought tooth and nail to carve her place in an industry that wasn’t built to welcome her.

The smear campaign against Harkness is exactly that: a campaign. Manufactured. Strategic. And dangerous.

Why It Matters
Because if they can take down Agatha Harkness with lies and fakes, they can take down anyone.

Hollywood has always had its villains. But this time, the real villains aren’t on screen. They’re in the shadows—organized, well-connected, and escalating.

The world deserves to know the truth. And Agatha Harkness deserves to keep telling her story—on her terms, not theirs.

 

“Your plan worked Rio, social media is blowing up and rallying behind Agatha #StandwithAgatha #ProtectAgatha and #AgathaSupremacy are trending, major news outlets are backtracking, celebrities are rallying.” Jen said smiling from ear to ear relieved. She was unsure of Rio’s plan at first but seeing it work in real time is a relief. 

@WitchyAgatha: Jessica Jones doesn’t play. That article laid out every single lie. Our mother is safe, loved, and respected. #StandWithAgatha

@CovenQueen13: A note in her trailer saying ‘you belong to us’? That’s not a scandal, that’s STALKING. Protect Agatha at all costs. #ProtectAgatha

@FilmNerdCentral: Reading Jessica Jones’ piece gave me chills. This isn’t gossip—it’s a campaign against Agatha. She deserves better. #JusticeForAgatha

@AgathasWhore: She was almost killed by a falling light and still went to set the next day?? That’s dedication. That’s professionalism. That’s QUEEN behavior. #StandWithAgatha

@Slvt4Agatha: Not Jessica calling out the smear and reminding everyone Agatha is hotter than hell on set. We win. Always. #AgathaSupremacy

@DrewBarrymore: I’ve known Agatha since we were kids. She’s one of the most generous people I’ve ever met, and I will shout that from the rooftops until the day I die. #StandWithAgatha

@CarolDanvers: Worked with Agatha for years. Professional. Talented. Kind. Anyone saying otherwise doesn’t know her.

@Peggy Carter: I will not stand by while one of the best actresses I’ve ever worked with is dragged through the mud with fabrications. Agatha Harkness has my full support.

Variety: “Jessica Jones Exposes Smear Campaign Against Agatha Harkness: A Targeted Attack”

Entertainment Weekly: “From Boycott to Support: How Fans Rallied to Defend Agatha Harkness”

Buzzfeed: “The Internet Tried to Cancel Agatha Harkness—Jessica Jones Just Saved Her”

“Crew members, co-stars, and fans are posting their own behind-the-scenes footage of you—bloopers, funny moments, just you being yourself,” Jen said, her head still bent over her phone as she scrolled through socials.

“You’re a genius, Rio. I don’t know how we would’ve managed this without your idea,” she added, her voice full of gratitude.

“I guarantee this will make the stalkers tuck tail and hide for a while, after their plan backfired so drastically,” Rio said, running her hands gently through Agatha’s hair.

Agatha stayed silent, staring at her screen, her expression unreadable. Rio gave Jen a look. Jen caught it, nodded, and quietly excused herself, wishing them both a good night before heading to one of the spare guest rooms to crash.

A few more minutes of silence passed, Rio giving Agatha the space to process. Then Agatha finally looked up at her, eyes shimmering with unshed tears.

“I’ve spent my whole career waiting for the world to turn on me, Rio,” she whispered. “To decide I wasn’t worth loving anymore, like my mother did. And now, seeing them defend me like this… it’s terrifying and comforting all at once.”

Rio reached over, covering Agatha’s restless hand with her own, grounding and steady. “You earned this, Agatha. Their love. Their loyalty. You didn’t trick them into it, and no smear campaign can erase who you are.”

Agatha let out a trembling laugh, though her eyes glistened. “You always know what to say, don’t you?”

Rio shook her head. “Not always. But with you, the truth is easy.”

That answer seemed to melt something in Agatha. She shifted closer, curling her fingers over Rio’s hand and pressing a gentle kiss to her knuckles. “You make me feel like I can finally breathe again,” she admitted, her voice raw but steady. “Like I don’t have to keep performing when the cameras stop rolling.”

Rio’s chest tightened at the confession. She leaned in, brushing her thumb along Agatha’s jaw, the smallest of touches but heavy with meaning. “That’s all I want for you. To be able to just… be.”

The silence between them wasn’t heavy now, it was warm, grounding, alive. Agatha’s lips curved into the softest of smiles, and for once, there was no teasing in it. Only truth.

Rio exhaled slowly, then made a decision. “Agatha,” she began, her voice lower, careful but sure, “you need a break. From the spotlight. From the chaos. You’ve given everything to everyone else for years, it’s time someone gave you something back.”

Agatha tilted her head, curiosity flickering in her eyes. “And what are you suggesting, hot stuff?”

Rio met her gaze directly, no hesitation. “Come away with me. To my cabin. Just us. No cameras. No fans. No stalkers. Just quiet, peace, and maybe a proper date.”

For a moment, Agatha froze, caught between surprise and the way her heart leapt at the offer. Then her lips parted into a grin, genuine, unguarded, and maybe a little in love. “A cabin in the woods with you? Sounds like the start of a scandalous novel. But sweetheart,” She brushed her hand across Rio’s cheek, eyes sparkling. “It also sounds like exactly what I need.”

Rio smiled, small but certain, and pressed her forehead to Agatha’s. “Then it’s a date.”
