Firelight Confessions

Chapter Summary

Reinforcements arrive. Agatha and Rio go on their weekend getaway.

Chapter Notes

I loved writing this chapter so much, we take a break from all the drama and the Lesbians can find peace for a little while.

Also, I've just started my 5th rewatch of The 100, because I apparently enjoy pain and suffering, and my younger sister has started watching Game of Thrones for the first time, without knowing anything or seeing any spoilers - good luck to her.

Comments and Kudos are always appreciated :)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio woke early, as always, and carefully untangled herself from Agatha’s arms. They hadn’t meant to fall asleep on the couch, but conversation had stretched late into the night until they were too comfortable—too wrapped up in each other—to bother moving.

When she sat up, she froze. Alice and Yelena were sprawled across the opposite couch, identical shit-eating grins on their faces, phones in hand snapping pictures of the two of them snuggled together.

“Don’t you two have anything better to do than watch me sleep?” Rio groaned, dragging a hand down her face.

“Nope,” Yelena said brightly. “I’m on my break. What about you, Alice? Anything better to do?”

Alice smirked without missing a beat. “Not really. It’s my turn to guard Agatha, so technically I am doing my job.”

Rio shot them both a look, but before she could retort, a muffled grumble came from the crook of her neck. “Why are you guys talking so loud?” Agatha mumbled, her face still buried against Rio’s skin.

Rio softened immediately, brushing her hand down Agatha’s arm. “We’ve got to get up, hermosa. Get packed and ready to go.”.

Alice frowned and pulled up Agatha’s schedule on her tablet, “Packed to where? There’s nothing on her schedule that requires travel.”

“I’m taking her out of town for the weekend,” Rio said firmly, gently peeling Agatha off her side. “She needs to decompress after everything with the stalkers. A little quiet will do her good.”

Yelena tilted her head, instantly serious. “Are you sure that’s safe? Those stalkers aren’t going anywhere. Shouldn’t you bring backup? At least one more person?”

“The stalkers are going to lay low for a while after Jessica Jones dragged them into the light,” Rio countered. “And the cabin I’m taking her to is remote. It’s not tied to me in any official way, so they won’t be able to trace us there. I’ll share the location with you and the others, and I’ll check in every couple of hours so you know we’re safe.”

Alice and Yelena exchanged a look, then Yelena shrugged. “Fine. But if you two lovebirds end up in trouble, I’m bringing a spray bottle and dragging you home myself.”

“Vidal, the reinforcements are here,” Bucky announced, poking his head in before heading back outside.

Sonya and Steve stepped into the room, both straightening immediately. They extended their hands, which Rio clasped firmly in turn.

“Thank you both for coming. I’m sure Maria briefed you, so I won’t bother repeating it. Your priority is this house, no infiltration, no tampering of any kind. This group has pulled that off before, and I won’t let it happen again,” Rio said, locking eyes with each of them to make her point clear.

“Yes, ma’am,” Steve replied with a sharp nod, his voice steady and resolute. “We’ve been briefed and are ready to do whatever it takes to defend our client and this home.”

“I have no doubt,” Rio answered. “That’s why I asked for you two specifically. Yelena will show you around the grounds, and you’ll relieve Natasha and Bucky. Ms. Harkness and I will be going out of town for the weekend, but you’ll treat this house as if she were still here.”

Agatha, now fully awake, perched on the arm of the couch and looked the new arrivals over with open appreciation. “Okay, seriously, where do you recruit from? Every single one of you looks sculpted by the gods. Save some attractiveness for the rest of us.” She gave a low wolf-whistle, which earned her a sharp glare from Rio.

“Don’t worry, hot stuff,” Agatha added breezily, waving her off. “You’re still my favorite, and the most attractive one here.”

Rio rolled her eyes, but the fondness in her expression betrayed her.

“Thank you, ma’am,” Sonya said, her accent thick with steel and certainty. “It is an honor to guard you. No one will get past us, at least, not alive. On that, I can promise you.”

Agatha arched a brow. “Are all Russians terrifying, or just the women?”

“Just the women,” Yelena and Sonya answered at the same time, exchanging a knowing smile.

Agatha leaned her elbows on the back of the couch, smirking. “Wait—you two know each other? Yelena, is this the mysterious girlfriend you’ve been refusing to tell me about?”

Yelena barked out a laugh. “No. This is Sonya. We grew up together, trained in the same assassin school. Known each other our whole lives.”

Sonya said something in Russian, and Yelena smirked but kept it to herself, only replying with a glint of amusement in her eyes.

“Come on,” Yelena said, leading Steve and Sonya away. She and Sonya were already trading words in Russian, their voices carrying as they headed outside.

Rio turned back to Agatha. “Go start packing and get ready. I just need to finalize a few things before we leave. Pack for both cold and warm weather.”

Agatha rose, tilting her head. “You going to tell me where this cabin is, darling?”

“Nope,” Rio said, leaning in to brush a quick kiss against her lips before heading toward the door. “You’ll just have to trust me.”

Rio finished debriefing the team on the plan. Skepticism lingered in their expressions—none of them were thrilled about her going alone with Agatha—but in the end, they trusted Rio. If anyone could keep Agatha safe, it was her. And if anything did happen, they knew Rio was more than capable of handling it.

A little while later, Agatha came downstairs, freshly showered, dragging a suitcase behind her. Rio was by the front door, murmuring something to Alice and chuckling at her reply. The moment she noticed Agatha, Rio straightened and hurried over, immediately relieving her of the suitcase with ease.

“So, any clues on where you’re taking me?” Agatha asked, her eyes glittering with playful curiosity as she tried to pry a sliver of information out of her bodyguard.

Rio only smiled, shaking her head as she led her toward the underground garage. She opened the passenger door of her personal vehicle, a sleek Lincoln Aviator SUV, gesturing for Agatha to climb in before stowing both their bags in the trunk.

Rio slid into the driver’s seat, the leather creaking softly under her weight. “I’ll tell you on the plane, cariño,” she said, pulling smoothly out of the garage and toward the back of the property.

They passed through the hidden exit, the reinforced back gate swinging open at Yelena’s signal. She gave Rio a knowing wink and Agatha a cheeky salute before closing the gate securely behind them.

“So this requires a plane,” Agatha said, raising a brow. “At least tell me—are we staying in California?”

Rio glanced at her, lips curving faintly. “Not a big fan of surprises, are you?”

“Absolutely not,” Agatha chuckled, shaking her head. “Never have been.”

Rio sighed in mock defeat, but there was warmth in her voice when she replied. “Fine. I’ll tell you, so you stop asking every three seconds and maybe enjoy the plane ride.”

Agatha perked up, leaning a little closer.

“We’re going to my cabin in Massachusetts,” Rio explained. Her voice softened as she continued, eyes focused on the road. “When I was finally medically cleared and came back stateside, my therapist told me I needed a project, something to keep my mind busy, to stop me from getting lost in memories. My dad was from Massachusetts. He always wanted to return, and I guess… I felt drawn there too. So I bought a piece of land and built the cabin myself. It took me a year, but it gave me purpose when I needed it most.”

Agatha watched her intently, not interrupting, sensing the weight of what Rio was sharing.

“It’s not even in my name,” Rio added quietly. “I had it put under Valkyrie’s. It was… my way of honoring her.”.

The car fell into a thoughtful silence after Rio’s admission, the hum of the road filling the gaps. Agatha let her hand linger over Rio’s, thumb brushing gently against her knuckles. For once, she didn’t fill the air with a quip or tease. She simply held on, her silence a quiet promise that she understood the weight of what Rio had shared.

By the time they reached the small private airstrip, dusk was painting the sky in warm streaks of orange and violet. Rio guided the SUV toward the hangar where a sleek private jet waited. It wasn’t marked with any airline insignia, just glossy white and anonymous.

Agatha arched a brow as they stepped out, tugging her coat a little tighter against the evening breeze. “A private jet? Darling, I knew you were full of surprises, but this one takes the cake.”

Rio smirked faintly, shouldering both their bags with ease. “It’s not mine. One of my former clients lends it out when I need to move without drawing attention. Anonymous, untraceable, and more secure than commercial flights.”

“Anonymous?” Agatha echoed, lips curling into a sly grin. “So you’re telling me no one will know where we are, where we’re going, or who we’re with?”

“Exactly.” Rio shot her a side glance, but the sharp edge in her eyes was softened by amusement. “And don’t even start, Agatha. This isn’t the setup for whatever scandalous thing you’re about to suggest.”

Agatha gasped dramatically, pressing a hand to her chest. “You wound me, hot stuff. I was only going to say how utterly romantic it is. Just us, alone, flying off into the sunset. Very movie-star runaway with her bodyguard chic.”

Rio shook her head, but couldn’t stop the corner of her mouth from twitching.

Inside, the jet was as plush as Agatha expected; cream leather seats, polished wood accents, and soft lighting that made the space glow with warmth. Rio set their bags aside and checked the cabin, ever vigilant, before finally taking a seat across from her.

Agatha immediately stretched out, crossing her legs and leaning back with the ease of someone perfectly at home. She tilted her head, watching Rio with open curiosity. “So, you built an entire cabin with your own two hands. Tell me, Vidal—can you do anything that doesn’t make me want to fall harder for you?”

Rio looked up sharply, caught off guard, her ears tinting pink. “Agatha…”

“What?” Agatha teased, her grin slow and dangerous. “It’s a valid question.”

Rio sighed, trying and failing to suppress a smile. “Eat your snacks and enjoy the peace, cariño. That’s what this trip is for. Rest. Quiet.”

Agatha leaned forward, eyes glinting. “Darling, I’ll rest when I’m dead. But quiet? With you around? I don’t think I want that.”

Rio groaned, leaning her head back against the seat. “You are impossible.”

“Maybe,” Agatha said, settling back with a smug little smirk, “but I’m your impossible.”

The engines hummed to life, and the jet rolled forward into the fading light, lifting them away from the noise and chaos of L.A. Agatha finally felt the tension ease from her shoulders. Just the two of them, alone in the sky.

The jet hummed as it lifted into the air, smooth and steady. Agatha lounged across her seat like she owned the plane, one leg crossed over the other, sunglasses perched on her nose even though the cabin lighting was dim.

“Not bad, sweetheart,” she drawled, giving the plush leather a slow once-over. “Whisking me away on a private jet? You know, some women would kill for this kind of treatment.”

Rio raised an eyebrow, buckling her belt. “Good thing you already have enough stalkers trying to kill for you. No need to add more.”

Agatha gasped dramatically, pressing a hand to her chest. “You wound me. Here I thought you were trying to sweep me off my feet, and instead you’re just worried about logistics.”

Rio smirked faintly, glancing out the window. “This isn’t me sweeping you off your feet, Agatha. This is me getting you somewhere safe.”

“Safe,” Agatha repeated, leaning forward so her voice dipped lower, more teasing. “Funny, because every time I look at you, I feel like I’m in danger.”

Rio groaned, tipping her head back against the headrest. “You really can’t help yourself, can you?”

“Not when you sit there all stoic and broody in your suit,” Agatha purred, twirling her sunglasses in her hand. “Do you know how unfair it is? Tattoos peeking out of your cuffs, muscles under that shirt, and those eyes…” She let the words trail, clearly enjoying Rio’s slow flush.

Rio cleared her throat, leaning forward to grab a folder from her bag just to break eye contact. “I swear, you’re worse than Yelena with her knives.”

“Darling,” Agatha said with a grin, “the difference is I want to play with you, not stab you.”

Rio’s head snapped up, eyes wide, caught between scandalized and flustered. “Agatha.”

“What?!” Agatha laughed, throwing her head back. “Don’t look at me like that. I didn’t even say anything dirty this time. You just went there all on your own.”

Rio pinched the bridge of her nose, muttering something under her breath, which only made Agatha grin wider.

“You know, cariño,” Agatha said, stretching out like a cat, “I think I’m starting to enjoy these little trips. Just you, me, and miles of sky. No one to bother us. Endless possibilities.”

Rio gave her a long look, a mix of warning and fondness. “Endless trouble, more like.”

“Same thing,” Agatha quipped, raising her glass of water in mock salute before sinking back into her seat, a smirk still firmly in place.

For the first time in days, the air between them felt lighter, still charged, still simmering with things unsaid, but light all the same.

The rest of the plane ride was filled with laughter, sharp quips, and a cutthroat game of checkers that escalated far too quickly. Agatha, scowling at her imminent defeat, flipped the board with a dramatic flourish, red and black pieces scattering across the plush carpet.

Rio laughed—really laughed. It burst out of her in a way that startled Agatha, deep and unguarded, a sound that made the small cabin feel warmer. Agatha froze mid-smirk, her breath catching as she watched Rio’s head tip back, hair slipping over her shoulder, her sharp jawline cutting against the soft light overhead. For the first time since they met, Rio looked utterly relaxed, and Agatha couldn’t stop staring.

Five and a half hours slipped by faster than either expected. When the jet finally touched down, the runway was silent, the private airfield deserted save for a sleek black Lexus parked near the hangar. The pilots taxied them smoothly to a stop, and Rio rose first, thanking the crew and sliding them a tip with her usual quiet efficiency.

“Ready, hermosa?” she asked, extending a hand to Agatha.

“After watching you cheat at checkers for five hours? Barely,” Agatha teased, slipping her hand into Rio’s anyway. Her fingers lingered longer than necessary before she let go, descending the steps with a little bounce in her step.

The Massachusetts air was crisp and cool, carrying the faint scent of pine and lake water even here. Agatha inhaled deeply, stretching her arms like a cat. “It already feels like we’re in a different world,” she murmured.

Rio only hummed in agreement, leading her toward the waiting car. She opened the passenger side door for Agatha before loading their bags into the trunk. Agatha slid into the seat with a grin.

“Sweetheart,” she said, tapping the dashboard as Rio settled behind the wheel, “if this is just the car that takes us to your secret hideaway, I can only imagine how good the cabin looks.”

Rio smirked, starting the engine. “Patience. You’ll see soon enough.”

“Patience isn’t really my strong suit,” Agatha shot back, turning to watch the treeline blur as they pulled away from the airfield.

Rio glanced at her, lips twitching into something that wasn’t quite a smile but wasn’t far from it. “I’ve noticed.”

The drive wound through tall pines and quiet country roads, the air outside crisp and clean in a way only deep woods could manage. By the time Rio pulled the SUV to a stop, the sky was painted in streaks of soft pink and gold, fading into dusk.

“If I didn’t know any better, I’d think you didn’t want me to bask in my adoring coven.”

“Not when half of them might be holding cameras for the wrong reasons,” Rio countered, her eyes scanning every face in the crowd.

By the time they reached the SUV, Bucky had materialized from nowhere, a towering presence making the photographers take a cautious half-step back. He held the door open, and Rio all but guided Agatha inside before following, shutting it firmly behind them.

The second the locks clicked, the noise outside muffled to a dull roar. Agatha exhaled hard, leaning her head back against the leather seat. “God, I missed anonymity.”

“You handled it perfectly,” Rio said, settling beside her but still watching the windows, muscles tight. “No cracks, no tells. Exactly what we needed.”

Agatha cracked an eye open at her, a little smirk tugging her lips. “You know, most girlfriends would say, ‘You look beautiful, darling, even after a five-hour flight.’ But no. I get a field report.”

Rio’s jaw twitched. She hesitated, then reached over, brushing her thumb briefly against Agatha’s hand where it rested on her thigh. “You do look beautiful. Always.”

Agatha blinked, her smirk softening into something warmer. She squeezed Rio’s hand once, deliberately, before letting it go. “That’s better.”

Outside, the SUV cut through the mob, cameras still flashing until the gates closed behind them. The noise faded. The city loomed ahead.

And just like that, the bubble of the cabin was gone. Reality, with all its dangers and demands, had reclaimed them.

Agatha tilted her head against the window, watching the blur of lights. “Back to the real world, huh?”

Rio glanced at her reflection in the glass, voice quiet but steady. “Not exactly. You still have me.”

The SUV rolled to a stop in front of Agatha’s mansion. The house looked the same as when they’d left, towering glass, ivy creeping up dark stone, a fortress dressed as art. But to Agatha, it felt different now. Less like a sanctuary, more like a cage. Reality pressed in from all sides.

Rio cut the engine and glanced at her. “You ready, cariño?”

Agatha smirked, though the edge of exhaustion dulled it. “Do I look ready?”

“No,” Rio admitted, lips twitching. “But I’ve got you.”

That was enough to make Agatha unclench her jaw and nod. Together, they stepped out, greeted instantly by Natasha and Bucky flanking the door. Alice stood off to the side, tablet in hand, Yelena pacing like a wolf on a leash. Inside, Clint sat at the dining table, already nursing a cup of coffee like it was whiskey.

It felt like walking into a war room, except the war was her life.

Agatha had barely set her purse down before Jen came barreling down the hall, phone in one hand, notebook in the other. “Where the hell have you been?” she hissed. “Do you have any idea the nightmare you’ve dumped in my lap? The press is frothing. Fans think you’ve been kidnapped. Social media is split between #WhereIsAgatha and #Agathario, trending like wildfire. And don’t get me started on Jessica’s article. You’ve been silent for three days. I need quotes. I need angles. I need damage control.”

Agatha groaned, tossing her sunglasses onto the counter. “Hello to you, too, Jen. Missed you.”

“Don’t sass me, Agatha.” Jen jabbed her notebook at her like it was a weapon. “People are demanding a comment. You can’t just disappear after an exposé about stalkers and smear campaigns drops. It makes you look guilty or worse, detached.”

“Detached?” Agatha snorted. “Sweetheart, I’ve been many things. Detached is not one of them.”

“Then prove it!” Jen snapped. “We need to put out a statement by tonight. Even if it’s just you thanking fans for support and confirming you’re safe. Otherwise, the vultures will write the narrative for us.”

Rio stepped between them, voice calm but firm. “She just walked through the door. Let her breathe, Jen.”

Jen’s glare slid to Rio. “And you, don’t think you’re off the hook. Half of Twitter is thirsting over you like you’re some tattooed Greek goddess, the other half is digging up your military record and spinning conspiracy theories. I have journalists asking me if your scars mean you tortured people for fun.”

Rio’s jaw ticked. “Let them ask. I don’t answer to them.”

Agatha, sensing Rio’s tension, reached for her hand, grounding her with the smallest touch. The whole team noticed. Yelena’s eyes widened, Alice’s brows shot up, and Clint spat coffee halfway across the table.

“Wait a damn minute,” Clint coughed, wiping his chin. “Did I just see what I think I saw?”

Agatha smirked, threading her fingers through Rio’s. “Depends. Did you see me holding the hand of the sexiest, most infuriatingly professional woman alive? Then yes. You saw correctly.”

Natasha arched an eyebrow, voice flat. “You two finally fucked.”

Agatha’s grin widened, wicked as ever. “Oh, more than once, darling.”

Bucky groaned, dragging a hand down his face. Alice let out a little cheer, clapping her hands together. Yelena just grinned like a cat who’d caught a bird. “Finally,” she muttered. Money exchanged hands between the team

“You bet on us?” Agatha asked, smirking.

“Duh, easy money, honestly.” Yelena laughed.

Rio flushed scarlet, tugging at her collar. “You’re all insufferable.”

“You love us,” Alice teased. Then she smirked. “But not as much as you love her.”

Rio shot her a look sharp enough to cut steel, but Agatha only leaned against her side, clearly enjoying every second of the reveal. “Don’t worry, hot stuff,” she said sweetly. “They’ll get used to us. Eventually.”

“Us?” Natasha repeated, tone dry but curious.

Agatha turned, chin high, voice firm. “Yes. Us. We’re official. Girlfriends. Partners. Whatever label you like best. And before you all start groaning, let me be very clear: she makes me happy. That’s non-negotiable.”

For a moment, the room was silent. Then Clint muttered, “Guess the spray bottle won’t cut it anymore.”

That broke the tension. Laughter rippled through the room, even Rio’s mouth twitching at the corners.

Jen, however, remained unimpressed. She flipped her notebook shut with a snap. “That’s all very sweet, but relationships don’t stop headlines, Agatha. We need a statement tonight.”

Agatha sighed, finally sinking into a chair. “Fine. Draft something. But I want it in my voice, not yours. Fans will know the difference.”

“Done.” Jen scribbled a note. “But you’re filming tomorrow. No disappearing again. Not unless you want a full-blown media circus parked outside your house.”

“I already have a circus,” Agatha muttered, gesturing to the team.

Yelena threw a balled-up napkin at her. “You love us.”

Agatha winked. “Most of you.”

Rio finally sat beside her, their knees brushing. The noise of the room faded for a moment, the warmth of Agatha’s hand in hers enough to drown out the chaos. But she could still feel it pressing in, Jen’s demands, the world outside clawing at the gates, the knowledge that the stalkers weren’t done.

She leaned closer, whispering low enough only Rio could hear. “Feels like the cabin was a dream, doesn’t it?”

Rio squeezed her hand. “Then we hold onto it. Let them scream, let them dig. We know what’s real.”

Agatha turned to meet her eyes, and for a second, it was just them again. No cameras. No threats. No lies. Just two women who had finally stopped running from what they felt.

Jen’s voice cut back in, sharp as a whip. “Alright, Agatha. Press statement first. Then we talk about social media strategy. Then we prep you for interviews. And for God’s sake, put on a shirt that doesn’t make you look like you just rolled out of someone’s bed.”

Agatha smirked. “But I did.” She tilted her head toward Rio.

Clint choked again. Alice nearly fell off her chair laughing. Natasha muttered something in Russian that sounded suspiciously like a prayer for patience.

Rio buried her face in her hands. “I hate all of you.”

But when Agatha rested her head on Rio’s shoulder, her smirk softening into something almost tender, Rio let herself breathe. Just for a second.

The cabin might be gone. Reality might be loud, messy, and dangerous. But they had each other. And that, Rio thought, might just be enough.

Morning sunlight filtered weakly through the tinted windows of the compound, but the atmosphere inside was anything but calm. Jen stood at the head of the dining table, laptop open, glasses perched on her nose like a general ready for battle. A thick stack of printed notes and highlighted drafts sat in front of her.

“Alright, Agatha,” she began briskly, “we need to talk about your first official response to Jessica’s article. You’ve been radio silent for three days, and while the piece has done wonders at painting you as the victim of a targeted smear campaign, the press is circling like sharks over your disappearance. They want your voice on record.”

Agatha groaned theatrically, dropping into a chair and stealing Rio’s coffee like it belonged to her. “Good morning to you, too, sunshine.”

“This isn’t funny.” Jen’s tone sharpened, though her eyes flickered between Agatha and Rio with something suspiciously close to a smirk. “#WhereIsAgatha has been trending since last night. People are convinced you’ve either fled the country, entered rehab, or joined a cult. We need to get ahead of it before conspiracy TikTok decides you’ve been replaced by a clone.”

Across the table, Yelena choked on her juice. “A clone would behave better.”

Agatha ignored her, swiveling toward Jen. “Fine, read me your masterpiece. Let’s see what the world apparently needs to hear.”

Jen adjusted her glasses and cleared her throat. “In light of recent events and harmful fabrications, I want to thank my fans for their unwavering support. Jessica Jones’ reporting has been accurate, and I stand by her article fully. I have always treated my colleagues, my fans, and my crew with respect, and I will continue to do so. As for the rumors—”

Agatha raised a hand, cutting her off. “Respectful, heartfelt, professional… and boring. You’re stripping me of my personality.”

“You’re not allowed a personality when your career’s on the line,” Jen snapped back, though there was a note of fondness buried under the exasperation. “This has to be airtight, Agatha. No smirks. No sarcasm. No hot stuff.”

At that, the entire table glanced toward Rio, who shifted uncomfortably in her chair. Agatha, of course, only smiled wickedly and reached over to squeeze Rio’s thigh under the table.

Jen pinched the bridge of her nose. “God help me.”

Bucky leaned back in his chair, arms crossed. “She’s not wrong, though. If Agatha puts out something too polished, it won’t sound like her. The fans who know her best will smell PR spin.”

“Exactly,” Agatha said, pointing at him like he’d just handed her the Holy Grail. “See? Even grumpy over here agrees with me.”

“I’m not grumpy,” Bucky muttered, though the corner of his mouth twitched.

Natasha sipped her coffee, unimpressed. “She has a point, Jen. Agatha’s reputation has always been tied to being brutally herself. If you take that away, the stalkers win. They get to rewrite who she is.”

Jen sighed, clearly outnumbered, though she wasn’t ready to fold. “Fine. Then what do you suggest? You can’t exactly tweet, ‘I’m innocent, screw you haters,’ and expect the world to forgive and forget.”

“Oh, but imagine the headline,” Agatha said with a wicked grin. “America’s Witch Tells World to Screw Off.”

Clint actually choked on his coffee. Yelena pounded him on the back while wheezing with laughter.

Rio finally stepped in, her voice calm but firm. “We need balance. Agatha, you can’t lose your voice, but Jen’s right, this isn’t the time for jokes. What if we keep the tone genuine, but add something personal at the end? A line that reminds people you’re human. Something only you would say.”

Agatha turned to her, eyes softening just slightly. “Like what?”

Rio shrugged, fingers brushing Agatha’s hand under the table in a grounding gesture. “Something simple. Like how much you appreciate the fans who stuck by you. Or how much it means to have people in your corner right now.”

The room went quiet for a moment, the weight of Rio’s words sinking in. Agatha’s smirk melted into something more thoughtful, and she squeezed Rio’s hand. “I like that,” she said softly.

Alice, who’d been typing away, finally looked up with a grin. “Wow. She listens to you. Noted.”

Agatha narrowed her eyes at her but didn’t let go of Rio’s hand. “Careful, Alice. I know where you sleep.”

“Please,” Yelena scoffed. “You’d get lost trying to sneak into her room.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but the tension at the table eased as Jen sighed and shut her laptop. “Alright, we’ll draft something that threads the needle, your voice, your tone, but professional enough to keep the wolves at bay. And we’ll schedule a brief, tightly controlled press Q&A in a few days. No surprises, no ad-libbing. Understood?”

Agatha made a face but nodded. “Understood, boss.”

“Good.” Jen started stacking her papers, muttering, “Though I still say clones would be easier.”

Official Statement from Agatha Harkness

Over the past few days, a series of false claims, doctored videos, and fabricated accounts have circulated about me. I want to be absolutely clear: these stories are untrue.

In my nearly forty years working in this industry, I have treated every cast member, crew member, and fan I’ve encountered with respect. I take pride in the relationships I’ve built on set and with the people who support my work. I would never jeopardize those relationships by engaging in the behavior that’s being alleged.

As confirmed by journalist Jessica Jones in her recent investigation, the so-called “evidence” being shared online is fabricated, including deepfake videos and false testimonies. These tactics are harmful not just to me, but to everyone who has ever been the victim of targeted harassment online.

To my fans—my Coven—you’ve been my constant source of strength and joy. I see you, I hear you, and I am endlessly grateful for your love and loyalty. Thank you for standing by me through this noise. You’ve always been my corner, and I promise I’ll always stand in yours.

I will not be giving the individuals behind this campaign the attention they’re seeking. My focus remains where it belongs—on my craft, my projects, and on the people who truly matter.

With love and gratitude,

Agatha Harkness
