The following month was hectic. Paparazzi and media attention were still at an all-time high, and fan speculation ran rampant, especially about Agatha and Rio’s relationship. The two kept things strictly professional in public, or as professional as Agatha was capable of being. Behind closed doors, however, their relationship had only grown stronger. Rio had taken to sleeping in Agatha’s room whenever she wasn’t on shift, and the two managed to steal private moments whenever they could.

Agatha’s filming schedule had finally kicked off, grueling as ever, but the stalkers had remained hidden. No further moves, no close calls. Still, Rio knew it was only a matter of time before they resurfaced.

Alice had been working tirelessly, tracking every lead she could get her hands on. Natasha had slipped away for a few days to meet with a contact in hopes of digging up more information on Raven. Meanwhile, Bucky was leaning on his old networks, speaking to contacts across the globe to gather intel on the group’s movements.

Now, the entire team and Agatha sat gathered around the dining room table, papers and laptops spread out across the surface as they prepared to go over the new information they had collected.

The dining room table was no longer recognizable as a place for meals. It was buried beneath papers, laptops, photographs, and maps covered in inked lines; the chaos was contained only by the focused energy of the people surrounding it. Coffee mugs, some full, most empty, marked the hours of work already poured into this war room.

Rio stood at the head of the table, hands braced against the wood, posture sharp and commanding. Around her sat the team: Natasha, relaxed but hawk-eyed; Bucky, glued to the coffee pot; Clint leaning in the corner with arms folded; Yelena twirling her knife with restless ease; Alice hunched over her laptop, scrolling through feeds at lightning pace. Jen perched at the far end with her phone buzzing nonstop, while Agatha sat beside Rio, tense, her usually unshakable bravado nowhere to be seen.

Alice finally broke the silence, her voice clear despite the fatigue etched into her features. “Alright. Here’s what we’ve pieced together.” She spun her laptop to face the group. The screen lit up with a symbol: a cicada, stylized and jagged.

“This image showed up buried in every breach of Agatha’s old security system. It’s their digital signature.”

Agatha’s brow furrowed. “Why a cicada?”

“Because cicadas are impossible to ignore,” Alice explained. “They’re loud. They disappear, then return. They’re announcing themselves every time they infiltrate. Which means this wasn’t random, it was deliberate. They wanted us to know it was them.”

Rio’s jaw flexed. “Them?”

Alice nodded. “Kyra Auden. Confirmed. I was able to track her IP address back to her, even though she is very good at covering her tracks. And I’m ninety percent certain her sister, Seren Auden, is the second hacker. I tracked them through old stan accounts and fan projects from years ago. They ran massive campaigns to promote Agatha’s early work. One of those campaigns went viral; you even acknowledged them once, Agatha. Retweeted them. Thanked them. And then…”

Agatha’s stomach twisted. “…And then I moved on. Didn’t engage again.”

“Exactly,” Alice said. “They built a fantasy where they ‘made you.’ When you stopped feeding that fantasy, they felt abandoned. Betrayed. And now they’re rewriting the story so you owe them.”

Natasha leaned forward, voice steady. “So we have two hackers, sisters, motivated by obsession and parasocial behavior. What about money?”

Alice pulled up another document: bank records. “Ralph Bohner, the shooter, wasn’t freelance. He was being paid through an offshore account opened right before the stalking started. The money traces back to an organization calling itself The Seventh Veil.”

The name dropped like a stone into the silence.

Bucky frowned. “Sounds like a shell org. A front for someone with serious reach.”

“Or a cult,” Yelena muttered, spinning her knife. “The name screams cult.”

Alice shrugged. “Could be either. But whoever it is, they’re funding everything: gear, payoffs, Ralph’s involvement. They’re not amateurs.”

Rio straightened. “The enforcer?”

“Still nameless,” Alice admitted. “But we can trace their work. Every time someone became a liability, they turned up dead. Ralph wasn’t the first. The pattern’s too clean.”

Before the weight of that could settle, Jen glanced up from her buzzing phone. “What about the smear campaign? The ‘difficult to work with’ stories, the fake video?”

“That wasn’t the Cicadas,” Alice said firmly. “It doesn’t match their signature. That was Renna.”

Agatha stiffened at the name.

“Renna ran your biggest stan Twitter back in the day,” Alice explained gently. “When you rejected her, when you refused to cross that line, she twisted it into humiliation. She’s weaponizing PR now, hitting the one place she knows will hurt most: your reputation. The timing lines up, too. The smear only started once the other moves escalated.”

Agatha swallowed hard. Her voice cracked despite her best effort to keep it sharp. “She was underage when I first met her. I would never. And years later, when she was older, she tried again. I told her no. That’s all it took? To turn her into this?”

“Obsession doesn’t need much,” Natasha said simply.

“And Raven?” Rio pressed.

Alice clicked through another folder: a grainy still of Agatha’s old assistant, Raven Corvin. “We don’t know her role yet. But her connection is too obvious to ignore. She’s been quiet, but too quiet. My gut says she’s in the mix. We just don’t know where.”

Clint’s brow furrowed. “And the others? We know there’s more.”

Alice nodded reluctantly. “At least two. Maybe more. First: the Watcher. Someone is shadowing Agatha in public. Always at a distance. Always blending into the background. I’ve spotted them in multiple fan photos and paparazzi shots, but haven’t gotten a clear enough photo to run through facial recognition software. They’re cataloguing her every move, feeding intel back to the group.

Second: the Infiltrator. Whoever broke into Agatha’s trailer and sabotaged the light clasp had direct access. Calm, methodical. No panic. This wasn’t a crime of opportunity. It was surgical. Whoever they are, they can get close. Very close.”

The words sat heavily over the table.

“So,” Clint summarized, voice clipped, “we’ve got: the Cicada sisters hacking cameras, Renna running PR sabotage, Ralph dead but connected, an enforcer cleaning house, Raven lurking somewhere in the background, a Watcher tailing Agatha, an Infiltrator breaking into her space, and a mastermind funding it all under The Seventh Veil.”

“That’s the picture,” Alice said grimly.

The words seemed to echo around the table. Agatha pushed back suddenly, standing too quickly. Her hands trembled as she braced them on the back of her chair, staring down at the wood like it might give her answers. “All of this because I didn’t retweet someone? Because I told a girl no? Because I fired an assistant who was stealing from me?”

Her voice rose, breaking under the pressure. “I have worked my ass off my whole life, and now what? A group of bitter, obsessed nobodies who think they can own me? That they can destroy me because I didn’t give them enough attention?!”

The team stayed quiet, the storm in her voice crashing through the room.

Agatha’s breath hitched. “I can’t—” Her voice broke completely. “I can’t keep waiting for the next attack. For the next lie. For the next body in the street. I can’t…”

Rio was already moving. She came up behind Agatha, steady hands reaching for hers, gently prying them from the chair. She turned Agatha toward her, their eyes locking.

“You won’t,” Rio said, voice low and unyielding. “Because you’re not alone. Not anymore. We’ll find them. Every last one. And when we do—” Her jaw tightened. “They’ll regret ever thinking they could touch you.”

Agatha let herself collapse against Rio, her forehead pressing into her shoulder, silent tears spilling down her cheeks. For the first time in weeks, she let herself break.

Rio’s arms closed around her like armor. Strong. Steady. Unshakable.

And though the room was still heavy with danger, for that moment, for Agatha, it was enough.

Agatha had excused herself upstairs to wash her face and breathe, leaving the team in the dining room. The quiet that followed her absence was heavy, but Rio knew they couldn’t afford to sit in silence.

“Alright,” she said firmly, reclaiming the head of the table. “We’ve identified the players. Now we focus on containment and counteraction.”

Alice straightened, already pulling up files. “Priority one is the Watcher. If someone’s tailing Agatha in public, we can catch them. I’ll set up facial-recognition alerts tied to every paparazzi and fan photo uploaded in real-time. If they’re in the crowd, we’ll know.”

“Yelena and I will take point in the field,” Natasha added. “We’ll shadow Agatha from a distance, spot anyone who shadows too close. If we find our Watcher, we’ll bring them in alive. They’ll talk.”

Bucky set down his mug. “That leaves the Infiltrator. Someone with access and nerves of steel. Could be crew. It could be someone bribed to get close. I’ll work my contacts, see if anyone’s selling passes or IDs.”

Clint nodded. “I’ll cover the catwalks and rooftops again. If someone tries another stunt, I’ll see them before they get the chance.”

Alice tapped a new tab open. “The Cicadas are sloppy in one way: they want credit. I’m going to bait them. Set up fake systems with Agatha’s name plastered all over them, see if they bite. Once they leave their signature, I can triangulate their location.”

“And Raven?” Natasha asked.

“Leave her to me,” Rio said, her voice flat and deadly calm. “She’s close enough to hurt us, but she won’t see me coming. When we find her, we’ll know her role.”

The team exchanged glances, grim, but unified.

Jen finally broke the silence, her voice softer than usual. “And what about Agatha?”

Rio looked toward the stairs, jaw firm. “We keep her safe. We give her enough space to breathe so she doesn’t feel like a prisoner, but not one of these bastards gets within ten feet of her. She’s our client, and she’s mine to protect.”

The finality in her tone left no room for argument.

 

A week later, Agatha was scheduled for a sit-down on The Late Night Spotlight with Peter Parker, a man known for his boyish charm and sometimes awkward delivery, but also for his genuine warmth and respect toward his guests. Agatha had always thought highly of him, even privately telling Jen she hoped he’d have a long career in Hollywood.

When the SUV pulled up to the studio, the sound of screaming fans was immediate. Jen and Billy got out first, ushered by security, while the wall of voices swelled around them. Fans pushed and shoved against the barricades, desperate for a glimpse of their favorite star. Some shouted Agatha’s name, others thrust posters and phones into the air, hoping for an autograph or selfie. Paparazzi were already shouting over one another, hurling incomprehensible questions while flashes went off in staccato bursts.

Bucky, Natasha, and Clint moved like a shield, pushing the crowd back with disciplined precision. Yelena had already melted into the mass of people, her eyes constantly scanning for any sign of the Watcher. Inside the building, Alice monitored security feeds, ready to intercept anything suspicious.

Inside the SUV, Rio’s gaze never left the scene outside. “As usual,” she reminded, her voice clipped, “no photos, no autographs, no stopping.”

Agatha’s hand shot out, resting over Rio’s arm before she could reach for the door handle. “No,” she said firmly. “I have to stop this time.”

Rio turned to her, sharp. “Agatha—”

Agatha shook her head, cutting her off. “I haven’t stopped for fans in weeks. Not since the smear campaign. They need to know I still love them, that I appreciate them. Hiding away just feeds into the lies. I need to give back, even if it’s just for a minute. Sign some things. Take a few pictures.”

Her tone left no room for doubt. This wasn’t a whim; it was something Agatha had decided long before the SUV pulled up to the studio.

Rio studied her eyes, saw the determination there, and knew the battle was already lost. With a sigh, she relented. “Fine. But only a few. And if I tell you it’s time to move, you move. No questions. Understood?”

Agatha’s smile softened some of the tension in the car. “Understood. I promise.”

She leaned in then, a quick impulse, lips tilting toward Rio’s for a kiss. But Rio drew back at the last second, her expression torn.

Agatha froze, hurt flickering across her face. “What—?”

“Not here, cariño. Not now.” Rio’s voice was low, almost apologetic, and the guilt in her eyes was unmistakable.

For a moment, Agatha just looked at her, a storm brewing in her expression. She hated hiding. She hated having to keep this part of them locked away. But she also understood the stakes and the risks. After a beat, she only sighed, glare fading into resignation. With a short nod, she gestured toward the door. “Then let’s get it over with.”

Rio wanted to say more, to reach out and fix the sharp edges she’d left in Agatha’s expression, but it wasn’t the time. Instead, she lifted her radio. “Change of plans. Harkness wants to stop for autographs. Keep formation, eyes sharp.”

One by one, the team’s acknowledgments crackled back through her earpiece.

Rio squared her shoulders, mask of control sliding back into place, and finally opened the SUV door.

The moment Agatha’s heels clicked against the pavement, the crowd erupted. Cheers, screams, and the crackle of camera shutters swelled into a wall of sound that nearly drowned out the hum of the city. Fans surged forward against the barricades, security holding firm as voices rose in a chorus of her name.

“Agatha! Over here!”
 “Please sign this, I love you!”
 “Mother, we adore you!”

Agatha plastered on her signature smile, that dazzling, magnetic grin that had charmed audiences for decades. But to Rio, who never let herself drift more than two steps away, the expression looked heavier than usual, as though Agatha was holding her mask firmly in place for the sake of the people who adored her.

Bucky flanked her left side, a towering wall of muscle that kept anyone from reaching too close. Natasha had positioned herself slightly ahead, her sharp eyes scanning every outstretched hand, every shifting figure. Clint had his long lens raised, not for glamour shots but for surveillance, photographing faces in the crowd to be run through Alice’s system later.

Agatha crouched slightly at the barricade, signing a glossy still from Agnes of Westview, then another from her early career. A young fan, trembling with excitement, asked for a selfie, and Agatha leaned in without hesitation, holding the girl’s phone steady and flashing a wink into the camera. The girl burst into tears, clutching the device to her chest as though it were a treasure.

Rio’s jaw clenched, her gaze never leaving the shifting tide of bodies. She could feel Yelena in the crowd, moving like smoke, brushing past fans with the casualness of someone who belonged, yet her hand was always near her blade. In Rio’s ear, Alice’s calm voice threaded through the noise:

“Nothing yet on cameras. The crowd’s excitable but clean so far.”

A paparazzo elbowed his way forward, shouting, “Agatha, is Rio your new girlfriend?”

Agatha’s head snapped up, sunglasses sliding slightly down her nose. Her smile didn’t falter, but her eyes hardened, cool as ice. “The only woman in my life right now is Wanda Maximoff,” she quipped, earning a laugh from the fans who caught the inside joke. She winked, pivoting effortlessly back to another autograph, but Rio noticed her grip on the pen tightened just slightly.

Rio stepped closer, her voice low but firm in Agatha’s ear. “Three more, then we move.”

Agatha nodded without argument, though her grin widened at the little boy holding out a handmade poster with “We love you Agatha!” scrawled in crayon. She crouched to his level, signed the paper with a flourish, and whispered something that made the boy beam as though he’d just been handed the world.

The third autograph went to a woman in her forties holding an old, battered VHS of one of Agatha’s first films. Agatha’s laugh rang out, genuine this time, as she signed the worn sleeve. “You’ve been holding onto this longer than I’ve held onto my self-respect,” she teased, and the woman laughed along with her.

Then Rio’s voice cut through again, steel in her tone. “Time’s up. We move.”

Natasha and Bucky closed ranks immediately, gently but firmly steering Agatha away from the barricade. Clint barked a sharp “Let’s go!” into his comm as Yelena peeled back from the crowd, slipping into formation seamlessly.

The disappointed groans of fans followed them, mixed with shouted “We love you!” and the endless staccato of camera shutters. Agatha waved one last time before slipping into the studio doors.

Once they were inside, the noise muffled behind the walls. Agatha leaned against the cool marble of the hallway and exhaled. For a heartbeat, the mask dropped, and Rio saw the exhaustion in her eyes, the faint tremor in her hand from the adrenaline.

“You okay?” Rio asked, her voice softer now.

Agatha nodded, forcing a smile back into place. “Better than okay. Did you see their faces? They needed that.”

Rio’s lips pressed into a thin line, torn between pride and frustration. “And you almost gave me a heart attack.”

Agatha smirked, slipping her sunglasses back into place. “Welcome to being in a relationship with me, darling.”

The house band wrapped a breezy riff as the stage lights warmed to a soft gold. Peter Parker jogged to his desk with that familiar mix of boyish enthusiasm and easy calm, then turned to the curtain with a grin.

“Ladies and gentlemen, please welcome—Academy Award winner, television icon, America’s favorite witch—Agatha Harkness!”

The audience roared as Agatha strode out in a tailored black suit with a silk lapel and a glinting amethyst ring, waving with easy charm. She crossed the stage, hugged Peter quickly, and settled into the chair opposite him. Her smile was dazzling but relaxed, her leg crossing effortlessly, the picture of composure.

“You look incredible. I feel underdressed, and this is my show,” Peter joked.

“Peter, please. We both know you were born in a suit,” Agatha fired back, then added with a grin, “The tie is excellent, though. Very ‘I pay my taxes on time.’”

The audience burst out laughing. Peter clutched his chest like he’d been mortally wounded, and Rio, watching from the shadows just beyond the cameras, shook her head faintly. She’d been with Agatha long enough now to know this was her in her element, razor sharp, charming, and just dangerous enough. Still, Rio couldn’t stop the ghost of a smile tugging at her mouth.

Peter grinned. “I try! Okay, we’ve got a lot to talk about. The new movie, a certain co-star, the internet being…the internet. But first, how are you?”

“I’m good,” Agatha said, her tone playful but warm. “Busy, grateful, caffeinated. In that order.”

“The holy trinity. Let’s start with Coven of Chaos. Fans are feral, respectfully feral for this project. What can you tell us?”

“That it exists.”

The audience howled, and Peter dropped his head into his hands. Rio, arms folded across her chest just offstage, allowed herself a soft exhale of amusement. Agatha always had a way of turning any question into a performance.

“Okay, here’s what I can say,” Agatha continued, her voice turning rich and animated. “It’s intimate but epic. It’s about power, who holds it, who’s afraid of it, and what happens when you refuse to apologize for it. There’s folklore in its bones and found family at its heart. And the action sequences? Absolutely bonkers. Like, please stretch before watching bonkers.”

Rio glanced around the studio, noting every exit and scanning the crowd, but her eyes flicked back to Agatha more often than she’d admit. She wasn’t just watching for threats.

Peter leaned forward. “You’re working with Wanda Maximoff again. Your chemistry together is legendary. What keeps bringing you back together?”

Agatha’s smile softened. “Trust. We met decades ago when we were both young. We looked out for each other, and we built a language. On camera, I can say, ‘Try it,’ and she jumps without asking how high. Wanda is generous and terrifying in the best actor way, she raises the stakes and somehow makes you feel safe. It’s rare. I don’t take it for granted.”

The conversation rolled on, warm and witty, until Peter finally steered toward the subject Rio had been bracing for. He lifted a card that read, “Agatha, blink twice if you’re dating your bodyguard.”

The crowd erupted. Agatha smirked and blinked…once.

“Peter, dear, I blink when I breathe.”

The audience roared. Peter grinned like a cat, but Rio’s spine went taut. She fought the urge to roll her eyes when Agatha’s gaze darted offstage and caught hers. Rio gave the smallest shake of her head, subtle enough that the cameras would never catch it. Agatha only tilted her head, lips quirking like she’d won a game no one else was playing.

Peter pressed on. “So, dating rumors. You and your head of security have been photographed together frequently. And, of course, there was a certain photoshoot that broke several servers and, allegedly, three marriages.”

“I plead attractive,” Agatha deadpanned, smirking.

The laughter was deafening. Rio shifted her weight, jaw tight. She could feel the heat creeping up her neck even though no one was looking at her. She wasn’t built for this kind of spotlight, and Agatha, wicked creature that she was, knew it.

Peter laughed along with the crowd. “Has the…reaction to your security team surprised you?”

Agatha leaned in, the teasing fading to sincerity. “Honestly? Yes and no. They’re absurdly competent and, infuriatingly, even better looking in person. But here’s the thing: internet thirst is fun, often hilarious, but these are professionals with huge responsibilities. I’m lucky to have them. I also want them to be safe and respected, not treated like props in my life.”

Rio’s throat tightened at that. Agatha didn’t just throw compliments around. The honesty in her voice left Rio both humbled and unsettled, and she shifted her eyes away before anyone could read too much in them.

The conversation flowed from there, boundaries, privacy, Jessica Jones’ article, and the smear campaign that nearly derailed everything. Agatha answered each question with equal parts wit and vulnerability, and the audience lapped it up. By the time Peter steered the interview toward a closing game of Spill Your Guts or Fill Your Guts, the crowd was fully under Agatha’s spell.

But Rio wasn’t watching the audience. She was watching Agatha. Watching the little tells in her posture, the way her smile dimmed for a heartbeat when Jessica’s name was mentioned, the way she snuck those glances toward the wings where Rio stood. And in those fleeting looks, Rio saw it: the anchor Agatha had started to use her for, steady in a storm of lights and noise.

Rio didn’t let herself smile, but the warmth in her chest was impossible to ignore.

Peter grinned as stagehands wheeled out a sleek black cart with silver platters on top. The audience broke into laughter and applause before the lids even came off.

“Ladies and gentlemen,” Peter announced, “it’s time for Spill Your Guts or Fill Your Guts.”

The crowd cheered. The band played a mischievous little riff. Agatha leaned back in her chair, crossing her legs like a queen settling into her throne.

“Oh, darling,” she drawled, smirking at Peter, “you don’t know what you’ve signed up for.”

“I think I do,” Peter said nervously, lifting one lid. The audience gasped as a plate of pickled pig’s feet was revealed. Another lid revealed something gloopy and unidentifiable, the third, fermented shark.

Agatha arched a brow. “Is this a game or a war crime?”

The crowd howled. Even Rio, lurking just beyond the curtain with her earpiece in, fought back a snort. She’d seen Agatha take down senators in interviews; fermented fish didn’t stand a chance. Still, Rio crossed her arms and braced herself. With Agatha, anything could happen.

Peter clasped his hands. “Alright, Agatha, you know the rules. Answer honestly, or take a bite.”

Agatha leaned forward, chin propped on her hand. “Ask me anything, Parker. I have no shame.”

Peter grinned, checking his cards. “Okay. First question: Which of your Coven of Chaos co-stars is most likely to break character during a serious scene?”

Agatha barked out a laugh. “Wanda. Absolutely Wanda.”

The crowd roared.

“Really?” Peter asked, surprised.

“She looks all mysterious and composed, but the woman cannot keep it together if I even twitch an eyebrow. And then, of course, I laugh, and then we ruin the take. Millions of dollars down the drain.”

Rio smirked faintly from the wings. She’d already heard Wanda’s name a hundred times in Agatha’s stories, but hearing it with that warm affection made her chest squeeze.

Peter grinned wickedly. “Alright. Next question…Rank your security team, from most to least likely to sleep with.”

The audience screamed. Agatha threw her head back and laughed, delighted. Rio froze, pulse spiking.

“Oh, Parker, you’re cruel.”

“Answer or eat the shark,” Peter teased.

Agatha pretended to deliberate, twirling a strand of hair. Then she leaned toward the mic, eyes sparkling. “Number one, obviously, is Rio.”

The crowd erupted. Cameras panned immediately toward the wings, catching Rio just as she schooled her expression into flat professionalism. Her ears burned scarlet.

Agatha wasn’t done. “Two, Natasha, discipline is sexy. Three, Yelena, chaotic, but I bet she knows what she’s doing. Four, Alice, underrated, but I sense potential. Five, Bucky, he broods too much, and is a man. Six, Clint…darling, he’s like a brother to me, so it would feel like incest. Sorry, Clint.”

The audience was losing it. Peter nearly fell out of his chair. “You actually did it, you ranked them all!”

“Of course I did,” Agatha said smugly, brushing imaginary dust off her lapel. “I told you, I have no shame.”

Backstage, Clint’s voice came dry over comms: “I didn’t need to hear that.” Yelena’s laugh followed: “I did.” Rio pinched the bridge of her nose. She was already imagining the memes.

Peter wiped tears from his eyes. “Okay, okay. Next question: Who’s one Hollywood star you swore you’d never work with again?”

Agatha’s smile sharpened, but she answered without hesitation. “Tony Stark.”

Gasps rolled through the crowd.

“Yeah, I said it,” Agatha continued. “He showed up late every day, treated the crew like garbage, and once called me ‘sweetheart’ in a tone that made me want to set him on fire. I don’t care if it tanks my career, I’d rather do dinner theater in Des Moines than ever share a set with him again.”

The audience exploded. Peter was wheezing with laughter. Rio just shook her head. This woman…

Peter leaned closer, a mischievous glint in his eyes. “Be honest, how much of the Jessica Jones article did you have to edit before it went public?”

Agatha laughed. “None. I didn’t touch a word. Jessica has a spine of steel, and she doesn’t need me to hold her hand. She did her job the way it should be done.”

The crowd cheered. Rio’s shoulders relaxed a little at that. She’d seen how much Jessica’s work had meant to Agatha, how it steadied her when things felt like they were spiraling. Hearing her affirm it so openly made Rio’s chest ache with pride.

Then Alice’s voice cut sharp into Rio’s ear: “Rio. We’ve got a problem.”

Rio stiffened immediately, posture snapping to attention. “Go.”

“Cicada. They’re inside the feed. I’m fighting to block them, but they’ve breached the overlays. They’re about to—”

The studio screens flickered. The laughter died instantly. On the massive monitors behind Peter’s desk, the broadcast jumped from the studio feed to a series of still images.

Rio’s blood ran cold.

The first was a private shot of Agatha, half-dressed in a trailer, clearly changing. Gasps erupted from the audience. More photos of Agatha in various states of undress. Peter spun around, horrified.

The next image was Wanda, candid and unguarded, at a dinner table. Then Jen in her office. Lilia at her home. Then, worst of all, files, documents, and data scrolling too fast to read, but undeniably personal. Pictures of Rio’s Delta team showed on screen, unblurred photos of the scene of the massacre, their dead bodies.

The audience buzzed in shock, confused murmurs rising like a wave.

Agatha froze in her chair, the blood draining from her face. For the first time all night, she wasn’t the composed star. She was just…exposed.

Rio didn’t hesitate. She strode onto the stage, ignoring the cameras, ignoring the audience, her focus entirely on Agatha. She put a hand on her shoulder, steady, grounding. “With me. Now.”

Peter, pale, fumbled at his earpiece, signaling producers. The crew scrambled, trying to cut the feed, but the images kept cycling, violations, invasions, every frame a taunt.

Rio leaned down, her voice low but firm. “Don’t look at the screens. Eyes on me.”

Agatha’s gaze darted to her, trembling on the edge of panic. Rio held it steady, a tether in the storm.

“Alice!” Rio barked into her comm.

“Almost, hold, got it!” Alice’s voice cracked through, and suddenly the screens went black. The studio lights buzzed, the silence deafening.

Then the feed returned to Peter’s show logo, the crisis smoothed over, but the damage was done.

The audience sat stunned, whispers ricocheting through the space. Peter looked stricken, already shifting into damage-control mode with his producers.

Agatha, still seated, pressed a hand to her mouth. For the first time in decades, she looked small on a stage.

Rio crouched in front of her, blocking the audience’s view as much as she could. Her voice was soft, but unyielding. “You’re safe. They didn’t win. Breathe, cariño. Just breathe.”

Agatha’s hand found Rio’s wrist, clutching it hard enough to bruise. “They showed Wanda…Jen…Lilia…You!”

Rio’s jaw clenched. Fury roared inside her chest like a wildfire, but her voice stayed calm. “And we’ll make them pay for it. But right now, we get you out.”

Agatha nodded shakily, letting Rio guide her up. The crowd didn’t matter anymore. The cameras didn’t matter. All that mattered was getting Agatha out of the spotlight before the cracks in her mask could break wide open.

Behind the scenes, Alice’s voice came back into comms, ragged but resolute. “I traced the breach. It was definitely Cicada. They wanted this spectacle—they wanted humiliation.”

“And I’ve got a trace, their signal is inside the building.” Alice’s voice snapped through the comms.

Rio didn’t hesitate. She stepped fully into the lights, placing herself in front of Agatha as the audience murmured, cameras still rolling and catching every second. “Locations, Alice.”

Natasha was already moving, boots hitting the stage with purpose as she came to flank Rio, one hand hovering near her concealed holster, eyes sweeping for angles and exits.

“I’m pushing photos to your phones now,” Alice said. “Running live face match on the crowd and backstage.”

A beat. Then Alice again, voice tight. “Got Kyra. Audience left side, aisle seat, eighth row. Black shirt, black pants.”

“Moving,” Bucky said over comms.

Yelena was a blur up the steps, Bucky right behind her. The crowd, stunned into silence moments ago, split on instinct at the sight of two armed professionals storming the aisle with intent written all over their faces. In the eighth row, a woman jerked to her feet as if shocked—Kyra. She hesitated one half-second too long, then bolted up the stairs.

“Clint?” Rio said.

“On it.” From the balcony above, Clint jumped down and planted himself at the top landing, blocking Kyra’s escape route. She pivoted, panicked, and tried to shoulder through the audience, shoving bodies with wild, flailing elbows. The crowd shouted, boxed her in, slowed her.

Yelena caught her by the wrist, pivoted, and used Kyra’s own momentum to slam her flat onto the carpet. A knee to the sternum, a wrist lock, clean, controlled, efficient. Bucky dropped to a crouch and zip-tied both of Kyra’s wrists behind her back before she could twist free. She screamed curses, the words dissolving into spit and fury. Phones were out everywhere now, dozens of angles capturing a hacker’s nightmare ending.

Onstage, Rio and Natasha were already moving. “We’re done here,” Rio murmured to Agatha, voice calm but iron-backed. “With me.” She and Nat shepherded her off the stage-left exit into a backstage corridor. Alice fell in behind, weapon out, slicing a hard look at every door they passed.

“I still can’t find Seren. Assume she’s on-site and waiting.” Alice warned.

Agatha didn’t resist being pulled along. Her face was pale, her eyes glassy, shock tightening her breathing. The images on the monitors, herself half-dressed, Wanda at dinner, Jen and Lilia in their homes, were stamped across her thoughts like a brand.

They hit the side door. Outside, the loading bay had already become a scrum. Paparazzi, tipped off by the live on-air chaos, had swarmed the alley. Flashes exploded. Voices layered over each other, feral, hungry.

“There she is! Agatha, look here—”

“Is it true your security—”

“Who leaked the—”

One of them lunged too close to Agatha, the camera practically in her face. Rio ripped it from his hands and slammed it lens-first into the concrete. The crack was a gunshot. The crowd startled backward a step.

“Back up,” Natasha barked, voice like a whipcrack. She and Alice pushed the press line away with controlled force, bodies forming a wedge. “Back up. Now.”

They drove a narrow corridor through the chaos to the SUVs. Rio yanked open the rear door and guided Agatha inside, then slid in after her and slammed it shut. The car became a sanctuary of steel and leather and quick breaths. Outside, Natasha shoved the last of the cameras back, circled to the front, and dove into the passenger seat. Alice dropped behind the wheel.

“Go,” Rio said.

The tires squealed, then found purchase. The SUV shot forward, leaving shouts and flashes bleeding into the distance.

“Status,” Rio said into her mic, one arm wrapped protectively around Agatha’s shoulders.

“Kyra secured,” Bucky reported, breath a touch elevated but steady. Sirens wailed faintly in the background of his feed. “Yelena and I are exfiltrating her to a secondary site for questioning. Clint’s tailing in case Seren pops, and will escort Jen and Billy. Nat, send me the nearest clean room.”

“Sending coordinates,” Natasha said, already tapping into the shared map.

Alice took the next turn hard. “I’ve scrubbed the broadcast for replay. We killed their feed mid-cycle; not everything made air, but enough. Cicada wanted humiliation and chaos, classic signature. I’ve pulled what I can, but copies will be floating.”

Agatha stared down at her shaking hands as if they belonged to someone else. “They showed Wanda,” she whispered. “And Jen. And Lilia. That was my bedroom. They showed your dead team!” Her voice cracked, shuddering on the last word.

Rio tightened her hold. “I know.” She pitched her voice low, steady as bedrock. “I’m here. They didn’t get you now. They won’t get you again.”

Agatha swallowed hard and dragged her gaze up to meet Rio’s. “I can’t, if they hurt any of them—”

“They won’t,” Rio said, firm. “We’re already moving.”

Silence for a few breaths. The city flickered by in streaks of light. Agatha leaned into Rio, letting herself be held. The tremor in her fingers softened, not gone, but contained.

“Bucky,” Rio said, professional mask sliding back into place. “Keep Kyra breathing and talking. No cowboy moves. We do this clean.”

Bucky snorted softly. “Copy. I’ll save the cowboy for the encore.”

“Yelena?” Rio asked.

“Kyra is loud,” Yelena said dryly, fabric rustling as she adjusted a gag in Kyra’s mouth. “But zip ties are louder. We will make her sing.”

“Clint, any eyes on Seren?” Rio pressed.

“Negative so far,” Clint replied. “I’ve got the east exit and a rooftop view. If she moves, I’ll see it.”

Alice checked the rearview, jaw set. “I’m scrubbing entry logs for staff and guests. If Seren badged in or piggybacked, I’ll find the trace. Also, cross-referencing faces that avoided every camera sightline, classic ghosting behavior.”

“Good,” Rio said. “We pivot the op right now. Priority one, Agatha’s home. We switch vehicles twice, enter via the south gate. Nat, call Sonya and Steve—tight lock. No one in or out without your voice or mine.”

“Already done,” Natasha said, phone to her ear, efficient and calm.

Agatha exhaled slowly, the world still too loud, too bright. “I can’t believe they did that. On live TV.”

Rio’s eyes were flint. “They wanted to scare you. And to show they could touch what’s private.” She angled herself so Agatha wouldn’t have to see Alice’s grim, confirming nod in the mirror. “So we show them what happens when they touch what’s mine.”

Agatha’s eyes flickered at the word—mine. Something steadied in her. “What happens?” she asked, voice small but fierce.

“We end this,” Rio said simply.

The SUV sped through the city, engine a low growl. For a while, the only sounds were the hum of the road and the quiet breath of a woman who refused to break.

“Agatha,” Alice said carefully, eyes staying on the road, “I’ve already reached out to Wanda, Jen, and Lilia’s teams. We’re sweeping their places for bugs, rotating passwords, and pulling device logs. We’ll lock everything down before the hour’s out.”

“Thank you,” Agatha said, voice barely above a whisper.

“Press is exploding,” Natasha added, scrolling through her secure tablet. “But Peter’s people are cooperating. They’re cutting all footage of the breach. We’ll get a statement drafted that says the show suffered a technical issue and the taping was paused out of respect for safety.”

“Jessica Jones will want a quote,” Alice said. “We’ll coordinate with Jen before we give her anything.”

Rio nodded, then squeezed Agatha’s hand. “You don’t have to decide tonight. We’ll shield you from the noise. We’ll handle the legal and the technical. You just breathe.”

Agatha nodded, the smallest of movements, but it mattered.

The SUV swung off the main artery and into the quieter veins of the city. Two blocks later, Alice pulled into an underground garage. They slid out, switched to a nondescript sedan waiting two levels down, then repeated the maneuver across town. Only when Rio was satisfied they’d shaken any eyes did they finally head for the hills.

“Home in ten,” Alice said.

Agatha tipped her head to rest on Rio’s shoulder, voice a rasp. “I hate that they saw me like that. I hate that they touched the people I love.”

Rio pressed a kiss to Agatha’s hairline, brief, hidden, just for them. “They didn’t touch who you are,” she said. “They never will.”

The gate to Agatha’s property opened on command. Sonya and Steve stood at attention just inside the drive, rifles slung, eyes sweeping. The sedan rolled to a stop beneath the portico. Doors opened in a practiced sequence—Natasha first, scanning; Alice next, popping the trunk; Rio last, guiding Agatha out with a palm at her back.

“House is sealed,” Steve reported. “No breaches. Perimeter clean.”

“Good,” Rio said. “We’re on high alert. No one sleeps until dawn.”

She angled Agatha toward the front door. The actress paused, fingers brushing Rio’s. “Don’t leave me tonight,” she said quietly.

“Never,” Rio answered, just as quiet.

Inside, the door shut with a soft, final click. The outside world, its cameras, its hunger, its cruelty, stayed on the other side of the wood.

For now.

Chapter End Notes

Poor Agatha!! Hope you enjoyed though.

Next Chapter: Team interrogates Kyra, learn new information, and media fallout from leak on air.

The Seventh Veil

Chapter Summary

Kyra's interrogation, Team is one step closer to ending the threat once and for all.

Chapter Notes

Consensus was to keep the title I have, so I will.

Enjoy, and please comment your thoughts.

Not proofread, so sorry for any mistakes

Rio didn’t let go of Agatha’s hand as she steered her toward the living room. Natasha was already inside, phone pressed to her ear, her clipped Russian consonants snapping across the line. Alice had her laptop out on the dining table, cords snaking like veins as she hooked into the house’s systems. Steve and Sonya swept the perimeter one more time, their heavy boots a steady rhythm fading in and out.

Agatha moved like a sleepwalker, her hand still twined with Rio’s, her eyes glassy but sharp, clinging to control by sheer force of will. She sank onto the couch, tugging Rio down beside her like an anchor.

Alice broke the silence first, her fingers flying across keys. “It wasn’t us.”

Natasha turned, brows arched. “Define ‘wasn’t us.’”

“The breach. Those images? The files? They didn’t come from my system. They didn’t even touch the new security protocols.” Alice’s voice was tight.  “They clawed it all out of the old feeds. Pre-S.H.I.E.L.D. install. Everything Agatha’s last team ran? Compromised to hell. That’s where the Cicadas got in.”

Rio’s jaw flexed, fury flashing through her eyes. “You’re telling me the last team left a back door wide open, and nobody caught it?”

“Not a back door,” Alice corrected grimly, spinning her laptop to show grainy timestamps. “A vault left to rot. No maintenance, no purge cycles, no encryption updates. They left all of it sitting in a cloud server under a dead company name. Old feeds, cache files, storage snapshots. The Cicadas didn’t need to break in, they just scraped what was abandoned.”

Agatha buried her face in her hands, her voice muffled. “So every moment I thought was private… it was just sitting there, waiting for someone to weaponize it.”

Rio tightened her grip on Agatha’s wrist, firm but grounding. “They exploited negligence. Not your fault.”

Before Agatha could answer, the front door slammed open, and two voices cut through the heavy quiet.

“Agatha!”

Wanda barreled in first, hair wild, eyes bright with panic. Right behind her was Lilia, her face pale and pinched, fury simmering beneath the surface. Both women dropped their coats on the floor and rushed forward, ignoring Natasha’s raised brow from the doorway.

Agatha stood automatically, and Wanda pulled her into a crushing embrace. “Are you alright?!”

“I’m fine,” Agatha soothed, though her voice cracked. “Rio had me the whole time. I’m fine, I swear.”

Wanda pulled back just enough to look her over, as if scanning for wounds the rest of them had missed. Satisfied, she brushed hair back from Agatha’s face and kissed her forehead, muttering something in Sokovian under her breath.

Lilia didn’t move to hug her. She couldn’t. She was trembling, her hands fisted at her sides. “They didn’t just come after you,” she said hoarsely. Her eyes snapped to Rio, and for a terrifying second, the rage there wasn’t directed at the stalkers, it was directed at her.

“They had Colten’s photo. Classified mission data. Files the public should never have even known existed. How—” her voice broke, raw with grief she usually kept buried deep. “How do they have my son’s name? How do they have pictures of his dead body?!”

The room went still. Natasha lowered her phone. Alice stopped typing. Even Wanda froze.

Rio stood, shoulders squared, but her voice was low and steady, not defensive. “I don’t know yet. But I swear to you, Lilia, I will find out. Nobody touches Colten’s memory. Not like this.”

Agatha’s breath hitched, and she looked between them. “Wait, Colten? You mean—”

“My boy,” Lilia whispered, eyes glassy. “Rio’s teammate. My son.”

Agatha nearly threw up, she didn’t actually get a good look at what was displayed on the screen, but she saw enough. She reached for Lilia’s hand, but the woman pulled back, not in anger at her but because she was shaking too badly. Wanda steadied her from behind, one arm circling her waist.

Alice’s voice cracked the silence again, quieter this time. “It wasn’t just Agatha. The Cicadas dumped fragments of military dossiers alongside the private photos. They don’t make sense, cut up and pieced together, but they’re authentic. Someone fed them intel, classified, real intel, and they mixed it in with the personal leaks to make it impossible to dismiss. They wanted the shock factor to land twice as hard.”

Natasha leaned against the mantel, arms folded. “So the question isn’t just ‘how did they get into Agatha’s old feeds.’ It’s: who sold them military intel. And why use it here, now?”

Rio’s face darkened, shadows under her eyes. “Because it ties me in. That intel was from my missions. My team. My past. They’re trying to weaken me while they shatter Agatha.”

Agatha reached out, grasping Rio’s hand tight, refusing to let her sink into guilt. “No. Don’t. This isn’t you. This is them twisting knives because they know where to cut deepest.”

Rio swallowed hard, staring down at their joined hands. She didn’t trust herself to answer.

Lilia finally sat, Wanda lowering her gently to the couch. She looked drained, her composure cracked in a way Agatha had rarely seen. “If they have Colten’s files, they have more. And if they’re willing to use him…” She trailed off, biting back a sob. “They’ll come after every ghost we’ve buried.”

Alice cleared her throat, forcing steel back into the conversation. “I traced the packets. The Cicadas used the same digital mark they always do, the insect sigil. But this wasn’t them alone. The smear campaign? That wasn’t their style. Too polished, too targeted. That was Renna’s hand. Raven’s still a ghost, but she’s circling this mess too. And now? Now we know someone with clearance-level access has joined their team. Somebody who could pull Colten’s file. It is possible the enforcer is former military and has access, or its possible its the work of the mastermind,” The weight of it pressed on the room.

Agatha’s voice, when it came, was barely a whisper. “They’re everywhere. Aren’t they?”

Rio crouched in front of her, forcing her to look down, into her eyes. “No. They want you to believe that. But we’re closer than ever. We have Kyra in custody. We have Renna in our sights. We’ll dig Seren out, too. And whoever gave them classified files? We’ll find them. We’ll rip them into the light.”

Agatha blinked, eyes shining with tears she refused to let fall. She searched Rio’s face, then finally let her hand rest against her jaw. “And what about you? They’re coming after you, too. They want to tear you apart with me.”

Rio covered her hand, pressing it closer to her cheek. “Then let them try. They’ll find I’m harder to break than they think.”

For the first time that night, Agatha let the tears slip. Wanda wrapped an arm around her shoulders from one side, Rio from the other, and Lilia sat across, fists still clenched but her eyes burning with something steadier now, not just rage, but resolve.

This wasn’t just about Agatha anymore. The stalkers had drawn blood from all of them.

And that meant all of them would fight back.

The house was quiet again, but only on the surface. Every phone on the table buzzed in a relentless, discordant chorus, alerts, calls, pings from social media. Jen finally snatched hers up, swiping furiously before tossing it down like it burned her.

“It’s everywhere,” she said flatly. “The leak. The broadcast. Every outlet from Variety to TMZ is spinning it. Twitter, TikTok, Instagram—#AgathaExposed, #PrayForAgatha, It’s wildfire.”

Agatha flinched at the words, Rio’s arm automatically tightening around her.

“All have been an outpouring support, but I need statements from all of you, Agatha, Rio, Wanda and Lilia. We need to get ahead of this,” Jen said sternly. Going though all of the articles and fan reactions flooding social media right now.

Variety: Chaos on Live Television: Hackers Interrupt Talk Show With Leaked Files

Last night’s broadcast with Agatha Harkness and Peter Parker took a dark turn when hackers infiltrated the live feed, displaying private images and personal information belonging to Harkness, her security chief Rio Vidal, and close associates. Security quickly moved Harkness offstage, and law enforcement sources confirm one suspect was apprehended on sight. Fans have flooded social media with support under the hashtags #WeStandWithAgatha and #ProtectRio.

E! News: Unprecedented Security Breach: Agatha Harkness Targeted During Live Interview

“This is bigger than celebrity gossip, this is a dangerous violation of privacy,” says cybercrime expert L. Tran. “The precision of this hack suggests an organized group.” Harkness’ team has not issued a statement yet, but allies across Hollywood are speaking out. Wanda Maximoff posted a simple but powerful message on Instagram: “Not today. Not ever. Agatha, we’ve got you.”

@HexMeDaddy: Whoever hacked Agatha’s interview is SICK. She doesn’t deserve this. None of them do. My heart hurts for her. 💔 #WeStandWithAgatha #ProtectRio

@Slvt4Harkness: Imagine being so obsessed with a woman you have to hack LIVE TV just to get noticed. PATHETIC. Agatha will outlast all this. She’s stronger than any of them. #UnbreakableAgatha

@WitchyCoven94: I can’t believe those monsters actually leaked military photos of Rio’s dead team. That’s not fandom, that’s cruelty. My heart breaks for her. 🖤 #ProtectRio #JusticeForTheFallen

@ProtectTheCoven: The fact they exposed Rio, Wanda, Jen, and even Lilia?? Not just Agatha?? This is cyber-terrorism, straight up. 

@RideOrDieRio Imagine surviving war, losing your team, building a new life, and then some psychos dig up your past trauma to torment you. Rio doesn’t deserve this. None of them do. #ProtectRio #CovenStrong

@AgathaUpdates:🚨 Confirmed: suspect detained is Kyra Auden, tied to multiple fan projects from early Agatha fandom. This runs deep, and it’s terrifying. Stay safe, Coven. #WeStandWithAgatha

@ThirstyForRio Real talk: Rio putting herself between Agatha + the hackers without hesitation??? That’s not just a bodyguard, that’s devotion. #ProtectRio #GuardianAngel

@WitchyMama: Watching Agatha get dragged offstage while private PHOTOS of her were broadcast?? I feel physically sick. Sending her nothing but love right now. #WeStandWithAgatha #JusticeForAgatha
