@Jessica_Jones: Tonight’s events weren’t drama, they were trauma. Privacy is not a privilege; it’s a right. The fact that this happened live on national television is proof this group won’t stop until they’re stopped. My heart is with Agatha.”

@Billy.Maximoff: You don’t come for our family. Period. #ProtectAgatha

@Wanda Maximoff: 📸: A photo of Agatha laughing between takes “She is joy. She is power. She is loved. That won’t change.” #WeStandWithAgatha

 

Rio’s voice cut cleanly through the room. “I need to talk to Maria first before issuing any statement, and lean on my military contacts, they can find who accessed my file. Then I’m meeting Bucky and Yelena to interrogate Kyra.”

She was already scrolling past the flood of notifications, thumb steady until she hit Maria Hill. She tapped speaker and set the phone on the table.

It rang once.

“Vidal,” Maria answered, awake and razor-sharp.

“Live breach on a network broadcast,” Rio said without preamble. “Cicadas pulled from Agatha’s old home feeds. They also surfaced classified mission fragments tied to my unit, including Colten, and my Delta team.” She glanced at Lilia; Lilia’s jaw trembled, but she nodded for Rio to continue. “Kyra Auden is in custody. Seren is still at large. We need a trace on who touched my file.”

A half-beat of silence, then Maria’s tone went flinty. “I’ll light a fire under the DIA. If this was an internal pull, we’ll see the audit trail. If it was a contractor or a leaker, we squeeze until they squeal.”

“Priority one,” Rio said. “Send me anyone we trust for a quiet chain-of-custody on the logs. I don’t want this contaminated.”

“Already in motion,” Maria replied. “You going to the black site?”

“Now.”

“Good. Send me your interview plan for Kyra and I’ll add questions. Don’t wait on me to start.” A pause. Softer: “You okay?”

Rio’s eyes flicked to Agatha. “I will be.”

“Copy. I’ll circle back with names and the first cut of the access logs within the hour. Have Nat call me when she has a second.” The line clicked off.

Jen exhaled. “Okay. Timeline: statements drafted tonight, released at 9 a.m. Rio, you can give me a placeholder quote about cooperating with authorities and your commitment to protecting Agatha, then update once Maria confirms anything.”

Wanda stepped closer to Agatha, fingers lacing with hers. “Go,” she told Rio. “We’ve got her here.”

Rio looked to Agatha. The actress read the question on her face and squeezed her hand. “Go,” Agatha echoed, voice steadier than she felt.

Rio nodded once, then turned to Alice. “Package Kyra’s digital footprint. I want her known aliases, burner phones, past handle changes, crypto wallets, and any offsite storage. Anything that looks like a dead drop or a panic protocol.”

“On it,” Alice said, already typing.

“Nat,” Rio continued, “scrub tonight’s venue. Anyone who touched the broadcast system, security, A/V crew, temp hires. Cross-check with our watchlist and Renna’s known circles.”

Natasha was already shrugging into a jacket. “I’ll take Steve. Sonya holds the gate.”

Lilia rose, eyes wet but steely. “If Colten’s records were touched, I want names. When you have them, I want the first call.”

“You’ll get it,” Rio said, meeting her gaze without flinching.

She turned back to Agatha, stepping in close. For a heartbeat, the room faded. “I’ll check in when I reach Bucky and Yelena,” Rio promised, low and certain. “Lock the house. Stay on the inner cams. If anything feels off, you don’t argue, you move.”

Agatha’s mouth tipped into the smallest, fierce smile. “Yes, ma’am.”

Rio’s dimples threatened; she tamped them down, kissed Agatha’s forehead, quick, grounding, and pulled away.

“Let’s roll,” she said to Natasha.

By the time the front door opened again, the team had already shifted like a living organism: Wanda and Lilia flanking Agatha, Jen at the table shaping language into shields, Alice a thunderstorm of keys and code, Sonya’s silhouette cutting across the hall as she moved to the east windows. The door thudded shut, and Rio’s footsteps faded down the porch.

War plan in motion.

 

On the way to the warehouse, Rio’s phone buzzed sharp against the console. Maria’s name lit the screen. She answered on the second ring, voice clipped.

“Any news?” Rio asked, skipping pleasantries.

“We’ve confirmed the enforcer,” Maria said, her tone grim. “Maera Rourke. Former Army. She’s the one who dug into your files, and the one who took out Ralph. Ex-bodyguard of Agatha’s for a very brief stint, but now she’s mercenary muscle, takes contracts, no loyalty, no conscience. I’m sending you her dossier now. I’ll meet you at Agatha’s house when you’re done.”

The line went dead.

Rio’s jaw tightened as her phone pinged with the incoming file. She opened it briefly, Maera’s photo stared back at her: sharp eyes, scars like unfinished sentences across her skin, the sort of face that had seen war and decided it preferred it. Cold. Ruthless.

Rio flicked the file to the rest of the team’s comms.

She pulled the SUV into the gravel lot outside the warehouse, engine humming low. The building loomed, dark windows, rust creeping up the siding, the kind of place no one asked questions about. Perfect for what they needed.

She killed the engine, silence settling like a weight. For a long moment, Rio just stared at the building, the faint flicker of the security light over the door. Then she exhaled and unbuckled.

Inside, there’d be no room for hesitation. Not with Kyra. Not with Maera’s shadow now hanging over them.

Rio shut the engine off, the gravel crackling one last time as the SUV settled into stillness.

The warehouse air was heavy, like dust and iron had seeped into its walls years ago and refused to leave. A single bulb swayed overhead, buzzing faintly, the shadows it cast moving like restless ghosts. Kyra Auden sat shackled to the table, chains rattling softly every time she shifted. And she shifted often. Too much energy in her small frame, like she might combust if left still for too long.

She was humming when the door opened. A lilting, off-key melody. Something that sounded like a lullaby but warped, broken.

Rio entered first. She didn’t slam the door or make a show of her presence. She just moved with deliberate calm, a predator’s silence. Yelena stalked in behind her, arms crossed tight, already looking irritated. Bucky shut the door last, his expression unreadable, a folder tucked under his arm.

Kyra’s grin stretched wide the second she saw them. “Well, well. Took you long enough. I was starting to wonder if you’re scared of me.”

“No one here is scared of you,” Yelena said flatly, leaning against the wall.

“Oh, kitten, you’ll forgive me if I don’t take you seriously. You’ve got the whole assassin vibe down, sure, but your eyes? They’re soft. Too soft.”

Yelena didn’t even blink. “Try me.”

Rio sat down across from Kyra. She didn’t waste words, didn’t rise to the bait. She just stared, and the silence stretched taut until even Kyra’s manic grin flickered.

Finally, Rio spoke. “You hum like you’re at peace. You’re not.”

Kyra chuckled. “Oh, I’m more than at peace. I’m winning. The world saw what we wanted them to see. You can patch it up with statements, with your pet journalist, with your fake smiles on talk shows, but the stain’s there. Agatha’s mine. She always was.”

“You don’t own her,” Rio said evenly.

Kyra’s eyes glittered. “Oh, soldier, everyone owns a piece of her. Fans, lovers, enemies. She’s carved up like a feast. We’re just the ones brave enough to take our share openly.”

Rio didn’t flinch, didn’t even let her breathing change. “Where’s Seren?”

The question made Kyra’s grin grow. She tilted her head, like a cat toying with prey. “Seren’s smarter than me. Faster. Quieter. She doesn’t need to get close. She’s the Cicada in the walls, in the wires. She can watch Agatha undress without ever stepping foot in the room. Want to know how many times she’s seen her vulnerable? Dozens. Hundreds. More than you ever will.”

Bucky stepped forward, sliding a photo onto the table. “And yet, you’re the one cuffed here, not her. Seren’s probably already figuring out how to cut you loose.”

Kyra’s laugh cracked like glass. “Seren won’t cut me loose. She needs me. She always has. I’m the mouth, she’s the hands. I’m the one who tells the story. She’s the one who writes it in code. Without me, she’s nothing but silence.”

“Without her, you’re nothing but noise,” Yelena countered, arms tightening across her chest.

Kyra snarled, jerking against the cuffs. “Don’t you dare. She’s brilliant. And she loves Agatha as much as I do.”

“Love?” Rio asked softly. “Is that what you call this?”

“It is love,” Kyra hissed. “Love is obsession. Love is pain. Love is knowing she owes you everything and still walking away. You’ll learn that too, soldier. When she leaves you the way she left me.”

Rio’s eyes narrowed, but she didn’t speak.

Kyra leaned closer, chains clinking. “Oh, I know you. Rio Vidal. Hero. Soldier. Protector. Lover. And still, you couldn’t save them, could you? Your team. Valkyrie.”

Rio’s hands clenched against the table, the only sign she’d heard.

Kyra smiled slow, cruel. “I can still picture it. You holding her broken body. Wondering if maybe this time it was your fault. Wondering if loving her killed her. That’s what you do, Rio. You curse people by caring for them. Valkyrie, Colten, Your family, the rest of Delta”

Yelena slammed her boot into the table leg. The crack echoed like a gunshot. Kyra startled, but the smile snapped back almost instantly.

“Touch a nerve? Good.” Her voice dropped to a whisper, almost reverent. “Because that’s how it’ll end with Agatha too. She’ll choke on your love. And when she’s broken, when you’re grieving, we’ll pick up the pieces. She’ll finally come home.”

Bucky’s voice cut through the tension, calm but sharp. “You’re not the only piece in this. We know about Maera Rourke.” He dropped another photo on the table: a hard-eyed woman with cropped hair and a face carved in stone.

Kyra’s smirk faltered.

“Muscle for hire,” Rio said. “Ex-military. Former security. Worked for Agatha once. She doesn’t care about Agatha, doesn’t care about you. She only cares about the paycheck.”

Kyra tried to play bored, leaning back as the cuffs rattled. “So what? She gets the job done.”

“She killed Ralph,” Rio said, voice low. “Because he got sloppy. That’s not loyalty. That’s business. And when you become inconvenient, she’ll slit your throat too.”

Kyra bristled, mask cracking. “She’s not sloppy. She’s precise. She doesn’t ask questions. You want someone scared of blood? Go hire a nurse. You want someone who’ll burn down a house with the family still inside if that’s the contract? You call Maera.”

Yelena gave a mirthless laugh. “Sounds like a lovely companion. How proud you must be.”

Kyra glared at her. “She’s not my companion. She’s a tool. And she’s perfect.”

Rio watched her carefully. “So Maera’s the hammer. Seren’s the hands. You’re the mouth. But there’s still more.”

Kyra froze, ever so slightly.

Rio leaned in, quiet, steady. “The Rat. The one who got into Agatha’s trailer. Rigged the light. Left the note. That wasn’t you, wasn’t Seren, wasn’t Maera or Renna. That was someone else.”

Kyra’s lips parted, and for a split second she looked startled, like a rabbit caught in headlights. Then she laughed, too loud, too forced. “Rat. That’s cute. Maybe you’re smarter than you look.”

“So there is another,” Bucky pressed.

Kyra tilted her head, feigning amusement, but her eyes were wild. “Oh, the Rat is special. She slinks in where no one notices. Crawls under doors, through cracks. She doesn’t need fame or fire. She just wants to watch Agatha bleed up close. Personal. Intimate.”

Rio’s stomach tightened, but her face stayed still. “And the Watcher,” she said softly.

Kyra froze again.

“You didn’t mean to,” Rio continued. “But you’ve mentioned someone else too. Someone always close, always lingering.”

Kyra’s smile wavered. Then it returned, sharper, jagged. “The Watcher… she’s always there. A shadow at the edge of the crowd. A whisper outside the window. Agatha doesn’t even see her, but she sees everything. Every smile. Every tear. Every touch she’s given you.”

Yelena’s lip curled. “Creepy.”

“She’s devoted,” Kyra whispered. “More devoted than me. And when the time comes, she’ll be the knife at Agatha’s throat while the rest of you blink.”

Rio leaned forward, her voice a low growl. “And the mastermind?”

Kyra went still. Too still. Her grin faltered, and for the first time, her eyes darted away.

Kyra’s jaw trembled. “She’s… untouchable.”

“No one’s untouchable,” Bucky said.

Kyra snapped back to life, slamming her hands against the table, chains rattling. “You don’t understand! She’s everything. She’s the beginning and the end. She loved Agatha. Hated her. Built her up. Tore her down. And she’ll finish what she started. You can’t stop her. You can’t even name her.”

“She’s using you,” Yelena spat.

Kyra laughed, a broken, wild sound. “Let her use me. At least she sees me. At least she loves me in her way. That’s more than Agatha ever did.”

Her gaze snapped to Rio then, sharp as a blade. “And you, she’ll leave you too. Just like she left me. Because that’s who Agatha Harkness is. She destroys everything she touches.”

“Congrats on getting farther then the rest, You’ve named the Fox, the Crow, the Cicadas and the coyote, but you haven’t found the Rat or the Snake. And they have some of the worst bites.” The bulb overhead buzzed louder, casting Kyra’s face in jagged light and shadow. Her grin was all teeth, her eyes all madness.

Rio stood, gathering the photos from the table with deliberate care. Her voice, when it came, was quiet but lethal. “You’ve told us more than you think.”

Kyra leaned back, chains scraping, humming that broken lullaby again. “And you’ve heard less than you need.”

Bucky opened the door, his face grim. Yelena shot one last look back at Kyra, disgust curling her lip, then followed Rio out.

Kyra’s laugh followed them down the hall, high and unhinged. “She’ll never be yours. She’ll always be ours!”

The door shut on her voice, but the echo lingered long after.

 

The convoy rolled back into Agatha’s property just as the horizon bled into twilight. The gates clanged shut behind them, Sonya and Steve resuming their positions like statues. Rio parked with deliberate calm, though her knuckles were pale on the wheel. The warehouse stench of fear and defiance still clung to her, Kyra’s manic laughter echoing in her ears.

Inside the house, the atmosphere was taut. Agatha, wrapped in a silk robe the color of midnight, sat curled on the couch with Wanda at her side. Lilia hovered nearby, arms folded, her sharp eyes flicking to every movement like she was cataloguing threats herself. Billy and Jen lingered behind the couch, their protective instincts so obvious they could’ve been carrying sidearms of their own.

Maria was already there, speaking quietly with Natasha by the fireplace. They stood close, Natasha’s hand brushing Maria’s wrist as she passed her a folder, Maria’s expression softening just briefly in response. Subtle, but anyone with eyes could see the tether between them.

When Rio entered with Yelena and Bucky, the room seemed to hold its breath.

Agatha immediately straightened. “Well? Tell me it wasn’t for nothing.” Her voice was steady, but her fingers twisted the hem of her robe.

Rio nodded once, signaling for Yelena and Bucky to take their places before she began. She shed her coat, laying the folder Maria had given her on the coffee table, and leaned forward against the edge. Every face was on her.

“We got more than we hoped,” Rio said, her tone clipped but sure. “Kyra was slippery, but we forced cracks in her act. Here’s what we know.”

She tapped the folder, flipping it open to reveal hastily printed dossiers. “They’re working under codenames. Animals. Each with distinct roles.”

Yelena smirked faintly, leaning against the wall. “Like some twisted petting zoo.”

“First,” Rio continued, ignoring her, “The Fox. Renna. She’s behind the PR sabotage and online smear campaigns. The sudden hashtags, the fake testimonies, the deepfakes? That’s her. And she’s good at it. Personal. Calculated. She wants the world to turn on you, Agatha.”

Agatha’s jaw tensed, but she only nodded, as if she’d expected Renna to still be haunting her.

“Second, The Crow. Raven.” Rio’s eyes flicked briefly to Agatha. “Kyra slipped, mentioned that the Crow watches everything. We believe Raven is also the Watcher. The one tailing you in public. Blending into crowds. Always close, but never caught. She sees, she records, she feeds it back to the others.”

Agatha swallowed hard. Wanda’s hand found hers, a quiet anchor.

“Third, the Rat.” Rio’s voice lowered, deliberate. “This one’s the infiltrator. They were the one who got into your trailer, wrecked your mirror, chewed your mail, left the note. They also rigged the light on set. Sabotage, up close and personal. But Kyra didn’t give us an identity. Just the codename.”

Jen muttered under her breath. “Fitting.”

“Fourth, the Snake. The mastermind,” Rio continued. “The one pulling all the strings, paying for it all, tying the rest together. Kyra confirmed it’s a woman. She refused to say who, but, ” Rio’s gaze shifted back to Agatha. “she said you know her.”

The silence that followed was thick, pressing. Agatha stiffened, then exhaled, looking away toward the fire. “Of course I do.”

Rio didn’t push. Not yet.

“Fifth, the Coyote. The enforcer. Maera Rourke.” She slid a photo across the table, Maera’s scarred face staring up at them. “Former Army. Ex-bodyguard. Now a mercenary for hire. She killed Ralph Bohner when he became a liability. She doesn’t care about you, Agatha, she only cares about finishing a contract and getting paid. Ruthless. Efficient. She’ll do anything including getting into my Miltary records and giving them to the Cicada’s.”

Lilia stepped closer, peering at the photo. Her lips pressed thin, the lines around her eyes hardening. “She worked for us once. I didn’t trust her then. I should’ve—”

“This isn’t on you,” Rio cut her off gently.

Bucky’s gravelly voice rumbled as he leaned forward. “Maera doesn’t leave loose ends. If she’s on payroll, we need to assume she’s capable of escalation. And if she’s got a personal history with Agatha, she knows routines, tells, even habits that make her dangerous.”

Agatha’s eyes lingered on the photo longer than she wanted. She remembered Maera’s presence, stone-faced, detached, a shadow that never smiled. It chilled her, even now.

“And lastly,” Rio finished, “the Cicadas. Hackers. Kyra and Seren Auden. Sisters. We’ve confirmed their handles and their signature, the cicada motif buried in their code. They’re responsible for hacking old security systems, pulling your private photos, leaking them. They started as fans. Built projects, ran accounts you once acknowledged. Then you stopped engaging. They twisted that into resentment. They convinced themselves you owed them your career.”

Alice, listening intently, added, “Their hacks all carry the same digital signature. I can track it. We’ll be able to find Seren soon.”

Wanda’s hand tightened around Agatha’s. “So it’s all women. Every one of them.”

Rio nodded grimly. “Yes. Every one of them has some history—direct or indirect—with Agatha.”

The room fell quiet. The fire crackled softly. Outside, the security lights buzzed.

Jen finally broke the silence, her voice low but fierce. “This is insane. These women aren’t fans, they’re predators. They built an identity around tearing her apart.”

Agatha stared at the photo of Maera, then the folder of Kyra’s twisted scrawlings, before finally closing it with a snap. Her voice, when it came, was raw but steady. “I can handle people hating me. I’ve lived with it before. What I can’t, what I won’t handle is them coming after the people I love. That’s where I draw the line.”

Rio’s gaze softened at her. She reached out, briefly covering Agatha’s hand on the folder. A silent vow.

Maria finally stepped forward, her presence commanding. “Then we draw our own lines. We’ve identified nearly all of them: the Fox, the Crow, the Rat, the Snake, the Coyote, the Cicadas. We’ll dismantle them piece by piece. But we need to be smart, coordinated, and faster than they are. No mistakes.”

Natasha slid a hand briefly against Maria’s back before stepping forward herself. “They think they can circle Agatha like vultures. Let’s show them what happens when they pick the wrong prey.”

A grim smile ghosted across Wanda’s face at that. “Let them try.”

Agatha’s chest tightened at the solidarity in the room. For the first time since the nightmare began, she felt something sharper than fear: the faint, burning edge of hope.

“I say, since we know most of these people’s names and faces, we release them to the public. Let Agatha’s real fans, her coven help us. They’ll be more eyes in the audience for us. We can include that in all of your statements, asking for the public’s help,” Jen offered, her tone practical but sharp, like she’d already started drafting headlines in her head.

“That could work,” Alice agreed almost immediately, arms crossed as her analytical gaze swept across the group. “Let the media and public be our eyes and ears. Your fans, the normal ones love you, Agatha. They want to see you safe. If we mobilize them, it puts the stalkers on notice. They won’t be able to move in the shadows if the whole world is looking for them.”

Every eye shifted to Rio. She stood still at the edge of the table, jaw tight, weighing it. Her instinct screamed against letting civilians play watchdog in something this dangerous. But she also knew Alice and Jen were right: the stalkers thrived on silence, secrecy, shadows. Dragging them into the light would cut away that advantage.

Finally, she gave a short, decisive nod. “Alright. Let’s draft up the statements now. The sooner we put their faces and names out there, the better.”

Jen clapped her hands once, already tugging her laptop free from its case. “Perfect. Agatha, you’ll have to give me direct quotes. Rio, Lilia, Wanda, you too, your credibility will go a long way here. We frame it not as panic, but as empowerment. These women aren’t fans, they’re criminals. And criminals don’t deserve silence.”

Agatha shifted in her seat, her robe drawn tight around her like armor. She tilted her head, a wry smile tugging at her lips despite the exhaustion in her eyes. “You want me to call my coven to arms.”

Jen’s fingers were already flying over the keyboard, but she looked up long enough to smirk. “Exactly. And trust me, they’ll answer.”

Lilia spoke then, her voice low but firm, carrying that maternal edge she always used with Agatha. “Just be careful in how it’s worded, Jennifer. If you make it sound like open season, we’ll have a thousand self-appointed vigilantes running around. Keep it measured. Focused.”

“Of course,” Jen said, nodding briskly. “We’ll release official images of Renna, Raven, Maera, and Seren. Confirm their past roles regarding Agatha. Emphasize that any information should go directly to authorities or to us, not handled personally.”

“Good,” Rio said. She leaned down slightly, resting her palms flat on the table, her voice brooking no argument. “The last thing we need is someone getting themselves hurt trying to play hero. These women are violent, trained, and organized. Fans can watch, they can tip us off, but no one approaches them. That’s non-negotiable.”

Maria added, calm but commanding, “And we’ll coordinate with our government contacts to make sure any tips filter back to us immediately. Information is power. Right now, it’s the best weapon we have.”

The room hummed with a strange energy, Determination and adrenaline

Agatha reached out, her hand brushing Rio’s on the table. “Then let’s do it. If they want to make me a symbol, let’s use it against them. They’ve stolen enough. Time we take something back.”

Rio covered her hand with her own, steady and grounding, before straightening. “Then it’s decided.”

Jen cracked her knuckles and grinned, her screen already glowing with half-written drafts. “Let’s make history.”

Agatha’s Statement 

My Coven,

Over the past weeks, I’ve been targeted by a coordinated group calling themselves The Seventh Veil. These individuals are not fans. They are criminals who have violated my privacy, my safety, and the safety of my loved ones.

Today, we can name some of them. Renna, known online for years, is behind the smear campaign and false narratives. Raven Corvin, my former assistant, has been identified as “The Crow.” Maera Rourke, ex-military and a woman who once briefly worked as my bodyguard, is the hired muscle. The hackers are Kyra and Seren Auden, known as “The Cicadas.” They once ran fan accounts for me and have now turned that passion into something toxic and dangerous.

These women are not faceless anymore. They are seen.

I want to be clear: my fans are not to intervene directly. If you recognize these names or faces, contact the authorities or my team. What you can do is continue doing what you’ve always done: show up with love, kindness, and joy. That energy is what carries me.

To my security team—Rio Vidal, Natasha Romanov-Hill, Yelena Belova, Bucky Barnes, Clint Barton, Alice Gulliver, Sonya Belikova, Steve Rogers—I thank you. You have stood by me through fear and fire. To Rio, especially, for never leaving my side, I am endlessly grateful.

I am safe. I am working. And I will not be silenced.

With love, always,
 Agatha

 

Lilia’s Statement 

My name is Lilia Calderu. I am Agatha Harkness’s manager, but more importantly, I am her family.

Recently, private photographs were leaked during a live broadcast. Among them was an image of my late son, Colten, who served under Rio Vidal in Delta Force. He died a hero. His sacrifice and memory should never have been violated in this grotesque way. To parade his body as part of some twisted game is not only criminal—it is inhumane.

My son’s death is not entertainment. It is not leverage. It is sacred.

I stand with Rio, who led Colten’s team with honor. I stand with Agatha, who has been targeted in ways no one should have to endure. And I stand with every family who has ever had their grief exploited by people who do not understand what loss really means.

To those behind this campaign: you think you are clever, but all you’ve done is unite us. We are not afraid of you. We will not give you power by cowering. We will see you unmasked and held accountable.

Colten’s memory deserves better. Agatha deserves better. And together, we will make sure she gets it.

 

Wanda’s Statement

Some of you know me only as Agatha’s co-star. Others know me as her sister in arms. Here is what I want you to know: I will always be by Agatha’s side.

The women who have organized themselves under the names of “The Seventh Veil” are not fans. They are predators. They have invaded Agatha’s life, tried to smear her reputation, and now they’ve endangered everyone connected to her.

I have fought with Agatha on screen for decades, but off-screen, I will fight for her in real life too. She is not alone. I am here. Her team is here. And her true fans—the ones who love her for who she is—are here.

To those behind these attacks: you will not break her. You will not break us. You wanted to turn her world upside down, but all you’ve done is prove how much stronger she is when we stand with her.

I love you, Agatha. And I’m not going anywhere.

 

Rio’s Statement: 

On behalf of S.H.I.E.L.D. Security, I want to address the recent breaches and coordinated attacks on our client, Ms. Agatha Harkness.

First, let me assure you: Agatha is safe. Our team is actively investigating and neutralizing threats as they arise. Several individuals have already been identified as part of this organized group. Their faces and names are being released to the public to assist in their capture.

These women—who call themselves “The Seventh Veil”—are not supporters. They are orchestrators of harassment, sabotage, and attempted violence. Their actions have crossed every line, and we will not rest until each one of them is held accountable.

As the co-founder of S.H.I.E.L.D., I take this personally. I have buried too many teammates, including my partner Valkyrie, who gave her life for me and for our mission. I will not allow Agatha, or anyone under my protection to become another name I mourn.

S.H.I.E.L.D. vows to continue our protection of Agatha Harkness and to work with authorities worldwide until this group is dismantled. We are professionals. We are relentless. And we will succeed.

—Rio Vidal
 Co-CEO, S.H.I.E.L.D.

Bound by Truth, Freed by Love

Chapter Summary

Team makes some game-changing moves

Chapter Notes

Rollercoaster of emotions this chapter, buckle up, my pretties.

Also, unrelated note, but I'm getting into Witchcraft, started researching it a while back, and kept being pulled back to it, started practicing under the guidance of older witches, I feel better mentally than I ever have before.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The next morning, Agatha woke wrapped securely in strong arms, cocooned against a body that radiated steady warmth. She shifted slightly, trying to ease herself free, but Rio instinctively tightened her hold, pulling her closer.

Agatha stilled. She had never once woken before Rio; her soldier was always up before dawn, sharp and alert, already moving through the day with precision. But this morning, Rio slept on, her breath slow and even, her face softened in a way Agatha rarely got to see.

For a long, unhurried moment, Agatha let herself simply look. Rio wore her usual nighttime uniform, sweatpants, and a sports bra, practical even in rest. But stripped of her armor, her walls, she looked impossibly gentle. Agatha reached up and traced her thumb along the line of Rio’s strong jaw, marveling at the stillness, at the peace carved into her features as if the world outside, stalkers, chaos, fear, didn’t exist.

Her chest ached with it. She swore she fell more in love every single day. They hadn’t said the words aloud yet, but the truth hummed between them, unspoken and undeniable. And Agatha thought, with sudden clarity, that it was time. Time to give those feelings a voice, to tell her soldier exactly how deep they ran.

Rio stirred at last, lashes fluttering open. She blinked herself awake, groggy and unguarded, and when her gaze landed on Agatha, a slow, soft smile spread across her lips.

“I hope you slept well, hermosa,” Rio murmured, her voice thick with sleep, warm and rasping like gravel smoothed by velvet. “You need it.”

Agatha stretched, reluctantly peeling herself out of Rio’s arms before she could be pulled back in again. “If I stay here, I’m never getting up,” she teased, pushing her curls out of her face.

Rio sat up slowly, running a hand through her sleep-mussed hair. Even half awake, she radiated discipline, though Agatha could see the shadows under her eyes. Rio hadn’t truly rested in weeks, and yesterday’s ambush had only added to the weight she carried.

“You look tired,” Agatha said softly, pulling one of Rio’s T-shirts over her head. “And don’t give me the ‘I’m fine’ speech, darling. Not after everything yesterday.”

Rio’s lips twitched. “I was going to say I’m functional. Which is true. But…” Her gaze dropped for a moment, then lifted again, steady. “I hated that you had to go through that live. Having your privacy torn open in front of millions—that should never have happened.”

Agatha crossed to her, cupping Rio’s cheek in her hand. “And yet, you were there. You got me out. You kept me safe. That’s what I’ll remember.” She leaned down and pressed a soft kiss to Rio’s temple. “We’ll get through this. Together.”

For the first time that morning, Rio allowed herself to nod. “Together.”

They dressed quickly and headed downstairs. The scent of strong coffee and something frying drifted from the kitchen. The murmur of voices grew louder as they rounded the corner.

Natasha was at the stove, sleeves rolled up, flipping eggs with military precision. Maria sat at the table scrolling through her phone, her reading glasses perched on her nose, while Lilia whispered something to Wanda that made her shake her head with a rare smile. Billy was already halfway through a plate of toast, eyes bleary but loyal as ever.

Alice had her laptop propped open on the counter, multiple feeds running. She glanced up when Agatha and Rio walked in. “Morning. You two sleep?”

Agatha smirked. “Define sleep.”

That earned her a chuckle from Clint, who was leaning against the fridge with a mug in hand. “I regret asking.”

Jen breezed in right on cue, tablet in one hand, her hair pulled up into a messy bun that screamed she hadn’t stopped working since the night before. “Oh, trust me, none of us are sleeping after yesterday. And you two—” she gestured between Agatha and Rio “—can save your blushes, because we’ve got bigger problems.”

Rio arched a brow, arms crossing. “Bigger than what already happened?”

Jen dropped the tablet on the table with a loud thunk. “Tips. Hundreds of them. My inbox is overflowing, my voicemail is maxed out, and every fan forum looks like a conspiracy board exploded. Your statements worked, people are combing through old photos, event clips, and even airport footage. They’re convinced they’ve spotted members of the Salem Seven everywhere from a coffee shop in Burbank to a dog show in Cleveland.”

Billy perked up, toast still hanging from his mouth. “Wait, a dog show?”

Jen gave him a look. “Yes. And before you ask, no, I don’t think the Salem Seven are moonlighting as poodle groomers. But mixed in with the noise are some solid leads, especially on Renna and Raven.”

Alice leaned forward, interest sparking. “What kind of leads?”

“Photos, mostly. A handful of fans dug up older convention pics, where Renna is lurking in the background near Agatha’s table. Someone else sent in a blurry shot from two weeks ago that looks an awful lot like Raven at LAX.” Jen scrolled with a swipe of her finger. “And then there’s Maera. Military circles are buzzing online; apparently, her name has come up in forums tied to mercenary work in Eastern Europe. It lines up with what we already know.”

Agatha’s stomach twisted, though she forced a steady tone. “And the media?”

Jen winced. “Well, they’re having a field day. Headlines are calling this ‘Hollywood’s Real-Life Witch Hunt.’ The leak of your photos was bad, but the statements turned the tide. Most outlets are leaning sympathetic now, Jessica Jones’ piece keeps getting cited, and Lilia’s words about Colten hit hard. People are furious on your behalf.”

Lilia, seated at the far end of the table, nodded firmly. “Good. They should be.”

“And the fans?” Rio asked.

Jen’s expression softened slightly. “They’re rallying. Hashtags like #StandWithAgatha and #ShieldHer are trending. Rio, you’ve got your own fanbase now—#RioVidal has over half a million posts. Some are just…thirsty,” she shot Agatha a dry look, “but most are people calling you a hero. The same goes for the rest of the team. You’re being painted as this unstoppable unit, and honestly? That’s good for us. Public pressure makes it harder for the Seven to hide.”

Alice whistled low. “Crowd sourcing manhunts. I like it.”

“Careful,” Natasha cut in, her voice even but sharp. “Public eyes are useful, but they’re not trained. If fans start thinking they can intervene, it could get someone killed.”

Rio nodded in agreement, her hand brushing briefly against Agatha’s shoulder in silent reassurance. “We’ll filter everything through us first. Nothing gets acted on without verification.”

Jen exhaled, rubbing at her temple. “Good. Because if one more fan emails me saying they’re ‘positive’ they saw Renna buying laundry detergent at Target, I might actually scream.”

Agatha laughed softly despite herself, breaking some of the tension. “Well, darling, I suppose everyone needs clean socks. Even stalkers.”

That earned a chuckle from Wanda, though her grip on Agatha’s hand remained firm. The humor was needed, but the weight in the room was undeniable.

Agatha pulled out her phone and read some of the reactions.

Variety: “Agatha Harkness Breaks Silence: Names Members of Alleged Stalker Ring ‘Seventh Veil’ in Personal Statement”

Hollywood Reporter: “From Smear Campaigns to Leaked Photos: Harkness, Team, and Family Issue Strong United Front”

Buzzfeed: “Agatha’s Manager Lilia Calderu Condemns Exploitation of Late Son’s Image: ‘His memory is sacred’”

Deadline: “S.H.I.E.L.D. Confirms Security Breaches, Vows Relentless Action: ‘We will not rest until all are brought to justice’”

Rolling Stone: “Wanda Maximoff Promises to Stand With Agatha ‘On and Off Screen’: Internet Goes Wild”

@CovenQueen89: Agatha literally named names. Renna. Raven. Maera. Kyra. Seren. This is insane. They’re DONE. #ProtectAgatha #CovenStrong

@MarvelousTea: Wanda saying ‘I’ll always stand by her’ got me SOBBING. These two are ride-or-die and I love it. 🥺 #StandWithAgatha

@PopCulturePulse: Lilia’s statement was devastating. To parade her son’s death like that? Absolutely disgusting. The Seventh veil should rot. #JusticeForColten

@ThirstyButRespectful: Ok yes I’m crying but also Rio saying ‘I will not allow Agatha to become another name I mourn’??? 💔😭😭😭 wife material. #RioVidal

@TabloidTerror: Question tho: Are we just taking these statements at face value? Where’s law enforcement in all this? I want arrests, not Instagram posts.

@WandaAndAgatha4Ever: Not Wanda making me feel like she’s about to hex the stalkers personally. 🔥🔥🔥 #StandWithAgatha

@Moonchild.luna: Agatha, we believe you. Always. Thank you for trusting us with the truth. We got your back. 💜✨”

@Witchybitch: Girl, you’re literally living a thriller series. Stay safe. And THANK YOU Rio + team. #ProtectAgatha”

@Softwitchy: I appreciate you telling us not to intervene but respectfully… if I see Renna on the street it’s ON SIGHT.

@MaximoffQueen: This is the wildest celebrity stalker case I’ve ever seen. It’s literally like something out of a Marvel movie but IRL.

@Rioismywife: I don’t think people realize how huge this is. Naming suspects publicly = Agatha’s team is VERY confident they have evidence.

@Coventrue: Lilia’s grief statement broke me. Imagine having your dead son’s body used like a weapon online. Absolutely vile.

“Wait, did any of you see these posts? I think they’re from the Seven.” Agatha’s voice was sharp with shock as she held up her phone.

“Let me see.” Rio’s hand was steady as she took the phone from Agatha, her eyes narrowing as she scanned the screen.

Jen was already pulling out her own phone, fingers flying across the screen as she tried to find the same posts. “If they’re on public feeds, they won’t stay buried long. The press will pick them up in minutes if they haven’t already.”

The rest of the team leaned in, their faces hardening as the mocking words glared back at them in black and white. The room, once filled with the faint hum of morning conversation, felt suddenly heavy, every breath sharper, every sound louder.

@CicadaSong: You call us criminals, but we’re the ones who made you unforgettable. Without us, you’re nothing. You’ll remember that when the lights fall again. #TheSevenRise”

@WitchyWatcher97: Funny how Agatha thinks she’s safe surrounded by her little army. Armies fall. Pedestals crack. Can’t wait to see her face when she realizes she belongs to us. #SeventhVeil”

“They are getting bolder; they want an audience for whatever they have planned next,” Maria said.

“So we will give them one,” Rio said. Rio pulled a tablet into view and turned it so everyone around the kitchen table could see the layout of the plaza where the pop-up meet-and-greet would take place. Her voice was calm, measured, the kind that cut through panic and shaped it into purpose.

“Listen up,” she said. “We bait them. They want to be seen. They want attention. We give them a stage, but it’s one we control.”

She tapped the screen. A satellite map filled the display, red lines and shaded zones marking sightlines and exits. “This is a small public plaza downtown. It’s a low-key venue, single entry, one main exit, and side alleys that we can seal off. Jen will announce a short, unscheduled ‘surprise’ meet-and-greet with Agatha. The goal: draw a crowd, but keep it manageable.”

Jen, already mentally sprinting, nodded. “We frame it as gratitude. ‘I refuse to be silenced. Come say hi.’ Fans will show. They’ll love it. The media will swarm, and honestly, that’s good; pressure lowers their patience.”

Rio continued. “We’re not walking into this blind. Maria and I have already approved an undercover detail. SHIELD will plant operatives in the crowd disguised as fans, concession workers, even photographers. We’ll also have plainclothes local law enforcement interspersed, uniformed officers only at the perimeter to avoid spooking genuine fans.” She pointed to a ring of blue on the map. “Bucky and Clint will hold far perimeter positions with overwatch. Natasha and Yelena will be closer, embedded in the crowd with comms. Alice will monitor all camera feeds and social chatter in real time.”

Alice’s fingers flew over her own laptop. “I’ve already set up facial recognition filters on the plaza’s camera network and a dozen high-traffic feeds. If any of the Seven appear, I’ll flag them instantly and push images to every agent’s HUD.”

Yelena smirked, tying her gloves on. “If Renna wants attention, we’ll give her fifteen minutes of it, in custody. I’m looking forward to the chase.”

Rio’s plan was surgical. “We’ll stage two decoy entrances. Fans with confirmed RSVPs go through the main gate, where we screen IDs and run quick electronics checks. Any red flags, unknown luggage, or blocked cameras, they will go through a secondary screening. The other entrance will be for the press, escorted and monitored. We will not allow unscreened access.”

Lilia, who’d been quiet until now, leaned forward. “And what about safe extraction? If things go sideways and the crowd surges…”

“We won't allow an environment that could create crowd surges,” Rio said flatly. “Controlled entry, limited tickets, metal detectors at both gates. But contingency is vital: we’ll have an extraction corridor, a neutral walkway we keep clear from the press side to the private exit. If we get a positive ID on Renna, Raven, or any other known member of the Seven, we move through the corridor. Local units will close the outer ring instantly to prevent interference. Medical will be staged two blocks away and ready.”

Agatha watched the plan like a general reading a battle map, her fingers braided in her lap. “You’re setting a trap,” she said quietly.

“A trap with a lot of backup,” Rio replied. “Not a stunt.” Her eyes softened when they landed on Agatha. “You’re not walking that line alone. We’ll be there, physically and legally. Jen, make sure the announcement doesn’t include precise timings or full location details. We want enough interest to draw them, but not enough to spawn copycats.”

“Copy that,” Jen said, already drafting a short, controlled post in her head. “We’ll push the narrative: Agatha refuses to hide. Come for a showing of support, but we’ll ask everyone to behave and use official channels for tips.”

Bucky, arms folded, growled softly. “If one person gets hurt because some keyboard warrior wanted to be a hero, I will personally—”

“You won’t have to,” Rio cut in. “We control the field. We control the exits. And no one engages suspects without backup present. That includes fans.” Her voice wasn’t harsh; it was final.

They all understood the stakes. The Seven had escalated from digital taunts to physical sabotage. Renna and Raven were the two pieces they needed to remove from the board. Capture them here, under the bright gaze of the public and press, and the group’s anonymity and structure would fracture.

Agatha let out a long breath and met Rio’s eyes. “If this works,” she said, “we get answers.”

“If it doesn’t,” Rio said, closing the tablet and standing, “we adapt. But we make it work.”

There was a taut silence, then a chorus of agreements. Jen finalized the message, Alice isolated the feed filters, Natasha and Yelena checked their kits, and Maria coordinated with local law enforcement contacts. Agatha sat taut but steady, flanked by the people who would move heaven to protect her.

Outside, the city carried on, ignorant and bright. Inside the kitchen, the map on the table felt like a spearhead pointing out from their quiet house, small and decisive, aiming to cut the Seven’s shadow down to size.

 

The plaza looked smaller in person than it had on Rio’s tablet, an open stone square cupped between brick buildings and a row of sycamores, with a single gated entry funneled through stanchions and a second, narrower lane for press escorts. Food carts flanked the far side, the sweet sting of kettle corn drifting over the low hum of a growing crowd. It smelled like city heat and sugar and nerves.

By the time Agatha’s SUV rolled to a stop at the service alley entrance, the place was already a sea of purple scarves and handmade signs. The announcement had been careful, no exact time, no map pin, but it didn’t matter. Word of mouth had done its work. Fans were lined up two blocks deep, and even the press kept to their penned lane under the watch of uniformed officers lounging like disinterested cats with very sharp claws.

“Final comms check,” Rio said softly, sliding her earpiece into place. “Alpha team?”

“North roof, eyes on,” Clint replied. “Glass glare is rough, but I’ve got the press lane and the crowd’s right flank.”

“West alley,” Bucky said. “Two blocks out. If someone bolts, I’ll be their problem.”

“Embedded in crowd,” Natasha added, her voice low-throated and calm. “Section B, left of the stage, third row.”

“Section D, vendor side,” Yelena chimed. “Pretending to buy a stale pretzel. Terrible choice.”

“In the van, backline,” Alice said. “City camera grid is mine. Facial-rec spun up, Renna, Raven, Maera, and the Cicadas are hot-listed. I’ll ping if I get a hit. Also, searching hashtags in real time.”

“Local units?” Rio asked.

Maria answered from the command tent they’d erected behind the stage, clipboard tucked under her arm like a ceremonial sword. “Six plainclothes inside the crowd, four in the press, two medics posted in the alley. The chief owes me three favors. Today I’m cashing two.”

Agatha smoothed her jacket and took a breath she hoped would reach the soles of her feet. “You all look like you’re going to war,” she murmured, half to herself.

“We are,” Wanda said quietly from behind her, the hand on Agatha’s shoulder both anchor and promise.

Rio’s gaze swept the plaza one last time. “We control the ground,” she said. “We control the exits. We do not improvise unless we have to. Agatha?”

Agatha looked at her. “I won’t wander. I won’t play hero. If you say move, I move.”

They stepped out into a roar that rattled the sycamores. The crowd pressed forward, then held, restrained by metal and good sense and the men in blue. Phones lifted like a field of stars. Agatha lifted a hand, smiling, and the volume shifted from wild to warm.

“Hey, Coven,” she called into the mic Jen thrust at her, voice steadying in the space that had been hers since she was a teenager. “I said I wouldn’t hide. So… hi.” Laughter rolled back to her like surf. “We’re keeping this short and safe. We’ve got a quick line for photos and hellos, and then I have to get back to work. But I wanted to see you. Thank you for showing up, for me, and for each other.”

She stepped down from the riser to the small rope-chute they’d built, flanked by Rio on the right and Maria two steps back. Fans came through one by one; teary, shaking, grinning, gruff. She signed posters, books, and a witch's hat. She posed for photos, brushed off apologies with jokes, and kept her breathing even.

After ten minutes, Jen lifted a hand; time to rotate. Rio touched Agatha’s elbow, and she pivoted smoothly. The crowd was a sea of faces and lenses, forgettable until someone wasn’t.

“Facial match seventy percent, left side, press lane, blonde with sunglasses,” Alice said in their ears. “Adjusting angle… ninety-one percent. Raven Corvin. Tagging feed.”

“It’s her,” Clint confirmed from above. “Press queue, second row. Black blazer, white tee, credential lanyard. She’s wearing a photographer’s vest.”

“Copy,” Rio said calmly, letting none of the adrenaline leak into her tone. “Natasha, you’re lead.”

“Moving,” Natasha replied. Her path through the bodies was a ballet of shoulders and apologies. She slipped into the press line and slid up alongside the blonde, close enough to share perfume. Raven’s mouth trembled, amusement? Fear? Her hand slid deeper into the vest pocket.

“Don’t,” Natasha said, voice pitched so low only Raven could hear. “Hands where I can see them.”

Raven lifted her chin instead. “You’re prettier in person.”

“Hands,” Natasha repeated.

Something flickered in Raven’s eyes, calculation, maybe, or an old habit of charming her way out of corners. She turned her palms up, empty. Natasha moved as if stretching, and the line shifted with her. In a heartbeat, there were two plainclothes at Raven’s shoulders and an officer moving a barricade to create a pocket of space that looked, to most eyes, like a routine adjustment.

“We’ve got her,” Natasha said, slipping the zip-tie on so fast it might have been a magic trick. Raven didn’t struggle. She smiled, slow and strange.

“Tell Agatha I loved her first,” she said, eyes wandering toward the stage. “Tell her to look at me.”

“Not a chance,” Natasha murmured, and signaled the extraction. Raven was taken into the side alley before most of the cameras realized anything had happened.

The cheer shifted; news of something moving in the press lane rippled across the plaza on the backs of whispers and phones. Rio kept her expression neutral and her body loose.

“Alice,” she said, “mass text the interior team: stay steady, stay smiling, no other moves unless we have a lock. We don’t spook the fish while we have one in the net.”

“Copy,” Alice said, and then her voice sharpened. “New ping. Left flank, fan section—row five, purple scarf, baseball cap. Renna. Eighty-eight percent match, rising. She’s watching Agatha, not her phone. She’s—yeah. Ninety-six percent match. Rio, that’s her.”

“I see her,” Clint said, the lens whirring in his tone. “She’s twitchy. Looking for cameras.”

“Yelena?” Rio asked.

“Already on my way,” Yelena replied, abandoning the stale pretzel without regret. “Do we want to take her quietly or loudly?”

“Quiet, if we can. Loud if we must,” Rio said.

Agatha was two fans away from the end of the segment when a woman at the barricade turned, eyes wide, and shouted toward the line of black suits. “Rio! It’s her! The blonde—the one from the posts!” She pointed, frantic, pulling at the sleeve of the girl next to her. “There! The cap!”

For a split second, the sound changed, the tone tilting like a glass set down too hard. Renna flinched, head snapping toward the cry. And then she bolted.

“Runner,” Clint barked. “Left flank, moving north toward the alley behind the coffee cart.”

“On it,” Yelena said, launching after her with a flurry of motion that made speed look like the most natural thing in the world.

“Bucky, cut her off at the second alley,” Rio said, already moving. “Agatha, with me.” She turned, and for a half breath, Agatha’s eyes clung to hers, fear, anger, resolve, and then she handed her mic to Jen and stepped back into the shadow of two agents who appeared as if conjured.

“I’ve got Agatha,” Maria confirmed. “We’re taking her to the corridor.”

And then Rio was running.

The alley smelled like fry oil and wet cardboard, the ground slick with something sticky. Renna’s cap flashed and vanished between service doors. Yelena’s braid snapped like a whip as she cut the corner. Bucky emerged from the cross street like a wall that had learned to move.

“Stop!” he barked. Renna juked hard right. Bucky swore and sprang after her.

They hit the sidewalk, and the city opened—horns, bikes, a bus sighing at a curb. Renna shoved past a man with a dog and sprinted across a patch of grass toward a construction fence, scrambling up like a feral cat. Yelena took the fence, too, and swung cleanly over, landing five feet from Renna’s stumble.

“Don’t make me embarrass you,” Yelena panted, almost cheerful.

Renna threw a handful of gravel and ran.

Alice’s voice was cool steel in their ears. “Traffic is heavy on 6th. If she goes east, you lose the clear line. West is better, fewer cars, more pedestrians.”

“Copy,” Rio said, her breath steady despite the burning in her legs. She gained on Renna at the crosswalk, boots pounding the white paint. Renna barreled through, eyes wild, and a horn blared so close the air bowed.

“Don’t—!” Rio shouted, reaching—

Renna darted between two cars and out into the next lane, head turned back over her shoulder, triumph like a fever on her face. She didn’t see the city bus until it was wholly there, an impossible rectangle filling her world. There was a single, collective sound, an inhale that belonged to a thousand throats, and then the impact slammed sound into silence.

Everything stopped.

Rio’s body made the decision her mind didn’t have time to form. She cut left, shoulder-checking a stunned pedestrian out of her path, and slid on her knees beside Renna’s crumpled body. Blood slicked the asphalt in an ordinary, obscene smear. She put pressure on what she could reach and spoke in the voice she used to talk people back from edge.

“Stay with me. Stay with me.”

Renna’s eyes flicked, the triumph gone, something bitter and childish clawing at what was left. Her lips moved; nothing came out. She tried again.

“She… owes… me,” she croaked, and then her eyes rolled back, and her body went lax under Rio’s hands.

“Medic!” Rio barked. “Now!”

“Two blocks out,” Maria said, voice distant and too calm. “On the way.”

Bucky crouched beside her, jaw set, hand outstretched and useless. Yelena stood very still, the wind lifting a piece of hair across her cheek like a private gesture of mourning she would never admit.

The siren rose before the medic’s shape, the cry of something designed to move through the world as if it owned it. It pulled up half on the curb, doors flinging open, and then there were gloved hands and the language of triage. Rio gave them everything: what had happened, how many seconds had passed. She fell back when they took over. Blood streaked her palms and the knees of her pants, and for a moment she saw another street, another body, another desperate press of hands.

“Vidal.” Bucky’s voice brought her back like a slap. “Look at me.”

She did. His eyes were the same as they’d been in a dozen countries, right before the ground learned to move and took men with it. “This isn’t on you,” he said quietly. “You did it right.”

Rio nodded once, the motion blunt and insufficient.

“Status?” Alice asked, voice carefully neutral.

“Renna is down,” Rio said. “EMS is actively working. Send an Agent to follow up at the hospital and notify PD. Secure the plaza. Keep Agatha moving.”

“Copy,” Maria answered crisply. “Raven is in custody, on the way to secure holding. Agatha is safe inside the corridor with Wanda and two agents. Press is… feral. Jen is doing her job.”

“Tell her to prep a statement,” Rio said, standing. “Accident during a police-assisted pursuit. Sympathy for the family. No further comment pending investigation.”

Bucky flanked her as they cleared the scene for the medics to load. The bus driver sat on the curb, white as winter, hands shaking between his knees. Rio paused, just long enough to touch his shoulder.

“I’m sorry,” she said quietly. “It happened fast. This wasn’t your fault.”

He nodded without looking, his eyes somewhere far away.

By the time they reached the plaza again, the energy had bent into something taut and brittle. News of a chase and a crash had reached the crowd before they did; information moved faster than feet. Agatha stood behind the stage screen with Wanda, the two of them bracketed by Sonya and Steve. She looked up when Rio approached, face searching hers like a hand in the dark.

Rio gave her the truth, not all of it, not here. “Raven is in custody,” she said softly. “Renna ran. There was an accident. She didn’t make it.”

Agatha’s hand came up, then fell, then came up again and found Rio’s sleeve. “Is that relief?” she asked in a voice that wasn’t hers. “Or am I going to hell because I don’t know what to feel?”

“It’s shock,” Rio said, and the kindness in her voice was a mercy. “And it’s okay.” She glanced past Agatha’s shoulder to Wanda, who nodded once, fierce and gentle.

Jen appeared, tablet already glowing with headline permutations. “I’ve got three drafts,” she said, eyes flicking between Rio and Agatha. “Short sympathy. Longer sympathy with safety emphasis. Or we say nothing and let SHIELD take the first hit.”

“SHIELD first,” Rio decided. “Neutral, procedural. Then Agatha echoes with thanks and a reminder not to engage, not to romanticize this. Lilia can speak to the cost, if she wants. We do not gloat. We do not taunt. We keep it human.”

“Copy,” Jen said, already typing.

Alice’s voice came in like a weather report. “Crowd still calm, if restless. Fans are talking about how they spotted Renna, there’s pride in it. We should harness that. It’s good for the narrative and for the tip lines.”

“Give them the right phrases,” Maria said. “They want to help; we tell them how to do it safely.”

Natasha stepped into the tent’s edge, as quiet as a blade. “Raven didn’t fight,” she reported. “But she smiled. We’ll see if she keeps doing that when the room gets small.”

Agatha swallowed. “Do I… go back out?” Her eyes flicked toward the stage, where a hundred paper signs still bobbed in hopeful hands.

Rio hesitated, then shook her head. “No. Not now.” She softened it with a touch to Agatha’s fingers. “You were seen. That mattered. Now we control the exit.”

They moved the pieces fast. The perimeter tightened; the crowd was thanked and dismissed in a voice Jen scripted and a volunteer read into a mic. The fans went like tide, reluctant but obedient, chattering like starlings. A handful lingered at the barricades and pressed small gifts into the hands of agents with soft smiles: letters, bracelets, a purple paper crane.

“Those are for her,” a teenager whispered to Sonya, eyes big. “Tell her we’re not scared.”

Sonya surprised herself by softening. “I will.”

The convoy rolled a different route, the city turning its usual indifference back on itself. In the second SUV, Agatha watched the feeds Jen had pulled to her phone, thumb hovering over a flood of messages that were neither hate nor worship but something stranger: gratitude, pride, grief for a stranger who had tried to ruin her life and died in the process.

At a red light, she caught her reflection in the glass, tired, composed, older than yesterday, and then Rio’s beside her, steady as a lighthouse. Agatha reached across the inches and intertwined their fingers, needing the answer their bodies had been giving each other for weeks.

In the lead car, Maria took a call on speaker. “EMS just confirmed,” she said, voice even. “Time of death at the scene.”

Silence answered, respectful and practical and tired.

“Bucky and I will handle PD,” Rio said. “Natasha, you and Yelena sit with Raven until I get there. No heroics. No theatrics.”

“Only professionalism,” Natasha said dryly. “And perhaps a smile.”

“Please don’t smile,” Maria muttered, but they could all hear the corner of her mouth lift.

 

The house was quieter than it had been in weeks, but the silence was deceptive. Outside the gates, paparazzi still prowled. Social media still churned with theories, hashtags, and blurry photos. And inside, every person in Agatha’s circle carried the invisible hum of exhaustion, the weight of the staged meet-and-greet, Raven’s capture, and Renna’s sudden death in the street.

Steve and Sonya patrolled the perimeter, shadows slipping across the windows whenever they circled the porch. Natasha and Yelena had claimed the dining room table, pretending to play cards, though both were listening on comms, eyes sharp. Bucky sat in the den with his rifle across his lap, disassembling and cleaning it with the precision of someone keeping his hands busy to keep his mind still. Alice, hunched in the surveillance van, muttered curses at code and firewalls. Clint is talking to his wife and kids in his room.

And then there was the kitchen, where Agatha lingered at the threshold, arms folded, unsure if she belonged in this moment of domesticity after so much blood and chaos. She still didn’t know what to feel about Renna—relief, sorrow, guilt. The woman had once adored her, and now she was gone. Agatha had built her career controlling a narrative, and this was one she couldn’t rewrite.

Rio emerged from the pantry with her sleeves rolled up and a paper bag in hand, flannel loose at the collar. There was something almost mischievous about her expression, something that looked out of place but desperately needed.

“How would you like to help me make Korean corn dogs for dinner tonight, cariño?” Rio asked casually, as though she hadn’t just spent the day hunting down enemies and running interference for Agatha’s life.

Agatha blinked at her. “Now? Really? Is this the time?” Her voice wavered, betraying the uncertainty in her chest.

Rio set the bag down on the counter and crossed the kitchen, cupping Agatha’s face in her hands. Her calloused thumbs brushed gently along her cheekbones, steadying her. “We’ve taken three pieces off the board, mi vida—Kyra, Raven, and Renna. Soon we’ll find the rest. This is a time for celebration, even if it’s just us. Besides—” her mouth twitched into the smallest smile— “I promised you I’d make these one day. Had one of the agents run out for the ingredients.”

Agatha’s lips quirked, unwillingly tugged toward warmth. “You’re ridiculous.”

“And you’re stalling,” Rio countered smoothly.

With a theatrical sigh, Agatha threw up her hands. “Fine. But if I burn this place down, you can’t blame me.”

“Good thing I’m fireproof,” Rio teased, pressing a quick kiss to her forehead before moving to the counter.

The kitchen soon filled with the clatter of bowls, the sharp hiss of oil heating, and a chorus of voices drifting in. Natasha and Yelena peeked in from the dining room, Yelena smirking. “If this is domestic bliss, I want no part of it. But also—save me two.”

“Two?” Natasha asked dryly. “She’ll want five.”

“Ten,” Yelena corrected solemnly, arms crossed.

Agatha swatted at them with a dish towel, earning a laugh from the sisters. “You vultures. Let us at least cook them before you steal them all.”

Bucky leaned in the doorway, arms folded, smirk tugging at his mouth. “Domestic life suits you two. Never thought I’d see Harkness in an apron.”

Agatha looked down at the borrowed apron Rio had tied around her waist, then flipped the towel at him. “Careful, Barnes. I may like you, but I’ve got a bodyguard who terrifies me in all the right ways.”

Rio didn’t even look up from skewering mozzarella sticks, but Agatha caught the faint smile tugging at her lips. The room warmed in a way it hadn’t in weeks.

And then the reinforcements arrived.

Lilia swept in first, coat draped around her shoulders like armor. Wanda followed, slipping her shoes off at the door. Jen and Billy trailed behind, bickering about whether pineapple belonged on pizza. The moment they spotted Agatha dusted in flour with Rio at her side, all conversation stopped.

“Oh, this is precious,” Lilia drawled, her eyes glinting. “Agatha Harkness cooking? Someone get a camera.”

“Already got it,” Billy said, phone halfway out of his pocket, before Agatha shot him a glare that could curdle milk.

“Put it away, boy,” she ordered, trying not to laugh.

Wanda perched against the counter, arms crossed, smirk firmly in place. “I thought you said you couldn’t even boil water without supervision.”

“I can’t,” Agatha admitted, brandishing the wooden spoon like a sword. “That’s why I’m letting Rio do all the dangerous work. I’m just here to look pretty.”

“You’re succeeding,” Rio muttered, so low it was meant only for Agatha.

But Wanda’s ears caught it. “Oh, my god. Did she just flirt in public? Mark the calendar.”

Jen clapped her hands together. “Finally! Our resident ice queen melts. Rio, what’s your secret? Is it the flannel? It’s the flannel, isn’t it?”

Agatha groaned, tossing the towel onto the counter. “This is harassment.”

“This is justice,” Wanda corrected.

“Justice with a side of fried cheese,” Lilia added dryly, settling into a chair.

The first batch came out golden and crisp, set carefully on a rack by Rio. Yelena darted in, grabbing one before anyone else could. She yelped dramatically when it burned her tongue, but didn’t stop chewing.

“Good,” she declared. “Too good. I call dibs.”

“On what? The whole tray?” Natasha asked, swiping one for herself.

Bucky snagged another, nodding his approval. “Better than rations. Don’t quit your day job, but… not bad, Vidal.”

“High praise,” Rio deadpanned.

Alice eventually wandered in, with dark circles under her eyes, but drawn by the smell. She grabbed two, muttering something about deserving sustenance after drowning in code all day. Steve and Sonya came in from their patrol, rifles still slung, faces softening at the sight of food.

And then the kitchen transformed into something Agatha hadn’t seen in too long: laughter, clinking plates, voices overlapping in warmth instead of strategy or fear. Wanda stole half of Agatha’s corn dog, only to get smacked with the towel. Billy teased Rio about burning oil, earning himself a firm swat from Lilia. Even Jen cracked a smile between bites, though she kept one eye on her phone, already bracing for the media storm that would follow tomorrow. Clint, Natasha, and Yelena are bickering over something Agatha doesn’t understand.

Agatha leaned back against the counter, watching the chaos unfold like it was a rare treasure. This team, this patchwork family, they had carried her through fire and fear. And at the center of it all was Rio, sleeves rolled, hair pulled back, laughing in a way Agatha hadn’t heard in weeks. It felt like sunlight breaking through storm clouds.

When the plates emptied and the chatter mellowed, the others drifted off, Natasha and Maria on a call, Wanda dragging Billy into a debate about which Disney princess would win in a fight, mother and son strongly defending their picks, Yelena guarding her last corn dog like it was classified intel. The kitchen quieted until it was just Rio and Agatha again.

Rio leaned against the counter beside her, wiping her hands on a towel. “See? Not so bad.”

Agatha tilted her head, smiling despite the heaviness still curled in her chest. “You’re infuriating, you know that? Making me laugh when I should be stewing.”

“Stewing doesn’t change anything,” Rio murmured, reaching for her hand. “But laughing reminds you why you fight.”

Agatha’s throat tightened. She let Rio lace their fingers together, her thumb brushing over Rio’s knuckles. “I’ll admit it. This was exactly what I needed.”

Rio bent down, close enough for her breath to ghost against Agatha’s lips. “Good. Because tonight? Tonight we choose joy.”

Agatha let her kiss her then—slow, tender, tasting breadcrumbs and warmth and something like hope. For the first time in weeks, she believed it.

Agatha’s hand lingered against Rio’s cheek, her thumb stroking across skin that had spent years set in stone but now softened beneath her touch. The rest of the world fell away, the hum of the fridge, the muffled laughter of the team down the hall, even the shadow of Renna’s death still clawing at her mind. All she could focus on was Rio: her warmth, her scent, the safety and danger all bound up in one.

Rio kissed her again, slower this time, lips coaxing instead of commanding. Agatha leaned in, sighing against her mouth, her chest pressing into Rio’s as though she could pour herself into her bodyguard and never have to stand on her own again.

When Rio pulled back, just barely, their noses brushing, Agatha whispered, “You terrify me.”

Rio stilled. Her brow furrowed, misreading the words. “Terrify you?”

Agatha smiled faintly, a tear threatening but not falling. “Because I’ve never wanted someone this much. Because if you ever walked away, I think I’d unravel.” She laughed once, sharp and self-deprecating. “And because I never thought I’d be reckless enough to fall in love again.”

Rio’s breath caught. For a moment, she said nothing, just searched Agatha’s eyes like she was scanning for a trap. But all she saw was raw, trembling truth.

“You’re in love with me,” Rio said, voice low and rough, as though speaking it aloud was dangerous.

Agatha tilted her head, a smirk tugging at her lips despite the vulnerability. “Was I not obvious? I thought the shameless flirting, the clinging, the jealous glares at anyone who so much as looks at you might’ve given it away.”

Rio huffed a laugh, shaking her head. “Agatha—”

“No.” Agatha pressed a finger to her lips. “I’m not joking this time. I love you, Rio. Completely. Irrationally. Hopelessly.” Her voice broke on the last word. “And if that scares you, well, it scares me too. But I can’t hold it in anymore.”

For a long moment, Rio didn’t move. Her chest rose and fell, eyes glinting like storm clouds caught in sunlight. Then she caught Agatha’s hand, pressed it flat against her heart, and whispered, “You think you’re the only one who’s terrified? I’ve spent my whole life building walls, keeping people safe, but never letting them close after Val. You kicked those walls down without even trying. And it scared the hell out of me.”

Agatha’s throat tightened. “Rio…”

Rio’s lips trembled, but she pressed on. “I love you. I’ve loved you longer than I let myself admit. From the moment you looked at me in that conference room, like you already knew me. I tried to fight it, because God knows, loving you makes me reckless. But it’s the truth. I love you, Agatha Harkness.”

Agatha didn’t answer with words at first. She surged forward, capturing Rio’s mouth with hers, pouring every ounce of relief, joy, and fire into the kiss. Rio groaned softly, hands sliding to Agatha’s waist, gripping her like she might vanish.

When they finally broke apart, panting, Agatha whispered against her lips, “Say it again.”

Rio’s forehead rested against hers. “I love you.”

Again, Agatha demanded silently with her eyes.

“I love you,” Rio repeated, firmer, surer. “And I’m not going anywhere.”

Agatha smiled so wide it almost hurt. “Good. Because I plan to keep you.”

Rio chuckled, then silenced her with another kiss. This one turned hot fast, urgency overtaking tenderness. Agatha’s hands tangled in Rio’s hair, pulling her closer, while Rio’s fingers dug into the curve of her hips. The spoon on the counter clattered to the floor when Agatha’s elbow knocked it aside. Neither of them cared.

They stumbled backward, mouths never parting, until Agatha’s back hit the fridge with a soft thud. She gasped, laughing breathlessly, but Rio swallowed the sound with her tongue, devouring her like she’d been starving for years.

Somewhere down the hall, Wanda shouted at Billy about stealing the last corn dog. The laughter and noise of the house felt far away, muffled beneath the pounding of their own hearts. For once, Agatha didn’t care who heard or saw, this was theirs.

Rio grabbed Agatha’s hand and tugged, half-leading, half-dragging her toward the hallway. They kissed sloppily as they went, bumping into the edge of the counter, stumbling over a chair leg. Agatha giggled into Rio’s mouth, biting her bottom lip playfully.

“You’re going to kill us both before we make it to the room,” Agatha teased, breathless.

“Worth it,” Rio growled, slamming her back against the wall to kiss her deeper.

They tripped down the hall, hitting picture frames and doorframes, never breaking apart. Agatha’s coat slipped from her shoulders, forgotten on the floor. Rio’s flannel came half undone, tugged impatiently by Agatha’s roaming hands.

By the time they reached Rio’s bedroom door, they were laughing and gasping between kisses, their bodies already pressed flush. Rio kicked the door open with a grunt, shoved Agatha inside, and closed it with a thud as their mouths met again.

The world outside could wait. For tonight, there was only this: love confessed, fear undone, and the heat of two women who’d finally stopped running from what was inevitable.

And for the first time in their lives, neither of them wanted to run again.

Whispers and Shouts

Chapter Summary

A little Bit of Downtime, Talks are had, bonds are forged. Menace Agatha makes a reappearance.

Chapter Notes

Sorry, this chapter took longer to come out. I was stuck on how to get this story to where I want to go. Also, my internet went down for a few hours, so I couldn't post.

A little rushed, so not proofread, Sorry

The morning light was pale and forgiving, the kind of gold that seemed to stretch time thin. Agatha stirred first, blinking at the faint smell of coffee drifting through the room. The space was quiet save for the gentle hum of the heater and the muffled shuffle of someone moving in the kitchen.

She turned her head to find Rio still beside her, propped up against the headboard with a mug in hand, hair mussed and damp from an early shower. She wore a gray T-shirt and loose sweatpants, utterly unguarded, utterly domestic. Agatha blinked, smiling softly.

“You made coffee,” she said, her voice still husky from sleep.

Rio handed her the second mug on the nightstand. “Of course. I wasn’t about to risk your wrath by letting you wake up uncaffeinated.”

Agatha took the mug, curling into Rio’s side as naturally as breathing. The warmth of the coffee seeped through her fingers, but the warmth of Rio’s arm around her shoulder was what settled her chest. For a long moment, they sat in silence, just sipping and letting the quiet stretch.

“Last night wasn’t a dream, right?” Agatha asked at last, tilting her face toward Rio.

Rio’s thumb brushed the back of her hand. “No dream. I meant every word, mi vida.”

Agatha exhaled softly, leaning her head against Rio’s shoulder. “Good. Because if it was, it was the kind I’d fight to stay in.”

Rio smiled, pressing a kiss to the crown of her hair. “You’re ridiculous.”

“You love it.”

“I love you,” Rio corrected gently, the words easier now, steady.

Agatha stilled, then smiled in a way that felt brand new, brighter than any stage light she’d ever stood under. “Say that again.”

Rio turned her head and did, brushing her lips against Agatha’s temple. “I love you.”

Agatha closed her eyes, whispering back, “I love you too.”

They didn’t need to fill the silence after that. It was enough to curl together in bed, coffee cooling on the nightstand, the world held at bay just a little longer. Agatha let herself believe that, for this moment at least, there were no stalkers, no threats, no cameras waiting outside. Just two women, warm and tired and stupidly in love, sharing a morning that felt almost ordinary.

“Do we have to get up today?” Agatha murmured.

Rio smirked, pulling her tighter against her chest. “Eventually. But not yet.”

So they didn’t.

Morning at the Harkness house felt…different. Lighter, somehow. The winter sun pooled across the kitchen tile, and the long farmhouse table was loaded with mismatched mugs, a mountain of toast, a skillet of scrambled eggs, and a suspicious number of empty hot sauce bottles that had “Yelena” written all over them.

Natasha sat at the head of the table, unbothered serenity incarnate, flipping through her phone. Yelena was elbow-deep in a jar of pickles like it was an emotional support animal. Clint was methodically buttering toast with sniper-level focus. Alice typed one-handed on her laptop while sipping coffee strong enough to dissolve a spoon. Bucky had the morning paper open but hadn’t turned a page in five minutes. On the other end, Lilia, Wanda, Jen, and Billy clustered like a committee, whispering in the very unsubtle way of people who very much wanted to be overheard.

Then Rio and Agatha walked in.

Rio: soft gray tee, joggers, wet hair. Agatha: oversized navy cardigan over a silk camisole, bare feet, a glow that could power Los Angeles. They were close enough to share a heartbeat, hands brushing, eyes doing that private, secret language thing that made everyone else at the table exchange the same badly concealed smirk.

“Morning,” Agatha sang, sliding into the chair beside Rio and promptly nabbing half the strawberries from her plate.

“Morning,” the table answered, too sweetly, in perfect chorus.

Rio poured coffee, pretending not to notice twelve eyes on them. “What’d we miss?”

“Sleep,” Yelena said, far too loudly. “Many of us missed sleep.”

Natasha didn’t look up. “Truly shocking for a security team used to night ops.”

“Night ops do not usually involve—” Yelena circled a hand in the air, grasping for a diplomatic term. “—theatrical sound design.”

Bucky coughed into his mug. Clint bit the inside of his cheek, losing the fight with a grin. Alice covered her mouth and typed, “theatrical sound design” into her notes, because of course she did.

Agatha’s lips parted in delighted scandal. “Did we… keep people up?” She sounded thrilled.

Jen dropped her forehead to the table. “Up? Honey, I learned new vocabulary.”

Billy fanned himself with a dish towel. “At one point I considered calling the fire department.”

Wanda raised a hand like a witness in court. “I put a pillow over my head and still learned… a lot about acoustics.”

Rio choked on her coffee, color blooming high on her cheekbones. “Okay, that’s, everyone can stop now.”

“Impossible,” Yelena said. “We are just getting started.”

Lilia lifted her mug with maternal gravitas. “As your manager and the matriarch of this group, I have a moral obligation to say: good for you. Also, perhaps next time, soundproofing.”

Agatha slid her hand to the back of Rio’s neck and scratched lightly at the hairline, the way she now knew made Rio melt. “Don’t listen to them, cariño. We were very tastefully loud.”

“Those words don’t go together,” Alice murmured, eyes still on her screen, though the corner of her mouth was betraying her.

Clint leaned in from across the table. “Look, I’m not saying it was a symphony, but there were… movements.”

“Allegro,” Bucky offered.

“Molto,” Wanda added, straight-faced.

Agatha pressed her knuckles to her mouth and giggled like a teenager. Rio gave up and laughed too, that low, warm sound that made several people at the table exchange a “there it is” glance.

“Okay, okay,” Rio said, palms up, surrendering. “We will… consider the soundproofing. And issue a formal apology to the household.”

Jen peeked up. “Accepted. In writing, please. With a fruit basket.”

“Done,” Agatha said instantly, then leaned into Rio’s shoulder and kissed her cheek. “Though for the record, I regret nothing.”

“You never do,” Wanda said dryly, fondness softening every word.

The teasing ebbed just enough for breakfast to resume. Plates circled. Toast vanished. Someone passed Yelena another hot sauce, and Alice finally put the laptop down long enough to inhale eggs.

In the soft lull, Lilia watched the two women with the kind of gaze that knew history and hurt and had been waiting for this. “You look happy,” she said, not as a question.

Agatha turned, face open, almost shy beneath the mischief. “I am.”
