Rio’s hand found Agatha’s beneath the table. Fingers laced. “Me too,” she said simply.

The room shifted, just a fraction, like the whole house breathed out. Whatever they’d all suspected, joked about, tiptoed around, was now warm and undeniable in the morning light.

Agatha reached for the jam, missed, and ended up smearing a stripe of raspberry on Rio’s wrist. She caught Rio’s hand without thinking and licked it off, slow and a little wicked.

The table went silent for a beat. Then Yelena dropped her fork. “Prison. I should be in prison. You cannot do that before 9 a.m.”

Bucky folded his paper at last, deadpan as granite. “We will pass out blindfolds at breakfast from now on.”

Rio set her forehead briefly against Agatha’s temple, groaning into her hair. “They’re never going to let us live, are they?”

“No,” Agatha said cheerfully. “And I love it.”

Wanda’s smile gentled. “It’s good to see you both like this. We needed a win.”

“We did,” Rio agreed. The steel in her eyes didn’t vanish, couldn’t, not with everything still ahead, but it softened around the edges. “And there will be more.”

Alice cleared her throat, business sneaking back in. “There will also be debrief at ten. Media fallout. Forensics from Raven’s devices. Leads from the tip line.”

Jen nodded, lifting her coffee. “And I’ve got talking points for the morning shows. We’ll control the narrative.”

“Mm,” Agatha hummed, already sliding her chair closer to Rio’s. “As long as none of those talking points include my nocturnal… cardio.”

“God, please,” Billy muttered. “I’m a child.”

“You are twenty-two,” Lilia said, patting his hand. “And last night you learned more than any internship could teach you.”

“Lilia,” Wanda warned, choking on her coffee.

“What? I’m supportive.”

They dissolved into laughter again, softer, easier this time. It rolled around the table and settled into the walls, another thread woven into the strange tapestry they’d made together: soldiers and spies, a publicist with a dragon’s bite, a manager with a lion’s heart, a genius with sleep-deprived eyes, a few misfits who’d become a family, and at the center, an actress and her bodyguard who were no longer pretending not to be in love.

Agatha finished her coffee and stood, tugging lightly at the hem of Rio’s shirt. “Walk me to wardrobe?”

“In your own house?” Clint asked.

“It’s about the journey,” Agatha said loftily.

Rio stood, fighting a smile, and let herself be led. At the doorway, she glanced back. “Ten a.m., war room.”

“Copy,” Natasha said.

“And, uh,” Rio added, cheeks pinking again, “thanks for… the notes on our volume control.”

“Buy a rug,” Yelena called. “Thick one. I’ll invoice you for the therapy.”

Agatha blew a kiss over her shoulder. “No refunds.”

They disappeared down the hall, hands brushing, laughter echoing after them. Around the table, the team traded looks, fond, exasperated, relieved. Outside, Steve and Sonya paced the line, watchful as ever. Inside, for one fragile morning, everything felt almost normal. 

Later that day, Rio and Agatha were curled up on the couch, locked in a mock-serious debate over which captain reigned supreme on Below Deck.

“Captain Sandy has the best leadership skills, end of story,” Rio argued, crossing her arms with military precision.

Agatha scoffed dramatically. “Please, darling. It’s Captain Lee. The man is iconic. Have you seen his one-liners? He could sink a yacht and still make it sound charming.”

Billy, perched on the armrest, jumped in eagerly. “Captain Glenn is underrated. Chillest guy in the franchise. I’d actually sail with him.”

Wanda, sipping from her wineglass, gave an approving nod. “I agree. Glenn doesn’t yell, and people still respect him. That’s power.”

The laughter that followed was easy, warm, four voices tangling together like a family dinner table argument. 

Then the air shifted. Jen swept into the room like a stormfront, tension clinging to her every step. Without a word, she dropped her laptop onto the table with a heavy thunk. The sound cut through the laughter, silencing it instantly. All eyes swung toward her, and then to the screen, as if the glowing device itself might explain the sudden weight pressing into the room.

Jen clicked a key, and the screen filled with news articles, headlines bold and sensational.

“Agatha Harkness’ Stalkers Finally Named – Two Captured, One Dead After Chase”
 “The Seventh Veil Unmasked: Online Fandom Shaken”
 “From Fan Pages to Felonies: The Dark Descent of Agatha’s Obsessives”

Jen’s voice was steady, though her eyes betrayed fatigue. “The media storm hasn’t slowed since last night. Every major outlet is running with the story: Raven in custody, Renna dead. Agatha, your name is trending globally again. Fans are torn, some are grieving what they thought were ‘beloved fan figures,’ others are furious on your behalf, and the majority? They’re demanding justice.”

Agatha’s jaw tightened, but she said nothing. Rio slid a hand across her knee under the table, grounding her.

Jen cleared her throat. “And then there’s this.”

A new set of posts appeared, the usernames generic, burner accounts. But the tone is unmistakable.

@CicadaSong89: You took my sister. You took Renna. And you dare celebrate? This isn’t over. Agatha, you’ll bleed for her death.

@SereneSpeaks: Kyra rots in your cage. Renna’s blood is on your hands. I won’t forgive. I won’t forget. You think cutting us down one by one makes you safe? You’re wrong. Every move you make, I’ll be watching. Every laugh, every kiss, every secret—I’ll burn it all down.

Alice leaned forward, scrolling on her own tablet. “Both posts match digital signatures tied to Seren Auden. No attempt to hide it. She wants us to know she’s pissed.”

“That’s putting it lightly,” Clint muttered.

“Good,” Natasha said coolly, arms crossed. “Anger makes people sloppy. She’s waving her hand like a flare. She’ll come to us.”

Bucky shook his head. “Or she’ll come at us. Seren’s not just mad. She’s unhinged. Kyra’s her twin, they built this thing together. You lock up one, kill the other, and she’s gonna make it personal.”

The room went heavy.

Agatha finally broke her silence. Her voice was low, trembling with something between fury and grief. “I didn’t want Renna dead. I just wanted this to stop. All of it. And now they’re using her like some martyr.”

Lilia stopped pacing, turned sharply. “Don’t you dare take that guilt, Agatha. Renna made her choice. She chose to hunt you, to smear you, to join this cult of obsession. Actions have consequences.” Her voice cracked, raw. “And Seren will pay hers.”

Rio squeezed Agatha’s hand, firm. “Listen to her. This isn’t on you. They put themselves in this fight when they came after you. And we’ll end it.”

Jen spoke again, softer now. “The fans know that, Agatha. They’re loud, angry, protective. They’re calling Seren’s posts what they are, threats. Hashtags like #ProtectAgatha and #ShutDownTheSeven are everywhere. But… so is #RennaDeservedBetter. It’s split. Which means Seren has an audience now.”

Wanda’s head snapped up at that. “Then we make sure Seren doesn’t get to use it. Amplify the truth. No one deserves to have their privacy violated, no one deserves to be hunted. That’s what we put out.”

Alice nodded. “And meanwhile, I keep tracking Seren’s movements. These posts weren’t just angry, they were careless. She left trails. I’ll find her.”

The silence that followed was sharp, everyone knowing the fight wasn’t close to over. Agatha exhaled slowly, lifting her chin, though her voice cracked on the words: “Then let’s finish this. All of it. Before anyone else dies.”

Rio pulled her closer, her steady gaze making the promise Agatha couldn’t say aloud. “We will.”

Agatha squeezed Rio’s hand once, quick and intimate, then excused herself toward the back door. “I need some air,” she said lightly, “and a moment alone.” Her smile was small but genuine; she gave Rio a look that said more than the words. Rio watched her go, then gave a single nod that was both permission and protection.

Bucky and Natasha were already up, moving like shadows that belonged to the room. They fell into positions along the back path, close enough to step in, far enough to preserve the privacy Agatha asked for. The house felt suddenly wide and thin without her presence, the soundtrack of normalcy missing a beat.

Rio was about to head to the study to sketch out bait lines and timelines, anything to keep the Seven off balance, when Wanda stepped up beside her. She approached without ceremony, that quiet inevitability people used to describe disasters and miracles. For a second, they simply regarded each other: two keepers of a woman they loved, both dangerous in their own ways.

“You and I haven’t talked,” Wanda said finally, voice low, steady. “Not really. And we should.”

Rio crossed her arms, schooling her face into neutrality. “Alright. What about?”

Wanda tilted her head, like she was measuring Rio’s heart rate through sheer will. “About Agatha. About what you mean to her. And what she means to you.”

Rio’s jaw tightened. “She means everything,” she said simply, but there was a weight in her tone that left no room for doubt.

Wanda stepped closer, softening slightly. “Then let’s be clear with each other. I’ve known Agatha longer than almost anyone. I’ve seen her fall in love, once. Her first love broke her in a way I didn’t think she’d recover from. It took years to piece her back together, years of work and trust. I don’t want to see her shattered like that again.”

Rio’s throat went dry. She swallowed. “I would never do that to her.”

Wanda arched a brow. “Not willingly, maybe. But you’re a soldier. And soldiers throw themselves into the fire. Don’t think I haven’t seen the way you stand between her and danger like you’re begging the universe to take you instead. You might not realize it, but to Agatha, losing you would break her just the same.”

The words landed heavier than Rio expected. She unclenched her fists, then rubbed the back of her neck as if to ground herself. “I’ve already lost one family like that. My Delta team. Valkyrie.” Her voice faltered, and she took a breath. “We were everything to each other. Then they were gone, and I survived. I still wake up feeling like I shouldn’t have. That guilt never leaves.”

Wanda listened quietly, her expression softening further. “And now you’ve found Agatha.”

Rio nodded. “She pulled me out of that spiral without even knowing it. At first, I fought it, hell, I fought it hard. I thought caring for her like this made me weak. But it doesn’t. It makes me want to fight harder. Still… I can’t lose her. I can’t survive another loss like that.”

Wanda’s hand came to rest lightly on Rio’s forearm, surprising them both. “Then don’t make it a choice between you or her. Protect her, yes. Love her, fiercely. But don’t martyr yourself. She doesn’t need another ghost to haunt her. She needs someone who stays.”

For a long moment, neither spoke. The weight of shared grief and shared love settled between them, and in that silence, an understanding formed.

“I love her,” Rio said finally, her voice rough but steady. “More than I’ve ever loved anyone. And I’ll do whatever it takes to protect her. Not just from the Seven, but from the fear that keeps her from believing she deserves to be loved.”

Wanda nodded slowly, her lips curving into something between a smile and a sigh. “Good. Because that’s the only way you’ll survive her. And she you.” She squeezed Rio’s arm before stepping back. “We’re on the same side, you and I. Different kinds of love, but the same fire.”

Rio let out a faint laugh, almost disbelieving. “Guess Agatha inspires that in people.”

“She does,” Wanda agreed softly. “She always has.”

The back door creaked open then, and Agatha stepped back inside, cheeks flushed from the night air. She caught sight of the two of them standing together, her brows quirking with suspicion.

“Well,” Agatha drawled, smirking faintly. “If this is the part where I find out you two have been in love this whole time and are plotting to murder me to get rid of the competition, because I can promise I will put up a good fight.”

Wanda only smiled and shook her head. Rio looked at Agatha, warmth blooming in her chest despite the heaviness of their talk.

“Nothing like that,” Rio said. “Just… understanding each other.”

Agatha narrowed her eyes, but she was smiling. “Mm. Dangerous. I should be worried.”

But when she stepped closer and took Rio’s hand, she looked more at peace than worried. And for Wanda and Rio both, that was enough. Agatha and Wanda walked to the kitchen, sharing secret laughs and whispers.

Rio lingered in the hallway long after Wanda and Agatha had left. She still felt the weight of that conversation in her chest, the unexpected honesty, the promise she’d made. She rubbed a hand down her face, thinking she should start working on a plan for Seren, anything to keep her mind sharp.

The study was dim when she pushed the door open. She expected quiet and papers, maybe a moment to collect her thoughts. Instead, she found Lilia seated in one of the leather chairs by the fireplace, a glass of red wine balanced elegantly in her hand.

On her lap rested a photo frame. Even in the low light, Rio recognized it: Colten. His sharp grin. His uniform.

Lilia didn’t look up at first. She traced the edge of the frame with her thumb, almost absently, like she’d done it a thousand times. Only when Rio cleared her throat did she speak.

“I didn’t expect company,” Lilia said softly, her Sicilian accent more pronounced with the weariness in her voice. “But maybe…maybe that’s not such a bad thing.”

Rio hesitated in the doorway, then crossed to the opposite chair after shutting the door. She sat slowly, her body stiff from the instinct to keep moving, keep fighting. But here, in this room, the fight felt different.

“I didn’t know you kept that picture here,” Rio said.

Lilia finally looked at her. Her eyes were wet, though no tears fell. “It’s the last one he sent me. He was smiling. He looked happy. I like to remember him that way.”

Rio swallowed. Guilt pressed against her ribs like it always did when Colten’s name came up. “He was happy, Lilia. Even out there. He was…he was a good soldier. Brave. Loyal. The kind of man you wanted beside you when everything went to hell.”

Lilia’s lips trembled into something between a smile and a grimace. “He always wanted to make you proud. Said once that you were the kind of leader he could follow through fire.”

Rio’s chest tightened. She leaned forward, resting her elbows on her knees. “I should’ve kept him safe. All of them. That was my job, and—”

“No,” Lilia cut her off, sharp enough that it startled Rio. The older woman’s eyes were fierce now, blazing through her grief. “Do not carry that weight alone. Colten knew the risks. He chose them. And he would hate you for sitting here and punishing yourself when you gave him purpose.”

Rio’s jaw clenched. She dropped her gaze to the floor. “I still regret not being there that day, not dying alongside my team.”

Lilia reached across the small table between them, her hand steady despite the wine glass she still held in the other. “You loved them. That is all a leader can do. And Colten…he loved you too. He spoke about you as though you were already family.”

The silence stretched, thick but not suffocating. Rio finally let herself breathe, the words tumbling out before she could stop them.

“Once, during downtime, Colten tried to teach the squad how to salsa. Said if we could survive gunfire, we could survive dancing.” Rio huffed out a laugh, shaking her head. “He had everyone stepping on each other’s boots, tripping over rifles. I swear, I thought Valkyrie was going to throttle him. But he didn’t care. He had this way of making the worst moments feel…light.”

Lilia’s hand flew to her mouth, her eyes crinkling as a laugh burst out, fragile but real. “That sounds like him. He never could sit still. Always had to make a scene.”

Rio allowed herself to smile too, the memory softening the edges of her guilt. “He saved me once. During a mission. I was pinned, exposed. He dragged me back behind cover, and when I told him he was reckless, he just grinned and said, ‘You’re reckless all the time, boss. Someone has to return the favor.’”

This time, Lilia’s tears did fall, but she was smiling through them. “That’s my boy.”

They sat there for a long moment, the wine between them, the photograph catching the glow of the firelight. For once, Rio didn’t try to fight the memories. She let them wash over her, good and bad, and let Lilia carry some of the weight with her.

“Thank you,” Lilia whispered finally. “For remembering him. For carrying him with you.”

Rio nodded, her voice low. “He deserves to be remembered. And as long as I breathe, he will be.”

The two women shared the silence, not as manager and soldier, but as mother and comrade, bound by the same loss.

For the first time since Colten’s death, Rio didn’t feel like she was carrying the burden alone. And Lilia, for the first time in months, didn’t feel like she was remembering her son by herself.

For the rest of the night, Rio and Lilia shared stories about Colten. Some made them laugh, others left their eyes shining with tears, but through it all, both women felt a little of the weight they’d been carrying slip away. By the time the bottle of wine ran dry, the study felt lighter, almost sacred, like Colten himself had lingered there with them.

When they finally rose, Lilia surprised Rio by pulling her into a strong hug. For a second, Rio froze. She hadn’t expected the gesture, but then she returned it just as fiercely. The embrace spoke of shared grief, of trust forged in pain. With a final pat to Rio’s shoulder, Lilia slipped away to her room. Rio lingered only a moment, then headed upstairs. Planning could wait until morning. Tonight, she needed her girlfriend.

She slipped quietly into their room and found Agatha curled on her side, eyes closed but not yet asleep. At the sound of Rio undressing, Agatha stirred, blinking up at her with a drowsy smile.

“There you are,” Agatha murmured, her voice husky from near-sleep. “I was beginning to think you’d gotten lost, or kidnapped by Wanda.”

Rio huffed a soft laugh and slid under the covers, tugging her shirt over her head before gathering Agatha into her arms. “I was with Lilia in the study,” she said, pulling her close until there was no space between them.

Agatha tilted her head back just enough to meet Rio’s gaze, eyes soft with understanding. “Good. You both needed that.”

Rio pressed a kiss to her temple. “We did.”

Half-asleep now, Agatha nestled further against her chest. “Jen wants me to do a livestream tomorrow,” she mumbled. “Alice will screen everyone before they’re allowed in, so Seren, or any of the Seven, can’t slip through.”

Rio brushed a hand through her hair, soothing. “We’ll talk more in the morning, mi amor. Rest now.”

Agatha sighed contentedly, letting the last of her tension drain away as she drifted toward sleep. Rio held her tighter, listening to the rhythm of her breathing. For the first time in what felt like forever, she allowed herself to close her eyes, knowing they were exactly where they were meant to be.



The next morning, the living room had been transformed into a makeshift studio. Jen fussed over lighting, adjusting stands until the glow was soft but flattering. Alice crouched beside the coffee table, her laptop tethered to Agatha’s, fingers flying as she fine-tuned the firewall and blocking protocols. No member of the Seven was slipping past her.

On the couch, Billy was in his element, fussing over Agatha’s makeup with all the concentration of a painter at work. He’d insisted on doing it himself, and judging by the smug little grin on his face as he dabbed at her cheekbones, he was proud of the results.

The house was quieter than usual. Wanda had left early for set to reshoot a few scenes, while Lilia had gone into town for groceries. Yelena, of course, had tagged along, not just for protection, but because she’d rattled off an absurd list of snacks that only Lilia was patient enough to fetch.

Rio moved in behind Agatha, her presence as steadying as ever. She rested her palms against the actress’s shoulders and began to rub gently, coaxing the tension out of her frame.

“Are you nervous, mi amor?” Rio asked softly, leaning down so only Agatha could hear.

Agatha exhaled, a smile tugging at her lips even as she admitted, “A little. Which is strange. I’ve never been nervous to talk to my fans before.”

Rio’s hands paused, then squeezed reassuringly. “It’s alright to be nervous with everything that’s happened. If you don’t want to talk about something, set that boundary when the Live starts and stick to it. No one gets to take your voice from you. And besides—” she dipped low, brushing a quick kiss to Agatha’s temple “—I’ll be right here, just off-camera, like always.”

A sharp pssst! interrupted them, followed by a cool mist of water across Rio’s face. She blinked in shock. Jen stood there, holding a spray bottle like a weapon.

“No kissing!” Jen scolded, wagging the bottle. “You’ll smudge her makeup, and we go live in three minutes. Shoo! You’re a distraction.”

Rio glared at her so darkly it could have peeled paint from the walls. Jen, unfazed, waved her off with a flick of her wrist and returned to fiddling with the lighting. Agatha, meanwhile, was doubled over laughing, trying not to smear the makeup Billy had worked so hard on.

“Two minutes,” Jen called, glancing at her watch. She leaned down, her voice softening as she gave Agatha one final pep talk. “Just be yourself. Don’t let the Seven change how you are with your coven. They don’t get that power.”

Agatha nodded, inhaling slowly, the weight of Jen’s words grounding her. She adjusted her posture, squared her shoulders, and placed her hands over the laptop keyboard.

Rio stepped aside to stand in the shadows, out of the camera’s frame but directly in Agatha’s eyeline. She caught her girlfriend’s gaze, gave her a slow nod and the faintest smile. Agatha’s lips curved in answer, strength surging back into her chest.

This wasn’t just a livestream. It was a reclamation.

Agatha adjusted the collar of her deep violet blouse and leaned toward the camera, a practiced but genuine smile curving her lips. The little red dot blinked to life. For the first time in weeks, she wasn’t standing on a film set or behind a line of bodyguards. She was right here, face-to-face with her fans.

“Well,” she began, voice a warm drawl, “look at you all. My coven, punctual as always. I don’t think I’ve been on time for anything in my life, so it’s nice to know at least one of us has discipline.”

The comment section exploded in hearts and emojis. Agatha laughed, eyes dancing. “Alright, ground rules. Let’s set a boundary right now. I’m not here to give any more power to the pests buzzing around my life lately. You know who I mean. This livestream isn’t theirs to ruin. It’s ours. This is for you—for us. So, if you want scandal and gossip, go elsewhere. If you want sarcasm, bad jokes, and the occasional overshare? Congratulations, you’re in the right place.”

The flood of comments seemed to agree. Agatha relaxed back in her chair, tilting her head thoughtfully.

“Alright. Let’s see what you want to know. Ah—this one’s easy. Yes, filming for Coven of Chaos is underway. Yes, it’s bigger and wilder than anything we’ve done before. And yes, Wanda and I glare at each other so much that our director threatened to get us sunglasses. Apparently, it’s too much heat for one frame.”

The chat exploded with laughing emojis and heart emojis. Someone wrote: “GIVE US SPOILERS” in all caps.

“Spoilers?” Agatha gasped in mock offense. “You think I survived twenty years in this industry by giving away spoilers? Please. I don’t even tell Lilia.”

She leaned closer, lowering her voice conspiratorially. “But between us… There is one scene where I conjure something so outrageous, the stunt coordinator walked off set for a full fifteen minutes to pray. To what? I don’t know. Probably to Wanda.”

Her grin widened at the wave of speculation rolling in. “Oh, you’ll stew over that until release day. You’re welcome.”

Another comment caught her eye and made her bark a laugh. “What’s your favorite sandwich? That’s the pressing question of the hour? Not my skincare, not the arc of my career, sandwiches.” She tapped her chin. “Fine. Tuna melt. But not too much mayo. If you give me too much mayo, we’re fighting.”

The chat scrolled faster, fans debating her answer, some mock-outraged, others delighted. Agatha basked in it, letting herself sink into the easy rhythm she’d always loved with them.

“Okay, next, what’s your guilty pleasure show besides Below Deck? Hah! Bold of you to assume I feel guilt about Below Deck. But alright… reality confessional time. I am shamefully devoted to baking competitions. The ones where people’s cakes collapse and everyone gasps dramatically? My Roman Empire.”

She threw her hands up in mock despair. “There’s just something about a sponge cake deflating that soothes the soul. Therapy who?”

The room around her buzzed with energy, not just from the stream but from the presence off-camera. Rio leaned casually against the wall, arms crossed, watching. Always watching. Agatha’s eyes flicked toward her without thinking. And again. And again.

The fans noticed, of course. The comments began to swell: “Why do you keep looking off-screen???” “RIO? WHERE IS SHE??” “We see you 👀”

Agatha laughed, caught. “Nosy, nosy coven. Fine. She’s here. Of course she’s here. Where else would she be? She’s glued to me like a very tall, very protective shadow.”

The chat immediately exploded with demands: 

“BRING RIO IN” 

“RIOOOO” 

“LET US SEE THE HOT TATTED LATINA!!”

Agatha smirked, turning in her chair to face Rio. “They want you.”

Rio shook her head instantly. “No.”

Agatha turned back to the camera with a sigh of mock tragedy. “See what I deal with? I get stabbed on screen ten times a week, but my greatest heartbreak is my bodyguard refusing to indulge me.”

The fans spammed harder, begging for Rio to appear. Agatha arched a brow at her girlfriend. “Carino, if you don’t at least come say hello, I may be forced to describe every single one of your tattoos in explicit detail.”

Rio groaned, muttered something in Spanish, and finally strode into frame. She perched stiffly on the arm of Agatha’s chair, clearly uncomfortable but too loyal to walk away.

The chat went feral.

“See? She exists,” Agatha said smugly. She nudged Rio’s thigh. “Say hello, darling. The people demand it.”

Rio gave the faintest nod. “Hello.”

“That’s it?” Agatha gasped. “You give Shakespeare-level protection every day of your life, and hello is all you offer? My coven, don’t worry. I’ll train her yet.”

Rio’s lips twitched, the closest she got to a smile under scrutiny. “I’m not here to be trained.”

“Oh, that’s a lie if I’ve ever heard one,” Agatha quipped, earning howls from the comment section.

Questions poured in now, dozens directed at Rio. Agatha scrolled dramatically. “Oooh, here’s one: Rank your security team from most likely to survive a zombie apocalypse to least.”

Rio exhaled, resigned. “Natasha first. Then Bucky. Yelena. Clint. Alice. And I suppose I’d be last, since I’d throw myself in front of everyone else.”

The fans spammed crying emojis. Agatha smacked her arm. “Absolutely not. We’re banning martyrdom from this livestream. New rule.”

Another question flashed up. Agatha read it aloud, eyes sparkling. “Rank your team from most likely to sleep with Agatha to least.”

Rio stiffened. “No.”

“Oh, but it’s tradition!” Agatha teased. 

“They are all in relationships; it's why I picked them for this team, so they don't sleep with you.” 

The chat was flooded with disappointed fans at the fact that none of the security team is available, half the chat is screaming about how Rio picked people who wouldn’t sleep with Agatha, poking fun at the fact.

“Fine, I’ll answer. Ready? Rio, Alice, Yelena, Natasha, Clint, Bucky last because he’s very gay..”

Rio groaned into her hand. “You’re incorrigible.”

The comments lost their minds. Fans clipped it instantly, hashtags blooming in real time. Agatha only grinned wider, thoroughly enjoying Rio’s blush.

A question popped up that made Agatha smirk mischievously. She leaned toward the screen, voice dripping with delight as she read it aloud:

“Are you single, Rio?”

Rio froze for just a beat, her shoulders stiffening as though someone had drawn a bead on her from across the room. Slowly, she cut her eyes toward Agatha in a side glance she prayed was subtle. Of course, Agatha caught it instantly, raising one arched brow in challenge, smirk widening as she gave Rio her full attention. She was practically daring her to answer.

Rio exhaled through her nose, the corner of her mouth twitching. “No,” she said at last, voice low but steady. “I am happily taken.”

The comment section exploded like fireworks, messages flooding in so fast the chat box struggled to keep up. Some fans immediately began speculating who Rio meant. Others spiraled into heartbreak emojis and dramatic declarations of ruined dreams. Through it all, Agatha beamed like she just won the lottery, winking at Rio before pivoting back to the screen as if she hadn’t just set off an internet-wide meltdown.

Rio shook her head, but the faintest smile tugged at her lips. She hadn’t missed Agatha’s reaction.

Another question surged to the top of the feed: “How many tattoos do you have, Rio?”

Before Rio could open her mouth, Agatha chirped, “She has twelve.”

Rio turned her head slowly, one brow lifting. The look on her face was half amusement, half disbelief. Agatha’s eyes went wide as she realized what she’d done. She gave a sheepish little wince that all but screamed, Oops.

Rio let her stare hang there a moment longer before smirking, clearly enjoying the shift in power. She looked back at the camera. “Yes. She’s right. I have twelve. And no—” she added firmly, cutting off the inevitable flood of fan demands before they could fully take shape, “—I will not tell you what they are or what they mean.”

Agatha chuckled softly, leaning into her mic. “Mystery suits you, carino. But for the record, I do know what they mean.”

The fans went wild again, spamming caps-locked questions and frantic speculation. Rio only sighed and folded her arms, but she didn’t miss the satisfied gleam in Agatha’s eyes.

Other questions flew, what was Rio’s favorite meal (simple: Arroz con pollo), whether she’d ever lost a fight (she said no, Agatha corrected her with “except to me, darling”), and what the team was like off duty.

“They’re chaos,” Rio said flatly. “Loud, competitive, impossible to control.”

“Like siblings,” Agatha added, softer now. “The best kind. The kind who fight over pizza toppings but would burn the world if you so much as bruised them.”

Rio glanced at her then, and something unspoken passed between them. It was subtle, but the fans caught it. The chat scrolled faster than Alice’s firewall could blink. 

“OMG LOOK AT THE WAY THEY LOOK AT EACH OTHER!!” 

“MARRIED VIBES???”

“SECRET GIRLFRIENDS 100%”

“KISS! KISS! KISS! KISS!”

Agatha ignored the frenzy, though her smirk said she’d seen it. She tapped the screen. “Next question!”

This time, the questions took on a more curious tone. “Rio, why did you become a bodyguard?”

Rio blinked, clearly not expecting it. Agatha tilted her head encouragingly.

“I was a soldier,” Rio said after a moment. Her voice was calm, clipped. “I served in the Special Forces. When I left, I still needed purpose. Protecting people gives me that. It’s simple. Direct. Someone tries to hurt my client, I stop them. That’s it.”

Agatha rested her chin on her hand, smiling sideways at her. “Simple, she says. Like she hasn’t made it an art form.”

Another question rolled in: “What’s one thing about Agatha we don’t know, but should?”

Rio hesitated. Agatha raised her brows. “Careful, darling. Remember, you live here now.”

Rio ignored her. “She hums when she cooks,” she said finally. “Sometimes it’s actual songs. Sometimes it’s just noise. She doesn’t even notice. But it means she’s happy.” Rio paused and then smirked before adding on, “Also, she can’t cook for shit.”

Agatha’s cheeks flushed, and the fans erupted with caps-locked screaming.

“Betrayed in my own home,” she deadpanned, but her eyes softened as she looked at Rio.

A fan asked: “What’s the hardest part of your job?”

Rio’s expression flickered. “Convincing her to take her own safety seriously.”

Agatha let out a mock gasp. “How dare you expose me like this to my own coven!”

“Truth hurts,” Rio said simply, and the comments cackled.

Another question popped: “What do you do to relax, Rio?”

Agatha leaned forward eagerly. “Yes, please, tell us. Because I’ve never seen you relax once.”

Rio smirked faintly. “Gardening. Reading. Cooking, sometimes painting.”

Agatha whipped her head toward her, stunned. “Painting?! You’ve been hiding hobbies from me?”

Rio shrugged. “You never asked.”

The fans exploded. “RIO THE ARTIST” “POST THE PAINTINGS” “BODYGUARD BY DAY, VAN GOGH BY NIGHT.”

Agatha was still staring at her like she’d sprouted wings. “This relationship is built on lies,” she muttered dramatically. “And I’m taking it to the court of public opinion, my coven.”

The chat sided gleefully with Rio.

They answered absurd fan asks for another half-hour, what Agatha would do in a bar fight (“win, obviously”), which Disney villain Rio secretly admired (“Scar, because strategy”), and whether Agatha could do a handstand (she attempted it on camera, wobbled, and nearly toppled into Rio’s lap, which sent fans into hysterics).

Finally, as the hour wound down, Agatha leaned closer to the camera. Her smile softened, all teasing tucked away.

“Alright, my loves. I have to wrap this up. But before I go, I want you to know that your laughter, your chaos, your constant presence in my life, it matters. More than you know. This livestream wasn’t just about answering silly questions. It was about reminding myself, and all of you, that joy is an act of defiance. And I refuse to let anyone steal it from me.”

Rio laid a hand on her shoulder then, quiet support. Agatha covered it with her own, squeezing. For a moment, the camera caught it, the unguarded closeness, the affection they didn’t name but couldn’t hide.

The chat erupted, hashtags already being born. Agatha only winked. “And on that note, stay safe, stay kind, and don’t let anyone tell you tuna melt isn’t a proper sandwich. Goodnight, my coven.”

She clicked the livestream closed, the little red light vanishing.

The room was silent except for Agatha’s soft exhale. She leaned back in her chair, tilting her head at Rio. “Well, darling. Think I ruined your stoic reputation yet?”

Rio shook her head, but her lips curved. “No. But you made me love you a little more.”

 

Night of a Hundred Shadows

Chapter Summary

The Seventh Veil, feeling backed into a corner, makes an unprecedented move, and the team faces a massive threat. The Rat is finally unveiled.

Chapter Notes

I'm not particularly pleased with how this chapter turned out, to be honest.

Warning: Character Death (NOT Agatha or Rio). I'm sorry in advance.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

“You know the fans are going feral over the livestream last night,” Agatha smirked. She’d already seen thousands of clips and speculation threads dissecting every moment between her and Rio.

“Let them. I’m not worried about that right now,” Rio said, leaning on her elbow to look down at Agatha. “The Seven are going to feel cornered after Renna’s death and with Raven and Kyra in custody. Raven won’t talk, we’ve tried. She just sits there humming. I’m afraid they’re going to make a rash, dangerous move.”

“Let’s not talk about the Seven right now.” Agatha’s smile softened into something more dangerous. “You’re practically naked in my bed, and I have other things on my mind.” She tugged Rio down into a kiss.

Agatha and Rio were tangled under the sheets Rio’s mouth on Agatha’s neck when Alice barreled into the bedroom without knocking.

Rio moved before she thought, an old reflex, a muscle memory that had kept her and others alive more times than she could count. She was up in an instant, hand slipping to the concealed spot Agatha hadn’t known about. Rio’s posture tightened into efficient danger. Agatha’s laugh cut off, replaced by a sharp inhale.

“For fucks sake—” Rio started, then stopped when she registered who’d come through the door.

Alice was breathless, hair loose, laptop clutched like evidence. “If you do that again, I am stabbing you,” Rio warned, low and dangerous.

She folded the blade away and slid back onto the sheets, tugging the duvet up as Alice pushed forward and set the laptop between them. Agatha’s fingers threaded through Rio’s, hard enough to anchor but not to panic.

“Never mind that,” Alice said, words fast, voice already stripped to business. “We have a problem.”

Rio leaned in. Agatha sat up, hair mussed, eyes wide. Alice tapped the mousepad. Her face had the look she got when she’d found a smoking thread in a thousand pages of code.

“I’ve been watching the Seventh Veil accounts,” Alice said. “The same offshore channels that paid Ralph Bohner. Tonight, there was a transfer. One million dollars. It was split and routed into a network of accounts tied to mercenaries and assassins for hire.”

Rio closed her fist around the duvet. “You mean—”

“A bounty,” Alice finished. “They’re offering payment for delivery: Agatha alive if possible, dead if need be. The money’s been laundered through intermediaries, we traced the paths. There’s liquidity, handlers, and paymasters. Whoever did this has the funds and the channels to recruit quickly.”

Agatha went very still. The color left her face, but it was anger that came in, hot and immediate, not fear. “A million dollars,” she repeated, tasting the words.

Rio shot a look at Alice. “Who posted it? Where did it appear?”

“Encrypted boards, private channels, and a few broker feeds,” Alice said. “Seren’s been amplifying it, she’s pushing the message hard. We think she’s trying to make the Seven look lethal and resourced. But the money doesn’t just buy attention. It buys people who don’t care why, only that they’ll get paid.”

Rio folded the laptop closed with a snap. The bedroom door clicked and opened; Maria slipped in without fanfare, steady, composed, the kind of person whose presence brought order. Behind her came Sonya and Steve, rifles slung across their backs, eyes already scanning exits. Outside, the rest of the team were assembling like a machine: Bucky at the door, Natasha moving toward the study, Yelena circling the perimeter. Clint manning front gate. The house itself seemed to breathe in readiness.

“We keep this in-house,” Maria said. “No press. No public statements. We call in local law enforcement we trust and our SHIELD legal team to issue emergency freezes where possible. This stays between us and authorities who can help. No matter what, we do not let the Seven weaponize the public.” Her voice left no room for argument.

Agatha met Maria’s eyes and nodded once. “Good. I don’t want them to amplify this by crying wolf to the world.”

Jen, already at the foot of the bed with a tablet typed while she spoke. “I’ll freeze public appearances. No red carpets, no interviews. We go dark except for controlled productions that Rio and I approve. We won’t feed the hunger.”

“Good,” Rio said. She turned to Agatha, voice softer. “We’ll also rotate your sleeping location nightly for the next two weeks. We use decoys and duplicate routes. If they want you alive, we make you a moving target with no predictable pattern.”

Agatha squeezed Rio’s hand. Her jaw was a hard line, anger in every set muscle. “They exposed Colten’s image. They showed a dead soldier and turned it into a spectacle. They want to humiliate me, and they think by making it public they’ll win.” Her fingers tightened until Rio felt the pressure. “I’m not letting them win.”

Lilia’s text came through—on my way—and the house exhaled a small, collective relief. Wanda’s message followed: Leaving set, I’ll be there. Those two were the only ones not in the room; everyone else was already present, already moving.

Rio looked at each of them in turn, Alice, Maria, Sonya, Steve, Natasha, Bucky, Yelena, Jen, and Clint, seeing not just colleagues but the people who would be the edge between danger and safety. “We’ll need contingency teams ready to move if any of those cutout accounts light up with activity. Bucky, get me a rapid response: two vehicles, heavy plating. Natasha, work with local PD, only officers we can verify. We’ll need warrants ready if we get a lead.”

Alice nodded. “I’ll push everything to the task force. Maria can coordinate with federal liaisons to get emergency freezes on the shell accounts. We’ll hit the cash flow hard first. That’s the easiest choke point.”

“Physical precautions,” Sonya added matter-of-factly. “Reinforce the gates, add ballistic barriers at likely approach points, flood lights everywhere so they can't use the dark to sneak in, and position quiet surveillance teams in the trees.”

Rio let out a breath that was half frustration and half a steel-calm resolve. “We take the initiative. We don’t wait for them to pick a target. We draw them into mistakes.”

Agatha glanced at the laptop, then at Rio. “And when this is over?” Her voice was small, for the first time vulnerable beneath the armor of her fury.

Rio moved in, closing the space between them and wrapping both arms around Agatha. “When this is over,” she said, fierce and low, “you walk wherever you want, public or private, without me needing to hold my breath.”

Agatha leaned into the promise and for a sliver of a second the room felt less like a staging ground and more like a home. Outside, engines idled, radios beeped, people moved with practiced efficiency. Inside, the people who had come to protect her sealed plans that left no place for spectacle, only for safety.

Phones began to buzz in a sudden, ugly chorus, Alice had pushed something priority to every device in the house.

Rio’s screen lit first. Two new burner handles. Two new posts.

The first was short, the typography oddly childish for how venomous it read:

@Siren_call
 funny how you sleep with your eyes open, captain. can you save her from what’s coming, or will you fail like you failed valkyrie? tick-tock.

Alice’s reply pinged in a heartbeat later: IP traces back to Seren She did not need to say more; everyone knew the voice—mocking, petty, precise.

The second post slid in like a cold knife:

@motheroftheseven
 Snakes shed skin as they grow. I’ve grown while you grieved. Three steps ahead, always. We won’t stop until we have what we want.

No emojis. No flourish. It read like the Snake herself stepping into the light for the first time.

Rio’s jaw locked. Her thumb hovered over the glass. You don’t get to use Valkyrie like a lever, she thought. The rage felt hot enough to taste, but she pinched it down into focus.

Agatha’s phone chimed. She read both posts, then let out a short, humorless laugh.

“Obsessed, pathetic, and predictable,” she said. “If they were really three steps ahead, they wouldn’t need to announce it.”

“Announcing is the point,” Rio said, already turning to Alice. “It’s a pressure game.”

Alice’s fingers were already moving across the laptop perched on the kitchen island, multiple windows open, dashboards and command lines humming with information. “Seren’s trying to destabilize you,” she said. “The Snake wants credit for escalation, brand-building. If the Snake moves from boasting to ordering, we need to expect things to get much worse.”

A ping on the comms; Steve’s voice, measured and crisp: Two incoming vehicles at the gate. Visual confirms: Wanda and Lilia.

Relief threaded through the room like fresh air. Wanda and Lilia’s arrivals were the calm center Agatha needed. The rest of the team tightened like a web being drawn taut, Bucky and Clint to the front hall, weapons at low ready; Sonya and Steve already moving to the gates. The house shifted, every motion practiced, precise.

Wanda stepped out of the Porsche first, hair loose from a hurried bun. Lilia followed, jaw set. Their hugs were full-body and immediate, no show, no cameras, just steady presence.

“You okay?” Wanda asked into Agatha’s hair.

“I’m furious,” Agatha said simply. “But very much alive.”

Wanda’s look flicked to Rio, sharp, seeing. Rio nodded once. No speech required: She’s in good hands.

Another gate chime. Yelena’s tone crackled: “More friends coming, sisters, actually. I called in favors.”

They arrived not as a crowd but as shadows made flesh, three women in dark civilian clothes, walking with the quiet precision of predators who don’t need to announce themselves. Natasha introduced them without ceremony. “Zoya, Ina, Masha, old ties, and loyal. They’re here because we asked.”

Widows didn’t hug. They acknowledged obligations with a tilt of the chin. “We’re in,” Zoya said.

Rio pulled up a property map on the big screen. The house, the perimeter, approach roads, vantage points: the geometry of safety. She liked maps; they smoothed the panic into a plan.

“Sonya and Steve have north and south gates,” Rio said, sweeping her hand. “They rotate with Bucky and Clint every two hours. Natasha and Zoya take the west roof; Ina and Masha the east roof. Yelena stays mobile, perimeter sweeps, interior float, and rendezvous with me if anything breaks through.”

“And me?” Agatha asked, arms crossed, chin high.

“You’re with me,” Rio answered. “Always. If something happens to me, Natasha. If she’s compromised, Yelena. If the unimaginable occurs and the entire team goes down, Wanda and Lilia will evacuate you.”

Lilia, already at the desk, tapped a finger on a corner of the property feed. “I’ll coordinate civics. I’ll call local neighbors personally, ask them to watch, to call if something looks out of place. No posts, no cameras, just eyes and a phone call.”

Alice didn’t look up from the laptop. “Seren is baiting us, testing comms, seeing what we reveal when we react. She’s looking for noise. The Snake? She wants credit. My guess is she wants to force us to show our hand.”

Rio’s fingers drummed the edge of the map. “They’re testing. We expect probes. We also expect escalation. Maera will likely show herself. She’s the enforcer; she doesn’t care about symbolism, she cares about pay. If they bring muscle now, it’s because they want to see what we’ll do when threatened.”

A hush fell. Maera Rourke’s name carried weight, former military, ex-bodyguard who’d once been close enough to Agatha to know the rhythm of her days. Maera had no love for Agatha, but she had a price. That price was now on the table.

“And the rat?” Maria asked from the doorway, always two steps ahead in logistics.

“The infiltrator who rigged the light and trashed the trailer,” Alice said. “They used tech and access. We have reason to believe the rat might be close, maybe even local. If they send Maera to probe, the rat could try to slip in under the chaos.”

“Then we set traps for both,” Rio replied. “Maera is the muscle, visible and loud. We’ll make sure the gates and sightlines catch anyone approaching. The rat will go for blind spots, equipment rooms, service entrances, the catwalk.”

Agatha’s face grew hard with the same steel Rio carried. “If Maera shows up, she’s not doing this because she hates me. She’s doing it because she was paid to be indifferent. That’s easier to deal with.”

“Indifference is lethal,” Rio said. “But it’s calculable.”

“Maria, did we get permission to use lethal force if necessary?” Rio asked, turning to the commander.

“Yes. The FBI and local police have given us the go-ahead, but only as a last resort,” Maria replied. “If lethal force is used there will likely be a brief investigation to ensure it was warranted, but we should be cleared.” Rio nodded.. 

They spent the next half hour refining, rings of defense, a rotation for guards, decoy routines so anyone watching would see patterns that were false. Alice set digital honeytraps that would look like vulnerable ports but were islands of lies. Yelena worked the physical tack: motion sensors angled at low points, Floodlights that illuminated the whole property, sound detectors that would flag a dropped tool. Sonya and Steve doubled the watch at the gate; A few trusted Cops would stage outward a block from the property to intercept any fast movers.

“If Maera comes, she’ll bring a crew,” Yelena said bluntly. “She’s not subtle. She’s the type to show up in a black truck and a smile. She’ll try to intimidate and buy access.”

“Which is why she won’t get either,” Natasha said.

Outside, the house breathed in. Teams took positions on roofs, windows, hedges, less like an army and more like a living, tense thing waiting to pounce if need be. People moved quietly, everything practiced, the rhythm of drills and the polish of repetition. The Widows melted into their posts like ink into water, present, potent, and silent.

Agatha’s hand found Rio’s wrist. “If they come with brutality,” she said softly, “I want them to know one thing.”

“What’s that?” Rio asked.

“That my life is mine, not their property.”

Rio looked down at her, the promise in her chest swelling. “Then we make them remember that.”

They checked each other: collars zipped, radios tested, batteries charged. Alice’s eyes flicked to the screens. “Seren poked the decoy; she’s watching to see whether we respond. If she runs the relay to any handler, we’ll get a trace. She’s getting sloppy without her sister.”

“And the Snake?” Maria asked.

“She’s enjoying the applause,” Alice muttered. “She wants the panic to feel like victory. But this, this is our floor. We don’t give them an audience.”

At the perimeter, Sonya and Steve adjusted night-vision sweeps. Sonya’s voice was blunt through the earpiece: “If Maera comes, she’ll look for an angle that hurts without touching us. She’s not a gardener; she’s a butcher.”

Agatha’s mouth twitched. “Lovely. She sounds charming.”

“She is,” Rio said flatly. “And money makes harlots of us all.”

The house shifted into motion: a quiet choreography. Bucky and Clint walked the lines outside; Yelena and Natasha checked the interior camera feeds physically, with their own eyes. Alice had planted tracking pings in the decoy ports; Maria was lining up federal call-ins and paperwork so action could be instantaneous when the team had the right warrant. Jen organized the logistics, meals, rest rotations, everything that keeps people human in the ugly gray hours.

“Lilia and Wanda staying?” Rio asked.

“Yes,” Lilia said from where she’d been cataloging neighbor contacts. “I’m here. I’m not leaving.”

Wanda’s hand found Rio’s shoulder in a quick, fierce squeeze. “Neither am I. If they think they can scare us into hiding, they haven’t met this coven.”

A horn announced a check-in from Bucky and Yelena; they were mid-sweep outside the far hedge. Alice’s laptop pinged again: Seren’s relay partially compromised; tracing now, local nodes.

They finished their checks. The house didn’t sleep, but it settled into a dangerous, vigilant calm, bright screens, clipped radios, men and women who’d chosen to protect standing like pillars against the dark.

Agatha rested her forehead against Rio’s temple for a single, grounding breath. “Whatever happens,” she said, voice small in the flood of plans, “thank you.”

Rio’s hold tightened. “Always.”

Outside, shadows moved with intent. Inside, the people who loved Agatha made themselves a wall. And when the Snake and the Cicadas and the rest finally chose to come for them, they would find a house that did not cower. They would find people ready to answer force with calculated, ferocious defense.

The night stretched. The plan waited to be tested.

The first two nights were tense but manageable. A handful of low-level mercenaries showed up, lured by the bounty, but they barely reached the street outside before Sonya or Steve intercepted them. Two would-be “assassins” had tried to climb the gate, only to end up zip-tied on the sidewalk for the police to collect.

The third night was different.

Rio felt it in her bones before Alice called it over comms. The air outside was too still, too thick, as though even the neighbors’ dogs sensed something lurking.

Then Alice’s voice cracked over the comms. “We’ve got movement. Multiple heat signatures. Too many to count.”

Natasha’s eyes narrowed as she glanced at the monitors. “That’s not a probe. That’s an army.”

“How many?” Rio asked, her voice steady even as her stomach clenched.

Alice’s fingers flew over her keyboard, pulling camera feeds. “A hundred, maybe more. They’re coming from every direction.”

Rio swore under her breath. Rio toggled the all-call. “This is it. Sonya, Steve: hold the gates as long as you can and fall back on my mark. Bucky, Clint: outer intercept, make them bleed yardage. Widows: roof and flanks. Yelena: You're mobile.” Rio ordered “Agatha, Wanda, Jen, Lilia, Billy, living room, now. Stay low. Don’t leave unless I or Natasha come for you.” With that she ran off towards the roof.

Billy tried to argue “I can fight” but Wanda snapped, grabbing his wrist. “No. You stay with me.” Her voice shook, fear disguised as fury.

The living room felt too bright, too fragile. The sound of boots crunching on gravel carried in from outside, mixed with the crackle of radios and shouted orders. The normal quiet suburban street had transformed into a battlefield.

Agatha sat stiffly on the couch, her hands clenched in her lap. Jen hovered near by, Lilia clutched her wine glass like it was armor. Wanda’s arm stayed locked around Billy, her nails digging into his sleeve.

Below, the south tree line peeled open, dark figures moving in disciplined lines, not the sloppy jog of scavengers. Rio clocked mismatched kit, some plate carriers high-end, some thrift-store surplus, mercenary soup, but the coordination was tight enough to worry her.

“Fireteam One, two, three—mark your lanes,” Rio said, then squeezed her first shot. A forward scout folded, clean head drop. The south line staggered, then surged.

The attack came fast.

Mercenaries swarmed the gates, shouting, firing blindly toward the house. 

On the roof, Natasha went surgical, two-round bursts, each pair more a sentence than a shot. Clint knelt stone-still beside a roof AC unit, firing on the exhale, calculating in slivers of breath.

Yelena didn’t settle. She was a dart, slipping from skylight to terrace to back stair, popping smoke where it funneled attackers, dropping flashbangs at the hedges to sow panic, then knifing the confused with efficient, brutal economy. Twice she vanished entirely, only for a merc to spin and crumple, a red line opening under an ear.

At the front gate, Sonya and Steve fought like myth, Sonya with her rifle tucked tight, stepping into recoil, Russian curses like a beat; Steve with that terrifying calm, double-tapping kneecaps and clavicles, so clean it felt like a clinic.

“Fence breach east,” Alice called. “Cutters on the third panel.”

“On me,” Ina said, already moving, Masha shadowing her. They hit the east fence like wind, Ina low and inside with a telescoping baton that shattered wrists; Masha up and over the fence line with a choke cable, dragging one climber down silent as a falling leaf.

Inside, the windows rattled as bullets pinged against the siding. Billy flinched hard at every sound, and Wanda pulled him close, murmuring, “It’s okay, it’s okay,” though her own voice shook. Agatha’s nails dug crescent moons into her palm, and Jen muttered prayers under her breath.

The mercs continued pressing relentlessly

“Fall back!” Rio barked. “Sonya, Steve, give me ten seconds and peel.”

“Copy,” Steve said, then tossed his last stun into a knot of bodies and dragged the iron crossbar shut by hand, buying those ten seconds with sweat. He and Sonya flowed backward, firing in the cadence of retreat: turn-shoot-move, turn-shoot-move.

Rio burst back inside, sweat glistening on her temples. “They’re pressing hard. We need to move you all somewhere safer.”

“Where?” Agatha asked, standing quickly.

Rio’s jaw worked. “The basement. It’s the most secure part of the house. No windows, one entry point.”

They moved quickly, Rio and Bucky flanking them as the others hurried downstairs. The sounds of shouting and gunfire grew louder upstairs. Every creak of the house made Billy jump.

“Mom,” he whispered as they crouched in the basement, “are we going to be okay?”

Wanda kissed his hair, eyes brimming. “Yes. You’re with me. You’re safe.”

Agatha leaned against the wall, trying to steady her breathing. “They won’t get through. They can’t.”

But the thud of footsteps overhead told a different story.

Upstairs, the Widows fought like shadows. Ina and Masha used wire and batons, slipping between doorways, striking and vanishing. Steve and Sonya held the entry hall, turning every doorway into a choke point. Natasha and Maria cutting down any before they can enter through the back.

Still, numbers wore on them. The mercs weren’t skilled, but they were relentless, throwing themselves at the house in waves. The wood frame groaned under the assault.

When the third wave hit, it hit everywhere. A garage window blew in, showering the Range Rover with diamonds; three mercs tried to pour through at once and met Clint’s blade before they found footing. In the library, two more rappelled through the skylight and landed in a snare Yelena had strung from curtain wire and stair banister; their guns clattered and one of them hung, strangling on his own web while Yelena rolled her eyes and cut him down to finish it properly.

Bucky stepped into the hall like a classical statue with a sidearm, elbowing one man’s barrel aside, punching the trachea, stepping into the next. Sonya vaulted a toppled chair and turned a double tap into a triple when she heard a second set of boots behind the first.

Natasha wiped blood from her arm where a bullet had grazed her. “They’re pushing too hard,” she hissed.

“They won’t break us,” Rio said. Her voice was steel, but her eyes flicked to the basement door. Agatha.

That was when Alice’s voice broke in, sharp and panicked. “Someone’s inside. They slipped through the crawlspace.”

Rio froze. “Who?”

“I don’t know. Small, fast. Too precise to be random. It has to be the Rat.”

Rio swore. “Keep eyes on her. Don’t lose her.”

Downstairs, Billy shifted nervously. “I heard something,” he whispered.

“It’s just the house settling,” Wanda said, though her eyes darted toward the stairwell.

But Billy was right. A faint scrape carried through the dark, a sound that didn’t belong.

Then Hela Odinsson stepped into view.

She looked almost unchanged from years ago, save for sharper angles, colder eyes. Her lips curved in a smirk when she saw Agatha. “Hello, Aggie.”

Agatha’s heart stopped. “Hela,” she whispered. Her first love, the woman who broke her heart all those years ago. 

Wanda shoved Billy behind her. “Stay back!”

Rio thundered down the stairs towards the basement, but Hela moved fast, slipping partly behind a support beam, her gun leveled. Her eyes flicked between Agatha and Wanda before settling on Billy.

And she smiled coldy.

The shot echoed like thunder.

Billy gasped, staggering back into Wanda’s arms. Blood bloomed on his chest, soaking her hands.

“NO!” Wanda screamed, cradling him, pressing frantically at the wound. “Billy! Stay with me, please, stay with me—”

Agatha froze, horror pinning her where she stood. “Oh god, oh god—”

Rio kicked the door down, firing toward Hela, but Hela was already gone, retreating into the crawlspace with a last cold smirk.

Chaos followed.

Wanda sobbed, rocking Billy as his breaths came shallow and fast. “No, no, you don’t get to leave me, not you—”

Jen collapsed to her knees, hands over her mouth. Lilia stood frozen, her wine glass finally slipping from her hand to shatter.

Agatha dropped to the floor beside Wanda, tears streaming unchecked. “Please, Billy, hold on—”

But his eyes fluttered once, then stilled.

The house went eerily quiet for a moment. Then Wanda’s scream shattered it, a sound of raw grief that clawed at the walls.

Rio crouched beside them, her face carved from stone. “I’m sorry,” she whispered. Her voice cracked. “I’m so sorry.”

Natasha’s voice broke over comms. “Mercs are pulling back. They’re retreating.”

“Maera’s with them,” Clint added grimly. “She’s seen and lost enough.”

Rio’s chest heaved, fury and grief warring. She touched Wanda’s shoulder, then Agatha’s, grounding them. “It’s not over,” she said softly. “Not yet.”

The night ended with blood in the carpet, smoke in the air, and Billy’s body lying still. Wanda was inconsolable, her cries echoing through the basement. Agatha held her, sobbing too, her own heart shattering as the weight of Hela’s betrayal, and her cruelty settled like lead.

Rio stood, staring at the crawlspace Hela had vanished through, her fists trembling. She had faced battlefields, buried her team, endured loss. But this, watching Agatha break, watching Wanda’s world shatter, lit something darker in her chest.

Hela wasn’t just the Rat anymore. She was a ghost from Agatha’s past, and now she had drawn blood.

And Rio swore she would not survive it a second time.

Chapter End Notes

I'm sorry!!!!! But the next few chapters bring vengeance. We are nearing the endgame, everyone. Just hang in there.

The Final Pieces

Chapter Summary

Team mourns their loss, plans their vengance, and gets one step closer to the end.

Chapter Notes

I am sorry about Billy, but he will be avenged!!

Also, some of you may have read the wrong version of the last chapter. I changed the Rats' name to Hela Odinson, not Mira. Sorry for any confusion.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Dawn came soft and gray, the sky reluctant to light the world after the night’s violence. The compound smelled like smoke and blood, and every surface seemed to hold its own small echo of yesterday: a scuffed boot print, the dent in the gate where the first breachers tried to wedge their way through, a smear of something dark on the gravel that Rio refused to look at too long. Inside, the silence felt like an accusation.

Natasha walked in first, a pad of paper in one hand, a makeshift bandage on the other where a grazing bullet had nicked her. She didn’t bother with small talk. “Final tally,” she said, voice thin. “One hundred and eight mercs dead. Twenty ran.” Her jaw worked like she was swallowing metal.

Rio closed her eyes for a breath and let the numbers settle in her chest like a stone. “Maera’s crew,” she said quietly. “She cut them loose.”

“Of course she did,” Yelena muttered, wincing as she sank into a chair and pressed the back of her hand to a split lip. “Cowards with contracts. They don’t sign up to die for pride.”

Clint sat with his side stitched and bandaged, rubbing at a wrist that still throbbed from where a blade had snapped skin. Sonya and a handful of the others were nursing shallow but ugly stabs and cuts; everyone wore the kind of exhaustion that reaches bone. They were breathing. They were alive. But the circle of life felt incomplete.

Wanda occupied a corner of the living room like a small, furious planet. She’d wrapped Billy’s jacket around her shoulders and wouldn’t let it go. Her face was raw from crying; now her eyes glinted with a terrible, bright fury. Lilia hovered, hands on Wanda’s back, murmuring something that sounded like a curse against God and luck and cruel people.

Agatha sat a little apart, hands clutching, jaw clenched so tight her knuckles were white. She had moved through the night like a dream; now that the adrenaline had ebbed, there were moments when her shoulders buckled and she had to breathe just to remember how to stand. Rio knelt beside her and threaded their fingers together. There was no elegant platitude she could offer that would fix this.

“He was just a kid,” Agatha whispered suddenly, as though saying it small might make it false. “He didn’t deserve—”

“No,” Rio said, voice steady but ragged. “No, he didn’t.” She turned and met Wanda’s gaze. Wanda didn’t look at her; she looked through her, at the hollow the boy left. Rio’s throat tightened at the sight.

Alice shut her laptop with a sound that cut the room. “You need to hear this,” she said. Her face was tight, not with adrenaline but with the brittle focus of someone who had just closed a file. “Jen and Agatha both named the rat, Hela Odinson. She’s the one who tampered with the light and broke into the trailer, and killed Billy. She was an assistant on sets, tried to be an actress, but never broke through, Disappeared for years, before being tied to a few violent crime organizations and rumored to be an assassin for hire.”

Hela. The name landed in the room and shifted the air. Lilia’s hand tightened on Wanda’s shoulder; she had a new look in her eyes: a slow, predatory grief that promised retribution.

“Daughter of Odin Odinson. Half-sister to Thor and Loki. Film dynasty. She’s got access and means, the kind money buys. She’s dangerous because she can walk onto sets like she belongs.” Alice explained. 

A murmur threaded through the room. The idea that a child of movie royalty would trade red carpets for contract blades made everyone’s stomach drop.

Agatha’s mouth moved before she could stop it. Small, breathless: “Hela… I —”

Rio’s hand tightened. She’d seen Agatha last night and how she reacted to seeing Hela. Now, even grief couldn’t mask the old wound. “What’s her connection to you?” Rio asked softly.

Agatha’s fingers trembled. “She started as a stagehand. I remember her hands, messy with paint. She was quiet, always watching. We… we were together, long before any of this. I found her in bed with the director when I came to surprise her on our 3rd anniversary; she was the only woman I ever loved before you.” Agatha looked up at Rio with eyes that screamed heartbreak.

“That explains how Hela knew of the Crawl pace that wasn’t on any blueprints. She has been here many times when you two were together,” Natasha said.

“She knew Billy; they hung out and bonded over being goth and having famous parents.” Agatha's voice cracked, still not believing the woman she loved was responsible for taking the boy she saw as a son away from her. Wanda flinched and let out another sob.

The room grew very still.

Alice pushed a folder across the table. Inside were screenshots, grainy photos, the kind of evidence that was clinical until you read names on the byline. “We found a note on the wall outside,” she said. “It’s from Hela. She left it at the scene, almost like she wanted you to find it, Agatha.” Her voice was soft but precise. 

Agatha’s skin went cold. She opened her hand and read the folded scrap in a voice that sounded like someone else’s. Rio reached out and took the paper, read it too. Hela’s handwriting was sprawling, oddly elegant for a person who used her hands to fix things in the dark:

Agatha,

Do you still remember those first nights on set? When the world hadn’t yet decided you were its darling, when you leaned against ropes and flats and told me your dreams like they were secrets only I was worthy of keeping? I was a stagehand then, faceless, unimportant, but you looked at me like I mattered. For a moment, I let myself believe I did.

You loved me with a ferocity I did not deserve, and I will never let you forget that. You gave me everything, your trust, your laughter, even the way your hands shook when you thought no one was watching. And what did I give you? Truth? No. I gave you what I had: access, connections, a way forward you didn’t even realize you needed. I was always playing a longer game. I told you once that I never really loved you, and you believed me. But that wasn’t the whole story.

The truth is uglier, Agatha. I loved what you made me feel, but I hated you for it. I hated that the spotlight wanted you and not me. That your name was whispered with reverence while mine was traded in back rooms and on sheets that never smelled like love. I clawed my way through this industry, directors, producers, favors spent and wasted, while you floated above it all, radiant, untouchable. You rose because you were brilliant. I rose because I was ruthless. And still, you soared higher.

So yes, I cheated. I lied. I used you. Because in the end, everything was always about you, wasn’t it? And I couldn’t stand being a shadow orbiting your sun.

But don’t mistake me, Agatha. The years haven’t softened me. I don’t want your forgiveness. I don’t even want your love, not anymore. What I want is to remind you that everything you’ve built rests on fragile ground. That I can take from you what I once gave so freely: access, intimacy, the illusion of safety.

You should have left me in the wings where I belonged. Instead, you made me believe I could stand on the stage beside you. And for that, I will never forgive you.

Yours in envy,
 Hela

 

The paper trembled in Rio’s hand. There was love there, but it was crooked and hot with a green, clawing envy. Hela’s confession read like a map; the stagehand detail explained how she’d moved backstage with ease; the mentions of access explained why she could get into trailers and tamper with things. It was a lover’s letter and a threat both.

Agatha’s eyes were wet, and for a construction of many public faces, she looked suddenly small. “She says she loved me, but she never did. I should have seen her for who she was; many warned me about her, but I didn't listen.” 

Rio’s fingers tightened around the paper until the edges went white. “She’s jealous, and she’s used her envy like a weapon.” She folded her head down for a moment, then lifted it. “We’ll use that. We’ll follow the path she left. Stagehands, production lists, and anyone who signed off on access for her. There are people on the film payroll who keep records. We’ll find them.”

Alice’s face, drained but furious, lit up behind her. “Good. Also, I froze every offshore account tied to the Seventh Veil; they’ve all been traced, flagged, and frozen. Those bounties were liquid; now they’re not. No more merc waves. Not on their money.”

A sharp, grateful huff sounded around the hungover room. Relief was short-lived but real. With the money trail cut, the cheap mercenaries were neutralized. It meant the rest of the attacks would be smaller, bloodier, and more personal. It also meant whatever remained of the Seven would escalate in other ways.

Outside, the world was already talking. Seren’s account, a blistering, petulant thread of posts and video rants, erupted an hour later. She posted a portrait of Kyra’s arrest with a caption like salt in a fresh wound: the pitiful, loud claim that if one of theirs fell, they would come back ten times worse. It read as a dare and a promise wrapped into one.

Rio scoffed bitterly. “She runs her mouth, but mouth alone can’t buy knives.” She tapped her comm. “Get me everyone who can open a line to Odin. Thor, Loki,  anyone with a name and a face. If Hela’s family has clout, they have records, payroll, and security. Someone will talk.”

Her military contact's answer came swiftly: “We have lines. The FBI will move in on Seren fast. She’s sloppy. She left metadata. We’ll have her tonight.”

True to word, an hour later, Rio’s contact called back. “FBI has Seren. They moved in at dawn. She’s in cuffs. She was vocal; she didn’t cover her tracks well.” The little victory was a cold one, a suspect in a small cell, scolding and defiant, but a step.

A low noise made its way through the room, not exactly relief, more an easing of pressure. They had blood, they had names, they had one less mouth breathing poison at large. But the hole that was Billy’s absence didn’t fill; it gaped.

Agatha pressed her forehead against Rio’s palm. The contact between them was a small, incandescent thing. “You won’t let them take another,” she said. It was a statement. It was also a prayer.

Rio swallowed an ache that had been waking with her for months, the old ghost of Valkyrie and the team she’d lost. “I promise,” she said. Promise had been the tool she’d used for years, binding it to duty and burying it in action. Now the promise had a name and a face: Billy.

Wanda rose, wiping at a face drawn taut with grief until she looked feral. “We go after Hela,” she said. “Not just for me. For Billy. For all of them.” She held Agatha’s gaze, and Agatha saw the steel in her friend’s face.

“We meet with the Odinsons,” Rio said. “We make them answer where Hela is. We keep the Media in the dark. We don’t play into their publicity machine. This is a law enforcement matter now; we don’t give it fuel. We have one more tool: Maria. She’ll help get us to the right MPs in the industry. Odin’s reach doesn’t make him invulnerable.”

Natasha’s mouth was a grim line. “And if they don’t cooperate?”

“We’ll make it costly,” Rio said. Her voice was not a threat; it was a plan. “But we’ll do it clean. We don’t become what they did.”

Agatha leaned forward, voice small and steady. “Promise me something else.” She looked each of them in the eye, finally daring. “Promise me you’ll live. All of you.”

Rio’s face broke for the briefest of seconds, not with guilt this time, but with a ferocious affection. “I can’t promise none of us will get hurt,” she said honestly. “But I promise I will not let them take any more without paying tenfold. I will not lose another body to hate.”

Lilia stepped close and took Agatha’s hand, squeezing with a fierce tenderness that felt like armor. “He was all our son,” she said simply. “We’ll bury him and then hunt them until the earth opens under them.”

Their grief braided into rage; their rage sharpened into strategy. Alice tapped at her keyboard, pulling up production call sheets and payrolls. Natasha compiled the wound reports and patrol blind spots. Yelena, still scabbed but burning with the need to move, started paging through camera footage.

Outside, the sky lightened. The compound’s rubble looked paler in the new light. A small victory pushed through the haze, Seren in cuffs, the offshore accounts frozen, but the story had become personal in ways none of them wanted: a former lover turned enemy, an innocent boy taken, Hela’s handwriting folded like a blade in Agatha’s skin.

Rio stood, shoulders set, and looked across the room at the faces she’d chosen to protect. “Call Maria,” she said. “Set a meeting. Quietly. I want Thor and Loki in the room. I want Odin to understand what his daughter has done. And Alice, I want an audit trail, everything Hela touched. We trace it. We find her safe houses.”

Agatha squeezed her fingers around Rio’s and let herself sink back into the chair for a second, grateful for the warmth. “Then let’s burn the map,” she said, bloodied but unbowed. “Let’s show them we are not prey.”

Rio bent and kissed the top of Agatha’s hand, an intimate benediction. “Piece by piece,” she said. “We take them apart.”

Outside, things warmed. Inside, they arranged. They would grieve, and they would hunt. They would honor. They would not rest here, not while anything of the Seven still stood. And when Hela Odinson’s name passed across their lips, it was not only as the ghost of a lost love, but as a target.

They all went their separate directions, needing to mourn in their own ways, Natasha and Yelena thanked the Widows for their help and showed them out, they slunk back into the shadows and disappeared like they were never there in the first place. 

 

Rio stood in the hallway outside the guest wing, hands flexing at her sides, the echo of gunfire and Billy’s last scream still lodged in her bones. She found Wanda sitting on the edge of the bed in Billy’s room, shoulders slumped, hands clasped tight in her lap. The proud tilt of her chin was gone, replaced by raw hollowness.

Rio lingered in the doorway for a beat, then stepped in. “Wanda.”

Wanda didn’t look up. “If you came to tell me you’re sorry, don’t.” Her voice was hoarse, but sharp. “I don’t want your guilt on top of my grief.”

Rio crossed the room slowly, sinking into the chair across from her. “I wasn’t going to say sorry.” She paused, pressing her thumb hard into her palm. “I was going to say it’s my fault.”

That made Wanda’s head snap up. Her eyes were red, furious in a way only a mother’s could be. “Don’t you dare. Don’t you dare. The only people at fault are those women. The Seven. Don’t you take my son’s blood onto your shoulders when it belongs on theirs.”

Rio swallowed, the words catching in her throat. “He was under my protection. Everyone in this house is. And I failed.”

Wanda surged forward, gripping Rio’s hand with surprising force. “No. You fought until you bled. You’ve kept Agatha alive through every attack, and you nearly got yourself killed doing it. Don’t stand there and carry my punishment along with yours. I won’t let you.”

For a long moment, Rio just stared at her, the soldier in her fighting against the truth in Wanda’s words. Finally, she exhaled, low and ragged. “Then how do you plan to survive this?”

Wanda leaned back, her eyes going distant. “I don’t know. I will scream until my throat bleeds, smash things until my hands split, and cry until my body gives out. And then, one day, maybe the pain will dull to something I can carry without choking on it.”

She closed her eyes, her jaw trembling. “But I can’t bury myself in anger and leave my husband and Tommy alone. So, I’ll do the only thing left: I’ll endure.”

Rio reached over and clasped Wanda’s shoulder. “Talk to Lilia.”

Wanda blinked at her.

“Talk to her,” Rio repeated softly. “She knows this pain better than either of us ever should. She’s carried the loss of a son every day since Colten died. She’ll know how to guide you through it. Don’t do this alone.”

Wanda’s eyes brimmed with tears, but she nodded, her lips trembling.

Rio squeezed her shoulder once more before standing. “Let one of us drive you home. You need to tell Vision and Tommy yourself. They deserve to hear it from you, not from whispers or headlines.”

Wanda bowed her head, silent, but after a long pause, whispered, “Thank you.”

Rio found Agatha upstairs in her bedroom. The actress sat curled in the corner of the bed, knees tucked under her chin, staring at the wall. Her hands trembled around a tissue, but she hadn’t cried, yet.

Rio closed the door quietly behind her, then sat on the edge of the bed. “My Love.”

Agatha turned her head slowly. Her eyes were swollen, her lips pale. “I keep hearing him, Rio. His laugh. His voice. And then the silence when he…when he fell.” Her voice cracked. “I promised Wanda I’d keep him safe. I promised.”

Rio reached for her, pulling Agatha into her arms. For a moment Agatha resisted, stiff with grief, then she crumpled against Rio’s chest, the sobs tearing free at last.

“I’ve got you,” Rio whispered, pressing her lips into Agatha’s hair. “Cry. Just let it out. I’ll hold you.”

They stayed like that for what felt like hours, Agatha clinging to Rio like a lifeline, Rio rocking her gently, eyes shut against her own tears. When Rio finally let herself cry too, it was silent, heavy, her chest aching as if it might split open.

In that room, with the weight of loss pressing down on both of them, they found something unspoken but undeniable: neither had to be strong alone.

For the first time since the fight, they allowed themselves to be simply two women mourning, bound not by duty, but by love.

And they wept together until exhaustion finally took them.
