Scars and Shadows

Chapter Summary

Rio's recovery at the cabin. Recovery brings back old memories, but brings new ones to replace the bad.

Chapter Notes

I love reading all the comments. I derive more enjoyment than I should from your guys' panic, but I do sincerely appreciate every single one of you who read my work, comment, and offer kudos and support. It truly means a great deal, and I couldn't thank you enough.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

It took another week at the hospital before the doctors agreed to release Rio, as long as she promised to keep up with physical therapy and admit herself back into the hospital if she feels any worse, or if she's not getting better by month three.

The cabin was quiet when they first arrived, the kind of silence that felt almost holy. Pines pressed close on all sides, their needles whispering in the late-spring breeze. The lake stretched out like a sheet of glass, reflecting clouds and gulls that swooped low. To Rio, it was a sanctuary. To the others, it quickly became the same.

The first storm rolled over the lake the day they arrived.

It wasn’t dramatic, no lightning, no theatrics, just a quiet gray that settled over the pines and stitched the water to the sky. The cabin breathed it in like a living thing: timber creaked, the hearth sighed, and the big windows went soft with damp. It should have felt heavy, but to Agatha it felt like an exhale. To Rio, still pale beneath the stubborn set of her mouth, it felt like a test.

The first hour was logistics. Bags to bedrooms. The fridge stocked with the grocery delivery Alice had arranged from all the way in L.A. Wanda and Vision walked the guest house with Tommy, checking locks and lights, while Yelena and Natasha moved through the cabin with a soldier’s eye, counting exits, angles, sightlines, then added a gentler layer that only family can give: extra blankets at the foot of the beds, tea on the counter, a note on the whiteboard that read: “Breakfast duty: everyone (except the patient).”

The second hour was pain.

“Slow,” Agatha murmured, bracing one hand at the small of Rio’s back and the other around her forearm as they negotiated the two broad steps from the mudroom into the great room. “We don’t get points for speed.”

“We get points for not being carried,” Rio said, only half-joking, teeth clenched as the left side of her ribs complained. The brace under her soft black tee dug in when she breathed too deep. Beneath that: stitches, tape, vivid bruises blooming like hurricanes. She handled the cane like an insult rather than a tool, but she used it. She used it because Agatha had asked.

They made it to the long leather couch. Rio hated sitting; sitting felt like surrender. But the room was a cathedral of wood and glass, the lake an altar, and surrender suddenly didn’t feel like the worst thing, at least not when Agatha curled beside her, tucking a pillow under her healing shoulder and smoothing a palm over her sternum, as if coaxing her heartbeat to remember the right rhythm.

“Doctor’s orders for today are embarrassingly simple,” Agatha said, reading from a folded paper like it was scripture. “Rest. Hydrate. Eat. Three five-minute walks inside the house, spaced through the day. Breathing exercises every hour. And no heroics.”

“No heroics,” Rio echoed, drily. “That’ll be new.”

Agatha’s smile was quick and warm. “I know a hero when I see one. Doesn’t mean I’m letting you act like one in the living room.”

For a while there was just breath and the slow patter of rain on the deck. Then the pain meds dipped, and the room tilted.

Rio’s chest hitched. She fought the cough; it fought back. One half-stifled bark of sound sent a red line of fire across her ribs and up into her shoulder. Agatha sat up at once, fingers gentle but firm along the brace, grounding her through the surge.

“Easy,” Agatha murmured. “Ride it, don’t fight it.”

“It fights first,” Rio gritted out. She didn’t like when her voice sounded thin. Didn’t like the way pain invited memory. Her hand closed briefly on the couch seam, tight, white-knuckled before she pried it open and let Agatha take it.

The cough eased. The thunder rolled somewhere very far away. When the worst was past, Agatha pressed a glass of water to her lips. Rio sipped, then frowned as a muscle jumped in her cheek, a reflex she couldn’t hide fast enough.

“Tell me,” Agatha said softly.

Rio didn’t look at her. “It’s stupid.”

“Try me.”

A slow inhale, measured. “Just memories trying to pull me under. Every time I close my eyes, I’m back in a different ambush, the one where it wasn’t me shielding someone else, but someone shielding me. Someone who’s no longer here. The sights, the smells, the sounds… they all blur together until I can’t separate then from now.”

Agatha’s thumb stroked along her knuckles. The pressure was steady, present-tense. “Then keep your eyes open,” she said, and tilted her head to kiss the corner of Rio’s mouth. “I’m here. I will always be here.”

Rio let out a breath she didn’t know she’d trapped. A small nod. “You’re infuriating.”

“Correct.” Agatha’s smile turned mischievous. “Want me to distract you with facts about my incredible beauty?”

“That does usually work,” Rio admitted, and earned a quick, delighted laugh.

By midafternoon, Wanda padded over with a tray of soup and tea, the Wanda special, which meant it was both healing and surprisingly delicious. She didn’t hover or fuss; she placed the tray on the coffee table and squeezed Rio’s shoulder with a sister’s competence. Vision followed with a laptop configured for Rio’s breathing app and a playlist Tommy had composed “For Healing,” he’d titled it, all gentle piano and ambient lake sounds recorded that morning.

“You’re all ridiculous,” Rio muttered. “And I mean that in the best possible way.”

“Get used to it,” Wanda said, a soft smile curving her mouth. “We’re not going anywhere.”

That evening brought the first walk.

“Five minutes,” Agatha reminded, tapping the timer on her phone. “And if you so much as think about rounding a corner too fast, I will handcuff you to a chair.”

“Promises,” Yelena called from the kitchen, where she and Natasha were arguing passionatly about the correct ratio of lemon to garlic in something that smelled like heaven.

Rio rose cautiously. Agatha stood with her. Bucky moved in from the porch door without a word, slotting to Rio’s left in an old formation that said I’ve got your weak side, don’t waste energy. The cane clicked once on the hardwood; Rio’s jaw flexed, but she set a pace a hair slower than her pride wanted, and they made the loop: great room, hallway, bunkroom, mudroom, back to the couch.

On the second lap, her balance wavered on the turn. The world went slightly to the right, like a drunk camera. Bucky’s hand was already there, just a brush at her elbow, not even pressure, a cue to trust the line of her own body.

“When did you get so annoyingly useful?” Rio asked.

“Since forever,” Bucky deadpanned. “But I appreciate you finally noticing.”

“How’s your stabbing, Grandma?” Yelena asked peeking her head in the room, followed by Natasha

Rio blinked. “My… stabbing?”

“The places you were stabbed,” Yelena clarified cheerfully. “Still stabby?”

Agatha snorted. Even Rio let a laugh slip; it startled her with how good it felt in her chest.

“Less stabby,” she conceded. “More achy.”

“Progress,” Natasha said, already satisfied.

By the time dinner, roasted vegetables, lemon chicken, and fresh bread hit the table, Rio’s edges had smoothed. The meds had landed. The rain had lifted. The lake had turned to molten pewter in the dusk.

They ate together at the long table. Wanda slipped easy jokes under the conversation, humor with padding around it. Agatha kept the pace light when Rio’s eyes went distant. Bucky swapped war stories for wilderness ones, wolves tracked in winter, the incredible stubbornness of raccoons. Yelena gave a dramatic retelling of being beaten by Bucky in a sprint that afternoon, complete with conspiracy theories about his “illegal leg length.”

Bucky, from the doorway, flipped her off with a smug smirk.

This, Rio thought, as warmth spread through her ribcage, was also medicine.

Night was harder.

Agatha woke to a sound that wasn’t a sound. A change in the air pressure, the way a room feels when someone holds their breath. She rolled, reaching instinctively.

Rio was sitting, not quite upright, hands clenched over the sheet, eyes open but not here. Breath quick and shallow. The scars, old and new, were stark against the silver moonlight.

“Hey,” Agatha said at once, voice low and clear. She put a palm on Rio’s sternum, not pressing, just there. “It’s me. You’re at the lake. You’re safe.”

Rio blinked once, twice, unfocused; her heart was a drum under Agatha’s hand. A tremor passed through her shoulders, then another, smaller. She swallowed.

“I know,” she said finally, hoarse. “I know.”

“Want to tell me?” Agatha asked. “Or want me to tell you something stupid until it passes?”

Rio’s mouth twitched. “Stupid, please.”

Agatha considered. “I once did an entire movie wearing a corset so tight I couldn’t sneeze, and on day seventeen I actually passed out mid-line and fell into a prop grave.”

Rio’s breath hitched, then curved, just barely, toward a laugh. “Impeccable timing.”

“Thank you.” Agatha softened. “Talk to me, mi amor.”

Rio closed her eyes. When she spoke, the words came out steady, even if her hands still shook. “The last time I was held together by tape and stitches… I was waking up to silence. Not the good kind. We were—” She paused, not to censor, but to choose. “We were ambushed. We took cover behind a burned-out Hilux. The world was loud and small and—” Her jaw worked. “She pushed me down. Valkyrie. She used her body as a wall. I lived because she died. And I keep thinking, what if I’m there again and I look left and—”

“And you’re alone,” Agatha finished softly, understanding blooming like bruises. She shifted up, palms framing Rio’s face. “You’re not.”

“I know,” Rio said. This time it sounded like a promise she wanted to believe. “I know.”

The door tapped once. Bucky’s silhouette filled the crack. He didn’t enter until Agatha nodded him in.

“You good?” he asked Rio, no preamble, because she hated preamble.

“Not yet,” she said. Honesty between soldiers was its own tenderness.

Bucky came to the foot of the bed, hands in the pockets of his sweatpants. “Remember that thing we used to do?” he asked. “Three true things.”

Rio’s eyes flicked to his. “I remember.”

“Alright.” He held up a finger. “One: You’re not in Syria. You’re in Massachusetts. The worst thing in this room is Yelena’s snoring three walls over.”

“Two,” Bucky continued. “You are not alone. Not on your left, not on your six. If your brain lies and says you are, I will personally set off the car alarm so you remember this is my extremely annoying presence.”

Rio’s mouth curved. “Please don’t set off my car alarm.”

“We’ll see,” Bucky said, deadpan. “Three: Valkyrie’s choice wasn’t permission for you to die later. It was the opposite. You honor her by living. By healing. And by letting us carry the corners when you can’t.”

Something unclenched in Rio’s chest, small and real. “Copy,” she said, voice steadier. “Three true things.”

Bucky nodded once, satisfied. “I’ll be in the chair on the porch. Yell if you need a raccoon wrestled.”

He left as simply as he’d come. Agatha slid down beside Rio again, tangling their legs.

“Three true things,” she echoed against Rio’s shoulder. “One: You are the most stubborn person I have ever met. Two: I love you more than all the bad parts of your brain combined. Three: You can wake me up a thousand times like this, and I won’t mind once.”

Rio turned her head and kissed her hair. “Copy,” she murmured, and this time when she closed her eyes, the rain was just rain.

Recovery measured itself in tiny victories.

Day four, Rio made it to the end of the dock and back, Agatha hovering like a mother hen who’d gone to finishing school but never forgot her roots. Day six, she managed the porch steps without needing Bucky’s hand. Day eight, she laughed hard enough at one of Yelena’s outrageous breakfast monologues that she had to clutch her ribs and wheeze, “Worth it,” while everyone cheered like she’d run a marathon.

There were setbacks. A muscle spasm that seized her back so abruptly she bit her lip bloody before Agatha eased her through it. A morning where the mirror showed her a stranger, hollow-eyed, stitched, not the blade-edged protector she knew, and she had to sit on the closed toilet while Agatha massaged moisturizer into her hands and told her exactly twelve terrible jokes in a row until Rio was glaring and smiling at the same time.

There were anchors. Wanda’s quiet competence as she wrapped and rewrapped Rio’s shoulder dressing with a medic’s hands. Vision’s gentle reminders to inhale for four, exhale for six, until the breathing app felt less like homework and more like a slow dance. Natasha’s lopsided grin when she beat Yelena in another spar, and then brought Rio a victory cookie she claimed was scientifically proven to promote healing.

And there was Agatha, always Agatha, flirting shamelessly when Rio’s brow knotted; stern as a general when Rio tried to do too much; a riot of warmth in the bed, on the couch, in the kitchen, perched on the counter watching Rio practice the smallest movements of lifting a kettle, turning a doorknob, buttoning a shirt without tugging the stitches.

“This is humiliating,” Rio muttered one afternoon as she worked a soft resistance band with her right hand, counting aloud to keep her breaths even.

“This is heroic,” Agatha corrected, sprawled on the rug like a cat, her long legs kicked out, reading off the PT sheet with exaggerated gravitas. “The noble warrior conquers the Band of Elastic Doom.”

Rio snorted despite herself. “You’re impossible.”

“And you love me.”

“Always.”

“Always,” Agatha repeated, and leaned up to kiss the underside of Rio’s jaw in a way that made her forget the ache for a full thirty seconds.

On the tenth day, the sun returned in full. The lake turned bright and blue, the world edged in green. Natasha and Yelena rigged a line from the porch beam and challenged Tommy to a pull-up contest; within five minutes, they were all cheating and everyone accused everyone else of egregious form violations. Bucky taught Vision how to skip stones with eerie precision. Wanda made lemonade so tart it made even Rio’s mouth pucker, and then she laughed like a bell when Agatha pretended to swoon dramatically onto the grass.

And later, when the afternoon softened, Rio stood on the dock with her cane hooked over one wrist, breathing the lake air, shoulders squared, profile steady, and said, very quietly, “This time is different.”

Agatha slid her hand into hers, their fingers interlacing. “Because you’re not alone.”

Rio looked at her then, really looked, as if cataloging a new definition of safety. “Because I’m not alone,” she agreed. “Because I have you.”

Agatha squeezed. “Always.”

Rio’s gaze drifted to the water. A memory flickered, stars over the lake, a screen and a mattress, laughter caught in their throats, and for once the past didn’t drag her; it buoyed her. She took a deeper breath, winced, then smiled through it.

“Bucky?” she called over her shoulder.

“Yeah?”

“Three true things.”

He grinned. “One: You’re ahead of schedule. Two: You still owe me a rematch at darts. Three: You’re going to be okay.”

Rio nodded once, letting the words land. “Copy.”

Agatha leaned in, brushed a kiss at her temple. “Add one more,” she whispered. “Four: You’re loved.”

Rio closed her eyes, the lake, the cabin, the people she trusted settling around her like armor she didn’t have to carry alone. When she opened them, the sky was brighter.

“Four,” she said. “Copy.”

By the second week, the house had shifted from solemn silence and pain to something closer to life. Bucky stood one morning on the porch with a mug of coffee, staring at the log beams and the joints fitted cleanly together. “You built all this?” he asked, tone halfway between impressed and disbelieving.

Rio, still wrapped in blankets, managed a small nod. “Every inch. Took me a year. Best therapy I ever had.”

Natasha arched an eyebrow from her seat beside him. “Most people buy a punching bag. You build a fortress.”

“Punching bag doesn’t keep the rain out.”

That earned a laugh from Yelena, sprawled across the porch swing, hair in a messy bun. “Honestly? Disgustingly impressive. If you weren’t already terrifying, you’d be intimidating just for being this handy.”

Agatha came out just then, balancing Rio’s pain meds on a tray with the smug air of someone about to win an argument. She leaned down to kiss Rio’s temple and quipped, “Oh, she’s disgusting, alright. Disgustingly attractive. Don’t get jealous just because your assassin resume doesn’t include ‘cabin architect.’”

“Impossible woman,” Rio groaned.

“Flatterer,” Agatha shot back, kissing her again before Yelena gagged loudly, flailing on the swing. Natasha smirked into her coffee, unbothered.

It was moments like these that reminded them all why they’d come here.

Wanda and Tommy wandered up the hill then, their footsteps soft, Tommy still moving like he wasn’t sure how to fill the empty space beside him. Wanda gave Rio a small smile. “The boys were saying how impressed they were with this place. You really did build it all?”

Rio hesitated, then nodded. “Yeah. For peace of mind.”

Wanda’s eyes softened. “I hope you get to keep it. You deserve peace.”

Rio had no sarcastic answer to that, only a quiet murmur: “So do you.”

One Day, Agatha was pacing in front of the porch, arms crossed. “I don’t care if I’ve got a coven on speed-dial and an ex-special forces girlfriend, I refuse to be the useless one in the room again.”

Natasha didn’t argue. She just tossed Agatha a pair of padded gloves. “Fine. Outside. Ten minutes.”

Yelena perked up like a cat hearing a can opener. “Oh, this is going to be good.”

Agatha showed up in a silk robe and slippers, which nearly made Natasha combust. “I’m not breaking a sweat in polyester.”

“Change.”

“But—”

“Change.”

Ten minutes later, Agatha shuffled back out in leggings and a fitted shirt that made Rio choke on her water. “Don’t break her,” Rio warned, though her eyes betrayed how little she actually minded watching.

“I’ll be gentle,” Natasha deadpanned.

She wasn’t.

Agatha cursed, tripped, and whined through push-ups and grappling drills, Yelena gleefully pinning her to the grass half a dozen times. But Agatha was stubborn. Every bruise only made her push harder. By the second month, she was holding her own. By the third, she was throwing Yelena hard enough that Bucky muttered, “Huh,” under his breath, which from him was equivalent to a standing ovation.

Rio watched every session, bundled in blankets on the porch, pride swelling in her chest. “That’s my girl,” she whispered once. Agatha caught the words on the breeze and fought twice as hard.

Meals became a ritual. Wanda and Vision cooked in the guesthouse but always brought dishes up to share, turning the cabin kitchen into a whirlwind of pots, laughter, and clashing accents. Tommy lingered more and more, until Agatha had him chopping vegetables and making sarcastic commentary like he’d been part of her chaos forever.

Evenings turned into card games and Below Deck marathons on Rio’s battered projector. Wanda and Natasha teamed up at poker, cleaning everyone out until Agatha flipped the table for “emotional damages.” Tommy laughed so hard he nearly fell off his chair, the first real laugh anyone had heard from him since Billy’s death.

The grief never disappeared. Some nights, Wanda slipped down to the water’s edge and sat there until dawn. Sometimes Agatha went with her, sometimes Tommy did, and sometimes Rio just watched from the porch, keeping vigil in silence.

Vision was the quiet anchor, always steady. And one night, Wanda murmured to Rio while Agatha slept curled at her side, “You can’t let her go before you. She wouldn’t survive it.”

Rio’s throat tightened, but she nodded. “I won’t. Not if I can help it.”

It was the closest thing to a vow either woman had spoken aloud.

The team would gather in the living room every few days, phones on speaker, tension coiled sharp getting run downs from Alice and Maria back in L.A on Hela, and Evanora’s movements. And when the calls ended, they deliberately relaxed again. Yelena demanded s’mores. Natasha taught Tommy how to clean a knife. Agatha curled into Rio’s lap, daring anyone to comment.

Because life had to keep moving.

By the third month, Rio could walk on her own, though every step still carried pain. Agatha made tormenting her a daily mission.

“Did you know,” she whispered one afternoon, sidling up to Rio on the porch, “that medically, orgasms can speed healing?”

Rio groaned. “You’re insufferable.”

“And you love it.”

“Unfortunately, yes.”

Rio talked everyone into going hiking with her to celebrate the fact shes getting her strength back. No one could find it in themselves to say no.

The trail wrapped like a ribbon around the lake, pine needles crunching beneath boots and the air sharp with the scent of water and moss. For the first time in months, Rio was walking on her own, no cane, no hand bracing her side, just her steady stride matching the others.

Agatha hovered at her side anyway, one hand brushing Rio’s arm whenever she thought no one was looking. “Darling,” she drawled, “I must say, the way you limp slightly is very… rugged. You could be the poster child for a wilderness survival magazine.”

Rio rolled her eyes. “It’s called recovering from multiple bullet wounds, Agatha. Not sexy.”

“Everything you do is sexy,” Agatha countered with a grin. “Even when you sneeze.”

Natasha groaned audibly from up ahead. “How do you people live like this?”

“With joy,” Agatha quipped, swinging Rio’s hand in hers like a schoolgirl.

Bucky smirked. “I think she does it just to annoy us.”

“Correct!” Agatha beamed, leaning over to kiss Rio’s cheek. Rio flushed, muttering something about regretting ever leaving the cabin.

Behind them, Yelena stretched her arms dramatically. “I can’t listen to this. Tommy! Race me to that rock.” She pointed toward a boulder half a mile up the trail.

Tommy raised his brows. “You sure? You’re not as fast as you think.”

“Please. I could run circles around you.”

“Bet?” Tommy smirked, already loosening his shoulders.

“Bet.”

And then they were off, pounding down the dirt path, Yelena’s braid flying and Tommy’s sneakers kicking up dust. Everyone stopped to watch.

“Ten bucks on the kid,” Bucky muttered.

“Make it twenty,” Natasha added.

Agatha cupped her hands around her mouth. “Don’t trip, Lena! Wouldn’t want to embarrass yourself in front of the children.”

“Shut up, witch!” Yelena yelled back without breaking stride.

They tore toward the boulder, neck and neck, until the final few yards when Tommy found a burst of speed and shot past her, leaping onto the rock with both arms raised like a victorious gladiator.

“I win!” he shouted, face split in a grin.

The group erupted in laughter. Wanda clapped proudly from the back. Vision offered Tommy a dignified nod like he’d just graduated from Harvard.

Yelena bent double, panting. “He—he cheated. He’s like half my weight.”

“You lost to a teenager,” Natasha said flatly. “Own it.”

“Tragic,” Bucky added, smirking.

Even Rio cracked a smile. “You’re never living this down.”

Agatha was practically doubled over with laughter, tears in her eyes. “Oh, Lena, sweetheart, I’ll tell this story at every dinner party for the rest of time.”

“Don’t you dare!” Yelena wailed.

But the mood had shifted, lighter, freer. For the first time since the ambush, since the funeral, since the hospital, they felt like themselves again. Like a family.

The trail bent closer to the water, the sunlight glittering off the lake. Agatha leaned her head against Rio’s shoulder as they walked, still holding her hand. “See? This is exactly what you needed, my love. Fresh air. Exercise. My unparalleled wit.”

“You talk too much,” Rio murmured, though her thumb brushed across Agatha’s knuckles, soft and reverent.

“And yet you love me for it.”

“Unfortunately, yes.”

“Stop calling your love for me unfortunate.” Agatha’s mock offense had everyone laughing again, including Rio herself, who gave in and kissed her quickly just to shut her up.

“Disgusting,” Natasha muttered.

“Adorable,” Wanda corrected softly, smiling at them both.

By the time they circled back to the cabin, the sun had begun dipping low, staining the sky gold. Tommy was still gloating, Yelena still sulking, and Agatha still teasing Rio mercilessly. But the laughter carried down the trail, mixing with the rustle of trees and the call of birds overhead.

For the first time in too long, they all felt whole again.

Agatha continued teasing her through training sessions, through meals, even mid-poker game, leaning close to murmur things that had Rio flushing scarlet while Natasha arched a brow. Yelena once caught them sneaking kisses by the lake and yelled, “Gross! Take it to the guesthouse!” only for Agatha to shout back, “That’s Wanda’s house, you menace!”

Tommy laughed so hard he dropped his marshmallow in the fire.

By the end of three months, Rio was no longer the pale, fragile figure who had died in Agatha’s arms. She was scarred, yes, but stronger. Her body had filled back out, her strength returning with every spar, every walk around the lake, every stubborn refusal to quit.

“You scared us,” Natasha admitted one evening as the sun sank behind the trees.

Rio nodded slowly. “I scared myself. But I had something worth fighting back to.”

Agatha leaned in and kissed her then, soft and certain. Natasha politely looked away, but not before the faintest smile tugged her lips.

 

The last night at the cabin settled over the lake like velvet. The air was cool but not sharp, carrying the scent of woodsmoke from the bonfire Rio and Bucky had coaxed to life at the edge of the shore. Flames licked high, crackling against the quiet symphony of frogs singing and the gentle slap of water against the dock.

Wanda stood near the fire with Tommy and Vision, her fingers tightening around the thin wooden handle of the paper lantern she held. The lantern glowed softly, ready for flight, its fragile skin painted with a simple star, Tommy’s touch.

Agatha, hair braided loosely over one shoulder, walked to Wanda’s side. “He’d have hated the quiet,” she said softly, her voice carrying a smile that didn’t quite reach her eyes.

Wanda gave a watery laugh. “He’d be teasing us already. Asking if we brought marshmallows.”

Together, the four of them, Wanda, Vision, Tommy, and Agatha, lifted the lantern, letting the flame inside heat the air until it began to rise. Their hands fell away at the same moment, and the lantern drifted upward, golden against the indigo night.

Everyone stood in silence as it climbed higher, its reflection shimmering across the lake’s surface. Rio’s arm slipped around Agatha’s waist, steady and grounding, while Natasha’s hand found Yelena’s shoulder. Even Bucky, quiet, watchful, bowed his head slightly.

The lantern drifted until it was just a star among stars, and only then did Wanda’s tears fall freely. Vision wrapped her into his chest, Tommy leaning into them both. Agatha reached for Rio’s hand, twining their fingers, her throat thick with the weight of memory.

“Goodbye, Billy,” Wanda whispered. “We love you.”

The silence that followed was full, not empty. Full of love, of grief, of the kind of family that clings harder after loss.

Later, laughter chased away the heaviness. They sat on logs pulled close to the fire, roasting marshmallows, trading stories that had nothing to do with battles or enemies. Natasha told the story of Yelena’s first attempt at driving. Yelena threw a marshmallow at her. Bucky claimed his cooking was superior to all of theirs, prompting Agatha to howl in protest and promise to duel him with a skillet.

Rio sat back, her arm slung over the back of Agatha’s chair, letting the fire warm the front of her while the cool night brushed her back. Agatha leaned into her, sipping wine, her laugh warm and free.

“This lake,” Agatha said suddenly, her tone shifting with nostalgia. “Do you know this is where Rio and I first became official?”

Rio froze. “Agatha.”

“Oh, don’t look at me like that, darling. Everyone already knew we were circling each other like wolves. This place sealed it.”

The group smiled, amused. Wanda’s lips curved faintly. Natasha raised an eyebrow. Yelena elbowed Bucky.

“And,” Agatha added with a devilish grin, “this is also where we first had sex.”

The silence was immediate, followed by choking laughter from Yelena and a groan from Natasha. Bucky muttered something under his breath before abruptly standing.

“Oh no,” Agatha said, realizing too late.

Bucky moved fast, scooping her up in a fireman’s carry despite her squirming. “You don’t get to traumatize us like that without consequences.”

“Bucky, put me down this instant!” Agatha shrieked, kicking her legs. “Rio! Save me!”

Rio only leaned back on her log, smirking despite herself. “I’d say you deserve this, mi amor.”

Bucky marched to the end of the dock and, without ceremony, launched Agatha into the lake. She hit the water with a splash and surfaced moments later, sputtering and laughing, her makeup streaked and her coat floating around her like seaweed.

“You absolute menace!” she shouted, flipping her soaked hair back.

The group erupted in laughter. Yelena whooped, clapping her hands. Tommy doubled over. Even Wanda, still raw with grief, laughed genuinely for the first time in weeks.

But Agatha wasn’t done. She pushed herself back onto the dock, dripping wet, and lunged at Bucky, grabbing his arm and yanking him into the lake. He went in with a curse and a massive splash.

That was the spark.

Yelena tackled Natasha into the water next, both shrieking as they went under. Tommy cannonballed in after them, sending a wave that drenched Rio and Vision, still sitting by the fire.

Rio shook her head slowly, wiping her face. “Children. All of them.”

“You’re just scared,” Agatha taunted from the lake, treading water with a grin that was pure trouble.

“Scared?” Rio stood, peeling off her flannel and tossing it aside. “You’ll regret that.”

Agatha’s smirk faltered. “Darling, wait—”

But Rio dove in with perfect form, cutting into the water and surfacing right beside Agatha. In one smooth motion, she swept the actress into her arms and dunked her under. Agatha came up spluttering and laughing too hard to even fight back.

“Betrayal!” she cried dramatically, throwing her arms around Rio’s neck.

Rio just rolled her eyes, but her smile was wide, her laughter real.

Soon, Vision waded in, shaking his head but indulging Wanda, who had rolled up her dress and slipped into the shallows. Natasha and Yelena splashed each other viciously, while Tommy egged them on. Bucky was already plotting revenge on Agatha, who kept swimming just out of reach.

The lake became chaos, screams, splashes, laughter echoing across the water. The fire burned steady on the shore, lantern light reflecting in ripples across the surface.

Agatha clung to Rio at one point, pressing her forehead to hers. “The last time we were here,” she murmured, soft enough only Rio could hear, “You took me on the best date I have ever been on.”

Rio brushed a strand of wet hair from Agatha’s face. “Best decision I ever made.”

“And I fell even more in love with you right here,” Agatha whispered. “Still am, every second.”

Rio kissed her, quick and fierce, before another wave hit them, courtesy of Yelena’s cannonball. They broke apart laughing, gasping for air.

Eventually, soaked and breathless, they all dragged themselves back onto the shore, collapsing near the fire. Clothes clung, hair dripped, teeth chattered, but the smiles were wide, unbroken.

For a while, they just sat, watching the flames lick the night sky, listening to the water settle back into calm.

It wasn’t perfect. There was still danger ahead, battles waiting for them beyond the lake. But tonight, here, they were whole. They were together.

And for the first time since everything began, they let themselves believe that maybe, just maybe, they’d make it through.

The fire had burned low by the time Agatha and Rio slipped away from the others, blankets pulled around their shoulders. Their clothes were still damp from the lake, hair clinging in curling tendrils, but neither cared. The porch overlooking the water was quiet, only the soft hiss of crickets and the gentle lap of waves against the shore filling the air.

Agatha nestled against Rio, her head tucked under her chin, legs drawn up under the blanket. The air carried the faint chill of midnight, but Rio’s arms kept her warm, steady and unyielding.

For a long time, they didn’t speak. They didn’t need to. The silence was full of the night, of their shared breath, of the peace neither of them had felt in months.

Agatha was the one to break it, her voice hushed, as though speaking too loudly might shatter the fragile stillness. “You know,” she murmured, “when we go back to L.A.… I don’t think I can live in that house anymore.”

Rio tilted her head slightly, pressing a kiss into Agatha’s hair. “Too many ghosts,” she said softly.

Agatha’s laugh was quiet, but it held no humor. “Every room feels tainted now. The living room where the leaks played on TV, the dining table where we planned defenses, the front gate they stormed through. Even Billy…” Her voice cracked, and she swallowed hard, curling closer. “I don’t want to keep walking through those doors, reliving it all over and over.”

Rio held her tighter, her hand rubbing slow circles down her back. “Then don’t,” she said simply. “We’ll find somewhere new. Somewhere that feels like home, not a war zone.”

Agatha hesitated, then pulled back just enough to see Rio’s face, her own eyes shimmering with nervousness. “There’s something else,” she admitted, biting her lip in a rare flash of vulnerability.

Rio’s brows lifted slightly, but her gaze stayed steady. “Go on.”

Agatha’s hand found Rio’s, fingers fidgeting with the rough scars that crossed her knuckles. “We’ve lived together for half a year now. I’ve gotten used to you being there every night, every morning. Even when you’re bossy and terrifying and make me eat actual vegetables—”

Rio smirked faintly. “You’re welcome.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but her smile was soft. “My point is, I can’t imagine not having that. Not having you. So…” She drew in a breath, nerves bubbling in her chest, and finally asked, “When I get a new place, will you move in with me? Not as my bodyguard. As my partner. As… us.”

The words hung between them, fragile and enormous. For a moment, Agatha feared she’d ruined the peace, overstepped, asked too much. But then Rio’s expression softened, the guarded lines around her mouth easing, her eyes warming in a way that made Agatha’s heart stutter.

“My Love,” Rio said, her voice low and reverent. “I thought you’d never ask.”

Agatha blinked, her nerves flipping into something like disbelief. “You mean, you actually want to?”

Rio cupped her face in both hands, her thumbs brushing along her cheeks. “I want nothing more. I can’t picture my life without you. Even when it’s been chaos and danger and loss… every morning I’ve woken up with you beside me has been worth it. I’ll follow you wherever you go. House, cabin, hell, even a shoebox apartment. Doesn’t matter. If you’re there, it’s home.”

Agatha’s throat tightened, her vision blurring. She tried to laugh, to deflect, but the emotion was too strong. “God, you really know how to make a girl cry.”

Rio leaned in, pressing their foreheads together. “I love you, Agatha. More than I ever thought I’d be able to love anyone again. So yes, when you find that new house, I’ll be right there. With you. Always.”

The tears slipped free then, but Agatha was smiling through them. She kissed Rio, slow and deep, pouring everything she felt into it, relief, devotion, gratitude, the wild, terrifying certainty of love.

When they finally pulled apart, Agatha laughed softly, brushing her thumb over Rio’s lips. “So it’s settled. We’ll find a new place. Together. And I’m decorating.”

Rio arched a brow. “We’ll see about that. I’ve seen your taste.”

“Please,” Agatha scoffed, her grin widening. “You’re lucky to have me. Otherwise, you’d still be living in this lumberjack fantasy cabin with nothing but wood and flannel.”

Rio smirked. “You love it.”

Agatha leaned back into her chest, closing her eyes as the sound of the lake wrapped around them. “I do,” she admitted. “But I love you more.”

The night stretched on around them, the fire embers glowing faintly in the distance, the lantern for Billy now just a memory among the stars. And on that porch, wrapped in each other, they let themselves believe in a future—one built not on fear, but on love, laughter, and the promise of a shared home waiting just ahead.

As they walked back toward the cabin, fingers still intertwined, Agatha’s phone buzzed in her pocket. She pulled it out lazily, expecting Jen or Wanda, but froze when she read the message on the screen:

Love makes you weak. I’ll prove it soon. – Snake.

The air seemed colder suddenly, the shadows around the lake a little darker. Rio read over her shoulder, jaw tightening, but when Agatha’s eyes met hers, the fear there hardened into something fiercer, resolve. Whatever Evanora thought she could take from them, she was wrong. They weren’t weak. They were stronger than ever.

Chapter End Notes

Next Chapter: IT'S THE FINAL SHOWDOWN!!!! Everyone hold each other's hands, we will get through this together, I promise.

Curtain Call

Chapter Summary

Final Showdown between the group and the remaining members of the Seventh Veil.

Chapter Notes

This chapter took me almost 8 hours to write. I kept rewriting it, trying to get it perfect, and wrap everything up in a nice bow; hopefully, I accomplished that.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

They hit L.A. just after dusk, the city smeared in neon and brake lights, the kind of glow that made every window look like an eye. The two SUVs rolled through the back gate and into Agatha’s drive; Sonya and Steve stepped out of the shadows like they’d grown there. Hugs were quick, hand squeezes were quicker. Everyone looked older than three months ago, not in years, but in grit.

Inside, the house felt both familiar and slightly wrong, like a favorite coat that didn’t fit quite the same after a long winter. Furniture had shifted; security cameras had multiplied. A framed photo of Billy that Wanda had quietly set on the mantle caught the lamplight. Agatha’s gaze hooked on it and stayed, just for a beat.

“Welcome back to the circus,” Alice said, already moving, already plugging in. She’d set up a war corner in the dining room: three laptops, a portable server, a whiteboard dense with timelines and codenames. Her hair was up, her eyes red from the plane and not-sleep. “I’ve got files for each of you, but let me give you the lay of the land before we drown in PDFs.”

Jen slipped in behind her with Lilia, both in black, both carrying the exhaustion of people who’d been keeping watch while others healed. Lilia crossed to Agatha first, cupped her cheek, kissed her forehead—maternal, fierce, finished with a whispered, “You look rested, thank God.” Then to Rio, a steady clasp of forearms that said what words didn’t need to.

They gathered around the table. Natasha and Yelena bracketed the back wall. Bucky took a chair and immediately turned it backward like he was interrogating it. Wanda perched on the arm of the couch, Vision beside her, their fingers laced.

Alice clicked a slide to life on the largest monitor. Headlines stacked like falling dominoes: 

Entertainment Weekly: Three Months of Silence: Agatha Harkness, Wanda Maximoff, and Rio Vidal Retreat from Spotlight After Tragedy

Following the heartbreaking death of Wanda’s son, Billy, and the near-fatal ambush that left bodyguard Rio Vidal in critical condition, the women disappeared from public view. Fans speculated endlessly, but the silence only deepened the mystery.

The Hollywood Reporter: From Tragedy to Resilience: Inside Agatha Harkness and Wanda Maximoff’s Three-Month Disappearance

Exclusive sources reveal how Wanda, Agatha, and Rio Vidal quietly retreated to heal—away from cameras, red carpets, and headlines. With Billy’s loss and Rio’s recovery, the trio returned stronger, bonded, and unafraid to live their truth.

“Media first,” Jen said, voice crisp, practiced. “Your complete blackout worked. It bought us quiet and infuriated the press. Speculation ran rampant: secret shoot, witness protection, breakup, breakdown. We fed them nothing,” She flicked her phone. “But your fans? The Coven held the line. They kept amplifying Jessica’s piece. They treated the silence like a boundary, not an admission of guilt.”

Agatha exhaled. She’d suspected; hearing it still loosened something in her chest. “Good. They deserve medals.”

“Or a pizza party,” Yelena offered.

Alice pulled up a second timeline, this one cold, clinical. “While you were healing, Evanora and Hela didn’t vanish. They went low. Quiet accounts, burner phones. We tracked movement through the Seventh Veil’s shell companies. Funds shifted, smaller amounts, more often. They were paying retainers, not hiring armies. My read? They were rebuilding the bones, safe houses, gear, favors.”

“Any public moves?” Rio asked, shoulders squared, face unreadable but for the darting pulse at her jaw.

“Two,” Alice said. “A fire at a storage facility in Orange County, arson, targeted. It housed evidence impounded from Raven’s apartment. Most of it survived thanks to sprinklers, but not all. Also, an attempted breach at the L.A. County evidence locker, where all the evidence from what we've gathered so far on the Seventh Veil is, was thwarted by a very grumpy clerk and a lock that refused to die. That one has Hela’s fingerprints, literally. Partial, smudged, but hers.”

Natasha’s head tilted. “Sloppy.”

“Desperate,” Bucky countered.

Jen slid a folder to Agatha, another to Rio. “We were granted limited access to interview Raven and Kyra in custody.”

Agatha’s brows shot up. “And you didn’t lead with that?”

“We wanted you seated first,” Lilia said, tone wry, eyes soft.

Jen opened her folder. “Raven first. She’s… cooperative in the way of someone trying to plead their way into witness protection. She insists she wasn’t the mastermind, just a courier and a door-opener. She named Renna as ‘the firestarter’ and painted Hela as the blade. She also tried to apologize to you on camera, Agatha, about the role she's played in all this.” Jen’s mouth tugged. “We did not give her that satisfaction.”

Agatha’s jaw worked once, then eased. “Good.”

“Alice and I cross-checked,” Jen went on. “Some of Raven’s detail aligns, addresses, dates, a storage unit that did, in fact, contain the same make of light clamps used to sabotage the catwalk rig. But when we pressed her on Evanora, she clammed up. Still loyal to the brand.”

Alice took the handoff. “Kyra was… a different flavor. She switches between rage and worship. She loves you, Agatha, and she hates you for not loving her back. She mocked Rio’s team again,” Alice’s eyes flicked to Rio, apologetic, “and called Hela ‘the knife with a heartbeat.’ She also slipped up twice. First, she muttered that ‘the Crow sees everything,’ which confirms Raven was also their watcher. Second, she referenced ‘the Fox’s ashes,’ which suggests Renna’s death rattled the hive more than they let on.”

“Kyra also tried to bargain,” Alice added. “Wanted us to transfer her to county lockup in exchange for helpful hints. We declined.”

“Wise,” Natasha said.

“Seren?” Rio asked. “What’s she done besides stew behind bars?”

“She’s gotten her hands on a few phones behind bars, posted a few angry and cryptic tweets, prison guards have her in solitary confinement to stop contraband from getting to her, but my gut tells me she still has access somehow,” Alice said.

Rio’s pacing slowed. “Evanora? Any more direct communication?”

Lilia’s mouth flattened. “She sent an email to my office last month. No demands. Just a line: I made you, and I can unmake you. I forwarded it to Maria, who forwarded it to the DOJ. Officially, it’s evidence. Unofficially, it’s trash.”

Agatha stared at the table, then lifted her chin. “She wants me back in the light. She wants the stage. We deny her that, she’ll create a stage.”

“Which brings us to now,” Alice said, pivoting to the final slide: a map of the city, pinpricks of red and blue. “Hela’s cards slowed. Evanora’s money moved. Seren continues to taunt us from behind bars. And today—” She zoomed on a red dot pulsing near the Fashion District. “—there’s a cluster of pings we’ve never seen before. Burners booted, killed, booted. It smells like staging.”

Jen exhaled through her nose. “And the media is hungry. They’ve gotten used to nothing; they’re ready to feast on anything. There’s already chatter that you’re back in town. We kept it quiet, but someone saw the SUVs at the gate.”

Agatha glanced at Rio. Rio’s look said what it always did: We move only when we say so.

They broke for a few hours of sleep in the house that no longer slept, alarms layered over alarms. Morning crept in gray and wary.

The morning began with static.

Alice had been tracking chatter since dawn, eyes bloodshot, coffee cooling untouched beside her laptop. Rio was restless, too restless, pacing the length of Agatha’s living room with a stiffness that betrayed her still-mending ribs. Agatha watched her from the couch, trying not to smile at the stubbornness that made Rio walk even when every step cost her.

It was Jen who burst in first, phone clutched white-knuckled. “She’s out,” she said flatly.

The room froze. Wanda, perched on the arm of a chair, went pale. Natasha’s hand drifted unconsciously to the gun at her hip.

“Seren?” Rio asked, though she already knew. 

“Prison transfer ambush. The whole convoy was killed. She’s gone.” Jen set the phone down on the table like it burned. “And she’s broadcasting.”

Alice spun the laptop around. The screen flickered with a grainy video feed: a sniper’s crosshairs locked on Rio. It was live. Somewhere.

The feed zoomed, sharpened, and showed her face in high definition.

Agatha felt her stomach plummet.

The comments were already scrolling, hundreds of them.


 “Who’s filming this?!”
 “Where is Rio?!”
 “This isn’t funny!”

Rio leaned forward, jaw clenched. “That’s not live,” she said after a beat, her voice hard with forced calm. “Lighting’s off. Sun’s wrong. They’re using stock.”

Agatha saw the muscle ticking in her cheek, the way her hand hovered near her sidearm, and knew. Rio was furious, but beneath it, afraid.

“They’re baiting you,” Alice confirmed. “Trying to make you reckless.”

Agatha’s hand curled into a fist in her lap. Reckless wasn’t Rio’s problem. It was hers.

Agatha lay awake in the dark that night, Rio’s steady weight warm against her side. The soldier was asleep, or close to it, her breaths shallow and uneven, the sound of someone whose body fought rest even when it needed it most. Every shift made the mattress creak, every soft groan of pain sent guilt spearing through Agatha’s chest.

On the nightstand, her phone glowed faintly. One message replayed in her mind: Seren’s video, the rifle scope centered on Rio’s chest as she walked across their balcony with a mug of coffee. Alice had confirmed it wasn’t live. Old footage, spliced, doctored. A bluff. But Agatha couldn’t shake the sick truth behind it, if not today, then tomorrow. If not a bluff, then the next shot could be real.

Her hand hovered over Rio’s arm, torn between waking her and letting her sleep. In the end, she bent close, pressing her lips softly to Rio’s temple. “I love you,” she whispered, a confession in the dark. “That’s why I have to do this.”

She slid carefully from the bed, pausing when Rio shifted in her sleep, her hand clutching at empty sheets before settling again. Agatha’s throat burned as she forced herself to move. She dressed quickly, in dark clothes, soft shoes, and tucked her phone into her pocket.

One call. That’s all it took. Evanora answered on the second ring, her voice low and mocking, velvet hiding the blade.  “My wayward daughter. I wondered how long you’d last.”

“You leave them alone,” Agatha said, her voice sharp, even as her hands trembled. “Rio. The team. Wanda’s family. This ends with me.”

A pause, then a cruel little laugh. “You sound just like her. Always ready to bleed for people who won’t survive anyway.”

“Where?” Agatha snapped, refusing to give her mother the satisfaction of hesitation.

Evanora purred out the address, the abandoned soundstage where Agatha had filmed her first big role. “Come alone. Or I’ll send Hela to finish what she started.”

The line went dead.

Agatha stood for a moment in the quiet room, the hum of L.A. traffic seeping through the windows, Rio’s uneven breathing steady behind her. She turned back once, memorizing the sight: Rio curled on her side, one hand reaching unconsciously toward the space Agatha had left, even in sleep.

Agatha swallowed hard. “I’ll come back to you,” she whispered. “I swear it.”

Then she slipped out into the night.

A van waited at the curb, its headlights off, engine idling low. Two masked figures stood beside it, weapons visible even in the dark. Agatha didn’t resist as they bound her wrists. She didn’t fight when they shoved her into the back seat.

The last thing she saw through the tinted glass was the faint outline of their bedroom window, a rectangle of gold against the night. Somewhere behind it, Rio slept, safe for now.

Agatha closed her eyes. And let herself be carried into the dark.

Rio woke slowly, the way she always did now, pain first, then awareness. The dull throb of her healing ribs. The faint pull of scar tissue when she breathed too deeply. The warmth of the sheets. And, always, the instinctive reach for the body beside her.

Her hand met cool linen.

Her eyes snapped open.

“Agatha?”

The room was dim, dawn only just brushing the curtains with pale light. The lamp on the nightstand was still on, though, casting its weary glow over the empty side of the bed. The blanket was folded back, not thrown. Agatha had gotten up carefully. Deliberately.

Rio’s chest went tight. She forced herself up, ignoring the flare of pain. Her eyes swept the room the way they used to sweep kill zones. Agatha’s boots were gone. So was her coat.

On the dresser, Rio spotted it, an envelope propped against her watch. Her throat closed as she reached for it, her fingers already trembling.

Her name. Just her name, written in Agatha’s looping script.

She tore it open.

My love,

I know you’ll be furious. I know you’ll never forgive me for leaving you like this. But I can’t keep letting you bleed for me. You’ve already given me more than anyone ever has: your scars, your strength, your love. If I let you give me your life too, then Evanora wins, even if she never touches me.

They want me, not you. If I go, maybe I can end this without another body on the floor. Maybe I can protect the only thing that matters anymore—you. Don’t follow. Don’t come after me. Please. Live.

Yours, always,
 Agatha.

The letter shook in Rio’s hands. She read it once, twice, then crushed it in her fist, rage flaring hot enough to make her wounds scream.

“Goddammit, Agatha.” Her voice cracked against the walls.

She stumbled to the window, yanking the curtain aside. The street outside was empty, save for the faint rumble of a distant engine disappearing into the early morning haze.

“She’s gone,” Rio muttered, half to herself, half to the ghosts that always followed her. Her heart hammered in her chest, uneven and panicked, the sound louder than the city itself.

Her comm sat on the nightstand. She grabbed it, thumb shaking as she keyed into the team channel. “Agatha’s gone. She left. She gave herself up.”

Voices erupted all at once: Natasha’s sharp curse, Yelena demanding coordinates, Bucky’s clipped stay calm.

Rio pressed her palm hard against her forehead, willing herself to breathe. She wanted to punch the wall, to throw the lamp, to tear the city apart brick by brick until she found her. But the only thing that left her was a hoarse whisper:

“She thinks she’s protecting me. She thinks, she thinks this ends if she gives herself over.”

For the first time in years, Rio felt helpless. Not because she didn’t know what to do, she knew exactly what to do, but because the one person she would burn the world for had asked her not to.

Her chest heaved. She looked at the crumpled letter in her fist. “Too late, mi vida. You should’ve known I’d never let you do this alone.”

And with that, Rio shoved down the pain, shoved past the fear, and started pulling on her gear.



The van smelled of cigarettes and old leather.

Evanora sat across from her, elegant even in cruelty. Her nails were sharp, painted a glossy venom green. “So easy,” she purred, tapping a nail against her wine-red lips. “My daughter walks into the wolf’s den all by herself.”

Agatha leaned back, crossing her ankles like she was lounging instead of shackled. “Well, I figured if I didn’t, you’d just keep sending badly edited livestreams. Frankly, it was embarrassing.”

The slap came quick, sharp. Agatha’s cheek burned, but she kept her smile lazy. “Careful, Mother. You’ll smudge your polish.”

Evanora’s lips curved in something between a snarl and a smile.

Across from her, silent, was Hela. Hood up, eyes shadowed, but unmistakable. Agatha’s chest tightened at the sight, though she willed her face to stay neutral. First love. First betrayal. And now, one of her captors.

“You don’t even have the decency to look ashamed,” Evanora hissed.

“Of what? Not turning into you?” Agatha shot back. “If that’s shame, I’ll pass.”

Another slap. Harsher. Agatha let the sting settle, then raised her brows. “Keep this up and the fans are going to think this is a reboot of Mommy Dearest.”

For a heartbeat, Hela’s mouth twitched. A crack in her mask. Then she looked away, jaw tight.

Evanora didn’t notice. She was too busy reveling in the small power of violence, the old patterns replayed.

They brought her to the abandoned soundstage.

It was ironic, really, poetic in a way Agatha could almost appreciate. This was where she’d first met Hela. A set dressed as a gothic manor, long rotted now, cobwebs in the corners, scaffolding rusting above. A hollow place built for pretending.

The soundstage smelled of dust and mildew, its rafters groaning in the night wind. Once, cameras had rolled here, lights blazing, extras laughing between takes. Now, the only lights came from rigs Seren had set up, cheap ring lamps, mounted phones, wires snaking across the cracked concrete. The glow painted Agatha like an actress trapped in a role she hadn’t agreed to.

Her wrists were bound, her knees driven into the floor. She held her head high anyway, hair tumbling wild, eyes burning into the shadows where she knew the cameras were.

Evanora made her entrance like she owned the stage. Cloaked in black, her presence heavy, magnetic, every gesture precise as if she’d rehearsed for this moment her entire life. Beside her stood Hela, silent as a statue, eyes fixed on Agatha with something unreadable, something that almost looked like grief before it hardened into ice.

“Roll it,” Evanora ordered. Seren, smirking, tapped the feed live. Notifications flared across the phones, millions of viewers flooding in instantly. The Seventh Veil’s audience had been primed, and now the whole world was watching.

Agatha squinted against the light. “You should at least have sprung for good lighting. I look washed out.”

The livestream exploded instantly.

“AGATHA???”
 “What the hell is this?!”
 “Evanora HARKNESS is behind the Seventh Veil?!  Agatha’s own mother?”
 “WHERE IS RIO?!”

The comments flooded faster than Seren could moderate. Tens of thousands, then hundreds. Agatha couldn’t see the numbers, but she could feel it, like the roar of a crowd.

Evanora sneered. “They don’t care about you. Not really. They’ll turn on you the moment I show them the truth.”

“What truth? That I have terrible taste in exes?” Agatha quipped, flicking her gaze at Hela.

The corner of Hela’s jaw flexed.

The comments scrolled faster:


 “She’s still funny?? Even now??”
 “RIO HELP HER”
 “Her own mother is behind all that's happened to Agatha?! That's messed up.”
 “Don’t let them win, Agatha!”

Evanora circled Agatha slowly, the click of her heels echoing through the cavernous set. “Do you see this woman?” she said, her voice carrying, smooth as oil. “The world calls her a star. They call her powerful, beautiful, untouchable. They worship her.”

She stopped abruptly, crouching to meet Agatha’s eye. Her hand shot out, crack! Across Agatha’s face. The sound echoed. Blood welled at Agatha’s lip, but she refused to look away.

“They should not worship her,” Evanora hissed, gripping Agatha’s chin hard enough to bruise. “They should be revolted by her.”

The livestream chat exploded in a flood of horrified comments. 

Agatha’s smirk, though faint, cut through the blood. “A bit theatrical, don’t you think, Mother? I give it a six out of ten. The punch could use more commitment.”

Evanora snarled, slamming her fist into Agatha’s stomach. Agatha doubled slightly, coughing, but still managed to wheeze, “Better. Seven.”

“You mock me even now,” Evanora spat, grabbing a fistful of her hair and forcing her head back so the cameras could catch her face. “Tell me, world, does she look divine now? Does she look powerful?”

She threw Agatha down, then turned to the cameras, her voice swelling with fury. “You don’t know who she really is. You don’t know what I gave up to bring her into this world. Do you think her talent, her fame, her beauty, all of it, was hers? No. It was mine. She owes me her life. She owes me everything. And what did she give me in return?”

She stalked back, striking Agatha across the cheek again, the sound sharp and ugly. “Nothing but shame. Nothing but sin.”

Agatha spat blood to the side, lifting her gaze with defiance. “You’ve hated me since I could crawl. Why? Why was it never enough, Evanora?”

For the first time, Evanora’s face twisted into something raw, primal. Her voice shook with venom. “Because you were born evil. Because I felt it, even before you drew your first breath. I should have killed you before you left my body. I should have snuffed you out before the world ever saw you.”

The words hung in the air, heavy and vicious. The livestream chat exploded, fans screaming in disbelief, horror, rage.

Agatha’s laugh was broken, but it was still a laugh. “And yet here I am. All the talent, all the love, all the power you’ll never touch. Doesn’t that burn you, Mother? That no matter how hard you try, I’ll never belong to you.”

Evanora’s fist cracked against her jaw again, snapping her head sideways. Hela flinched, almost imperceptibly, but did not move. Her jaw clenched, eyes flicking briefly away from the cameras.

Evanora loomed over Agatha, breathing hard, her hands trembling with rage. “You are a disgrace. A parasite. A disgusting sinner playing goddess while the world bows. But tonight, they will see you as I have always seen you. Weak. Pitiful. Broken.”

She seized Agatha’s chin again, forcing her face toward the lens. “Look at her, world. Look at your so-called star. This is what she truly is.”

Agatha’s swollen lip curled into a bloody smile. “Still better than you.”

The chat exploded again, Agatha’s fans refusing to accept the narrative Evanora tried to spin. 

WE BELIEVE IN YOU AGATHA! 

YOU ARE OUR STAR!

HANG ON, RIO’S COMING!

Evanora’s fury sharpened. She raised her hand again, but this time she hesitated, her eyes flicking toward Hela. The ex-lover’s face was unreadable, carved from stone, but her fingers twitched at her side as though she’d reached for a weapon and thought better of it.

Agatha saw it, and for a heartbeat her heart clenched, not with fear, but with memory. The woman who had once held her, once whispered love against her skin, still lived somewhere inside that rigid frame. But the coldness in Hela’s eyes told her it wasn’t enough. Not anymore.

Agatha raised her chin, blood dripping, voice raw but steady. “Go on then, Mother. Hit me again. All you’ll prove is what I’ve always known: that I was never the monster here. You were.”

Evanora’s hand trembled as it hovered above her, her fury and need for control warring with the undeniable truth in Agatha’s words. She snarled, lowering her hand only to strike again, harder, desperate now.

The livestream roared, a chorus of outrage and devotion. And though every blow landed, every bruise bloomed, Agatha’s spirit only burned brighter, her sarcasm a shield stronger than any Rio could have given her.

Back at the house., Rio was pacing like a caged wolf.

Alice had the stream mirrored on every screen. Natasha, Yelena, and Bucky were gearing up fast. Maria was barking orders into a secure line.

“She’s stalling them,” Natasha said under her breath, eyes on the feed. “Buying us time.”

“Or trying to provoke them,” Yelena added, checking her sidearm.

Rio’s fists clenched. “Every second she’s in there, Evanora’s breaking her down. We have to move.”

“We don’t have location confirmed yet,” Alice shot back, fingers flying over her keyboard. “Give me a few minutes.”

“We don’t have a few minutes!” Rio snapped, voice breaking. “She’s bleeding on camera and cracking jokes, how long do you think she can keep that up?”

Agatha’s face filled the screen then, blood at her lip, but a smirk cutting through it.

“Funny thing about family,” she said to the camera. “They’re supposed to love you. Mine just livestreams me getting slapped. Five stars on Yelp, would not recommend.”

Rio’s chest constricted. God, she loved her.

Rio leaned on the table, knuckles white. “I swear to God, if we don’t get there in time—”

“You will,” Maria cut in sharply. Her tone brooked no argument. “You’ve been with her through worse. You’ll get her through this.”

Rio closed her eyes, forcing a breath. “Hold on, mi amor,” she whispered. “I’m coming.”

On the stream, Evanora grew more unhinged with each passing second.

She yanked Agatha’s head back by the hair, eyes wild. “Smile for them now, darling. Show them your ugly side.”

Agatha bared her teeth, a parody of a smile. “You always did love directing. Shame you were never any good at it.”

The comments exploded. Seren cursed, trying to wrestle with the flood of text.

Hela stood in the shadows, knife glinting, chest rising faster now. Watching Agatha defy every blow. Watching her endure. Something burned in her eyes, jealousy, rage, a flicker of that old love. It was impossible to tell which would win.

Agatha, still bleeding, still bound, tipped her chin at the camera and smirked again.

The livestream timer ticked past twelve minutes. In internet time, that was an eternity, long enough for the world to light up, long enough for fury to harden into action.

“Got it,” Alice breathed. Her fingers flew, splitting windows, pulling satellite overlays and municipal records into a dizzying lattice. “Power draw spike at a decommissioned soundstage in Sunland, Stage 14. Someone’s piggybacking broadcast bandwidth off an old fiber trunk. That’s your feed.”

“Gear up,” Maria snapped. “Widows on point. Barton on Overwatch. Barnes with Vidal. I’m calling LAPD to cordon the outer blocks, but we'll go first.”

“You’re not cleared,” Natasha said to Rio without looking up, already clipping a blade to her thigh.

“I don’t care,” Rio shot back, voice iron. “She’s in there.”

Bucky stepped in before the argument could flare. “You’re with me, Cap,” he said in the old way, half-tease, half-battle cry. 

The van rolled dark, quiet, breath held. In the back, Yelena checked a compact SMG with the humming, content energy of a cat about to knock over a priceless vase. Natasha’s eyes were half-lidded, and that calm she wore like armor. 

Alice spoke in their ears. “Two heat signatures on the roof, lookouts. Four on the ground level at the south loading bay. One on the catwalks, moving. And a cluster in the main stage. That’s your show.”

“And Seren?” Maria asked.

“Main stage, behind a control bank. Hands on the stream.”

“Cute,” Yelena muttered. “We cut the hands.”

“Rules of engagement,” Maria said. “Alive if possible.”

“Alive,” Yelena echoed, like the word tasted wrong.

The van braked in the shadows. Doors opened, and the night breathed cold.

Rio stepped out last, pain like a private storm moving under her skin, and beyond it, a discipline honed to a razor. She rolled her shoulder gently, breath measured. Every nerve said go. The part of her that had died on a sidewalk a few months ago said Don’t ever stop.

“On me,” Natasha murmured.

The team split, each person going exactly where they needed to be.

Clint ghosted up a fire escape with a long case. Sixty seconds later, two soft thwips and the roof lookouts went still, stunned, zip-tied by lines that descended out of nowhere.

Yelena slid along the southern wall, knife flying through the air towards the door cam, disabling it. Natasha flowed past her, a flash of dark and metal, and two guards dropped without a sound, one sleeping, one whimpering gently around a dislocated shoulder.

Bucky took the north side, moving like a shadow with weight. A guard blinked, and then the world tilted as Bucky knocked him unconscious with a precise elbow to the temple.

“Perimeter clear,” Clint said in the comms. “You’ve got one on catwalks.”

“Mine,” Yelena sang.

“Yelena,” Natasha warned.

“Alive,” Yelena sighed. “Probably.”

Inside, the soundstage was all ghosts and scaffolds. Every footstep kicked dust. Somewhere, a generator thrummed, steady as a threat.

Rio’s chest tightened when she saw the glow through the thin seam of the main-stage doors, the too-bright white of production lights. She heard Evanora’s voice before she saw her, high and fevered, the brittle edge of someone who’d bet everything on a single hand.

“—and you thought they loved you,” Evanora spat, words knifing through the air. “They love a mask. I’ll peel it for them.”

Agatha’s laugh slid out like velvet and steel. “Good luck, Mother. I’ve been doing my own makeup since I was seven.”

The team fanned out along the doors, weapons drawn, nerves tuned to a razor’s edge. Maria raised three fingers. Two. One.

They breached.

The old film set blazed under harsh lights, once-grand walls now peeling flats. Cables snaked across the floor, cameras on tripods blinking red. At the control desk, Seren jolted, feral-eyed, her hands flying over keys. Hela’s hooded head snapped up from the shadows. And Evanora—Evanora turned, lips curling, eyes catching the sniper red dots trained on her and then on Rio.

For one stretched beat, everything narrowed to that line of sight: predator and protector recognizing each other across the set.

Agatha saw Rio then. Relief cracked through her mask, the smallest drop in a drought. But she smoothed it over in the next breath, tilting her chin with a bloody smirk.


“About time,” she drawled. “I was about to start reading monologues.”

“Cut the stream,” Maria barked.

Seren slammed her hands on the board. The feed stuttered, then doubled, stronger, filling every screen in the world. Her grin was jagged, fever-bright. “Say hi to the world, heroes.”

A knife thunked into the desk an inch from her palm. Yelena leaned in, voice honey-sweet. “Hi. Move again, and I’ll turn your fingers into keycaps.”

Seren froze. Yelena smiled like a shark.

“Agatha,” Rio said, and the name trembled with every way it could break.

Evanora yanked Agatha back by the rope, dragging her into the center light, face tilted to the main camera. “You don’t get to stage your own rescue,” she spat.

Hela stepped forward, not shielding Evanora, not yielding either. Her gaze cut to Agatha for a heartbeat, softening before snapping cold again.

“Hands where we can see them,” Natasha ordered, calm as iron. “Evanora Harkness, you’re under arrest for kidnapping, assault, conspiracy to murder, and a list my wife will enjoy reading in court.”

Evanora’s laugh was jagged glass. “Arrest me? It should be you on trial!”

Rio didn’t wait for the theatrics. She stepped in, pistol steady, voice low and lethal. “Step away from her. Now.”

“And if I don’t?” Evanora purred.

“Then I make you,” Rio said flatly.

Bucky slid left, drawing Hela’s line. Clint’s red dot settled at Hela’s shoulder seam. Yelena clamped Seren’s wrist in a lock. Natasha advanced like weather moving in, calm and unstoppable.

It might have ended there.

But Evanora’s gaze snagged on the monitor where chat screamed in real time: 

RIO’S HERE!!

EVANORA GO TO HELL!!

GET HER RIO!!

Something in her cracked. She leaned in so close to Agatha that their foreheads almost touched. “You think they love you?” she hissed. “Watch them love this.”

Her knife hand twitched.

Rio fired.

The shot blew through Evanora’s wrist. The blade clattered to the floor. Evanora shrieked, blood blooming bright.

“Don’t,” Rio growled.

That was when Hela moved. Knife flashing, jealousy like wildfire, she lunged straight for Agatha’s throat.

Steel rang, the sound of Bucky intercepting her, blades sparking as violence became language. Hela fought like a dancer turned to a weapon: coiled, ruthless, each strike meant to kill. Bucky answered with soldier’s precision, blocking, twisting, punishing with weight instead of speed. The floor cracked under their feet.

“Rotate!” Rio snapped, instincts overriding pain.

Bucky disengaged. Hela spun and met Rio head-on.

Her ribs screamed, her shoulder burned electric, but Rio didn’t care. She let the knife graze her side, stepped inside Hela’s arc, and slammed her pistol butt into Hela’s wrist. Metal clanged. The blade skittered.

Hela went barehanded, clawing for Rio’s throat. Rio pivoted, caught her wrist, and flipped her hard to the concrete. Hela rolled, cat-fast, and drew a backup knife. Of course, she had one.

They circled, breaths ragged.

“Always had a thing for brunnettes,” Hela hissed, eyes flicking to Agatha. “But this one? She’ll break.”

Rio smiled without humor. “Not before you.”

Hela struck high, low, and fast. Rio countered with the discipline of someone who spent her life fighting. A knee to the sternum, a twist of the wrist, a headbutt that cracked bone. Blood ran hot down her collar, but she pressed forward, relentless.

For a heartbeat, Hela backed off from Rio, and the world narrowed, just Agatha and Hela, staring at each other across the set they fell in love on. The old scenery loomed like hollow ghosts of the life they’d once dreamed together.

“You could have walked away,” Agatha spat, voice raw. Blood streaked her lip, but her eyes burned hotter than the lights overhead. “You could have stayed with me. But instead, you sold me out. You killed Billy. You betrayed everything we had.”

Hela’s smile was sharp and broken. “We never had anything but lies, Agatha. You, the star. Me, the shadow. You think I didn’t notice? You think I didn’t know I’d always come second to your fans, to your coven, to your shine?”

Agatha’s laugh cracked, harsh and furious. “Second? You were first. You were my first love, my first home. And I still had no ill will toward you, not even after you broke my heart, that was, until I learned you were the rat. Until you made my worst nightmares real.”

For the first time, Hela faltered. Rage flickered with something else, something that looked dangerously like regret. “I did what I had to,” she whispered, and for a flash it wasn’t the assassin speaking, but the girl who once shared her jacket with Agatha on a drafty set, who once kissed her under buzzing stage lights like it was the whole world.

Agatha shook her head, grief cutting through her anger. “No. You did what you wanted. And you wanted to destroy me more than you ever wanted to love me.”

That landed. Hela’s face twisted, fury fighting with a flicker of pain, old love clashing with the ruin she’d chosen.

Then, just for a breath, Hela looked at Agatha.

The longing was naked, raw, before it hardened into fury. And Rio knew.

“Don’t,” Rio warned.

But Hela smirked. “If I cant have her, you don’t get to have her.”

She pivoted, faster than breath, and flung the knife at Agatha.

Rio was already moving. She caught the arc, body intercepting steel. Pain exploded under her collarbone as the blade bit shallow, slowed by her vest. Hela lunged again for Agatha.

Yelena’s pistol coughed. “For Billy.”

Hela’s body crumpled, lifeless, strings cut.

Silence. Then Agatha’s ragged breath, Evanora’s screech, Seren’s whimper.

Rio staggered, blood slick down her chest, but forced her hands steady as she cut Agatha free. “I’ve got you,” she rasped.

Agatha surged into her arms, half sob, half laugh. “You always do.”

Maria’s voice snapped, “Cut the stream.”

Alice’s voice crackled over comms: “Feed dead. Whole world just saw the ending. Hashtags trending already.”

Natasha had Evanora by the wrist, twisting her down to her knees as she thrashed. “Don’t,” Nat said calmly.

Agatha turned, eyes sharp as glass. “They saw you hit me, Mother. They saw what you are. I never had to prove a thing. You did that yourself.”

Evanora spat, “You’ll never be rid of me.”

Agatha leaned closer, voice cold steel. “No. You’ll rot in prison. That’s your legacy.”

Sirens wailed outside. Maria barked orders, cops surged in. Seren was zip-tied and dragged, Yelena blowing her a sarcastic kiss. Bucky bent to close Hela’s eyes, face unreadable.

And Rio, Rio sat hard, finally letting gravity win, blood blooming dark across her chest. Agatha caught her, furious and tender all at once.

“You promised me,” Agatha whispered, tears streaking.

“I kept it,” Rio breathed. “Still here. Always.”

Agatha kissed her, fierce and trembling, as the cameras were hauled away, as Evanora screamed and was shoved into cuffs, as the night shifted from chaos to aftermath.

The fight was over.

They had won.

Chapter End Notes

I have decided to make a sequel to this story, but it won't be posted for a while, most likely. It will be less action-packed than this one. It will just focus on Agatha and Rio and their future together.
