The Fire We Survived

Chapter Summary

Epilogue

Chapter Notes

This brings us to the end of this road, but I will be making a sequel. I'm just not sure when that will be. It might be tomorrow or next week, or next month. But for now, we end it here.

I would like to give a special shout-out to a few individuals who have been with me every step of the way and have commented on basically every chapter. Carol and pv2011, thank you so much, and thank you to all the other people who left comments and showed their support in other ways. It truly means a lot to me.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The world didn’t sleep that night.

The livestream had cut mid-chaos, but the internet never stopped rolling. Within minutes, hashtags burned across every platform like wildfire: #FreeAgatha, #SeventhVeil, #RioSavedHer. News stations ran the grainy footage in loops, pausing on Evanora’s rants, on the moment Agatha smiled bloody but unbroken into the lens, on the flash of Rio throwing herself between her and the blade.

Headlines flooded in:

Variety: Seventh Veil Threat Neutralized: Agatha Harkness Survives Captivity in Stunning Final Confrontation

The New York Times: A Mother’s Hate, A Daughter’s Defiance: The Evanora Harkness Trial That Will Grip the Nation

People Magazine: Rio Vidal’s Heroics: The Bodyguard Who Saved Agatha Again

Rolling Stone: The Livestream That Shook Hollywood: How The Coven Fans Outlasted Terror

@CovenForever: I can’t believe Agatha stood there, bleeding, still making jokes. She’s everything. 💜 #FreeAgatha #OurStar

@WitchsCoven13: Rio literally took a knife for her AGAIN. She’s not just a bodyguard, she’s family. #RioSavedHer

@BillysLight: I lit a candle tonight. For Billy, for Agatha, for Rio. For all of them. The nightmare is over. 🌙✨

@ShieldWatchdog: Thank you SHIELD, Rio Vidal, and every bodyguard who kept her alive through this hell. Heroes, all of you.

 

By morning, Maria Hill was standing at a podium in front of the S.H.I.E.L.D. seal, her voice measured, her suit immaculate, her eyes shadowed with exhaustion.

“As of 0400 hours this morning, all known members of the Seventh Veil are either apprehended or confirmed deceased. Seren is in custody. Raven and Kyra remain in federal holding. Evanora Harkness has been remanded to a maximum-security facility to await trial on charges of conspiracy, kidnapping, attempted murder, and a bunch of other charges the DA will announce at a later date. The immediate threat to Ms. Harkness’s life has been eliminated.

While continuous round-the-clock protection is no longer required, S.H.I.E.L.D. will continue to provide event security, logistical support, and monitoring. Ms. Harkness will never be without resources, should she or her loved ones be threatened again.”

BuzzFeed: From Chaos to Calm: SHIELD Confirms Reduced But Ongoing Security for Agatha Harkness

Deadline: Maria Hill Promises Continued Oversight: Fans Thank SHIELD for Protecting Agatha

Fans flooded social media with gratitude:

@AgathaSupremacy: SHIELD gave Agatha her life back. Thank you Maria, Natasha, Yelena, Clint, Bucky, Alice all of them. 🖤

@HexedAndBlessed: Glad SHIELD is still watching. And with Rio and Agatha dating, Rio will never be too far.

@OurWitchAgatha: She’s safe. That’s all that matters. Thank you SHIELD. Thank you Rio.

In the living room, Agatha sat very still on the couch, her fingers linked with Rio’s like a lifeline.

“Well,” Agatha murmured, exhaling. “That’s one way to make an exit.”

Rio gave a small shake of her head, jaw tight. “Not an exit. Just a change in perimeter.”

Bucky leaned against the wall, nodding. “She’s right. You’ll still have backup when you need it. But the world saw Rio take a knife for you. Nobody doubts she’ll still be glued to your side.”

“More like stapled,” Yelena muttered, sprawled in a chair. “But fine. Better her than me.”

That pulled a weak laugh from Wanda, and even Agatha’s lips quirked, though her eyes shimmered with unspoken relief.

“Speaking of,” Maria said as she entered from the hall, jacket slung over her arm. Her voice softened, rare in its warmth. “It’s time.”

The words landed heavily.

For months, the house had been full of agents, a war camp disguised as a home. Now the team was packing duffels, stowing gear, and preparing to leave the constant guard behind.

Agatha stood, her hands tightening around Rio’s before she let go. “No,” she said softly. “Not like that. We’re not ending this like it’s another mission. We’re a family. So if you’re walking out that door, you better be prepared to come back once a week. Movie night, game night. Bring your partners, your kids. I don’t care. You don’t get to leave me like this.”

Silence, then Clint grinned, tired and warm. “Laura’s gonna love you for this.”

Bucky smirked faintly. “Sam won’t shut up about wanting to beat Barton at charades.”

“Kate’s going to make me watch Mean Girls again,” Yelena muttered.

Natasha’s smile was small but real, her eyes finding Maria’s. “Guess I’ll finally learn how to play Uno.”

Agatha sniffed, lifting her chin. “Uno is sacred. Don’t cheat.”

Rio slipped an arm around her waist, tugging her close. “She will cheat,” she said dryly. “She’s terrible at losing.”

“Not true,” Agatha argued, resting her head on Rio’s shoulder. “I just refuse to accept it.”

The goodbyes lingered at the door, heavier than anyone admitted. Natasha embraced Agatha firmly before stepping back into Maria’s orbit. Yelena hugged her quickly, whispering something about keeping Rio out of trouble. Clint kissed her cheek and promised baked goods from the Barton kids. Bucky clasped Rio’s shoulder, murmuring, “She’s yours now. But we’re still here.”

When the SUVs pulled out of the drive, the house felt emptier. But the echoes of laughter, of promises made, lingered like incense.

Agatha exhaled, leaning into Rio. “So… it’s just us now.”

Rio kissed her hair. “Just us.”

“Good,” Agatha said softly, glancing at Billy’s photo on the mantle. “Because I’m not letting anyone else pick the movie next week.”

Agatha stood in the middle of her living room, if it could still be called that, staring at the space where her team had just been. It felt both too empty and too full at once, like the air still hummed with all their voices.

Rio eased down onto the couch with the carefulness of someone still mindful of healing scars. She patted the cushion beside her. “Come sit before you start haunting the house like a gothic heroine.”

Agatha blinked, then gave a weak laugh, crossing over and curling into her side. “You make it sound like I’d look dramatic in cobwebs.”

“You’d look dramatic in a potato sack,” Rio muttered, pressing a kiss into her hair.

“I know I said it before, but I don’t want to live in this place anymore,” Agatha said, studying the room after a beat of silence.

Rio pulled back a little to study her, eyes sweeping the room, landing on the reinforced windows, the camera tucked high in the corner, the faint gouges in the floorboards from one too many frantic nights. “This house has been nothing but a battlefield since the day I walked in. You deserve better than to keep reliving every fight in your living room.”

Agatha exhaled, leaning her head against Rio’s shoulder. “I was just thinking the same thing. I can’t look at the steps to downstairs without remembering the night Billy—” Her voice cracked. She swallowed hard. “Wanda’s been saying the same thing about their place. Too many ghosts.”

“Then it’s settled,” Rio said simply. “We move. You and me.”

Agatha tilted her head, a sly smile tugging at her lips. “Oh? Straight to the practical talk, no dramatic proposal?”

Rio smirked faintly. “Agatha, you already asked me at the cabin. Unless you want me to get on one knee and make a PowerPoint about mortgages, I figured we were past the dramatics.”

Agatha snorted, laughter cutting through the heaviness. “Okay, fair. But if we’re going to do this, we need to agree on what we want.”

Rio leaned back, stretching her legs out. “Something low-key. Not too big. Modern lines, clean space. Something where we don’t feel like we’re living in a museum or on display.”

Agatha’s eyes widened. “Modern? You want us to live in a glass box like the Bond villain’s lair you currently live in?”

Rio smirked. “I said modern, not a fish tank. I just don’t need a castle, mi vida. I want a place that feels lived in, where we can actually breathe.”

Agatha crossed her arms, mock-offended. “Well, I was imagining something a little bigger. Enough space for the team to crash when they inevitably invite themselves over. Maybe stone walls, ivy crawling up the side. Something with a witches-cottage-meets-manor vibe.”

Rio arched a brow. “You want to live in a fairytale.”

“I am a fairytale,” Agatha shot back, grinning. “Besides, you’d look fantastic standing in front of a stone fireplace in a cozy sweater.”

Rio groaned but couldn’t hide her smile. “You’re impossible.”

“You love it.”

“Yes, yes, I do,” Rio said, brushing her thumb over Agatha’s knuckles.

They fell into a comfortable silence for a beat, both imagining futures layered over the present. Then Agatha perked up. “But we do agree on one thing.”

Rio tilted her head. “What’s that?”

“A pool,” Agatha said firmly. “Non-negotiable. I want to host pool parties. Margarita nights. Float around with you all day when we’re too tired to do anything else.”

Rio chuckled. “Fine. A pool. That I can agree to.”

Agatha looked satisfied, leaning into her again. “See, we’re halfway there already.”

Rio kissed her temple, thoughtful. “You mentioned Wanda earlier. About moving.”

Agatha nodded. “She’s been saying it a lot. Every room in their house reminds her of Billy. She wants a fresh start, somewhere Tommy doesn’t feel like he’s walking through a mausoleum.”

Rio hummed in thought. “What if we looked together? Not the same house, obviously,” she added quickly, seeing Agatha’s raised brow. “But maybe the same neighborhood. Or even a piece of land where two houses can be built. One for us, one for the Maximoffs. That way you’re close. They’re close. Everyone has space, but no one’s alone.”

Agatha blinked, visibly moved. “You’ve really thought about this.”

Rio shrugged, suddenly self-conscious. “I know how much Wanda means to you. To both of us. And if this past year has proven anything, it’s that family, found or otherwise, needs to stay close. We could build something. Together.”

Agatha’s smile softened, a rare blend of mischievous and tender. “You’re full of surprises, Vidal.”

“Don’t get used to it,” Rio muttered, though her eyes warmed.

Agatha curled closer, her voice hushed now. “I like the idea. All of it. A new house, a new start. With you. With Wanda nearby. Somewhere that doesn’t feel like a battlefield.”

Rio brushed a stray strand of hair from her face, her tone steady. “Then we’ll start looking. Tour houses, check out land. Whatever it takes until we find the one that feels like home.”

Agatha kissed her then, slow and certain, tasting like the promise of something brighter. When they pulled back, her eyes glinted with playful mischief again. “But seriously. Stone walls.”

Rio laughed, shaking her head. “We’ll see.”

Agatha smirked, triumphant already. “That’s not a no.”

Rio kissed her again just to shut her up, and for the first time in too long, the house didn’t feel haunted anymore.

 

House-hunting with Agatha and Rio was chaos, Wanda decided. Organized chaos, maybe, but chaos all the same.

The first house they toured was sleek and modern, with floor-to-ceiling windows and white walls that screamed “don’t touch me.” Rio walked through the kitchen like a general inspecting troops, tugging on the built-in range hood and running her palm along the marble countertops. “I could cook here,” she admitted with a nod.

Agatha leaned against the counter, smirking. “Oh, I could think of a few things we could do here.”

Wanda didn’t even hesitate; she whipped out the spray bottle Jen had shoved into her bag that morning, spritzing Agatha square in the shoulder. “Behave,” Wanda scolded.

Agatha gasped dramatically. “Are you serious right now?!”

“Jen warned me,” Wanda deadpanned. “Said the two of you need constant supervision.”

Rio chuckled under her breath, muttering, “She’s not wrong.”

By the third house, Agatha was making a game out of seeing how fast she could make Rio blush. In the library of an old Tudor, she whispered, “Just imagine bending me over this desk…” only to yelp when Wanda spritzed her again.

Rio, face pink, just muttered, “I hate you both.”

The day rolled on in a blur of hardwood floors, echoing staircases, and Agatha’s increasingly inappropriate commentary. At one ranch-style home, she dragged Rio into the pantry and whispered something so outrageous that Rio nearly dropped the shelving bracket she was testing. Wanda groaned and sprayed them both this time.

By the fifth house, Wanda was threatening to move without them if Agatha didn’t stop.

And then they saw it.

The stone-front house with the sloped roof, warm lights glowing in every window like it had been waiting just for them. A firepit nestled into the patio, a pool glittering under string lights, and a guesthouse at the back that practically begged to be turned into a game room.

Agatha froze in the entryway, fingers brushing the rustic wood banister. “It feels…like the cabin,” she whispered, glancing at Rio.

Rio walked slowly through the kitchen, eyes softening at the sight of the wide farmhouse sink, the six-burner stove, the sprawling counter space. “Yeah,” she murmured. “Big enough for everyone. But still home.”

Six bedrooms, five and a half bathrooms, a living room large enough for movie nights and family chaos, a large library, and a study, it was everything they didn’t know they were looking for.

“This is it,” Agatha said firmly, curling her fingers through Rio’s.

Rio nodded once, decisive. “This is it.”

Two houses down, Wanda found her own perfect fit: a cozy five-bedroom with a pool curving under a canopy of green. She could already picture Tommy’s laughter echoing in the yard, the garden Vision would plant, the dinners they’d host.

When the realtor mentioned the proximity, Agatha nearly squealed. “Wanda, we’re going to be neighbors!”

Wanda gave her a long-suffering look. “I suppose that means I’ll need two spray bottles.”

Agatha grinned. “Three. Just in case.”

Rio groaned, but even she couldn’t stop the smile tugging at her lips.

For the first time in a long time, it felt like they weren’t just surviving. They were building something together.

 

Two months later, the house was no longer just walls and beams; it was home. Agatha and Rio had officially moved in, with more help than they knew what to do with. The entire S.H.I.E.L.D. team had shown up like an unofficial moving company, dragging boxes, assembling furniture, and occasionally arguing over which direction the couch should face. Wanda and Vision had settled comfortably into their own home just down the street, and the cul-de-sac that once felt ordinary now felt like the center of a very peculiar universe.

By the time the last box was unpacked, the place already bore their fingerprints: Agatha’s shelves stacked with books and scripts, Rio’s knives gleaming in the kitchen, photos of the whole mismatched family tucked along the mantle and hallways.

Laura Barton and Rio had gravitated to each other almost immediately. Within hours of meeting, they were in the backyard, trading tips on herb gardens and meal prep, comparing how often they had to rein in Clint and Agatha’s wilder impulses. “I swear,” Laura had laughed, handing Rio a basket of fresh tomatoes she’d brought from her farm, “keeping Clint out of trouble is a full-time job.”

Rio snorted, leaning against the new stone counter. “Try keeping Agatha from flirting with the realtor when we toured this place.”

Agatha, passing by with a wine glass, only smirked. “Flirtation got us a better price. You’re welcome.”

Meanwhile, Kate Bishop and Agatha had discovered a shared love for chaos. Within minutes, Kate was sprawled across Agatha’s new sofa with her shoes kicked off, excitedly suggesting ways to test the acoustics of the new house. “We should see how loud we can get music going before Rio comes storming in to yell at us.”

Agatha’s eyes lit up. “Or karaoke. Imagine Wanda trying to belt Adele at midnight.”

“Not happening,” Wanda called from the kitchen, but the smirk tugging at her lips betrayed her amusement.

Rio pinched the bridge of her nose. “God help me.”

Bucky and Yelena meanwhile were arguing over the proper way to start a fire, Steve was cutting the wood needed for the fire, and when they argument turned physical between Yelena and Bucky, Sonya stepped in laughing and shaking her head at the childish antics, dragging the small angry Russian inside to her girlfriend who listened and tried not to laugh at Yelena’s dramatic retelling of the argument.

Sam Wilson found his place beside Rio easily, the two of them slipping into an easy camaraderie forged from shared military history. They compared scars like badges, trading stories over a couple of beers while everyone else bustled around them. “So how do you like this new life you’ve built?” Sam asked quietly.

Rio smiled softly. “Didn’t think I’d get a second chance. Certainly didn’t think it’d look like this.” She glanced across the room, where Agatha was dramatically gesturing at Kate about paint colors. “But I’ll take it.”

Sam grinned. “She’s good for you.”

“Yeah,” Rio said softly. “She really is.”

The housewarming turned into a party before either Agatha or Rio could stop it. Lilia showed up with bottles of wine, Natasha and Maria slipped in late with armfuls of groceries, Clint brought sparklers for no reason other than “it felt right,” and Tommy darted between both houses with Wanda trying, unsuccessfully, to keep him from sneaking cookies before dinner. Alice and Jen, now officially together, much to the enjoyment of everyone, showed up with almost half a dozen pizzas.

By the end of the night, the firepit was blazing, the pool lights reflected across the water, and everyone lounged around in varying states of exhaustion and laughter. Rio sat with Agatha tucked against her side, their new home alive with warmth and voices.

It wasn’t just a house. It was a safe place, a new chapter. And for the first time in what felt like forever, both of them allowed themselves to believe they’d earned it.

.

Three weeks after the last moving box was flattened and slid into the garage, the new house had settled into a rhythm that felt suspiciously like peace. Morning light spilled through the kitchen’s tall windows; Rio’s herbs, basil, thyme, a brave little rosemary, had already claimed the sunniest sill; and Agatha had reorganized the pantry three times because “chaos is a creative choice, darling.” Their days were a mix of small domestic things, Rio experimenting with sourdough starts; Agatha pretending not to eat the evidence, and normal work, which finally looked normal again.

So when Jen strode in one late afternoon, tablet in hand and the kind of smile that meant “great news that will also be a problem,” both women paused mid-banter.

“Before you say anything,” Agatha warned, lounging at the island in loose linen, “if this is about another magazine wanting to photograph us 'candidly' in the grocery store, I’ll stage a dramatic faint in the produce aisle.”

“Tempting,” Jen said, dropping her bag on a chair. “But no. This is better. Or scarier. Depends on your tolerance for soft couches and America’s favorite chaos aunt.”

Rio looked up from the cutting board, knife hovering over a pile of cilantro. “Define chaos, Aunt.”

“Drew Barrymore,” Jen said, like a magician revealing the card you picked.

Agatha’s eyebrows shot up. “Oh.”

“Joint interview,” Jen continued. “Her team reached out directly. They want a long sit-down, talking about your relationship, the Seventh Veil, Rio’s recovery, and the infamous photoshoot that launched a thousand thirsty tweets. Drew wants to do it her way: warm, candid, human. She’ll also play a silly game at the end because she’s physically incapable of not bringing out a bowl of popsicle sticks with questions written on them.”

Rio set the knife down very carefully. “I don’t…do interviews.”

“I know,” Jen said evenly. “And I’d never push you into a machine interview. But Drew’s team promised no gotcha, no ambush. She’s been there for survivors. She’s big on boundaries. You can set lines before the cameras roll.”

Agatha turned on her stool, softening. “What do you think, my love?”

Rio kept her gaze on the cutting board for a long beat. “I’m not afraid of telling the truth,” she said, voice pitched low. “I’m wary of…putting it in a place where it gets edited into something else.”

“That’s fair,” Jen said. “We’ll get editorial input. And her producers are willing to let Alice monitor in real time for safety, no live feed, nothing that could be hijacked. You’d approve everything.”

Rio’s throat worked. She looked like she was weighing the cost of something heavy and then measuring it against Agatha’s face. “Would it help?” she asked finally. “To talk about it. To talk about us.”

Agatha’s smile curved, edges fragile and real. “It might help me,” she said. “And it would help them, the people who stuck with us when everything felt impossible.”

Rio exhaled through her nose, and Agatha could see the moment some internal knot loosened. “Okay,” she said. “But if she makes me play charades on television, I’m invoking the Geneva Conventions.”

Jen’s grin flashed. “I can work with ‘okay.’ We’re looking at two weeks from today. She's in Burbank. I’ll send pre-interview questions, and you can strike anything that feels like a landmine. And for the record,” she added, glancing at Rio with a softer steadiness, “you don’t owe the world anything. You choose this because it helps you. Or not at all.”

Rio nodded. The guard in her eyes eased, a fraction. “Thanks.”

After Jen left to begin a flurry of legal emails and schedule gymnastics, Agatha drifted around the island to Rio’s side. “We can say no,” she murmured, brushing her knuckles over Rio’s rib where scar tissue still pulled tight. “We can always say no.”

Rio caught her wrist and turned it, pressing a kiss to the inside. “I know. But I also know you. You’ve never been afraid of a stage.”

“I was,” Agatha said quietly. “That night on the soundstage, when—” She stopped herself before the memory could become the room. “I want to choose the stage this time.”

“Then we choose it,” Rio said simply. “Together.”

The day of the interview came wrapped in that peculiar studio sunshine, too bright, a little unreal. Drew’s set was a living room exploded into a cozy pastel dream: soft chairs, a side table with fresh flowers, a basket of cards that promised mischief. Through the wall of windows, a fake skyline glowed perfect and oblivious.

In the green room, Rio checked exits out of habit and then chided herself because today wasn’t a battle. Today was a conversation. Agatha squeezed her hand anyway.

“You look beautiful,” Agatha said, which was true. Rio wore a black suit that looked formal on anyone else and dangerous on her, shirt open at the throat, necklace glinting. The faint line of a scar peeked above her collar; she hadn’t bothered to hide it. Agatha wore deep plum silk and a smile that had stopped traffic and at least two executives’ hearts.

“Don’t look at me like that,” Rio murmured. “You’re going to make me forget how to form sentences.”

“That’s the plan,” Agatha said.

Drew swept into the green room with a hug that felt like a heated blanket. “You angels! I’m so glad you’re here.” She was barefoot in soft trousers, hair in a cheerful tumble, eyes bright with that familiar mix of empathy and mischief. “We can throw out anything you don’t like. We can stop whenever you want. We can just drink tea and talk about your herb garden if we panic.”

Rio blinked. “You know about my herbs?”

Drew beamed. “Your basil was in the background of three of Agatha’s Instagram stories. We’re doing investigative journalism here.” She squeezed Agatha’s fingers. “Thank you for trusting me.”

The lights in the studio were bright, the air buzzing with the soft murmur of a packed audience waiting for the curtain to rise. Cameras stood like patient sentries at every angle, red tally lights winking alive as the crew finished last-minute checks. Behind the velvet curtain, Rio adjusted her jacket for what felt like the tenth time, ignoring the way her pulse hammered. She’d faced ambushes, interrogations, and firefights in deserts where the heat swallowed sound. She had not, however, faced a live studio audience in Burbank.

“Breathe,” Agatha whispered beside her, smoothing an invisible wrinkle from Rio’s lapel. “You look devastating. Half the audience is already in love with you, and you haven’t even spoken yet.”

“That’s what I’m afraid of,” Rio muttered, scanning exits, counting cameras.

Agatha tilted her chin, dark eyes gleaming. “Darling, it’s Drew Barrymore. This is as safe as it gets. And besides—” her voice dropped low, wicked, “—if you start panicking, I’ll just distract you with innuendo.”

Rio’s lips twitched despite herself. “You’re insufferable.”

“And irresistible,” Agatha shot back.

Before Rio could answer, a stagehand gestured them forward. The band kicked up Drew’s cheerful theme, the curtain parted, and applause rolled like a wave. Drew stood center stage, barefoot and glowing, arms open.

“Ladies and gentlemen, today is special,” she said over the roar. “Please welcome—together for the first time on television—Agatha Harkness and Rio Vidal!”

The audience leapt to their feet. Cheers, whistles, and camera flashes erupted. Rio blinked hard against the flood of sound, her body tensing automatically. Agatha, of course, drank it in, her smile wide and dazzling as she led Rio by the hand to the chairs.

They settled, Agatha crossing one elegant leg over the other, Rio stiff but steady, shoulders squared as if bracing for gunfire instead of questions. Drew perched opposite them, eyes sparkling.

“First of all,” Drew said, beaming, “thank you both. I know being here, like this, took a lot of thought, a lot of courage. And I think the world is grateful.”

The applause swelled again, softer this time, touched with warmth.

Agatha inclined her head graciously. “It’s us who should be grateful. To you, to them,” she gestured toward the audience, “for holding the line when things were… very dark.”

Rio shifted, uneasy under the weight of so many eyes. Her hand curled against her thigh. Agatha noticed. Without missing a beat, she leaned over, threading their fingers together. “See? Not so terrifying.”

“Give me a knife fight over this any day,” Rio muttered.

The crowd laughed. Drew grinned. “She’s funny! Who knew?”

“She’s hilarious,” Agatha said fondly. “She just doesn’t share with anyone but me.”

The audience melted at that. Rio groaned under her breath.

Drew leaned forward, conspiratorial. “Okay. Let’s get this out of the way. The photoshoot. The Suit, the Tattoos. The TENSION. The internet explosion.”

The audience whooped. Someone shouted, “RIOOOO!” and half the crowd laughed.

Rio’s ears went pink. “It wasn’t supposed to be me. A model called out last minute. They needed a stand-in, and Agatha was insistent that it should be me.”

“Best Decision of my life,” Agatha purred.

Applause, laughter, catcalls. Rio shook her head, muttering something in Spanish.

Drew clutched her chest dramatically. “Listen, I have lived through internet thirst. But the way the world went feral over you two? Over her in particular?” She mimed fanning herself. “How did that feel?”

Agatha’s grin went sly. “Vindicating.”

Rio groaned again, but the flush on her cheeks betrayed her. “I didn’t…expect it,” she admitted. “I’ve spent my whole life in shadows. Seeing… that reaction was strange.” She glanced at Agatha. “But if they were cheering because she was happy? Then I’ll take it.”

The audience “awwed” so loudly that Drew waved her hands like a conductor.

Agatha tilted her head. “Also, I personally enjoyed the tweets. Very creative.”

“Don’t encourage them,” Rio hissed.

“Too late,” Drew laughed.

When the laughter eased, Drew steered them into deeper waters. “Rio, I want to ask something I think everyone wonders. You run the top private security firm in the world. Why take this case personally? Why Agatha?”

Rio sat straighter, eyes flitting to the audience and back. For a moment, she looked like she might retreat behind deflection. Then she exhaled.

“Because I knew Lilia’s son,” she said. The crowd stilled. “Colten. We served together. He was good. Solid. The kind of soldier you trusted with your life.” She paused. “When Lilia came to SHIELD, she specifically asked for me to lead the team. I didn’t know who she was at first, but when she told me…I couldn’t say no. Not when it was her family.”

The audience’s silence was reverent, weighted.

Agatha’s hand squeezed hers. “She showed up in my life because of loyalty. And she stayed because I was relentless.”

Drew’s smile tilted. “Relentless, how?”

Rio smirked faintly. “She threw every innuendo at me she could think of.”

“I’m thorough,” Agatha said, unapologetic. “And before you ask, yes, I was her first celebrity crush. Imagine my delight when she admitted it.”

The audience erupted again. Drew gasped theatrically. “Stop. You had a crush on her first?”

Rio’s flush returned. “I watched her films when I was younger and then again when I was overseas. They reminded me there was still light. That’s all.”

“That’s everything,” Agatha corrected softly.

For a moment, the air between them felt fragile, tender. Then Drew, an expert at shifting tones, leaned in. “Rio, you almost lost your life protecting her. More than once. People know you were hurt. They don’t know the details. What do you want them to understand?”

Rio’s jaw flexed. “That it was ugly,” she said bluntly. “Multiple gunshots. Stab wounds, collapsed lung, internal injuries. More blood on sidewalks than anyone should see. I died. More than once. The doctors brought me back.”

The audience gasped, a ripple of shock.

“But,” Rio continued, voice steady, “I don’t regret it. Not for a second. If it meant she’s sitting here now, alive, laughing, infuriating me—” she shook her head, a ghost of a smile tugging at her lips, “then it was worth every scar.”

The audience surged to their feet in applause. Agatha blinked hard, her hand tightening on Rio’s. She kissed her knuckles without shame, eyes wet.

Drew let the moment breathe before turning gently to Agatha. “The world saw your mother. Saw what she did. How do you even begin to process that?”

Agatha drew herself tall, shoulders regal. “By naming it. It was abuse. It always was. No camera can rewrite that truth. She tried to make me a monster. Instead, she showed the world her own face.”

The audience murmured, nodding, clapping softly.

“And while I am endlessly grateful to my fans,” Agatha went on, her voice warm but firm, “I need them to hear this: I do not owe anyone my attention. Or my story. Or my pain. I share it because I choose to, not because it’s theirs to demand. Boundaries are not ingratitude. They are survival.”

A swell of applause rose again, louder this time, fierce and supportive.

Drew’s eyes glistened. “That’s…beautifully said.”

Agatha smiled, then reached for Rio’s hand again. “But I do owe them gratitude. For standing by us. For refusing to let lies be louder than love.”

That earned cheers.

“And speaking of love,” Drew teased, “tell me about this new project. I’ve heard whispers.”

Agatha’s expression softened. “Yes. Wanda and I are starting a foundation in Billy’s name. Billy’s Light. It will help victims of stalking and harassment get the help, protection, and legal resources they need. We’ve partnered with S.H.I.E.L.D. because they know the cost of silence and are equipped to protect the victims like they did me.”

The audience erupted in applause, some even standing.

Agatha’s smile wavered, grief threaded through pride. “No one should lose a child the way Wanda did. If we can spare even one family that pain, then Billy’s light will never go out.”

Rio slipped an arm around her shoulders, steadying her through the thunderous applause.

“For this next segment, I’ve asked the audience to send in their burning questions, the ones they really want answered.” Drew wiggled her brows at the crowd, who immediately erupted with cheers. “Are you two ready?”

“As ready as we’ll ever be,” Rio said, sitting with her usual composure, though the way her arm rested protectively across the back of Agatha’s chair betrayed her.

Agatha smirked. “Oh, I was born ready.”

“Alright,” Drew grinned, glancing at the card. “First question: who made the first move?”

“Agatha,” Rio answered without hesitation. “She was relentless from the very first meeting. She flirted so much that Jen, her publicist, actually brought a spray bottle to spray her every time she said something inappropriate toward me. Which was… a lot.”

The audience howled.

“Didn’t work,” Agatha purred, flipping her hair back dramatically. “I always get what I want. And I wanted you. Jen only made me wet with that spray bottle… just not wetter than when I’m with you.”

Rio went scarlet as the crowd exploded into screams. Drew fell forward, laughing so hard she nearly dropped her cards. “I’m crying already!”

“Next question,” Drew wheezed, trying to compose herself. “Funniest memory involving the other?”

“Oh, I got one,” Agatha said gleefully. “The first time I stayed over at Rio’s house, I went to take a shower. She came in to bring me clothes, sweet, right? Except she didn’t realize I was naked. I have never seen someone gay-panic so hard in my life. She ran into the door, apologized to the door, tripped over her own feet, and fell into the dresser. Funniest thing I’ve ever seen.”

The audience lost it. Drew had actual tears running down her cheeks.

Rio sighed like a woman resigned to her fate. “There was one time we went hiking,” she countered smoothly. “Agatha tripped over a tree root and fell face-first into a puddle. Then she panicked and nearly drowned herself… in three inches of water.”

The laughter doubled. Agatha didn’t even look embarrassed, just turned those soft, fond eyes on Rio, smiling like she’d do it all over again just to make her laugh.

Once Drew finally caught her breath, she managed, “Most annoying habit about the other one?”

“Agatha cheats at every game,” Rio said instantly. “And when she loses, because sometimes I do catch her, she flips tables.”

“I do not cheat!” Agatha gasped in mock offense. “I just interpret rules… creatively.”

Rio arched a brow. “Scrabble is not an interpretive game.”

The crowd roared.

Agatha smirked and leaned forward. “And for Rio? It’s her savior complex. She throws herself into danger without a second thought. But…” Her hand slid into Rio’s, squeezing gently. “It’s also one of the things I love most about her. That instinct to protect, to put others first. Even when it drives me mad with worry.”

Rio squeezed back, silent but steady. The audience aww’d.

“A few more here,” Drew said, shuffling the cards. “What’s something you do to stay grounded and keep a healthy relationship, especially with the public scrutiny you both face?”

Rio tilted her head, letting Agatha take the lead.

“When the world gets too loud, we run away,” Agatha said simply. “We’ve got a place where it’s just us. No cameras, no scripts, no responsibilities. Just quiet. Just love.” She glanced sideways at Rio, and the soft smile that pulled at her lips told the audience everything they needed to know about the cabin.

Rio cleared her throat. “We also talk. We banter, we argue sometimes, but we don’t let things fester. And we surround ourselves with people who call us out. People who’ll spray us with water if we’re being dumb, or literally lock us in a room until we work it out.”

The audience erupted in laughter again. Drew clutched her chest. “That is the most adorable, and honestly, the most sappy, thing I’ve ever heard.”

“Don’t encourage her,” Rio muttered, though the smile tugging at her mouth betrayed her.

“Next one’s a good one,” Drew said, grinning. “What’s the most surprising thing you’ve learned about each other since getting together?”

Agatha’s hand shot up like a kid in class. “She sings when she cooks. Badly. Off-key. Like, so off-key. But it’s the cutest thing I’ve ever heard, so I let her believe she’s Beyoncé.”

Rio covered her face as the crowd roared. “It keeps the kitchen morale up,” she muttered.

“And for me?” Rio added, recovering with her usual composure. “Agatha actually hates scary movies. She’ll insist on watching them to prove she’s fearless, then spend the whole night under the blanket with one eye peeking out. And she jumps at shadows for a week after.”

“I do not!” Agatha gasped.

“You made me check the closet for clowns,” Rio said dryly.

The audience screamed with laughter.

Drew wiped her eyes, barely holding it together. “Okay, last one, this one’s mine. What does the future look like for you two?”

Agatha and Rio looked at each other. They didn’t need words; the conversation passed in glances, the kind of silent dialogue that comes only with trust. The audience leaned in, holding their breath.

“Right now?” Agatha said finally, voice soft. “It’s to love each other. We just bought a house, our first real home together. Even though we’ve lived together twenty-four seven for the past six months, this is different. It’s not her place or mine. It’s ours. We’re building a life. I’ve got new roles coming up, Rio’s back at S.H.I.E.L.D., and we’re just taking it one step at a time. Together.”

She leaned in and kissed Rio softly, unapologetically, the crowd erupting in delighted cheers.

Rio’s hand lingered at the back of her neck when they pulled apart. “That’s the only future I need,” she said simply.

The audience melted. Drew fanned herself dramatically. “Ladies and gentlemen, if you weren’t believers before, you are now. This is love.”

The applause thundered, long and loud, filling the studio with something bigger than noise, something like hope.

 

The night after the interview was warm, the kind of late-summer hush that carried cicadas and the faint hum of sprinklers from distant lawns. Agatha had dragged a dozen candles outside, lining the edge of the pool until their flames wavered like stars fallen to earth. The water caught the light and threw it back in ripples of gold and blue, soft and endless.

Rio sat with her legs stretched out, toes just grazing the surface, a half-empty glass of wine dangling from her fingers. The scars along her collarbone and ribs caught the glow, pale reminders of everything they’d survived. Agatha settled beside her, pulling her silk robe tighter around herself, though the air was gentle. For a moment, they said nothing, listening to the stillness of their own backyard.

“You realize,” Agatha murmured at last, tilting her glass toward the water, “this is the first pool I’ve been near where someone hasn’t tried to throw me into it.”

Rio’s mouth curved. “Give it time.”

Agatha nudged her knee against Rio’s. “Don’t you dare. These candles make me far too mysterious and beautiful to ruin.”

Rio huffed a laugh, low and quiet, then sobered, her eyes on the faint trail of moonlight across the water. “Feels strange, doesn’t it? To sit like this. No teams on watch. No alarms. Just…” She gestured at the pool, the candles, the night. “Us.”

Agatha studied her in the glow, all sharp edges softened by the light. “Strange,” she agreed. “And perfect.”

For a long breath, Rio didn’t answer, just leaned into the silence. When she did, her voice was steady but low. “I keep thinking I’ll wake up, and that this, ”she gestured again, helpless this time, “was a dream. And I’ll have to start the fight all over.”

Agatha set her glass down and reached for her hand. “No dreams. No battles. Just us, in a house with too many bathrooms and a pool I plan to scandalize the neighbors with.”

Rio turned, brow arched. “Scandalize?”

Agatha smirked, her thumb brushing along Rio’s knuckles. “Skinny-dipping, of course. Don’t look at me like that, you knew what you were signing up for.”

Rio shook her head, but her smile was soft, pulled from some place deep. She lifted Agatha’s hand and pressed a kiss into the back of it. “You make even the scars feel worth it.”

Agatha’s throat tightened. She leaned in, resting her forehead against Rio’s. The candles flickered around them, the pool lapping gently against its edge. “Then promise me,” she whispered. “No more knives, no more bullets. Just life. With me.”

Rio’s answer was simple, a vow sealed in the still air. “Always.”

They kissed, unhurried, the kind that carried no fear of being interrupted. When they finally broke apart, Agatha glanced up at the sky, stars scattered like embers across velvet. For a fleeting moment, her voice softened into something almost prayerful. “For Billy. For all the light he left behind.”

Rio followed her gaze, squeezing her hand gently. “He’d like this. Us. Here. Peace.”

Agatha blinked hard, then smiled through it. “Then we’ll keep it. For him. For us.”

She tugged Rio toward the water, laughter slipping out like a balm, and together they stepped into the shimmering glow. Behind them, the candles burned steadily, as if holding the night in place just for them.

The scars, the grief, the battles, all of it had led them here, poolside in the quiet glow, where loss had become memory, and love had become home.
